# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 26

## 9591

[9591](#_ftn_1)

[B"H](#_ftn_2), 5th of Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal needs,

[Mr.](#_ftn_3) Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding your birthday,

You have surely followed the custom of anash in recent times regarding one’s birthday. May it be the will of Hashem that this be a year of success for you, both materially and spiritually, and may you increase your study of Torah and the fulfillment of its mitzvos with abundance.

With blessings for a Gmar Chasima Tova and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

The donations (tzedakah) that you write of—[should be given] to the esteemed Chossid, etc., Rabbi D.B. Chen, may he live [of Kfar Chabad](#_ftn_4).

Regarding your note on the Iggeres HaKodesh, the maamar beginning "Oteh Or"—see the Tzemach Tzedek’s Reshimot on the verse ([in Yehal Or](#_ftn_5)).

## 9506

B"H, 5th of Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 9/19,

– You should have **all** the mezuzos as well as the tefillin in your home checked (inspected) to ensure that they are all kosher according to law. – However, this does not apply to those that have been checked within the last twelve months.

And at a time of favor, you will be remembered at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for a Gmar Chasimah Tovah.

## 9597

[9597](#_ftn_6)

B"H, Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos, in which you write regarding your son, may he live.

Generally speaking, to our great sorrow, such a case is not rare in these times, and surely you have heard from the attending physicians that there are quite a number of cases similar to his. I write this not because "the distress of the many is half a consolation"—I do not know if that is appropriate here—but rather to emphasize that the doctors have extensive experience in this field, and there is also intensive research being conducted regarding methods of treatment and healing for this, etc.

Therefore, it is understood that there is no place to predict that the prospects are unfavorable or the like. In any event, one must add the caveat that this is only according to the current state of medical science, and in the aforementioned field, as mentioned, the research is extremely intensive since many are in need of it.

A second point in my aforementioned writing: Therefore, it is worthwhile to maintain contact **with those who are engaged** in this research, or those close to them, and to ask them from time to time what has been newly discovered in this field. The emphasis is on those engaged in the aforementioned research, because by the time the results of the research reach the attending physicians, a very long time passes, since the attending physicians hear about this from medical journals, where the articles are printed in long reports, and in general, they are only published after the remedy has been tested and proven over a long period of time.

In similar cases, good results have been seen when one takes the person in need of healing out of his "four cubits" by requesting his participation in an activity, an institution, or the like, as a request for a favor from him. For in the vast majority of cases, when one asks them, they refuse, because the impression they have is that the intention is to do them a favor or to heal them, etc. This is not the case when the approach is that a certain institution or a certain activity is in need of the person's help and participation, etc., and it is impossible otherwise; often they are willing to provide their help, and consequently, little by little, they become more involved with people. However, as mentioned, the conversation must be in a manner that does not arouse suspicion that there is a ruse here to take him out of his framework.

B"H, the *pidyon nefesh* will be read at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevgam, zya*, in accordance with your letter.

Knowing you, I surely do not need to mention that an increase in Torah and *mitzvos* adds to the blessing of Hashem, Who heals all flesh and performs wonders. And in matters connected to the *Ein Sof, Baruch Hu*—namely, matters of Torah and *mitzvos*—even when the situation is good, there is room to increase many times over (which is why everyone is commanded [to ascend](#_ftn_8) in holiness). And when it concerns a public figure who has influence in his environment and in a wide circle, the full utilization of his influence to instill Yiddishkeit and its values without any compromises is one of his primary tasks, [and in the language](#_ftn_9) of our Sages, *z"l*, this falls under the category of a *mitzvah* that one must be extra careful with.

With respect and with the blessing of *Chasimah v’Gmar Chasimah Tovah*.

## 9578

B"H, 11 Tishrei, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I am writing to acknowledge receipt of your letter (undated), in which you write regarding your state of mind, etc.

It is a great wonder that a Jew should be in such a state of mind, for a person in general, and a Jew in particular, is forbidden to despair. This is explained and emphasized in our Torah, the Torah of life—*Torah* coming from the word *hora'ah* (instruction), instruction for daily life. It is also understood that since every Jew possesses a soul that is literally a part of G-d above, there is no room for despair. Rather, one must maintain a connection and an open channel with Hashem Yisbarach, the source of life and blessing. This connection is maintained through conduct in daily life according to the instructions of Hashem in His Torah, starting with the laying of tefillin every weekday, the kashrus of one’s food, and so on. If you contact our office in Paris, they will gladly provide you with all the necessary information.

May it be His will that you share good news, especially now that we have entered a new year—a year that is good and sweet, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

In the secretariat, we do not write in French, but you may continue to write in French in the future; however, please indicate whether you would like us to reply in Lashon HaKodesh, Yiddish, (or English).

## 9599 

[B"H, Chol Hamoed Sukkos, 5729]

Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.

R' Moshe Avraham, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

We hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 8th of Tishrei. Transcribed below is the text of the telegram that the Rebbe, shlita, was pleased to send you today:

To the honorable participants in the Hakafos of Simchas Torah in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu, together with all our brothers, the Children of Israel, who are rejoicing in the Simchas Torah wherever they may be — shlita.

At a time when Simchas Torah—the joy of Israel in the Torah and the joy of the Torah in Israel—encompasses and unites all our people, those near and those far alike, there is a special power and content to this joy in the united Jerusalem, which our Sages of blessed memory informed us was not divided among the tribes, for it is the eternal inheritance of all of Israel, given to them by the G-d of the world, as it is written in His Torah.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that Jerusalem befit its destiny —that from it shall go forth Torah and the word of Hashem, and all the peoples of the earth shall see that the name of Hashem is called upon it and upon our people, one nation on earth. And very soon, may we merit to see the true and complete Geulah, as per the word of Hashem: "Behold, I will bring them from the north country and gather them from the ends of the earth... a great company shall return here. They shall come with weeping, and with supplications will I lead them; I will cause them to walk by the rivers of waters in a straight way... and they shall come and sing in the height of Zion."

Participating in your joy, which is our joy, and signing with a prayer for a year of joy and Torah, for a year of Geulah.

**Menachem Schneerson**

The telegram was surely received in due time. With respect and blessings for the holiday.

Secretary

## 9580

[9580](#_ftn_22)

[B"H](#_ftn_23), 25 Tishrei, 5729

Brooklyn.

To the Committee of the Tzemach Tzedek Synagogue in the Old City of Jerusalem,

May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

Transcribed here is the text of the telegram that the Rebbe shlita was kind enough to send them last night:

["As in my letters](#_ftn_24) from the past — regarding all matters of the synagogue, both spiritual and material; the *nusach*, customs, management, construction, and so on: the committee is the representative of *anash* and my own representative, and it is they who judge, determine, and decide, both internally and externally. It is a great wonder that there is even a question regarding this.

May Hashem grant you success in the holy *avodah* of establishing, expanding, and growing the synagogue in both quantity and quality. Certainly, all *anash* will assist you, and may the house be great in *tefillah* and in Torah, both the revealed and the inner dimensions, just as instructed by the Baal Shem Tov and the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, until the coming of the *Tzemach*—who is our righteous Moshiach.

With blessings for success, and for an active *farbrengen* in the synagogue this coming Shabbos Bereishis.

**Menachem Schneerson"**

Respectfully,

S.M. Simpson – Secretary

## 9581

[9581](#_ftn_27)

[B"H](#_ftn_28), 2nd day of Rosh Chodesh Cheshvan, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, a young man of the people and elevated above the people, who seeks the good of his nation and possesses noble character, a branch of the tree of the forefathers, [R' Schneur Zalman](#_ftn_29) Shlita,

Peace and blessing!

The guests who returned to Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—surely conveyed to you orally [my blessing](#_ftn_30) regarding the matters of the day, [the dedication](#_ftn_31) of the house named after him in Kfar Chabad.

And through the [drink](#_ftn_32) that brings hearts closer, [from the beverage](#_ftn_33) of the Simchas Torah farbrengen and its continuation on Shabbos Bereishis, may it be the will of Hashem that the house befit its name, serving as a center for Jewish youth in the aforementioned spirit: Torah with joy, and joy in all of a person’s affairs through Torah. For all the affairs of man and of creation in its entirety have their source in the Torah, as our Sages of blessed memory stated (Bereishis Rabbah at the beginning) that the Torah is the ledger and register according to which the Holy One, Blessed be He, created His world. From this, it is also understood that all matters of creation have their source in the Torah and reach their perfection when they correspond to their source, through the person who lives and exists in accordance with his source, and this is well understood.

And since "Love your fellow as yourself" is a [great principle](#_ftn_35) in the Torah, I pray and hope with strong confidence that this youth will grow to be, each one of them, a center for many, many of our people’s youth, who will also grow in the spirit of Torah and mitzvos, until the joy is doubled—[as interpreted](#_ftn_36) by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, regarding the concept of Simchas Torah: the joy of the Torah within each and every one of them, and their own joy in the Torah.

With appreciation, honor, and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

On this occasion, enclosed is what was recently published. Although it may have been sent separately, perhaps this letter will arrive first, and "an hour earlier is better."

Also enclosed is the receipt for the sum that was delivered by the people of Kfar Chabad, may they live, before Rosh Hashanah. And if the charity of an individual is equivalent, etc., and brings the Redemption closer (Tanya, ch. 37; see there)—how much more so is this true of a person who is a center for many, chosen from among the many, whose influence extends to the many.

## 9582

[9582](#_ftn_37)

B”H, 2nd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5729
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter containing a request for a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh* dated 13th of Tishrei.

At an opportune time, it will be read at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote concerning a *shidduch* proposal: When one of the parties (or both) decides that they will only be interested in pursuing a *shidduch* a year (or more) from now, it is not advisable to "bind" (*binden*) or even restrict either of the parties or the parents—**at all**. There are several reasons for this, and it is easy to understand. Each case should be treated as if it has not even begun.

I trust you are keeping up with the three daily study portions—*Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—that are incumbent upon everyone.

With blessings,

Regarding what you wrote [concerning](#_ftn_38) *bitachon*—it is understood that the matter does not depart from its literal meaning, as is proven **in many places** in the Written Torah and the Oral Torah. See *Chovos HaLevavos*, *Shaar HaBitachon*. [See also](#_ftn_39) *Biurei HaZohar* (by the Mitteler Rebbe and the Tzemach Tzedek—it was just published) at the beginning of *Parshas Va’era*.

## 9583

[9583](#_ftn_40)

[B"H](#_ftn_41), 5 Marcheshvan, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned Rabbi Adin [Steinsaltz](#_ftn_42), may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I am writing to acknowledge receipt of your letter from the night following Shemini Atzeres, in addition to the [telegram](#_ftn_43). You are surely aware of the subsequent developments, which are in accordance with the telegram I sent to the Committee that represents the Chabad institutions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and Anash, may they live and be well, who are in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and who were elected by them, etc.

Through this, my position on the matter is also clarified: they—the Committee—are the ones who decide on all matters concerning the shul. This would be the case even if it were an ordinary shul; how much more so when it was founded by the Tzemach Tzedek and is named after him, etc. This means that the Tzemach Tzedek’s revealed Torah—including his [halachic ruling](#_ftn_44) regarding the growing of a beard as it pertains to **gaba'im and the like**—as well as his inner teachings, must be evident in all matters of this shul and beis medrash, and first and foremost in the customs of the shul, the shiurim taught there, and so on. A word to the wise is sufficient. And this is easy to understand.

It was a pleasant surprise for me to just now receive Maseches Shabbos (Part One), which you have published with the addition of your explanations, etc. Fortunate is your portion to see good fruit from your labor. May it be His will that you go from strength to strength, increasing in light, for in matters of holiness there is always room to add—and we are also [commanded](#_ftn_45) to add—since they are connected to the Holy One, Blessed be He, who is infinite. May Hashem grant you success in improving and adding to the aforementioned, and the merit of the many will surely assist you.

Moving from one topic to another, this is the place to express my sorrow and great astonishment that the [collection](#_ftn_46) dedicated to the Alter Rebbe has not yet been published. Although one does not cry over the past, I will express my hope that by the festival of the Alter Rebbe’s redemption—which is also our redemption and the salvation of our souls—the aforementioned collection will already appear, bound, etc., in such a way that on this day, or better yet, even before it, it will increase knowledge of the Alter Rebbe’s approach and his Torah, in a manner that [leads](#_ftn_47) to action: "walking in the straight path that he taught us, from his ways, and we shall walk in his paths, may he rest in peace" (Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 27). And according to the information I have received from several people, the matter depends solely on you.

With respect and blessings for success in all your endeavors and for good tidings regarding the above,

**M. Schneerson**

Surely you will also send here the other materials you have published, and I thank you in advance.

## 9584 

 7 Marcheshvan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter and its enclosure regarding the job offer in...

Regarding the position itself, you should consult with friends on the spot who know the details of your current position and the details of the offer in... And it has already been said, "In the multitude of counselors there is safety." It is understood that it is appropriate to discuss the offer [to see] if, by doing so, no damage will be caused to the institution in...

2) Regarding the authority of the school in... etc., the question and the doubt are surprising. For it is understood and simple that in a community worthy of the name "community in Israel"—a *kehillah kedishah*—the final arbiter in all matters of the community is the Rav, the *mara d'asra*. This is all the more so in the area of education and in our current times, because the future of the students—and through them, the parents as well—depends on education, and so on.

It is my hope that you are also participating in the dissemination of the study of *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, which has just been published as a separate booklet, etc., in order to increase its distribution, and the merit of the public will assist you.

Regarding... — as per the response to the committee.

With blessings for good news regarding the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9785

[9785](#_ftn_52)

B”H, 13 Marcheshvan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Monday, Parshas Noach, along with the enclosure, which is returned herewith:

In my opinion, you should make every possible effort to continue in your professorship at [the university in]... Beyond the good prospects of the position itself, there is this—which is the main thing—that it provides you with the ability and significant opportunities to disseminate traditional Judaism in..., and the same applies to your wife, may she live.

Even if one were to argue that you could do this in another location as well, one cannot predict in advance the necessity and success in a new place. Furthermore—and this is also a primary consideration—the ruling of our Sages, of blessed memory, is that [the needs of] your own city take precedence. 

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your wife and children, may they live; I take this as a sign that everything is in order. The life of a Jewish man and woman is one of going [from strength](#_ftn_54) to strength in matters of Torah and mitzvos, and [ascending](#_ftn_55) in holiness.

You are surely aware that *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our Alter Rebbe has been published in a special edition in connection with the campaign to disseminate the study of this section of the holy Tanya, and that an English translation of *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* has also been published in a special edition. I have strong hope that you will include the dissemination of this study in your outreach activities—and, of course, [study](#_ftn_57) that leads to action, for [action](#_ftn_58) is the essential thing.

With blessings for good news.

## 9896

[9896](#_ftn_59)

[B"H](#_ftn_60), 13 Marcheshvan, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal affairs, etc.

R' [Moshe](#_ftn_61) Tzvi, may he live, Halevi

Greetings and blessings!

I have just received your letter, which was an addendum to the letter from Mr. Beer, may he live. Enclosed is [the response to the aforementioned](#_ftn_62). Surely, if further explanation is needed, you will find the appropriate words for it.

Your letter [regarding](#_ftn_63) Hebron was received some time ago. It is somewhat surprising, for since you are on the scene, you are surely aware of the doubts and the back-and-forth regarding Hebron on the part of those who determine the course of events in Eretz Yisrael. Among them—to our great sorrow and shame—at least for the time being, those who lean to the left far outnumber those who lean to the right and believe; and a word to the wise is sufficient. You are surely also aware of the restrictions, etc., that were imposed upon those who "dared" to settle in Hebron. There is no need to dwell at length on this distressing matter, which is painful to the extreme.

It is understood that the discord regarding the "Tzemach Tzedek" [shul](#_ftn_64) in the Old City is most distressing. My hope is that you will do everything in your power—not only to diminish the discord, but to eliminate it once and for all. This is based on the point that this is not a shul like all other shuls, and not even like other shuls in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). Rather, it is the "representative of the shuls" of Anash wherever they may dwell, both in Eretz Yisrael and abroad. From this, it is understood—and it is also simple—that the administration must be in the hands of the representatives of Anash in every location. [This is the law](#_ftn_65) even in the revealed realm regarding a shul that belongs to Jews located everywhere. This was also the reason I appointed a committee not of private individuals, but of Anash institutions in Eretz Yisrael, as well as Kfar Chabad (with the exception of the late R' A. Pariz, of blessed memory, since it was impossible to hold elections from Aguch, Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, so I chose them based on my estimation). It is also simple that, first and foremost, it is for the aforementioned administration—elected from the aforementioned institutions—to determine the customs of the shul, the gabbaim of the shul, etc., etc. It is a great wonder that there is any doubt in the matter, and a wonder that there is an argument to negate the high value of the shul and make it subject to the authority of those who happen to come to pray there on Shabbos, weekdays, or festivals.

It is simple that my intention is that after contemplating the above, those same congregants will surely, out of a yearning and desirous soul and true will, cooperate with the administration—accepting its ownership and authority with joy and a good heart. And the desire of Hashem will succeed in their hands to expand the shul in both quantity and quality, [as in my letter](#_ftn_66) from some time ago regarding this shul.

May it be the will of Hashem that they succeed, and may He bless them to bring good tidings regarding all of the above, and speedily. A true good, which is good for Heaven and good for people alike, as per the ruling of our Sages, of blessed memory (Kiddushin 40a). And may it be that at the first opportunity, you will all hold a Chassidishe farbrengen together for this purpose, and may the saying of our Rebbe (the Alter Rebbe) regarding these farbrengens be fulfilled in it: "What a Chassidishe farbrengen can accomplish, the Angel Michael cannot accomplish, as explained in a wonderful parable" (see *Kovetz Michtavim* at the end of *Sefer Tehillim Ohel Yosef Yitzchak HaShalem*, [p.](#_ftn_67) 723, 5723).

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. It is strange that you wrote [that the telegram](#_ftn_68) did not reach him directly, for it was written on his address: Old City, Chabad Street.

## 9587

[9587](#_ftn_69)

[B"H](#_ftn_70), 13 Marcheshvan, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and upright man, engaged in communal needs,
Mr. Aharon Bir

Greetings and blessings!

I have just received the *pidyon nefesh* written for you and for your wife, *tichye*. I will mention you at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for good and for blessing.

Based on what I have heard about you, it is superfluous to emphasize that an increase in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* increases the blessings of Hashem. This is especially true when one is in need of a special blessing. After all, in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, there is always room for increase, since they are infinite, as their source is in the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He.

May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all of the above.

I have a strong hope that you have set times each day for Torah study, both in the *nigleh* (the revealed aspects of Torah) and in the *pnimiyus haTorah* (the inner dimension of Torah), which is the teachings of Chassidus. The necessity of studying both is explained in many places. [And certainly](#_ftn_71) our friend, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and upright man, engaged in communal needs, R' Moshe Tzvi Halevi Segal, has already spoken with you about these matters.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9588 

B”H, 13 Marcheshvan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished scholar, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., [Rabbi](#_ftn_73) Hillel Medalie, may he live, Chief Rabbi and Av Beis Din of the Jewish community in Antwerp.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 8th of this month, as well as your previous ones.

At an auspicious time, I will mention everyone you have mentioned at the holy gravesite. May it be His will that just as you have brought the request, you will also share good news regarding each and every one of them—and, of course, first and foremost regarding your brother, the esteemed Chassid, etc., R’ D.B., may he live.

Regarding what you wrote concerning "the innocent writer" (ha-sofer ha-tamim), it is unclear to whom you are referring. In any event, if the books that are about to be published are in the appropriate spirit—that is, in the spirit of Torah, etc.—then it is certainly the right thing to do. This is especially true since, to our great sorrow, [much of](#_ftn_74) the literature that illuminates (or more accurately, darkens) the period of the Holocaust describes the role of Torah-observant Jews in a way that is the opposite of the truth, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Your reasoning is correct to approach the Claims Conference regarding the printing of the memorial book, although I do not know the situation this year as to whether they have a special fund for this project or if it should be attached to another program.

And regarding what you wrote about your birthday: May it be His will that this be a year of success in both private and communal matters alike, for an ascent [from strength](#_ftn_75) to strength in all [three](#_ftn_76) lines—Torah, avodah, and acts of kindness—upon which the great world [and the small world](#_ftn_77)—which is man—stand.

Since you do not mention anything regarding your health, I wish to maintain the assumption of fitness (chazakas kashrus) for everyone, which includes physical health. For the ruling of the great teacher—the Rambam—is that having a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem (Hilchos De’os, end of chapter 4). [I have previously noted elsewhere that, in my humble opinion, the original copyist omitted one word, and this omission has persisted in subsequent copies; it should read: "among the ways of the **avodah** of Hashem" (see there, end of chapter 3).](#_ftn_78)

With respect and blessing for good news in all the above.

## 9,889 

 15 Marcheshvan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, 
Rabbi Shalom Dovber Lipshitz

Greetings and blessings!

Mr. Yosef Klarman visited me recently, and we spoke at length regarding his new position, the aliyah program, and so on.

Naturally, the conversation focused primarily on the continuation of religious education for all those immigrants who have received such an education until now, and so forth. He promised definitively that everything will be handled in the best possible way. He also added that he has already met with you and your colleagues—whom he mentioned by name—and told them the same, with the addition that he requests that if there should be any complaint or grievance, etc., you should notify him as soon as possible, and he will conduct the appropriate investigation in order to rectify what needs to be rectified, etc. He also stated that his door is open to you at all times and that he is prepared to provide the names of the immigrants, etc., although this last point was not discussed clearly, as the situation regarding this is not known here.

On his way back to the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, from his travels, he will be in New York again, and as discussed, we will meet once more. Therefore, it is worthwhile that before then, you inform us here in detail regarding all of the above and anything related to it, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

It has been a long time since we have received any letters or news from you, and may it be G-d’s will that this is a sign that everything is in order, both in general and personal matters alike.

With blessings for success in the above and for good tidings.

## 9590

[9590](#_ftn_82)

B"H, 15 MarCheshvan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.
[Rabbi](#_ftn_83) Chaim Yaakov Shlame, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I trust you arrived home safely and found your family, may they live and be well, in good order, including the students of Beis Rivkah, may they live. I am certain that matters have settled into their proper order and course, and the order in matters of Torah and holiness is such that no day is the same as the one before it, for the [commandment](#_ftn_84) is to ascend in holiness, and this is in full force every single day, and this is well understood.

With blessings for success in all that was mentioned, including true nachas from all your descendants, may they live.

P.S. Enclosed is a copy of the letter to Mr. Lubetzky, may he live. If further explanation is needed, etc., I am sure you will find an appropriate opportunity to do so in the proper manner.

## 9,591

[9,591]

[15 Marcheshvan, 5729]

It is **obvious** that the existence of a created being is within its own reality, and the **truth** of Torah explicitly states: "In the beginning, Hashem created the heavens and the earth." On the contrary, it is precisely in this that the "power and capability" (of the One "whose existence is from His own Essence") lies, "to create **yesh** [something from nothing], etc." (Iggeres HaKodesh, section 20, 130b; see there). See also Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, chapter 3: "And behold, it is **obvious** that this light and radiance **exists** also within the body, etc.," except that "the **name** [of the body] does not apply to it, etc." Rather (in the language of the Rambam at the beginning of his work), this existence is (being brought into being at every moment) from the truth of His existence. See also the [maamar entitled] *Mi Kamocha*, 5629.

[Regarding] Divine Providence and free choice—it is possible to say that this is within the Divine Providence that in matters of Heaven (Iggeres HaKodesh, section 25, 140, bottom of 2b) it will be dependent on choice, and there is no need to elaborate here.

**He who splits the sea for those who fear Him**

## 9192

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Ariel, may he live, General Sharon,

Peace and blessing!

I trust my letter of 12 Elul was received in due time, and surely you will respond at the appropriate time.

Especially since, in the weeks that have passed since then, there have been several developments and events which, in my opinion, further strengthen the premises set forth in that letter.

As we discussed in our conversation, in this period of ours, which is full of confusion and differences of opinion, the statement written in our Torah—Torah Chaim—is prominent: **"From my enemies You make me wise."** My intention, as we discussed, is that the words of the enemy who rejects a certain opinion or action serve to emphasize that this should have been the method and the action all along. Enclosed is a clipping from the main local newspaper, regarding which I also asked you during your visit here, and you surely remember your response.

With respect and with a blessing for success in the efforts to defend our land, the Holy Land, and our people who dwell therein—who are a holy nation in the land—and for good tidings regarding your personal matters as well.

## 9594

[9594](#_ftn_96)

[B"H](#_ftn_97), 20 Marcheshvan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of action, engaged in communal needs, etc.
Rabbi Mordechai HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through your son, Rabbi Menachem HaKohen, along with your book, "The Western Wall." Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me. Certainly, if other publications have appeared in the meantime, please send your works here for the benefit of the many—even if the publications are not related to current events, and certainly regarding a book such as the aforementioned, which is highly relevant to the day and the current era.

As is the custom of the Children of Israel, one should not be satisfied with mere praise and accolades, but rather add a comment, etc. Especially regarding printed matters that reach the many—and not only the many in the present, but also those in the future—it is my duty to offer a general observation: In your aforementioned book, several matters are presented together in one stroke, without any distinction or separation between them. For the majority of readers, this serves as proof that their authority is equal, or at the very least comparable, even though in truth they are far removed from one another, and sometimes even diametrically opposed. Furthermore, from this, the reader concludes that their authority is also the same in other matters, or at the very least similar. The seriousness of this matter certainly requires no explanation for someone of your stature.

Although my intention is surely clear, for the sake of further clarity, I will cite at least two examples. In the chapter "In Aggadah," there is a mixture, presented in the same style ("The Aggadah tells"), of both the Aggadah from the Torah—regarding which our Sages, of blessed memory, ruled: "Do you wish to know the One who spoke and the world came into being? Study Aggadah"—and, under that same heading, excerpts from books, etc. (p. 71, etc.).

Similarly, in the chapter "Lament and Song," which begins with a lament by Rabbi Elazar HaKalir and others—which is "based on the Aggadah in Eichah Rabbah"—you have included in that same chapter authors over whom one ought to lament. And the intelligent person will understand.

I am certain that you will not take offense at this comment, as in my opinion it is for the benefit of the many. This is not a matter of "one does not cry over the past," but rather for the future. My hope is strong that for many years to come, you will utilize the talents with which you have been gifted to spread traditional Judaism wherever your hand can reach—the authentic Judaism, for the truth rejects all matters of compromise.

You are surely aware of the assessment of [Rabbi](#_ftn_100) Elazar HaKalir and the importance of his piyutim according to the Arizal (Pri Etz Chaim, Shaar 1, at the beginning).

With respect and blessing.

## 9,995

[9,995](#_ftn_101)

[B"H](#_ftn_102), 20 Marcheshvan, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and G-d-fearing, who engages in the needs of the community,

Rabbi [Moreinu HaRav](#_ftn_103) Avraham Eliyahu, may he live, Ki Tov

May it be the will of Hashem that His desire succeeds in your hand to disseminate traditional Judaism without compromises, etc., in all ways, and especially through your writings; and may you do so with health, joy, and a good heart.

For bringing the word of Hashem to our brethren, the Children of Israel, is the most sublime expression of Ahavas Yisrael—the fulfillment of the mitzvah of "[And you shall love](#_ftn_104) your neighbor as yourself," which is a [great principle](#_ftn_105) in the Torah. This is especially so according to the [adage](#_ftn_106) of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, that "love your neighbor as yourself" and "love Hashem your G-d" are bound and dependent upon one another. All of this is explained in the drushim, maamarim, and sichos of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, in general, many of which have already been printed; and surely, for one such as yourself, further elaboration is unnecessary.

**M. Schneerson**

996

B”H, Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, Mevarchim Chodesh Kislev, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, a person of stature, a seeker of his people’s welfare, possessed of noble character, a scion of an illustrious lineage, [R’ Schneur Zalman] shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In connection with your upcoming birthday, I wish you a year of success and blessing, both in general matters and in personal matters—for the two are interdependent, and one should not separate what is joined, especially regarding a Yid in general, and all the more so regarding you and your role. May this be with proper health, joy, and a good heart.

Since it is my hope that, [as is your custom] in the past, you will be on that day in the Tzemach Tzedek shul and beis medrash in the complete Jerusalem, the [city] that is joined together, I have enclosed [what] has been published these days from the Torah of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, Da”Ch—both the revealed and the hidden aspects of Torah together—as in the [maamarim] of the Tzemach Tzedek, one sees this unification more openly than in the maamarim of our Rebbeim, the Nesi’im, before and after him.

To my regret, the binding was not completed, and therefore the sheets were sent as they are.

With respect and blessing for long, good years, and for good tidings in both material and spiritual matters alike.

Since you have merited that the [foundation] of Kfar Chabad has fallen to your share and lot—and may it be His will that soon, a second [Kfar] Chabad, and after it a third, and so on, will be established—it occurred to me to suggest to you, in connection with your birthday and in connection with the Tzemach Tzedek shul, given the good news I received that there are other plots, lands, or even buildings on that street belonging to Chabad and Chabad institutions—in any case, the street is called "Chabad Street"—that it is appropriate, correct, proper, and good that several more buildings on that street, as well as the plots, be joined and added to the aforementioned shul and beis medrash, as well as apartments for Anash and institutions, and first and foremost a yeshiva, or at least a yeshiva ketana (in size), and perhaps also with an attached dormitory, etc. Given the pace of events and developments in recent years, it is possible that this could happen soon, and not only that, but even in our immediate time, if all the factors that can assist in this and decide this truly desire the aforementioned matters.

It is understood that I am not unaware of several difficulties in this, both regarding the evacuation and removal of the entities currently in the aforementioned location, and regarding the construction and establishment of the desired matters. But certainly, with the appropriate will, all the aforementioned difficulties will be overcome with relative ease. And with a slight change [in the style] of our Sages, of blessed memory, to put it plainly—not only the street, but the entire quarter should be called "Chabad Quarter."

In continuation of what is written above, I will copy here a point from what [was discussed] today at the farbrengen of Shabbos Kodesh, Mevarchim Kislev, Parshas Chayei Sarah.

The [adage] of the Rebbe HaZaken is well known, which we heard several times from the mouth of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "One must live with the times," meaning to learn from the weekly parsha for the events of that week.

There are times when one must contemplate the order and the parsha of the week until one finds in it instructions regarding the events of the week, and there are instructions that are easier to understand from the weekly parsha. By the mercy of Hashem, it is understood that if there is room for doubts and bias that would incline the mind of the one studying the parsha to find in it an instruction that is appropriate without distorting it or interpreting it contrary to the truth, sometimes the instruction comes in a manner so clear that it is impossible to interpret it otherwise. This is the case with this week's parsha, and immediately at its beginning, which, according to what is explained below, also helps us understand the length of the narrative and the negotiation between Avraham and the Bnei Ches, which seemingly, what difference does it make?

There was a plot of land and a cave in the city of Chevron, and in it were buried Adam and Chava, and the cave and the field surrounding it and the city surrounding them were under the hand of the Bnei Ches, who are seemingly also descendants of Adam and Chava, and they were many in number, etc.

And the parsha relates that Avraham comes—for [one] was Avraham—and requests that they give him the Me'aras HaMachpeilah, and not as a temporary arrangement but as a possession, meaning permanently; a demand, seemingly, against justice and fairness, for they are the ones who are in the place, and they are the many, and they have a share in Adam and Chava just as Avraham does. And from whom does this demand come? Specifically from the one who dedicated his entire life to hachnosas orchim and acts of kindness, until the Creator of the world and man testifies about him: ["For I have known him] that he will command his children and his household after him, and they will keep the way of Hashem to do charity and justice." This is to say that the demand is certainly and surely just. And not only that, but even the Bnei Ches agree to this in the end, and in ways of pleasantness and peace, without any quarrel, let alone wars. However, the beginning of the conversation with the Bnei Ches must be ["A stranger] and a resident I am with you," and as Rashi explains (which is to say that this is understood even by a five-year-old beginning Chumash, that is, one who learns Chumash with Rashi): "If you wish, I am a stranger; and if not, I will be a resident and take it **by law**, for the **Holy One, blessed be He,** said to me, 'To your seed I have given this land.'" And behold, a wonder: the Bnei Ches not only agree to fulfill the aforementioned demand, but Efron, the owner of the cave and the field, who speaks in the name of the Bnei Ches, gives him not only the cave but also the field, and in the end also ["all] the trees that were in the field, that were in all its borders round about." Regarding the money—on the contrary, ["For the full] price he shall give it to me," and even in this, as is the nature of the Bnei Ches, ["They say] much and do not even do a little," and they demand four hundred silver shekels, current for the merchant.

And from then on, the Me'aras HaMachpeilah and everything belonging to it became a possession for Avraham, etc., that is to say, for his children after him until the end of all generations, with the agreement of the Bnei Ches and all the nations that come from their power and in their stead—a simple and clear instruction for everything similar to this, and all the more so regarding this matter itself, clear, as mentioned above, even to a five-year-old beginning Chumash. However, regarding the manner of speaking, a five-year-old, and even a ten-year-old, etc., could err and say that the manner must be ["And he bowed] to the people of the land," according to the literal meaning of the verse (see [Ibn] Ezra). And our [Sages], of blessed memory, came (a lesson for one who has already reached fifteen, for Gemara and Talmud) and explained and clarified the conduct: "And he bowed—from here we learn that one gives thanks for good tidings," that is to say—to the Holy One, blessed be He, but it was "before the people of the land," meaning that he explained before them, and they understood that the praise and thanksgiving are to Hashem, may He be blessed.

And from the matters of the Me'aras HaMachpeilah, it is in this way also regarding Chabad Street in the Old City of Jerusalem, etc., as mentioned above.

998

[998](#_ftn_131)

B”H, 26 Marcheshvan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you conclude that you wish to come here to receive instructions regarding the dispute with the company, etc.

The astonishment is understandable and simple: even if this did not involve any expenses or trouble, it is a waste of time, etc. For how to conduct oneself, what to do, etc., must be decided on the spot in consultation with friends on the ground, including a lawyer, etc. This is especially true since there will certainly be various changes from time to time, as has been the case in the past, and so on. Due to the magnitude of my astonishment, this letter is being sent via express mail.

However, this is the place to add—and I ask your forgiveness—that it seems your conduct now is the same as your conduct in the past: not to include anyone else to consult with, and consequently, not to share with them everything that is happening—not only after the fact, but even during the process, and furthermore, even before taking action. This is the opposite of the instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory. As it is related that even [Rav](#_ftn_132) Ashi—who was the one who sealed the entire Talmud Bavli, and certainly in his own city he was the mara d’asra in every detail, and all the more so regarding a halachic ruling on a question concerning an animal—his **constant** conduct was to "gather and bring all the butchers of the city [to examine the animal], saying, 'so that the splinter may reach the beam'" (Sanhedrin 7b). This story does not appear in the tractate of the Shas that explains the trait of humility, but rather in the tractate of the Shas that explains the conduct of a leader of a city, etc. It is understood and simple, too, that the purpose of the Torah is not to tell beautiful stories for the sake of their beauty, but rather that every matter and detail in the Torah is an instruction. And since the Torah is eternal, the instruction is also eternal for all places and for all times.

I have refrained until now from commenting on this, because I hoped and expected that, eventually, you would arrive at this conclusion on your own, especially since it was reported to me some time ago that people had complained to you about this and demanded a change. It appears from this letter of yours, and from the general situation with the company, that the matter still requires correction. And the correction is not to travel overseas for a one-time visit, etc.—which, as mentioned, serves no purpose—but rather to consult on the spot as mentioned above, and to learn from this event for the future, as mentioned above, and so on.

I was pleased by the report I received regarding how you conducted the [inauguration](#_ftn_133) of the Youth Center in Kfar Chabad, and the impression it made on those present. My hope is that you will see how there is no contradiction between these lines and what was said before; rather, **on the contrary**: since you have been gifted with talents, if you utilize them as you should—and even more than you should—the prospects for great success are high. And in such a case, conduct modeled after Rav Ashi is even more essential, for the loss, G-d forbid, would not be a loss of a minor or small matter, but a great and significant one.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that these words be accepted as they are. My intention is not as a "complaint," but as an instruction regarding a matter that requires change, and—most importantly—that they should have their intended effect.

With blessings for success and for good news in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

The pidyon nefesh mentioned in this letter and in previous ones will be read at the holy gravesite.

## 929

[929](#_ftn_137)

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the Chanukas HaBayis of the [institution](#_ftn_138) Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch, and foremost among them the esteemed activists B. Goldfarb, Yoel Gaska, and Binyamin Zucker,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the upcoming Chanukas HaBayis of two buildings for the summer camp, which is scheduled to take place on the 10th of Kislev, in a good and auspicious hour.

It is surely known to all that the 10th of Kislev is the Yom HaGeulah of the Mitteler Rebbe, the son and successor of the Alter Rebbe, the founder of the Chabad approach in Chassidus.

Chassidus in general, and Chabad in particular, bestow special attention and weight upon the field of child education.

And if in the early era of Chassidus the matter of chinuch was emphasized so strongly, it is certainly clear how vital institutions of chinuch al taharas hakodesh are in our time, when the educational institution must also provide the child with that which a child once received at home and in their environment.

It is therefore to be hoped that the occasion of the Chanukas HaBayis will be utilized to the fullest extent to strengthen and expand the institution, both in gashmius and in ruchnius, in accordance with the ideals and directives of the Alter Rebbe, the Mitteler Rebbe, and the Nesi’ei Chabad who followed them, up to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, whose name the institution bears.

Especially since the Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok institutions are permeated with the spirit of the [verse](#_ftn_140) that is connected with the redemption of the Alter Rebbe and the redemption of his son: **"He has redeemed my soul in peace"** (Tehillim 55:19), etc., which our Sages of blessed memory explain (Berachos 8a) refers to those who "engage in Torah, perform acts of kindness, and pray with the community." Thus, the students of Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch are permeated with Torah understanding and comprehension, with inner feeling and kavanah in tefillah, such that the Torah and avodah penetrate all their limbs and animate them to perform acts of kindness and maasim tovim.

Great is the zechus of all those who take part in supporting and expanding the institution Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch. May Hashem Yisbarach bless everyone and their families with everything they need, in gashmius and in ruchnius alike.

With respect and with a blessing for success and for good tidings.

## 9301 

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Hillel shlita, known as Dr. Medalie,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 26th of Marcheshvan (and those preceding it), and thank you for the good news contained therein. May it be the will of Hashem that you continue to bring good news in the days to come. We are, after all, commanded to ascend in holiness regarding matters of Torah and mitzvos, which includes sharing good news and causing *nachas ruach* to a fellow Jew—all the more so since "love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle of the Torah.

Regarding your mention in your letter from some time ago concerning the rejection of participating in the rabbinical conference in Europe, etc.: these days, the Chief Rabbi of Great Britain, Rabbi Dr. Jakobovits shlita, is here, and naturally, the conversation turned to the aforementioned topic. I explained my position to him as well: while a rabbinical conference for a specific region, country, or several neighboring countries on a continent like Europe is necessary—and one can hope for benefit if it is organized by the appropriate people and in an appropriate manner—if representatives from other countries and other continents participate in such a conference, the *Gedolei Yisrael* have always been concerned about such a thing, and with the greatest apprehension. Some say that this matter has already moved beyond the realm of mere apprehension—following the conference of synagogues held last year in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, and the strange and dangerous explanations that followed in its wake (regarding "reforms," assemblies, and the like), because the majority of the rabbis of Israel participated, and so on and so forth, **and a word to the wise is sufficient.** As for the explanation that so-and-so participated as an observer, or that another came as a guest or lecturer, etc., this is merely a deception, as was seen **tangibly** at the aforementioned conference in Jerusalem.

Certainly, for someone like you, there is no need for length, especially since in matters such as these, length and publicity are not advisable; on the contrary, the less said, the better, and *kal v’chomer* [it is understood].

Regarding the remainder of your letter, it will be read at the *tziyun* [the Rebbe’s resting place] following the above and the *pidyon nefesh*.

With respect and blessings for success in all matters.

## 9305 

, 13 Kislev, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

 Leah, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

Through your husband, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker, Rabbi Menachem Shmuel Dovid, may he live, Halevi, your check for tzedakah has arrived in connection with your decision, which amounts to more than a maaser.

You are surely aware of the greatness of the merit of the mitzvah of tzedakah in general, and especially that it arrived during these auspicious days between the 10th and 19th of Kislev, the days of the geulah of the Alter Rebbe and his son, the Mitteler Rebbe. In mentioning the merits for which they were redeemed—which was a geulah for each and every one of us for all generations— they emphasize that the merit of the mitzvah of tzedakah stood by them in a special way.

From this, it is understood that the mitzvah of tzedakah is one of the ways through which every man and woman can be redeemed from all undesirable matters, and be constantly in joy and with a good heart. And this brings an addition of blessing and success in all good matters, especially in having true nachas—which is Jewish-Chassidic nachas—from each of the children, may they live, and from all of them together, in good health and with abundance in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for Chag HaGeulah and for good tidings regarding all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9007

[9007](#_ftn_158)

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Tzvi Itzkovitz, Lod

Shalom u’Bracha!

I receive your regards frequently, and recently also a photograph in connection with the gathering in Lod where you were present and delivered words of blessing.

It is my pleasant duty to express the great *nachas ruach* I derived from this, and to see your positive attitude toward the affairs and institutions of Chabad, which is a continuation of your visit here.

*Megalgelin zechus l’yom zakai*—it was conveyed to me that on this day you are laying the cornerstone for the fourth building of the Shikun Chabad in Lod. You certainly have a significant part in its establishment, just as in the previous buildings—and, in fact, surely with an increase, in accordance with the instruction of our Sages, *ma’alin b’kodesh* (we increase in holiness) and in every good thing.

Building a home is, in general, a good thing, for Hashem hopes to be able to say regarding every home in Yisrael, "And I will dwell among them" (*v’shachanti b’tocham*)—within each and every one of them. How much more so regarding a new home in our Holy Land, the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are at all times, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.

May it be the will that soon this block will be completed and filled with tenants, as well as the blocks that have already been finished—tenants from our brethren the Children of Yisrael in general, and immigrants from that country in particular and especially. May each and every one of them come to their rest and their inheritance, until the fulfillment of the promise that Hashem Yisbarach will bring each and every one of the Children of Yisrael to their rest and their inheritance, an eternal inheritance, with the coming of the *Goel Tzedek* speedily in our days.

With respect and with blessings for a bright and joyous Chanukah.

## 903

[903](#_ftn_173)

B”H, 17 Kislev, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished [individual] engaged in communal work, [Mr.](#_ftn_174) Tzvi, may he be blessed,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 3 Kislev, in which you outline the situation among the youth in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and the background explaining the unique difficulties in bringing their hearts closer to our eternal and true values—the values of our Torah, the Torah of truth, given by our G-d of truth, the living G-d, and its mitzvos, [regarding which it is said,](#_ftn_175) "that he shall live by them."

As we stand a few days before the Chag HaGeulah of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, 19 Kislev—the essence of which is also the redemption of the Baal Shem Tov’s Torah, the Torah of Chassidus, from [a state of] Tzimtzum and restriction among a select few, and bringing it to all strata of our people, the Children of Israel—this is the place to quote one of his teachings (as transmitted by the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, as recorded in the notes of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory). Its content is relevant to the subject of your letter, and it serves as the foundation for my response, as well as an explanation of my approach, my words, and my previous letters to you. This is the aforementioned teaching of [the Baal Shem Tov:](#_ftn_176)

"It is written, 'For you shall be a land of desire, says Hashem Tzeva-os.' Just as the greatest sages will never be able to fathom the great natural treasures that the Holy One, blessed be He, has placed within the earth—for [everything came from the dust](#_ftn_178)—so too, no one can fathom the great treasures that lie within Jews, who are the 'land of desire' of the Holy One, blessed be He." The Baal Shem Tov concluded: "I want to make it so that Jews will yield the produce that a 'land of desire' of the Holy One, blessed be He, is capable of yielding."

We learn from this that the Torah of truth, which is also the Torah of life—meaning that truth is truth in our lives in this world—testifies that within every single one of our people, the Children of Israel, there exist great and hidden treasures, etc. However, just as regarding treasures hidden in the earth, one must remove the dirt and filth, etc., that cover them, so too it is regarding a person. For every person is a world unto himself, and therefore, the quality and quantity of the layers covering [these treasures] differ from one person to another.

It is further understood from the above that if the treasures have not been revealed, it is proof that one has not dug deeply enough to reach them.

It is also understood that when the digger finally reaches the treasure and reveals it, the owner of the treasure himself will feel a deep, soulful, and genuine gratitude toward him for having brought him to his own treasure—which is his own inner essence.

And if you would say that the analogy of treasures hidden in the earth holds true in every detail, we see regarding that which is hidden and stored in the depths of the earth that the deeper something is found, the more precious and important it is, and the rest is understood.

Surely, for one such as yourself, a more detailed explanation of the above is unnecessary.

The point and summary of the above is that one who strives to bring the heart of a Jewish son or daughter closer to our Father in Heaven is guaranteed that he will eventually be rewarded and succeed in his efforts. Furthermore, the very person upon whom he worked and whom he placed in a "corner of light"—the true light of [the candle of](#_ftn_179) mitzvah and the light of Torah—will become his true lover and his greatest helper in revealing the treasure in all its preciousness and importance. This includes helping him in the work of spreading Yudaism and its values in his own surroundings as well, in a manner of "increasing and ascending" in light. [In the phrasing](#_ftn_180) of our Sages, of blessed memory: "A person sanctifies himself a little below, and they sanctify him greatly from above."

It is my hope that you will participate in the farbrengen of 19 Kislev, the Chag HaGeulah, and I will conclude in connection with this,

With blessings for the Chag HaGeulah and for good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

## 9712

[9712](#_ftn_183)

[B"H](#_ftn_184), 15 Kislev, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To each of the well-wishers — according to the list from the administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad HaMerkazis, may they live — Brooklyn, N.Y.

May Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letter dated 14 Kislev and the enclosure.

Many thanks for the blessings in connection with the forty-year period.

In the words of Chazal: "Your word has already been spoken," meaning that your blessing is written, and He (Hashem) will bless you.

May it be Hashem’s will that it be in a manner of **addition**, for the addition of Hashem is greater than the essence.

It was most pleasant and brought great joy to learn that many of the well-wishers accompanied their blessings and reinforced them through the performance of mitzvos — a donation to tzedakah, studying a topic in Torah, etc.

There are three levels in this, each higher than the other: performing a mitzvah adds (in this world and the next) not only to the person performing it, but to the entire world. Furthermore, it adds to the person who causes it to be done (even without their knowledge). And the greatest of all is when the action is done for his merit and on his behalf.

I would like to propose and request that each member of the group of well-wishers do both, Torah study and action, together — for each has what the other lacks. Moreover, the act of tzedakah adds elevation to "all the performance of mitzvos, and Torah study is equivalent to them all." And Torah study, which is the life of Bnei Yisrael and is like fish in water — it is understood that by adding to it, one adds to the vitality of the person, and through this, to all his actions.

Especially since these days — between the days of redemption of the Mitteler Rebbe, 10 Kislev, and the Alter Rebbe, 19 Kislev — the redemption of both was (and is connected to) the reading (and content) of the verse: "He has redeemed my soul in peace from the battle against me, for there were many with me." Chazal explained its meaning: Hashem said, "Whoever engages in Torah, performs acts of kindness, and prays with the community, I account it to him as if he had redeemed Me and My children from among the nations."

With blessings for a Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

## 613

[15 Kislev, 5729]

P.S. I received your letter as mentioned, and enclosed is a copy of my response to Rabbi Levinger, who also approached you regarding this matter.

As I wrote in my letter, I had great hesitation about whether to write the above, and even after resolving that doubt, the writing remained extremely brief.

I spoke about this at greater length with the G-d-fearing [individual], etc., R’ Y. Alinson. One of my intentions in this (as I requested of him) was that he convey my words to you, as for understandable reasons I did not want to put them in writing as long as there is an alternative to prevent danger, Heaven forbid, to human lives—by other means.

I rely on your insight, as I also told Mr. Alinson, as to whether to convey the content of my letter to those who approached you regarding Chevron and the like, and also regarding the content of my conversation with Mr. Alinson. Although, in any event, I requested that the matters be conveyed to Mr. Ch. M. Shapiro, since according to reports, he is among the leaders of those who speak and organize for those favoring the return of territories—at least in part—which endangers not only the security of the border, but the security of the entire Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, in the natural order of things, and a word to the wise is sufficient. [And the "wisdom" of pressuring military and security personnel not to express their opinion openly and with full force—I do not understand this at all.] Especially since there is no benefit or gain in returning territories, for their mouth spoke vanity, as has been seen in the past regarding all promises of peace, etc. In the language of Rashi in Sifrei, Behaalotcha (9:10), from last week: **It is a halacha** that it is well-known that Esav hates Yaakov, and our Sages, of blessed memory, elaborated on all the nuances of "the kindness of the nations is a sin." It is clear that they will gain nothing by returning territories, as has been seen in the past, and even in the "recent" past when they returned [territories] twelve years ago from the Suez Canal, and so on and so forth, and a word to the wise is sufficient. Especially in the last year, whenever the publicizing of the opinion regarding returning territories and charity to the gentiles, etc., intensifies—the wave of sabotage intensifies, to the point of adding casualties and victims in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, may Hashem avenge their blood, as has been seen tangibly.

Similar to what I wrote in the copy of my attached letter, there is much to elaborate on here as well—but these are matters for which silence is appropriate. It is not worthwhile for a Jew to write in disparagement of Jews—all the more so, it is forbidden to speak in disparagement of Jews.

It is wondrous to what extent the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, are correct at every step, as they said that whoever adds, detracts. According to this, the connection between the two commandments "you shall not add" and "you shall not subtract" in one verse and in one breath (Va'eschanan 4:2; see 13:1) is understood. For specifically those who are "boiling" in our times [claim] that a new mitzvah has been added (to ascend to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and specifically as part of the 613, contrary to the opinion of the Rambam), and some add that the fulfillment of all the Torah and mitzvos, the existence of the Jewish people, and the existence of Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, depend solely on this. Consequently, it is permitted to travel on ships with public desecration of Shabbos, etc., for everything is pushed aside for the sake of this mitzvah [and all the more so for lesser prohibitions]. They have added matter upon matter, declaring publicly that this is the "beginning of the redemption" (*atchalta d'geulah*), contrary to the explicit halachic ruling in the Rambam (who certainly knew of the Yerushalmi, the foundation of the Ramban regarding Shir HaShirim, the discussions in Sanhedrin, and elsewhere, etc.). Yet, specifically among them, those who wish to return the territories, or part of them, have multiplied, etc., etc.

I do not wish to elaborate on this, as I fear touching upon your train of thought [as I once heard from our friend, shlita—that in his meetings with people, he strives to find the common denominator and the side that is equal between them and that which unites them—and not to emphasize and dig for that which separates and divides, or at least that which creates a rift between them. It is obvious that this is the case regarding our relationship—mine and yours—and my hope is that this is "as water reflects the face to the face"]. Even now, I would not have written all of the above had I not seen in this—the declaration of "beginning of the redemption"—a matter of danger. For this is the only explanation I have found (for now) for the matter of the casualties and victims in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, among whom are even those who were saved from the Holocaust and saw open miracles in that, and despite all this, they fell in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and also in an unnatural manner as mentioned, may Hashem avenge their blood.

The explanation is along the lines of what was seen every time a false messiah arose and incited and drew someone after him—the matter ended in casualties, Heaven forbid. Along these lines is also the idea that the redemption has already begun. [And although the situation is **miraculous, a salvation, and a greatness** for millions of Jews, nevertheless—this is not the redemption from the fourth exile. On the contrary—according to all the signs, this is a descent further into the double and redoubled darkness of this exile, [as they call] darkness light, etc.]. And the bitter punishment is—that another Jew falls and another victim in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and another, may Hashem avenge their blood.

"By the way," I received information in response to my argument regarding the danger posed by relinquishing any territory as I elaborated on, and my words were conveyed by a reliable source on his mission, etc.—and according to the information, it reached the point of discussion among government officials; the response was that they do not pay attention to an argument and proof... coming from a person who has not even visited Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, once. Although, of course, my argument was that this endangers millions of Jews who are in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and it is not a matter to be judged regarding me, etc., but rather by relying on the principle: "Accept the truth from whoever says it."

And similarly regarding the "beginning of the redemption." To my argument that it is an explicit halachic ruling in the Rambam, and the Rambam certainly knew the text in all the aforementioned places—the response was that they copied an interpretation from one more person and an explanation from another person, without responding to or mentioning the Rambam at all. And this response came even from those who know that the halachic ruling for practical application is in the books of the *poskim*—and not in the *midrashim* of our Sages, of blessed memory, and not even in the difficult discussions in the *Shas*—after the law has been clearly decided by the *batarai* (later authorities) and the *poskim* by whose light we shall walk until the coming of our righteous Moshiach.

By the way, I received a strange argument and proof—that there are several places where it is written or understood that this is the "beginning of the redemption," etc.—even though the interpretation there is not related to our matter at all! It is like the story in Eicha Rabbah (1:51) that at the time of the destruction of the Beis HaMikdash, a Jew's cow lowed, and an Arab said, "Now the Beis HaMikdash is destroyed." Immediately, the cow lowed a second time, and he said, "Now the savior and redeemer of Israel is born," meaning, the "beginning of the redemption." It is obvious that our discussion is not along these lines.

Furthermore, the wondrous statement of our Rebbe HaZaken is well-known, that before souls as lofty as Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, the Beis HaMikdash was not destroyed at all (*Pelach HaRimon*, beginning of Parshas Shemos, p. 7). And surely the Admur HaZaken knew that Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai [hid] in a cave for thirteen years because of the decrees of the Roman kingdom. And in *Chana Ariel, Toldos* (47:2), it is written: Tannaim and Amoraim and the great Tzaddikim.

And due to the importance of the matter, I repeat once again: Seemingly, what does it matter (to me) that Jews convince themselves that the redemption has already begun; it makes the heart more joyful; and the greatness of the joy of the Jewish people is explained, especially according to the teachings of Chassidus. However, as mentioned—the punishment is severe, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

I was very saddened by the lack of letters from you for a long time—contrary to your habit and nature to write with alacrity about events and *farbrengens*, etc. [about the unveiling of the tombstone of the great Gaon and Chassid, etc., R. B. M., of blessed memory, the *farbrengen* in the Tzemach Tzedek shul on Rosh Chodesh Kislev, etc., etc.]. My spirit was somewhat calmed by the receipt of your letter just now, and also the regards from those coming from there to here who saw you and spoke with you face-to-face.

In continuation of the discussion from then—regarding *Pesach Rishon* and *Pesach Sheni*, etc., I happened upon the book *Yosef Ometz*—a book of responsa by the Chida, in which a responsum from his father-in-law is brought, and he writes simply—and with several proofs—that sometimes the congregation was delayed and performed *Pesach Sheni*, and according to Tosafos—it even comes with impurity, etc., but not according to the Rambam, see there (Section 6).
