## 9717

[9717](#_ftn_234)

[B"H](#_ftn_235), 20 Kislev, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, who served as the administrator of the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch since its founding, and later as its Nasi, and who transplanted the Yeshiva to America 29 years ago—where, with the help of Hashem, it has flourished and branched out in an extraordinary manner—[conveyed](#_ftn_236) a teaching from the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, whose Chag HaGeulah we have just celebrated.

It is a teaching of special significance, not only in connection with 19 Kislev, but also in connection with the upcoming annual celebration of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva (29 Teves, G-d willing):

**Jewish gashmius is ruchnius. Hashem gives us gashmius, so that we may transform it into ruchnius.**

In these few words lies a profound lesson and a timely directive as to how a Yid’s approach to matters of tzedakah in general, and to yeshivos and mosdos chinuch al taharas hakodesh in particular, ought to be:

The entire relationship of Yidden—an [am](#_ftn_237) kadosh l’Hashem—to gashmius is because **Jewish** gashmius—gashmius as a Torah-observant Yid understands and achieves it—is essentially ruchnius, and a Yid certainly has a great connection to ruchnius. Consequently, Hashem gives a Yid more gashmius so that the Yid may transform it into more ruchnius.

The highest level of ruchnius is, of course, limud haTorah and kiyum hamitzvos, until one reaches the level of **"Know the G-d of your father and serve Him with a whole heart and a willing soul"**—to **understand** Elokus and to serve Hashem with one’s entire **heart** and good **will**, as this is indicated and explained in Chassidus—up to the point of serving Hashem through all the affairs of daily life.

The most potent form of gashmius is money—the fruit of a [person’s](#_ftn_239) toil with all his strength.

A Yid must therefore transform this most potent form of gashmius into the highest form of ruchnius.

In the Lubavitcher Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim, the aforementioned teaching of the Alter Rebbe receives its fullest practical expression. Supporting this institution—a fortress of Torah and Chassidus—is therefore one of the best ways to fulfill this directive of the Alter Rebbe.

Now that the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim is making preparations for its [annual](#_ftn_240) celebration, it is to be hoped that all lovers of Torah, and especially the askanim and friends of the Yeshiva, will make a special effort to ensure the success of this endeavor. And the more that each man and woman gives of their gashmius—money, as well as their effort and time—and transforms it into ruchnius—Torah, avodah, and gemilus chasadim—the more gashmius Hashem will grant them, [from](#_ftn_241) His full, open, holy, and expansive hand, and He will grant success to each and every one of you and your households, may they live, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9118 

 21 Kislev, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, who engages in communal affairs, etc.
Rabbi M. Levinger, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of the 7th of Kislev, in which you also mention your previous letter:

The reason I did not answer your previous letter is in accordance with the instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory, that one does not respond to [a matter that is already known/a foregone conclusion]. My intention was that the fate of the holy city of Chevron—to our great sorrow and shame—is still hanging in the balance.

It is simple that I do not refer to its true fate, for it is the City of the Patriarchs, the site of the Me'aras HaMachpeilah, one of the four holy cities in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, etc., etc. This is especially so according to what has been explained and emphasized by the Nasi'im of Chabad throughout the generations, including what is printed in the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Mitteler Rebbe, the successor to the Alter Rebbe (author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch), at the time he established the settlement in the holy city of Chevron, may it be rebuilt and established, in the year 5583 (recently printed in the book **Me'ah She'arim**, page 15). See the conclusion there: "And he himself purchased in the aforementioned holy city the small shul in his own name, so that he would have a portion of his inheritance there." The Nasi'im of Chabad who followed him did the same.

Rather, I am referring to the negotiations being conducted in secret, behind closed doors—yet they are well-known among the nations, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient—regarding what to return of the liberated territories and what not to return, etc. Although for a year or more there has been a grave debate regarding Chevron, and even then opinions were divided regarding its return, recently their opinion is gaining strength. It is not possible to elaborate on this alarming matter. In general, I did not wish to put this in writing, especially since the hand of Hashem is not shortened, and just as until now the aforementioned matter has not come to fruition—due to the open miracle that the **nations** do not agree to enter into negotiations regarding the return of the territories, even though the only condition they are asked to meet is to agree in words to make peace, [and everyone knows that these words have no validity regarding their future conduct]. Their refusal is nothing but what was mentioned above: an open miracle from Heaven, completely above the way of nature, [in order to prevent the return of the territories].

However, our Sages, of blessed memory, have said that one should not rely on a miracle (even though may it continue, etc., etc.). Therefore, I am not in a position to fulfill the requests of your honor regarding the matters you write about. As mentioned, it is not from the **nations** that I fear, Heaven forbid, for they have no free choice; rather, my concern is from the opinion of those who are mistaken (and even if the mistake is unintentional or due to duress, etc., it makes no difference regarding the results and the actual deed) among our brethren, the Children of Israel, who do possess free choice. There are some among them who have cloaked the matter in the guise of a mitzvah, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

As mentioned, one could elaborate at length on this entire matter, but it is not my intention at all to weaken your honor and those who join you in your approach and your activities. Everything written above is solely in accordance with the commandment, "And you shall be clear before Hashem and before Israel," in response to the content of your letter.

With respect and blessing,

## 9261

[9261]

B”H, 1st of Chanukah, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yosef Bentov,

Shalom u’Bracha,

Your letter and its enclosure were received with some delay. I was pleased to read of your impressions from your visit to our Holy Land—a land that even all the nations of the world call the Holy Land, and as it is written in our holy Torah, it is a land "upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year."

May it be the will of Hashem that a spirit of holiness and purity be added to everyone who visits our Holy Land, in such a way that the impression remains evident throughout all the days of his life. As our Sages of blessed memory taught, this should extend to matters of actual deed in daily life, for [the deed] is the essential thing.

I will take the liberty of expressing my hope that your putting on tefillin in Eretz Yisroel was a good beginning for continuing to do so in the days to come, every weekday morning, at the very least for a few moments. And although every mitzvah must be performed because it is a mitzvah—that is to say, a commandment of the Creator—there are certain mitzvos that possess unique spiritual qualities. [One] of these qualities, and indeed the unique quality of the mitzvah of tefillin, [which is placed] on the hand opposite the heart and on the head, is to bring [peace] and harmony between the intellect and the emotions: the understanding in the head and the feelings and desires in the heart. This is so necessary, especially in our current times.

I am confident that you will not mind my intervening in your life and conduct, as this intervention is based on the tone of your letter and on the declaration of our Sages of blessed memory that [all] of Israel are friends.

Thank you for sending me a Sefer Tehillim at the request of your mother, tichyeh. Following the Jewish custom of finding a hint and a connection in everything, this gives me the opportunity to ask you to also accept a gift from me, [measure] for measure: a pair of tefillin together with a small Siddur, which was also printed in the Holy Land, at the printing press of Kfar Chabad.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above, with joy and a glad heart, and wishes for days of Chanukah filled with light that increases and grows.

P.S. Please be so kind as to forward the enclosed letter to your mother, tichyeh.

## 9726

[9726](#_ftn_287)

B”H, 5 Teves, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and accomplished individual, a man of fine character, etc.,
Rabbi Y. Kling, shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

For several reasons, this letter of mine has been delayed, and I ask for your forgiveness.

In continuation of our conversation during your visit here, and in accordance with what was discussed then, enclosed is a check for the building fund of the educational institution based on pure holiness in your city, which is under your leadership.

May it be the will of Hashem that He grant you success and bless you to add strength and courage in the dissemination of traditional Judaism—the Judaism of our Torah, the Torah of truth (for the essence of truth is that it leaves no room for compromises or concessions, etc.)—and its mitzvos, regarding which [it is said](#_ftn_288), “And he shall live by them.” This means that for every Jewish man and woman, in every place and at every time, the Torah and its mitzvos are their true life, even here on earth in this physical and material world. Their conduct in this path depends on the education they receive; furthermore, any positive influence during one’s youth is magnified many times over when the student grows up.

[As is known](#_ftn_289), there is the analogy that a small improvement in the quantity of a seed or a sapling is of immense importance once that seed or sapling grows and becomes a fruit-bearing tree. Certainly, for one such as yourself, there is no need for an explanation of all this.

May Hashem, Yisbarach, grant success to each and every one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, [to ascend](#_ftn_290) in holiness regarding matters of Torah and mitzvos, going from strength to strength, [in accordance with the instruction](#_ftn_291) of the days of Chanukah, which we are currently leaving, that we increase in candles—"a mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light"—from day to day.

With respect and blessing.

## 927

[927](#_ftn_293)

B.H., 5 Teves, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. [Benzion](#_ftn_294) Goldberg
Shalom u’Bracha!

I received with pleasure your letter of 12/5, confirming receipt of my previous letter. Thinking that perhaps we would see each other at the Yud-Tes Kislev farbrengen, as you have been accustomed to attending in the past, I had wanted to confirm the letter personally, in accordance with the [maamar](#_ftn_295) of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "a mitzvah is better performed by oneself than by one's agent"—for a personal letter is, after all, no more than an agent. Assuming that you have traveled away, I am confirming the letter in writing.

At the same time, I wish to express a wish based on one of the allusions of the days of Chanukah, from which we have just emerged:

Although one has fulfilled the mitzvah of the Chanukah lights on the first night in the fullest measure by lighting one candle, it is [indicated](#_ftn_296) to every Jew that one must not be satisfied with that same state the following day. Rather, since another day has passed in physical growth, there must be a corresponding elevation in the soul and in all things connected to the soul—first and foremost in Torah and mitzvos, which are themselves like candles and illumination, for "the mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light" [Mishlei 6:23]. No matter how good the situation may be on a given day in a spiritual sense, it is not good enough for the day that follows; just as if one were to light only one candle on the second night of Chanukah, one would be lacking in the fulfillment of the mitzvah as it ought to be.

I do not believe my role is to be a preacher, and I do not assume your role is to listen to sermons. However, the above is—in addition to the wish that this alluded lesson of Chanukah be fulfilled by you and by all of us—an answer to one of the most painful problems of our time: the delusion that as one becomes more advanced and more educated, one no longer needs the fences and restrictions, or in other words, the negative mitzvos and the stringencies that were necessary when a person was primitive, uneducated, uncultured, etc., etc.

The answer in the aforementioned allusion of the Chanukah lights is, on the contrary: progress and growth in any field of human life must be accompanied by progress and growth in one’s spiritual life, or in other words, in one’s soul-life, or more simply put—in mussar, Chassidus, and the like.

And furthermore: if physical progress is not accompanied by progress in the realm of the soul, it is used in many cases—and unfortunately, very often—as the opposite of progress in soul-life. Because the balance between the two has been disturbed, and the disruption in spiritual progress—in other words, the regression in that area—must eventually lead to a regression and destruction in one’s physical life as well.

Unfortunately, in our generation, we have seen many examples of this, and in the words of the verse, **"They are wise to do evil"** [Yirmiyahu 4:22]—that the increase in "freedom" in the simple sense, which has been used to liberate oneself from all manner of safeguards and limitations, has also led to physical decadence.

It is remarkable that—as you have likely heard—when thinking of flying to the moon, one seeks safeguards so that the bacteria and viruses to which one is accustomed on earth are not taken along, because one does not know if, under the conditions there, one will be able to withstand them; and likewise, the reverse. Fantasizing about walking on the moon, one seeks to protect oneself against possible local viruses. In other words: progress to the point of flying to the moon must be accompanied by additional precautionary measures and limitations, and this is not considered merely a matter of convenience, but a matter of life and death. This is the very same idea regarding progress in any technological field.

With respect and blessing.

## 9228

[9228](#_ftn_299)

B"H, 5 Teves, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, a man of many accomplishments, etc., [Rabbi](#_ftn_300) Moshe, may he live, known as Dr. Munk,

Peace and blessing!

After a long interval, I was pleased to receive your letter from Rosh Chodesh Kislev, which reached me after a significant delay.

Beyond the pleasant surprise of receiving your letter in general, I also found great satisfaction in its content, which demonstrates that your interest in the Chabad schools in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, remains in full force.

In particular, it is my hope that it has not only remained in force but has increased in strength, in accordance with the directive of our Sages of blessed memory to always ascend in matters of holiness.

This is also one of the lessons of the days of Chanukah, from which we derive the principle of [increasing](#_ftn_302) the lights [(the candle](#_ftn_303) of the mitzvah and the light of Torah) from day to day.

I am writing regarding the content of your letter to the administration of the [institutions](#_ftn_304) about which you write. Although I am writing specifically to [Rabbi](#_ftn_305) T.G., may he live, since they wrote to me that he does not wish to accept the position, if he were to accept it out of compulsion—or at the very least, out of obedience to a directive coming from across the sea—it is questionable whether this would not affect the inner quality of his fulfillment of the role. Even though he would certainly strive to carry it out faithfully, the mind does not always rule over the heart. This is especially relevant in matters of education, for the student is often most sensitive to such shifts, and for someone like you, no further explanation is needed.

As mentioned above, my hope is strong that your interest, sir, is not directed only toward the Chabad institutions about which you write, but also toward the other Chabad institutions. It is simple that in this, too, you will act with a generous eye and in a manner that is ever-increasing. We have been [assured](#_ftn_306) that one who comes to purify himself is assisted—a heavenly assistance that has no limitations.

With respect and blessing.

## 9331

[9331](#_ftn_320)

B"H, 5 Teves, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, which was received with some delay, I will mention you at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires, and especially regarding the improvement of your health.

It is self-understood that conducting one’s life in accordance with the command of Hashem, as detailed in the Shulchan Aruch, opens the path to receiving Hashem’s blessings in all that is needed. This also applies to strengthening one’s bitachon (faith) in Hashem, who guards every individual; therefore, there is no reason for fear or distress. Even when something occurs that appears to be a hardship, Heaven forbid, faith itself has the power to transform everything undesirable so that it leads to good results, as per the well-known adage of our Sages: "This, too, is for the good." [321]

If the kashrus of your husband’s mezuzos and tefillin has not been checked during the past year, they should be checked now. Likewise, regarding the lighting of candles before the onset of Shabbos and Yomim Tovim, it would be good for you, as the mistress of the house, to give charity from your own money at that time. [322]

According to the Shulchan Aruch, a Jew must do what is dependent upon them through natural means. This means, in your case, following the instructions of a specialist doctor. Regarding which doctor to consult in your situation, it is best to seek advice from a doctor you trust who is familiar with your family (in Milan).

Since we recently celebrated Chanukah, [323] may Hashem grant that you, too, experience an increase in matters of holiness from day to day, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Nissan Mindel – Secretary

## 9332 

 16 Teves, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Rabbi Akiva Moshe Gottlieb, shlita
Organizing Committee for the Rabbinical Conference –
Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, speedily in our days

Shalom u’Bracha!

I am hereby acknowledging receipt of your letter dated 11 Teves, regarding the Rabbinical Conference. It is somewhat surprising that the letter was sent such a short time, relatively speaking, before the date of the conference, and also that it contains no details regarding the scope of the conference, who the invitees are, etc.

However, since according to rumors and reports, rabbis from various countries and different organizations are being invited, the opposition of the great Torah leaders of the previous generation to a conference of this type is well-known, as are their well-known and famous reasons. In our current generation, these concerns not only remain in full force, but on the contrary, they are even greater and closer to being realized. Therefore, my opinion—based on the clear and firm view of the aforementioned great Torah leaders—is that this conference should not be held at all.

It is also understood that calling it an "emergency conference" or the like does not change anything, for the main point is how it plays out in practice. This is especially true given that the aforementioned great Torah leaders warned that the sages—the eyes of the community—must take into account the future consequences following such a conference, the "new faces" that will emerge as a result, etc. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

My hope is strong that you will stand in the breach, that the aforementioned Rabbinical Conference will not take place, and that you will bring good news.

With respect and blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 9733

[9733](#_ftn_328)

B"H, 18 Teves, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and Peace!

In response to your letter of 1/5,

Since you describe the event that occurred as a "tragedy," there is surely no need to explain the event itself, nor how it affects not only the three individuals involved, as you wrote, but also the children of the couple, for it is natural for sons and daughters to feel the shock of the relationship dynamic that has occurred between their parents. Furthermore, the impressions of the event have a continuation, and it is impossible to know whether it will last for weeks, months, or a longer time, which is not the case for the "pleasure," which was only for a moment and only for two individuals.

On the other hand, every man and woman of the Jewish people is commanded to reject [the feeling of](#_ftn_329) despair, for [there is](#_ftn_330) nothing that can stand before teshuvah. [The essence](#_ftn_331) of teshuvah is a complete regret from the depths of the soul regarding the past, and consequently, a firm resolution for the future, including also being careful and rejecting any matter that might, chas v’shalom, place the individuals in a position of temptation once again; any additional caution in this is to be praised. [And Hashem](#_ftn_332), who sees into the heart and knows that the teshuvah in the aforementioned details is genuine and from the soul—He is [abundant in forgiveness](#_ftn_333), even to the point of complete forgiveness according to the capacity of Hashem, which also includes minimizing the pain and shame caused to all those involved in this event and affair, [in the style](#_ftn_334) of the verse, "Is Hashem's hand shortened?" This is indeed one of your heart's desires for the good, to eliminate the pain, etc.

According [to](#_ftn_335) what is explained in the books of the Rambam—who was both a physician of the body and a physician of the soul—it is understood that every event that requires teshuvah must be utilized to **increase** in the good, by increasing in the performance of what is good and upright between man and Hashem, and also between man and his fellow, just as the Creator of man and his Guide has outlined in His Torah, which is called *Toras Chaim*—a guide for life. My intention is simple: daily conduct according to the Torah, with even greater precision than a person required previously, and as mentioned above, [there is](#_ftn_336) nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for success in all the aforementioned, and for good tidings in this.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 9375

[9375](#_ftn_339)

[B"H](#_ftn_340), 22 Teves, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Religious Council of **Ramla**, may they be preserved,
Led by Rabbi Dr. M. Frankel, Chairman,
And Mr. Dov Osterman, General Secretary,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and Blessing!

It was with pleasure and special satisfaction that I received your letter of the 5th of this month, bearing good news regarding the *Mivtza* Tefillin and its success in your city, in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days.

Surely you will not be content with the achievements thus far, but will increase your efforts in the aforementioned *Mivtza* and similar ones, in strengthening the *mitzvos* of our Holy Torah, the Torah of life (which includes the [interpretation](#_ftn_342) of *hora'ah*—instruction—in life, the day-to-day life in this world of ours).

May it be His will that other cities and settlements of Bnei Yisrael, wherever they may be, will see this and act accordingly—and all the more so the cities of our Holy Land. Especially since Bnei Yisrael, wherever they are, are—in the [style](#_ftn_343) of our Sages—like one sheep among seventy wolves; yet [Hashem](#_ftn_344) is your shade at your right hand, a shield and a refuge. And even more than that, in the [style](#_ftn_345) of the verse: "The fear of the Jews fell upon them," until "[you shall dwell](#_ftn_346) securely in your land, and I will grant peace in the land, and you shall lie down and none shall make you afraid... and the sword shall not pass through your land"—which our Sages [explained](#_ftn_347) to mean even a sword of peace.

This is the special *segulah* of the *mitzvah* of Tefillin, [as it is written](#_ftn_348) (and also quoted at the end of your letter): "And all the peoples of the earth shall see that the name of Hashem is called upon you, and they shall fear you," and [it is taught](#_ftn_349)—these are the Tefillin of the head.

May it be His will that the precision in the language of our Sages mentioned above be fulfilled—which the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, founder of the Chabad approach (whose *yahrzeit* is during these days, 24 Teves), [explained](#_ftn_350)—that the ultimate purpose and perfection of Tefillin is that what is written in the Tefillin that are **on** the head (and **on** the arm) should also be **in** the head.

May Hashem, blessed be He, grant you success in managing the city and its affairs according to the instructions of the Torah and its *mitzvos*, the Torah of life, "[and live](#_ftn_351) by them," and to merit to influence others—other cities and settlements—in this as well; and there is no influence greater than a living example.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 936

[936](#_ftn_352)

[B"H](#_ftn_353), 24 Teves, the Hillula of the Alter Rebbe, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all the participants in the 29th annual dinner of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

On this auspicious day of the Hillula-Yahrtzeit of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch and founder of the Chabad approach, I send my greetings and blessing to all the participants in the annual celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch.

One of the fundamental principles of the Chabad approach is that the head and the heart (intellect and emotion) should govern and animate a person’s daily life in complete harmony with one another, and in a manner of **moach shalit al halev** — that the head should control the heart.

When this inner harmony between intellect and emotion exists, then all the diverse activities of a person in every detail of daily life — both the "weekday" and the "Shabbos and Yom Tov" aspects, both the material and the spiritual — are carried out as they should be, without conflicts, without contradictions, and without wavering.

It is clear that the terrible confusion and restlessness that dominates the general youth today, which expresses itself in rebellion and revolt against the most elementary laws of human society, is a result of this inner fragmentation and disharmony between intellect and emotion, which unleashes unbridled emotions. It is unfortunately also a sad fact that these symptoms have also affected significant segments of the Jewish youth.

In this critical time, it is especially a life-necessity to strengthen among Jewish youth the spiritual equilibrium, the only path to which is through Torah and mitzvos, with unity and harmony between intellect and emotion and — **moach shalit al halev**.

For a Yid, this aforementioned inner unity is more than just the secret and foundation of a satisfying personal life. According to how this matter is explained broadly and deeply in Chabad, this unity is the key to unity in the world, and is internally connected with the concept of Achdus HaBorei, the realization of which in life is the special task of the Yid and the Jewish people. This is indicated in the words **"Goy echad ba'aretz,"** as the Alter Rebbe explains (Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 9), that the Jewish people, who are a **"Goy echad,"** realize **"Hashem echad,"** so that it should be **"echad ba'aretz."**

The Lubavitcher Yeshiva educates its students in Torah and yiras-shamayim, permeated with this spirit of unity of head and heart and **moach shalit al halev**, not only to achieve this within themselves, but also later, when they go out into the world, they should help others to achieve and implement the same in their daily lives.

The [annual](#_ftn_356) banquet of the central Yeshiva Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch provides a special opportunity for the askanim and friends of the Yeshiva to become true partners in this unity. The money, as well as the effort and time that one gives for the Yeshiva, is transformed into Torah, avodah, and gemilus-chasadim — [the](#_ftn_357) three pillars upon which the world stands, the great world, as well as [the](#_ftn_358) "small world" of every Yid, for every Yid, man and woman, is a world unto themselves. And through this, the bond of the Yid with the Ribono shel Olam is strengthened and deepened, and the Ribono shel Olam, for His part, gives everything one needs in children, life, and ample sustenance, [from](#_ftn_359) His full, open, holy, and generous hand.

With respect and blessing for outstanding success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9337

B"H, 25 Teves, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Menachem Begin, may he live and be well,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 4 Teves, and the confirmation of receipt of my own letter.

I am confident that our esteemed friend, Dr. Yosef Klarman, has surely conveyed to you the content of our conversation, and as I requested—in words that come from the heart, with the added hope that you, too, are in agreement with the opinion I expressed.

Since in recent weeks there has been a change in the desired direction, in my opinion, regarding the matters we touched upon in our aforementioned conversation, if—as I hope—you had a part in this change, may a blessing come upon you and upon all those who cooperated with you in this direction. I will add my wishes that you will surely not be satisfied with this change, which is merely a beginning in the desired direction, but rather that you will increase your efforts, etc. May it be His will that this be with great success, for this is for the benefit of our people, the Children of Israel, in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established [and it is understood, naturally, that this is also for the benefit of the Children of Israel in all the places where they dwell].

With respect and with blessings for success and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 9738

25 Teves, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the Kfar HaNoar – Be’er Yaakov
In our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily
May Hashem keep them alive

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to receive your greetings through your teacher, educator, and director, Mr. Chaim Yitzchak Glazer, may he live. I was especially happy to learn of your progress, both in your studies and in your conduct. This is the duty of every Jewish person, and all the more so for the youth and the young generation—to go from strength to strength, not only in the growth and development of the body and the material, but primarily in progress and ascent in the life of the spirit and the soul.

Mr. Glazer conveyed your questions to me, which are:

My opinion regarding: a) The aliyah of Jewish youth from America to Eretz Yisrael, and b) Regarding the expected peace with our Arab neighbors.

Regarding question (a), my opinion on this is preceded by an introduction:

The period of a person’s life is generally divided into two stages. The first stage is one in which the person is primarily a passive recipient. The second stage is one where the hope is that, at the very least, he will be a provider and an active participant in the life of his surroundings and his family—and his surroundings in the broadest sense—active in the desired direction.

It is self-understood that first and foremost, one expects a person to be active in upholding the good, establishing it, and increasing it, and in banishing the bad. This is, in a sense, the repayment of a debt, since he acquired the strengths and knowledge to discern the good and wishes to act upon it, having received all of this from the people in his environment throughout his first stage of life. Therefore, first and foremost, he is obligated to show gratitude and pay the debt imposed upon him to bring good into action in all the areas that influenced him, and also to the point that he will influence others to continue in this direction together with him, and even afterward.

To what can this be compared? To someone who wants to give tzedakah to someone to whom he is not obligated—that is a great thing, but the repayment of a debt takes precedence over the giving of tzedakah.

It is also understood that if, along with the repayment of the debt, there is an additional point—that his creditor is in need of help, even to the point of *pikuach nefesh*—then the repayment of the debt also contains the element of reviving the soul of the creditor and his household.

My opinion regarding your question is based on the above:

Youth who possess energy that has not yet been tapped, and who still need to enter life and become an active part of their society and environment, have a priority to utilize all their efforts for the benefit of the environment in which they were born and from which they received their strengths. In all these matters, they should be active in the desired direction, even if the society is not so desperately in need of their specific help, and it is in their power only to add and establish. All the more so when the society is in a precarious state, etc., and at the same time, those engaged in its stabilization are few in number—then it is clearly the greatest necessity. Only after he has repaid his debt can he think about activity in another place or another country.

From this, it is understood *halacha l’maaseh* that youth in every country and city, when they reach the age of maturity, are obligated first and foremost to utilize their strengths in the country where they are located. Especially in those countries where, to our sorrow, the spiritual state, as well as the moral state and the connection to the eternal values of Judaism, are not in a strong and established condition. Anyone who can do something in this regard is performing an act of *pikuach nefesh* in the literal sense, saving souls from assimilation, *chas v’shalom*, etc. Only after the youth has paid his debt in the place where he was raised and educated can he think about what he can do for his Jewish brethren in another place.

It is also understood that there is no contradiction in the fact that sometimes, and perhaps often, youth need to visit a different environment or a different place—or in the present case, to be for a certain period in our Holy Land—as preparation and training for more intensive and successful activity in their own environment and country, where they must first and foremost act to pay their moral and spiritual debt, etc., as mentioned above.

It is likewise understood that it can also happen, and often does, that the environment itself chooses someone from the youth to send to another country, or in our case, to our Holy Land, to be active there for a certain period or even to settle. In that case, this too is included in the sphere of activity for the benefit of the environment and country in which he was educated and raised.

To summarize: My opinion is that the youth and the young generation should utilize their strengths and opportunities first and foremost in their places of residence—to utilize them and increase the good. More precisely, to disseminate Judaism and its values among the youth, a large portion of whom are in need of influence in this regard and constant education—not once a year or from time to time. The chances for the success of this education are greater when the educator is a native of the country of the students who are in need of guidance and influence, and he knows the nature of their souls, etc., since he grew up and was educated among them. This is not the case with an educator who is an emissary from another country and another environment.

Certainly, there is no need to emphasize that my aforementioned opinion concerns the problem in its generality, in the spirit of the question, for regarding individual persons, it is understood that one must take into account the specific conditions of the individual, the family members, health and economic conditions, etc.

One could elaborate further on the aforementioned problem, but I hope that even these few lines, small in quantity relative to the importance of the matter, will suffice to clarify my opinion.

And regarding your second question concerning peace:

True peace can only exist if it is based on the goodwill of both sides. I do not see a reason or cause for the Arab neighbors of our Holy Land to want to make a true peace, which includes within it a total despair on their part regarding many territories that were recently captured, and all the more so regarding territories they captured twenty years ago, as well as an admission that the people of Israel in Eretz Yisrael have every right to live there without any dependence on anything else, etc. On the other hand, the state of non-peace and war holds all the advantages for the Arabs. Furthermore, it gives them the possibility to come with demands for aid from various powers outside of this region. By inciting competition between one power and another as to who has greater importance to the rulers of a certain Arab country, they increase the aid, assistance, gifts, etc.—which would not be the case if the tension in the region were to dissipate, matters were settled, and life entered a normal course, etc.

To add to this, and perhaps this is an even greater fundamental point: several powers outside the region, especially the large ones, are apparently interested in having tension in the region and having it divided among several peoples, regimes, and kingdoms, etc. This situation opens the door to influence, and even to the rule of one power or another in the region, by helping one of the sides in the region. This is not the case when peace prevails among the peoples located in the region and they cooperate with one another; then the possibility of rule by a foreign power is diminished, and even its influence will decrease.

After all this, it is simple that no Jewish man or woman should despair, *chas v’shalom*, of peace. For the entire existence of the people of Israel throughout the generations, including the existence now in our Holy Land, is completely above the path of nature. For according to all economic and political theories, etc., a small and impoverished people has no right to exist. Especially to hold on in the manner that it is now, at the focal point where the interests of immense kingdoms collide, situated at the crossroads of several continents and the strongest blocs in the international arena.

It is a wonder that throughout all of history, and up to the most ancient times, the territory of Eretz Yisrael has been a place of agitation and strife among all the peoples and kingdoms that ruled the world in their times—Egypt, Assyria, Babylon, Greece, Rome, etc. It did not enjoy peace and tranquility except for a few years and relatively short periods in which the people of Israel were faithful to Hashem and walked in the way of Hashem, the way of Torah and mitzvos, such as in the days of David and Shlomo, etc.

And since Eretz Yisrael is a land [which] the eyes of Hashem your G-d are upon it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, surely He who guards Israel will neither slumber nor sleep. And just as until now, so too in the future, He will protect His people Israel from every trouble and distress. And the more the **foundation** of the existence of the people of Israel is established—**one** nation in the land—which is the way of life in daily living according to the instruction of the Torah, for the Torah is **one** for all of us, given by the **one** Hashem, so too will the security in our Holy Land increase, until the fulfillment of the promise: "And you shall dwell in your land in safety, and I will grant peace in the land, and you shall lie down and none shall make you afraid."

In this, too, there is a special role for the youth, who are not afraid of the truth as it is, who do not seek compromises, whose strength is with them, and who are not ashamed before those who mock or [worry about] what the nations will say, etc. Upon them is the duty to be the vanguard going before the people of Israel in every place they are, in the land and also abroad, to walk in the way of Hashem as Hashem has taught us in His Torah, to walk securely on His path.

With a blessing for success in going from strength to strength in the way of Torah—the Torah of life—and the mitzvos, of which it is said: "And you shall live by them."

## 939

[939](#_ftn_370)

[28 Teves, 5729]

[In my opinion](#_ftn_371) it is **obvious** that under **no circumstances** should one of the holy Names be made the subject of a doctoral dissertation—for reasons of sentiment, for reasons of "dry" halacha, because it constitutes a breach of boundaries for **all** who follow to seek permission to write a paper on this topic and the like, and for many other reasons.

– [And in the language](#_ftn_372) of Chazal: The reward of the master will be great for **abstaining** from this topic for his dissertation, and he should choose a subject of an entirely different nature.

## 9,340 

 B"H, Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the activists and friends of the Bais Rivkah schools—in general, and to the participants in the annual Melaveh Malkah—in particular,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Brachah!

Since the annual Melaveh Malkah for Bais Rivkah is taking place this year a few days after the day of the histalkus (yahrzeit) of the founder of Bais Rivkah, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, it is especially timely to recall a statement of his which, at the time—and until this very day—created a turning point in the state of Yiddishkeit in this country.

Immediately upon arriving in America in the year 5700, when the Rebbe, my father-in-law, revealed his Divine mission in this country—to make America a place of Torah and yiras shamayim— he was asked: "But this is America, it is not like 'back home'?" The Rebbe, my father-in-law, replied:

"**America is no different**; regarding Torah and mitzvos, America is no exception!"

This statement is of special significance for Jewish women, and in certain respects, even more so than for men. Women in general have a tendency to follow the latest "fashions," and not infrequently, fashion touches upon [the matter of tznius]. Jewish women must know that the same Torah and mitzvos, and the same principle of **kol kevudah bas melech penimah** (the entire glory of a Jewish daughter is **internal**), which were valid back home, are also valid in America. The same tradition of heartfelt Jewish women, who were the first to help build the Mishkan (Sanctuary) for the entire people of Israel, and the mishkan and sanctuary in their own homes—so that it would be a home about which the Ribono shel Olam can say **v’shachanti besocham**, that it is a home for the Divine Shechinah, as it were—is also valid here in America, just as it was once back home on the other side of the ocean.

And to help realize these traditions and maintain the continuity of Torah and mitzvos, tznius, etc., among Jewish women—for the woman is the **akeres habayis**, the foundation of the Jewish home—the Rebbe, my father-in-law, founded the "Bais Rivkah" schools al taharas hakodesh.

It is therefore superfluous to elaborate on the importance and necessity of the Bais Rivkah institutions for Jewish daughters, and on the great zechus that each one of you, activists and friends of Bais Rivkah, has in supporting these institutions and helping to strengthen and expand them. This is also a "vessel" to receive Hashem's blessings in everything one needs: Yiddishe nachas from children, health, and parnassah in abundance, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

With respect and with blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9842

[9842](#_ftn_387)

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Bo, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letter...

As we stand a few days before the tenth of Shevat, the yom hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and relying on the words of our Sages that "one does not urge [to perform a mitzvah] except those who are already eager,"

I wish to arouse [the need for] strengthening and increasing our efforts in walking the straight path that he taught us, and to follow in his ways,

Through actual deeds in the three pillars upon which the world stands—including this "small world," the human being—Torah, avodah (tefillah), and gemilus chasadim,

Together with teshuvah—for then the good deeds are illuminated and shine,

And in the language of the Rambam, then one receives them (the mitzvos that one performs) with contentment and joy, etc., and furthermore, one yearns for them.

For teshuvah, too, must be present in every person, as our Sages say, to be in a state of teshuvah (ila'ah) all one's days, to extract and elevate one's neshamah elokis from its exile and return it to its Father’s house (all the days of one's life in this world), so that it may be included and unified with Him, may He be blessed, by directing all one’s focus and desire toward Torah and mitzvos.

For the good deeds that one performs return one's soul—which is a "part of Hashem"—to the Source and Root of all worlds.

This is in regard to avodas Hashem, both in spiritual matters and in worldly matters. The words of our Nasi, the master of the hilula, are well known, that this day is auspicious to connect to the Tree of Life, etc., and to be blessed with children, life, and ample sustenance.

With blessings for success and for active farbrengens in Torah, avodah, and gemilus chasadim, in a manner of "growing and increasing."

**M. Schneerson**

## 9747

[9747](#_ftn_414)

B”H, 18 Shevat, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. [Aryeh](#_ftn_415) Eliav, shiyichyeh,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letter in due time, along with the enclosure, and I also received regards from you through anash who have met and continue to meet with you. Although this attitude of yours is not surprising—especially after our meeting several years ago, when we spoke about [your work](#_ftn_416) in Arad, and we also discussed the eternal values of Yiddishkeit, etc., and your promise regarding this—a matter in anticipation is not the same as a matter in actuality. My hope, based on the reports from anash, is that you are acting in this regard in a manner of "increasing and ascending," for that is how it should be in every matter that possesses a spirit of life, and especially for a Jew who is [commanded](#_ftn_417) to ascend in holiness. It is understood that when one sees that the opportunities to do good are growing, this is a clear indication from Above that they must be utilized to their fullest, especially since your good portion is to do this [in the Land](#_ftn_418) upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year.

It is my hope that by the time you receive my letter, your health has improved and you are acting in the aforementioned direction in a manner of "increasing and ascending," especially regarding our brethren who have just arrived from that country. Surely, they will be given the opportunity to continue together in the environment most familiar to them, and they will not be scattered or separated, etc.

With blessings for good tidings, in good health, regarding all that has been mentioned.

P.S. Please excuse the fact that your inquiry regarding affiliation has not yet been answered; for the time being, a suitable [affiliation] has not yet been found, and we are still searching; once it is, a response will naturally be sent.

## 9748

[9748](#_ftn_419)

B"H, 18 Shevat, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of "Young Israel,"
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and Blessing!

I received your letter in due time, in which you write [regarding](#_ftn_420) the question of establishing a technical religious front in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. Please forgive the delay in my response. The reason for this is that I wanted to obtain as much information as possible regarding the prospects for this, from various sources, [and after](#_ftn_421) until now.

Based on the latest information that has reached me, and for which I have received confirmation from both sides, the situation regarding this in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, is the same as it was before the last elections there. I only hope that the results will be different than they were then, when the front did not materialize. In truth, it is no wonder that there has been no change in the situation, because the same people who decided against the front then are the ones currently determining the course of events in this matter, and the reasons that moved them to prevent a front then still exist now. It is a great pity that they do not want to learn a lesson from the failure in the last elections, and also that they do not want to learn from the changes that have occurred since then until now.

[And as](#_ftn_422) I wrote at the time of those elections—if there is not the greatest and most unequivocal public pressure, showing that they are serious, then to our greatest sorrow, the prospects for this are the same as they were then.

It is understood that I am not giving up, G-d forbid, for that is the opposite of the Jewish approach to any good thing that encounters difficulties, especially in a matter as serious as the establishment of a **technical** religious front [and I emphasize "technical," meaning solely and exclusively for the sake of the elections, because my opinion is clear that just as it is necessary for the elections, so too it is necessary that there not be a merger of the parties after the elections, for many, many reasons]. And without a vow, I will do everything possible on my part for the sake of establishing the aforementioned technical religious front, and surely "Young Israel" will also utilize all of their influence to realize the idea as stated in your letter. But the time to apply pressure is close to the elections.

With respect and blessing.

Mr. Dov Ettinger
Shalom u’Bracha!

I am hereby acknowledging receipt of your letter from 15 Teves, along with the enclosure. Thank you very much.

On this occasion, I would like to express the great satisfaction I felt regarding the activities and the ceremony for the unveiling [unveiling](#_ftn_429) of the monument for the great Gaon and Chossid, etc., Rabbi Boruch Mordechai, zt"l, Ettinger, one of the greatest students of our Alter Rebbe.

As with all matters of true goodness, my hope is strong that there will be a continuation of this in fruits and fruits of fruits, and first and foremost in the same method and direction to which Rabbi B.M., zt"l, dedicated his life: the method of Chabad and the Torah of Chabad. One of the points of this is that it is not a matter for special times or for select individuals, etc., but rather to illuminate and permeate the daily life of every single person, as the heritage [heritage](#_ftn_430) of the entire nation. And surely for someone like yourself, there is no need for further explanation on this.

I read with special interest the lines you wrote regarding the idea of organizing a book on 200 years of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily. In my opinion, in all responsible matters such as this, there is a great responsibility for many reasons. On the face of it, it would be better if, at first, you were to publish a booklet or collections whose content is not so comprehensive and not so binding. It is possible to begin regarding Chabad in Chevron and Chabad in Yerushalayim and the like, or at the very least, not a book on "200 years of Chabad," etc., but rather a comprehensive survey, with the addition and emphasis that this is a sort of introduction and preface. In the course of time, when all the material is gathered, etc., you will proceed to the publication of a comprehensive book, and so on.

It is understood that the above does not at all rule out gathering the material on the aforementioned subject and processing it to a certain extent, since the final editing will certainly depend on the quality and quantity of the book; that is to say, it will be decided upon in the final stages. And certainly, regarding a practical discussion on everything written above, all those you mention in your letter should consult among themselves. I am sure you will inform me of the developments in this matter, and thank you in advance.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. Regarding financial participation in the publication of the book, it is understood that it depends somewhat on the quantity—that is to say, the sum of money—and even more so on the quality. My intention is that the entire book should be consistent with the worldview of the great Gaon and Chossid, etc., Rabbi B.M., zt"l, Ettinger, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

## 9555

[9555](#_ftn_453)

[B"H](#_ftn_454), Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled,
Parshas Im Kesef Talveh Es Ami, 5729.
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Board of the Shomrei Shabbos Gemilas Chasadim Society,
May Hashem protect them and may they live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to the announcement that the annual meeting of the society and the Melaveh Malkah will take place on Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Im Kesef Talveh Es Ami, in accordance with your fine custom year after year—

May it be Hashem’s will that it be a time of good fortune and success, with an increase and elevation over the previous years—in accordance with the directive (which is also the granting of strength): "We increase in matters of holiness."

Now, the greatness of Gemilas Chasadim through the lending of money is immense (even greater than tzedakah)—for it applies both to the poor and to the wealthy.

Furthermore, even regarding the poor—it is "the greatest level (of tzedakah), above which there is nothing," and "less than this is one who gives tzedakah."

On the face of it, tzedakah possesses a quality that Gemilas Chasadim through a loan does not—for in tzedakah, with these funds, one could have purchased the life of his vital soul, and thus he is giving the life of his soul to Hashem—a gift of money with no expectation of return.

However, it can be said—and in the language of the verse—that for every person whose heart prompts him to contribute gold and silver, etc., to the Gemilas Chasadim fund, all the aforementioned levels are present in this contribution.

And furthermore—and this is also fundamental—according to the words of the Alter Rebbe, that among the matters of (the higher) teshuvah is to "cleave to Him, may He be blessed"—to align one’s attributes with His attributes, may He be blessed, just as He is merciful, etc., and the action is the act of tzedakah, to revive the spirit of the lowly, as it is written, "For in six days Hashem made," etc., as is known in other places.

See the Maamar entitled *Im Kesef Talveh* by the Rebbe Maharash—from the year **5629**—regarding how in the "making of the six days," etc., there is the concept of a loan. See there.

May it be Hashem’s will that you conduct yourselves as mentioned above with joy and a glad heart.

With respect and with a blessing for success in a way that is good and revealed, and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is my contribution to the Gemilas Chasadim fund.

## 956

[956]

[B"H], Erev Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Adar, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

As we stand on Erev Shabbos Kodesh Mevarchim Chodesh Adar, whose essence is the upcoming days of Purim, it is well known that the content of these days [mentioned] and re-enacted year after year—

Relates both to the sphere between man and Hashem: the strengthening of bitachon—that matters conducted through the way of nature (Esther’s efforts with Achashverosh, etc.) succeed only if they are connected with tefillah and requests to the Ribono shel Olam, for salvation belongs to Hashem. This is why even now we precede the celebration of Purim with the fast of Taanis Esther.

And it also relates to the sphere between man and his fellow: for among the mitzvos of Purim is the mitzvah of mishloach manos ish l’re’ehu, [the reason] for which is to demonstrate the drawing together of hearts and friendship between one another. Furthermore, and most essentially, there is the mitzvah of matanos l’evyonim—to help the needy—which surpasses even one’s own mishloach manos and seudas Purim. In the golden language of the [Rambam], who ruled as halacha: "It is better for a person to increase his gifts to the poor than to increase his own meal and his mishloach manos to his friends... for one who gladdens the hearts of these unfortunate ones is like the Shechinah" (end of Hilchos Megillah).

***

I was happy to hear about your service in the army and your good conduct, starting with the putting on of tefillin every weekday. [A mitzvah] leads to another mitzvah—the fulfillment of the rest of the mitzvos of the Torah, Toras Chaim, which means, literally, instruction for life—the life of this world—so that they may be lives worthy of the name. Especially since keeping the commands of the Creator, Yisbarach, [is what] protects and saves one from anything undesirable. It is understood that if the observance of Torah and mitzvos is mandatory at all times and in all places, then all the more so in our Holy Land, and particularly in a situation where one is in special need of the blessings of Hashem, the Giver of the Torah and the Commander of the mitzvos.

It is my hope that you also utilize your influence in the aforementioned direction for the benefit of others, for [v'ahavta] l're'acha kamocha is a [great principle] in the Torah. May it be His will that your words come from the heart, for then they surely [enter] the heart and achieve their effect, especially when the words are accompanied by a living example.

An additional point here: if words that come from the heart achieve their effect at all times and in all situations—because the [heart] of a Yid is awake to Torah and mitzvos—then all the more so when one is within the framework of the army, [whose foundation] is discipline and kabbalas ol, the level of [naaseh] preceding nishma. And if this is true regarding the orders of human beings, then all the more so regarding the orders of the "Commander-in-Chief," the Ribono shel Olam, Creator of the world and its Guide.

To add: just as it is in the army, where an individual cannot claim that his conduct is his own business and that others have no say in it—for we see that the conduct of an individual, even a simple soldier, can sometimes determine the success of the entire mission, the victory of the platoon, and sometimes the entire front and the fate of the entire country, and conversely, an undesirable action, chas v'shalom—so too, and with greater force, does this apply to the private conduct in the daily life of every Yid, the armies of Hashem.

Furthermore, when one is in the aforementioned framework, one often sees hashgacha pratis with one's own eyes. While that hashgacha pratis is, of course, active at all times and in all places, it is usually hidden within the way of nature and requires hitbonenus, etc. This is not the case within a military framework and the situation in which you are placed, where one sees hashgacha pratis in a revealed manner. Surely, any further elaboration on all that has been said above is superfluous.

With blessings for happy days of Purim, and [in the words] of the text: "For the Yidden there was light, and gladness, and joy, and honor."

## 9602

[9602](#_ftn_505)

B"H, Erev Purim, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yosef Yoel, known as Prof. Dr. Rivlin,

Shalom and Bracha!

After the longest of intervals, it was a pleasant surprise to receive your letter, along with the book **Mathematical Writings** by Dr. Pesach Chabrani. Thank you for your kindness in conveying my thanks to all the members of the committee for the second copy of the book. Especially, as you wrote, since the author, a"h, was of Chabad lineage.

I see it noted in the book that this is part of the estate of the late author, and I would be interested to know, at least, the content of the rest of the estate, especially since there are apparently notes among the writings regarding the family history, etc.

I find this an opportune moment to remind you of your promise while you were here to also send me the fruits of your own labor from all these years, as only one book that you published in recent years is found in my library. Thank you in advance.

On this occasion, I will also express my hope and wishes that all is well with your family, including the head of the household—that is, yourself—and that it is a true peace, in the well-known phrasing, both physically and spiritually, and in a more internal way—in both body and soul, and at an even more internal point—peace between the two souls that every person of Yisrael possesses, in the language of Rabbeinu HaZaken: the nefesh elokis and the nefesh habahamis, and of course, simply, in the manner of the dominance of form over matter and spirit over the physical.

With respect and blessing, and with a blessing for a happy Purim.

I will take the liberty of making a suggestion, and although it comes after the signature, it is essential and also spiritual: since the committee has taken upon itself the publication of the late author's writings, it will surely also ensure that everything related to the elevation of his neshamah is in order—observing the yahrtzeit, studying Mishnayos, giving tzedakah, etc. And surely for one such as yourself, there is no need to elaborate on this.

See also the introduction you wrote, right in its first chapter, where after the understanding, comprehension, and depth in the wisdom of mathematics, which is the foundation for the other sciences, you say that now "begins the unknown, known only to the Unknown of all unknowns." The intention here is understood and also simple and unambiguous, in the style of the great [Teacher](#_ftn_506], the Guide for the Perplexed of all generations: "The foundation of foundations and the pillar of wisdom is to know that there is a Primary Being... and His truth is not like the truth of any of them (the other existences)... for the power of the human mind is not sufficient... to grasp His truth"—the Unknown of all unknowns.

## 963

[963](#_ftn_507)

[B"H](#_ftn_508), Shushan Purim, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 27th Annual Banquet of the "Netzivei HaYeshiva" supporters of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

The annual banquet of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, which takes place a few days after Purim, will surely reflect the spirit of Purim as well, for there is actually a special connection between them.

Haman’s decree was bound up with the claim: **"There is one people, scattered and dispersed among the nations... and their laws are different from every people."** [Haman](#_ftn_510) argued that the fact that Jews are isolated, do not assimilate into the surrounding society, and maintain their own laws, is not good for the state, nor for the Jews themselves.

The outcome proved to be the exact opposite: the salvation came not through changing the character and essence of the Jews and the Jewish people, but on the contrary, specifically through strengthening Jewish unity and distinctiveness—the **"one people"** and **"their laws are different."** This not only preserved the Jewish people but also brought an elevation to all the provinces of Achashverosh, when the leadership of the state was placed in the hands of Mordechai HaYehudi—the Jew who **"does not bow down and does not prostrate himself"** (**lo yichra v'lo yishtachaveh**).

The clear lesson from this is that while Jews are in galus, scattered and dispersed among the nations, one must never, Heaven forbid, think that by abandoning Jewish distinctiveness and the Jewish way of life, and by imitating the surrounding environment, one will secure one's own situation or help the society in which one lives. The truth is the exact opposite: maintaining Jewish unity and distinctiveness, and specifically through **"their laws are different,"** conducting daily life in accordance with the eternal laws and values of the Torah HaKedosha—this is the only way to ensure Jewish survival, and incidentally, also to gain the trust and respect of the nations.

It is understood that in order to maintain this complete Jewish independence while being a small minority in an overwhelming and often unfriendly environment, a strength of character is required, up to the point of **mesiras nefesh**, just as it was in the time of Purim of old. Therefore, it is a life-necessity to begin developing this true Jewish spirit from the earliest youth. And this is also the task of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal—to educate the students in this spirit, up to the point of mesiras nefesh, so that they should be "Temimim"—**whole** Jews in their physical, spiritual, and soul-life. In this lies their true happiness, and consequently, the happiness of their parents, of Klal Yisrael, and of the entire environment.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant success to this annual endeavor, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success in all the above and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9604

[9604](#_ftn_513)

B”H, 15 Adar, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Nshei Chabad in Montreal
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive greetings regarding your work through Rabbanit Golda Shwei, along with the *ma'os chitim* funds that were raised, as per the enclosed receipt.

Success in the area of *ma'os chitim* is certainly evidence of success in the other activities of Nshei Chabad as well, and may Hashem Yisbarach help that all activities should proceed to an even greater and broader extent. And although we all have the inner desire that Yidden should be self-sufficient and not need to rely on *ma'os chitim* and the like, until that is the case, it is necessary to provide the greatest possible assistance to those in need, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

And how important the participation of Jewish women is, is underscored during these days of Purim, and especially in the Megillah, as was also mentioned at the [farbrengen](#_ftn_514). For although Esther did everything according to the instructions of Mordechai ("And Esther performed the [maamar](#_ftn_515) of Mordechai"), and indeed precisely because of this, the Megillah is not called by Mordechai’s name, nor by both of their names, but [davka](#_ftn_516) by Esther’s name alone — Megillas **Esther**.

With blessings for success in a manner of "going and increasing," and for good tidings.

## 9,606 

[B"H, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the celebration of the laying of the cornerstone for Kfar Chabad Bet — in our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

With great joy, I received the news regarding the laying of the cornerstone for Kfar Chabad Bet, on the day of 11 Nissan, which is approaching for us and for all of Yisrael for life, goodness, and peace.

It is my hope that in the near future, the two will be distinct only in time, but will be unified with the existing Kfar Chabad, which has stood for twenty years. Furthermore, that in the course of time, a third, fourth, and so on, village will arise, in such a way that they will all together be one unified entity with one spirit.

As has been discussed many times: even though, in the style of our Sages, it is a sign of the greatness of the Ribono shel Olam that the faces of human beings are not alike and their opinions are not alike, nevertheless, Hashem Yisbarach, the Creator of man, demands the drawing together of the hearts of all our people, the Children of Yisrael, to the point of their total unification — one great Jewish heart.

And the true and lasting unification of those who are different and separate is possible only through a unified life founded upon the Torah of life, the Torah of the living Elokim.

For there is one **Torah** for us all, given by one **Hashem**, through which **Yisrael** becomes one nation on earth.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that just as we have merited the laying of the cornerstone for Kfar Chabad Bet, so too, may we soon merit the completion of the construction of this Kfar, its perfection, and its full habitation with joy and gladness, and following this — and immediately — to Kfar Chabad Gimmel, Dalet, and so on — all of them founded,

As was the will of the founder of the first Kfar Chabad, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe,

Upon the threefold love: love of **Hashem**, love of **Torah**, and love of **Yisrael**.

For true love is that which draws near and unites — *ahavah* (love) has the same gematria as *echad* (one).

And from the Chabad villages, the fountains of the words of the living Elokim will spread outward, and with them, they will carry the aforementioned spirit of love, and it will be revealed in every place where they are spread.

For Yisrael, the Torah, and the Kudsha Brich Hu — the hidden and the revealed — are all one.

And from the building of this Kfar Chabad — to the fulfillment of the prophecy through Dovid, King of Yisrael (and its fulfillment very soon):

"Let Elokim arise, let His enemies be scattered, and let those who hate Him flee before Him."

And are there enemies before He who spoke and the world came into being? Rather, these are the enemies of Yisrael.

"And He will save Tzion and build the cities of Yehudah, and they shall dwell there and inherit it."

With respect and with a blessing for great success in the work of their hands, and with a blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9767

[9767](#_ftn_527)

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5729

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 21st of Adar,

It is understood that he must finally [study](#_ftn_528) in a yeshiva where only holy studies are taught. The importance of this matter and the necessity for it are understood.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary
