## 969

[969](#_ftn_529)

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Ruth Ratner, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

Your letter was received with much delay, in which you ask how to understand the verse [530](#_ftn_530) "You shall not make for yourself a graven image or any likeness," etc. You also ask whether there is a fundamental difference between painting and music.

Regarding the practical halachic ruling contained in the aforementioned verse, you can consult a rabbi in your area, who can provide all the details that interest you.

I will only add one essential point: a painter—whether male or female—has a vast field in which to utilize their talents to the fullest without infringing upon the laws of the Torah, which is *Toras Chaim*—meaning, an instruction for life, simply put, in this world, so that life may be worthy of the name in every respect. On the contrary, through the power of painting, one can add vitality, understanding, and deeper perception to matters of the world in general, and specifically, an internal understanding of the words of the Sweet Singer of Israel: "How [great](#_ftn_531) are Your works, Hashem," "How manifold are Your works, Hashem." Through this, one can attain admiration, reverence, and *yiras haromemus* for the Creator, may He be blessed, in a wondrous way.

There are [several](#_ftn_532) *sichos* from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the impression and depth experienced by his father, the Rebbe Rashab, when he saw paintings created by an artist. To such an extent that, although it is known how precious every moment was to him, he nevertheless dedicated several hours while in Paris to visiting the Louvre, particularly the painting department. Afterward, he shared with his son and successor, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Chassidic insights that had sparked in his mind while observing the paintings.

It is my hope that the fact that you cite the aforementioned verse—which is at the beginning of the Ten Commandments, the foundation of the entire Torah, extending even to the most recent halachic rulings in the Oral Torah—indicates that you are organizing your life to conform to these halachic instructions, and that you are doing so with inwardness and sincerity. Especially since it is the role of the painter to grasp and convey the inwardness of the subject they are painting, to the point that even one who is not a painter will also feel the inwardness within that thing.

May it be Hashem's will that you exert influence in your surroundings in the aforementioned direction—influence in an appropriate manner and through appropriate means, and primarily by being a living example.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 974

[974](#_ftn_533)

[B"H](#_ftn_534), 11 Nissan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

The Yom Tov of Pesach, the "first of the months" and the first of all the Yomim Tovim, and its content—*Yetzias Mitzrayim* (the exodus from Egypt), when the Jewish people became a nation—possesses a special significance as a comprehensive, all-encompassing event. Indeed, all its details are universal directives and, naturally, eternal ones, just like all matters of Torah, which is eternal and not limited by time or place.

We will focus here on one aspect of the *Korban Pesach* and *Yetzias Mitzrayim*.

The *Korban Pesach* requires and is bound up with the *mitzvah* of *milah*, as it is stated: **"Let every male be circumcised, and then he may draw near to perform it... but no uncircumcised person shall eat of it."** Furthermore, the entire event of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* came about, as our Sages explain, in the merit of these two *mitzvos*: *Pesach* and *milah*.

There is also an internal connection between these two concepts.

**Bris Milah**, performed on the eighth day immediately after birth, represents the covenant (*bris*) between a Jew and Hashem at the very **beginning** of life, ensuring that the entire life will be according to the will of Hashem.

**Korban Pesach** was first commanded to the head of a family ("A lamb for a father's house, a lamb for a household"). It takes place at the **midpoint** of life, when the Jew is already a family man and a master of his own home.

At the first *Korban Pesach* in Egypt, it also states: **"Draw back and take for yourselves"**—draw back (from idolatry) and take to perform the *Korban Pesach*. This teaches us that at this stage of life, there is a past (*avar*), and it is possible that the past was not entirely as it should have been, and one must rectify it.

Applying the content of these aforementioned matters to daily life, the lesson is as follows:

Every moment of life is a **beginning** of the hours and days that follow it. It is also a **continuation** (*hemshech*) of the past. More generally:

There are days and times when a person begins **new** matters, and there are days and times when a person continues and works on his **previous** matters.

After all, "I was created to serve my Creator," and even more—we are **subjugated** to "I am Hashem your G-d, Who took you out of the land of Egypt."

The two aforementioned characteristics of *Bris Milah* and *Korban Pesach* are also reflected in two general types of *avodas Hashem*: the *avodah* of a **tzaddik**—who deals primarily with **new** matters and new achievements; and the *avodah* of a **baal teshuvah**—who deals primarily with rectifying and improving the past. Even in the higher sense of *teshuvah*—returning to the source—it implies that one was previously close to the source and drifted away. For the *neshamah*, before it descended to animate the body, was pure spirituality, and one must ensure that even while the *neshamah* is in the body, it remains spiritual—and even more, it must also make the body and the *nefesh habehamis* spiritual.

So too, **specifically** every day for every Jew: immediately upon waking from sleep, he is a **"new creation"** and begins a new life with *Modeh Ani*, etc. And at the other extreme, before going to sleep—the *cheshbon hanefesh* (accounting of the soul) of the past day during *Krias Shema She'al HaMitah*, before he entrusts the deposit to Hashem: "Into Your hand I entrust my spirit."

***

This is also the concept of *Zeman Cheiruseinu* and *Yetzias Mitzrayim* in daily life: to be free and to emerge from the limitations (*Mitzrayim* and boundaries) of one's own nature and from enslavement to the surrounding environment. This requires *avodah* in a **twofold** manner: like the *avodah* of a *tzaddik*—constantly beginning new good things, **"do good"** (*asei tov*); and the *avodah* of a *baal teshuvah*, **"turn from evil and do good"** (*sur meira v'asei tov*)—to rectify what is necessary from the past and reach ever higher and closer to the original source in G-dliness.

And even when one finds oneself, G-d forbid, in circumstances like those of old in Egypt, where very many undesirable foreign things have attached themselves—if only he decides with truth to be Hashem's, if he says **"Hashem our G-d** (our power and our life-force) **Hashem is One"**—then immediately, "I am Hashem your G-d Who took you out of the land of Egypt" becomes true now just as it was then. His enslavement to Pharaoh and to the "nakedness of the land" of Egypt is nullified; he crawls out of the swamp, rectifies the past, and begins a new life, a truly Jewish life—true freedom through Torah and *mitzvos*.

***

May it be the will that all this should be as it was at the first *Yetzias Mitzrayim*—**with a high hand**, with pride, with song, and with joy.

And through all this, to draw near and hasten the realization of the prophetic promise: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders"—in the true and complete *Geulah* through *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*.

With blessings for a kosher and happy *Chag HaPesach*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9771

[9771](#_ftn_550)

[B"H](#_ftn_551), 11 Nissan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as we are commanded in our Torah—the Torah of life—encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and night, [as](#_ftn_554) it is said: "In all your ways, know Him."

With appreciation, respect, and holiday blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9272

[9272](#_ftn_556)

[B"H](#_ftn_557), the day after Shabbos HaGadol, 11 Nissan, 5729.
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our dear brothers, the Children of Israel, who are settling in "Nachalat Har Chabad" — among all the immigrants settling in our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days,

May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

Surely the two Sifrei Torah sent from here have already arrived and been received.

My words, and the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, have already been stated [in a letter](#_ftn_559) he wrote:

"On Friday, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, after midday, in the week of the parsha 'When you come to the land... and the land shall rest a Shabbos to Hashem' — 5709,"

at the time he sent a Sefer Torah "to our dear Anash and the students of the Temimim who are now settling in the Holy Land, may it be built and established." And this is what he wrote:

"At the beginning of your settlement in the Holy Land, may it be built and established, you must contemplate well and know, with recognition, feeling, and inner hiskashrus, that Divine Providence has brought you and your families, may they live, to the land upon which the eyes of Hashem our G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year. And you are in the palace of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, at every time and every hour.

"May the receipt of the Sefer Torah that I am sending you serve as a constant reminder in your minds and hearts to arrange all your private and communal lives according to the Torah, and as our holy forefathers and Rebbes, of blessed memory, have taught us: to educate your sons and daughters, may they live, in its path, without any compromises; and to radiate its spirit—the spirit of the Israel of old—upon the rest of our brothers, the Children of Israel, may they live, both those who are near and those who are far for the time being, by influencing them to guide them on the path that ascends to Beis-El. This is the path of Torah study with yiras shamayim and the performance of mitzvos with hidur, out of true closeness that stems from ahavas Yisrael and the middos of Chassidus, which are according to the Torah of the words of the living G-d.

"And may each and every one of you be a candle to illuminate the darkness of the galus in which you and we find ourselves, with the light of Hashem, [until](#_ftn_561) Hashem fulfills His promise through His holy prophets to let us hear the voice of the herald announcing salvation, that Hashem has comforted His people, and Hashem goes before us to gather our exiles and redeem us with an eternal redemption.

"May the Name, blessed be He, be your help and bless you and your families, may they live, with all that you need in children, life, and ample sustenance, both materially and spiritually, and may He redeem us all through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, Amen.

"Please, I ask you to convey the content of this letter to your wives, sons, and daughters, may they live, to each and every one individually."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you fulfill everything written above with joy and goodness of heart, with expansion, and in a manner that is constantly increasing and illuminating,

[until](#_ftn_562) the fulfillment of the promise, "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders" — with the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, very soon.

With respect and blessing for a successful settlement, both materially and spiritually,

And with the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach holiday,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9763

[9763](#_ftn_563)

B”H, 11 Nissan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi S.Y. Frankel Teomim, may he live
Kiryat Ono

Shalom u’Bracha,

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Nissan, in which you write regarding the continuation of the construction of the Talmud Torah, etc., and that I had supposedly agreed at the time to finance its completion under certain conditions, etc.

I must ask your forgiveness and state that while I do recall the general meeting [564] with the council member from Kiryat Ono when he was here, due to the passage of time I do not recall any such promise or the conditions mentioned. On the other hand, because of the passage of time, I cannot be entirely certain about the matter. Seemingly, this is puzzling, as I generally do not have funds at my disposal for the stated purpose. In any event, I do not have absolute certainty to deny it.

However, since that conversation, a great deal of time has passed, and the resources at my disposal are tied up in projects that have already begun and cannot be delayed now. Furthermore, these resources are not sufficient at all, and we are currently working to raise additional funds to cover the deficit. Therefore, at this time, there does not appear to be any possibility of entering into other commitments.

This is especially true given that, most recently, a Chabad settlement was established—Nachalat Har Chabad [565] near Kiryat Malachi—and construction has begun on a second Kfar Chabad [566] near the first Kfar Chabad. This construction will continue for some time and will require significant resources, even though a large portion of them will certainly come from various budgets of the appropriate institutions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

I ask for your forgiveness that, in accordance with the above, I am unable to fulfill your request to commit to financing, etc. I have a strong hope that you will judge me favorably, including before your colleagues, may they live. After all, the instruction [567] of our Sages of blessed memory to judge others favorably also provides [568] strength. In particular, I am sure you will judge me favorably in the eyes of Mr. [569] Yaakov Cohen, may he live. My heartfelt thanks in advance.

With respect, with regards to your colleagues, may they live, and with blessings for a Kosher and Happy Pesach.

## 9716

[9716](#_ftn_579)

[B"H](#_ftn_580), 26 Nissan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Moshe ben Nachum, may he live,
Center for the Conference for the Sake of Shabbos, P.O. Box 9, Tel Aviv

Shalom u’vracha!

In the name of the Rebbe, shlita, we hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter regarding the Second National Conference for the Sake of Shabbos, which is scheduled to take place on the upcoming 23rd–24th of Iyar.

The blessing of the Rebbe, shlita, is extended to the organizers and all the participants, that the will of Hashem shall succeed in their hands to strengthen the observance of Shabbos—which is necessary and vital in every place, and with even greater intensity and strength in our Holy Land, upon which [always](#_ftn_581) the eyes of Hashem your G-d are, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.

It is certainly unnecessary to elaborate on the immense importance of Shabbos observance, which is equal to all the mitzvos, [as stated](#_ftn_582) by our Sages, of blessed memory. We also see tangibly that the power of Shabbos Kodesh is great enough to draw from its holiness into the lives of Jewish men and women throughout the weekdays that follow, so that these weekdays, too, become holy.

And if what has been said applies with full force in all eras, how much more so in these days, when all Bnei Yisrael, wherever they may be, are in need of an additional blessing from Hashem, the Guardian of Israel. For there is a special quality to the mitzvah of Shabbos, [as interpreted](#_ftn_583) by our Sages, of blessed memory, that Shabbos "causes harm to cease from the world." And although this is said regarding the general Shabbos of the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, it is also understood from this that a source and a microcosm of this exists in every single Shabbos.

From this, there is also an answer to those who are mistaken—or, at the very least, are misleading others—by saying that Shabbos observance is merely a private matter for each individual, and that one should not intervene, strive, or involve oneself in this, and so on. As is known, the analogy regarding every matter of Torah and mitzvos is that an undesirable act by a Jewish man or woman, even if it is in their private lives, is like a group of people sailing in a ship tossed upon a sea of raging waters, where the sea is growing ever more turbulent. Anyone who bores a hole in his own cabin—in what is "his" in the ship—endangers the many. The analogy is understood.

May it be the will that very soon we shall see and merit, [in the phrasing](#_ftn_584) of our Sages, of blessed memory, that if Yisrael would observe Shabbos as it should be observed, they would be redeemed immediately.

With respect and blessing,

In the name of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 978

[978](#_ftn_585)

[B"H](#_ftn_586), 3 Iyar, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of action, etc.,

Rabbi Shmuel Tuvia [Stern](#_ftn_587)

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 14th of the month. Although I had hoped that a summary of the [transcript](#_ftn_588) of the remarks from Acharon Shel Pesach regarding the abandonment of Jewish neighborhoods would appear [in "HaPardes"](#_ftn_589), I desired to fulfill your request, and a copy is enclosed herewith (incidentally, it also includes the places in the Shulchan Aruch regarding which you write at the end of your letter).

For understandable reasons, expressions befitting the strange, distressing, and alarming conduct of selling homes in these neighborhoods in order to move to other neighborhoods were not included in the transcript. There is an additional reason for this: my strong hope that the rabbis of the United States—the **authorities of Jewish law** in Israel, who are obligated to stand in the breach in all matters concerning our brethren, the Children of Israel, and all the more so in this most important matter mentioned—will issue a powerful call commensurate with the magnitude of the issue, with great publicity, based on what is said, "Do not fear any man," and the merit of the many will assist them.

Another point that I mentioned briefly during the farbrengen, and which I omitted from the transcript for understandable reasons, is that those who flee from the neighborhoods to other neighborhoods—a flight that is contrary to the law—bring with them, Heaven forbid, the very "conditions" from which they are fleeing. That is to say, they pose a danger to the new neighborhood at the time of their relocation and even afterward, for they are a living example, a reminder, etc., of every Jewish person who is in that place contrary to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of truth, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient. As I have noted several times, in Hashem’s compassion upon this orphaned generation, the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, we see many matters of Torah openly even through the ways of nature. The same applies in the present case: even by way of nature, when a non-Jew walks down the street and encounters the aforementioned Jew—a new face in this neighborhood—and asks where he came from and why he moved from his previous residence, etc., and they tell him the story, this teaches him to try to do, Heaven forbid, as the enemies of Israel who drove this Jew from his previous place, etc., etc.

It is wondrous that precisely in the affluent countries, where the Children of Israel should seemingly be more firm in their position and not be impressed by, etc.—even [though](#_ftn_591) you are the fewest of all peoples—the feeling of demoralization before a "small nation" is great, and all the more so when it is not a small one, to the point of self-nullification. One of the expressions of this alarming inferiority complex is the aforementioned phenomenon of flight, in addition to the striving (in the style of the verse) to "be like all the nations," and even to the alarming phenomenon highlighted [in the style of](#_ftn_593) our Sages of blessed memory in a few words: they **enjoyed** the feast of that **wicked one** (the pleasure that the **wicked one** invites them to his feast). From here, too, comes the strange phenomenon in the U.S. that any party where someone who is not Jewish is not seated at the head table is not a party worthy of the name; all the more so if it is a party for the distribution of honorary titles, it is understood and simple who receives the first honorary title, etc. And there is no need to dwell on this distressing matter.

May it be the will of Hashem that, as we find ourselves in the days between the time of our freedom and the receiving of the Torah, each of us, within the entirety of the Jewish people, will succeed in freeing ourselves from exile and the yoke of exile in our inner lives [for it is obvious that I do not mean, Heaven forbid, against the [statement](#_ftn_594) of our Sages of blessed memory not to "climb the wall," nor even to [provoke](#_ftn_595) a "small nation," but this has no connection whatsoever to all the aforementioned phenomena]; and to increase every single day in the yearning for the receiving of the Torah and its mitzvos, as is recounted in the Aggadah (Ran, end of Pesachim) in connection with the mitzvah of Sefiras HaOmer.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in general, and also regarding the above, that you may utilize all your influence wherever your hand can reach to define the aforementioned breach and even to nullify it, and may you succeed.

## 9784

[9784](#_ftn_613)

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

And with a blessing for success in your work for the benefit of the daughters of Yisroel, may they live.

## 9289

[9289](#_ftn_631)

[B"H](#_ftn_632), during the days of Sefirah, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Fourteenth Annual Convention
of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and Peace!

Since the annual convention is taking place this year during the days of Erev Rosh Chodesh and Rosh Chodesh Sivan, it is appropriate to reflect on the significance of Rosh Chodesh in general, and Rosh Chodesh Sivan in particular, in relation to the Jewish woman. In certain respects, Rosh Chodesh has a special significance for women even more than for men, which is why there are specific [Rosh Chodesh](#_ftn_633) customs for women alone.

Rosh Chodesh [Sivan](#_ftn_634), the day the Jews arrived at Mount Sinai, reminds us of and emphasizes in a striking manner the special spiritual qualities of Jewish women, as well as their unique merit in connection with Kabbalas HaTorah, and immediately thereafter, in connection with the first test following Matan Torah.

[As](#_ftn_635) our Sages of blessed memory emphasize, the Ribono shel Olam instructed Moshe Rabbeinu to speak about Kabbalas HaTorah first to the women and then to the men. This highlighted that women have a special responsibility for the maintenance of Torah and mitzvos, and this sense of responsibility was clearly expressed during the first test after Matan Torah, when the women stood firm completely and categorically refused any connection with it, even indirectly by giving any of their gold jewelry. Therefore, the women merited that Rosh Chodesh brings them a special reward in this world and a special reward in Olam HaBa, as is recounted in [Pirkei](#_ftn_636) D'Rabbi Eliezer (Chapter 45). Conversely, when it later came to [building](#_ftn_637) the Mishkan, the women were again the first to give of their most precious jewelry for the Mishkan.

Thus, both in the realm of **sur meira**—turning away from evil—and in the realm of **aseh tov**—doing good—Jewish women have distinguished themselves with their readiness and self-sacrifice. So too, in all times, it is expected of women that they be the first and provide a model for the men, which also means that the Ribono shel Olam has endowed them with special strengths and qualities to fulfill these expectations.

The auspicious time of the convention, which is connected with the Rosh Chodesh of Kabbalas HaTorah, will therefore certainly evoke and strengthen the appropriate mood. For the entire Torah is divided into these two mentioned traits: **sur meira** and **aseh tov**, which is also the content of the first of the Aseres HaDibros—**Anochi** and **Lo Yihyeh Lecha**—which the Jews heard [mipii](#_ftn_640) HaGevurah (directly from G-d).

Therefore, it is to be hoped that each and every participant will be encouraged through the convention to strengthen their activity to spread Yiddishkeit with Chassidic vitality and warmth, within the framework of the program of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, in an ever-increasing manner.

With blessings for success in both spiritual and material matters, and for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9792

[9792](#_ftn_646)

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual event of the N.Y. Committee for the Seminary for Teachers and Girls' Schools in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,

Therefore, it is understood that in order to fulfill this special task, the education of Jewish daughters must begin from the earliest youth. If this was necessary in all times, this necessity is even more serious and urgent in our time, when harmful winds and undesirable influences are raging outside.

This underscores even more the importance of the work of the N.Y. Committee for the Seminary for Teachers and the girls' schools in Kfar Chabad, in our Holy Land, may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu; and this work must be continued with increased and strengthened efforts, in order to enable these educational institutions *al taharas hakodesh* to continue their educational work in an ever-increasing measure.

## 9793

[9793](#_ftn_649)

[B"H](#_ftn_650), 2 Sivan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner
for the educational institution "Oholei Torah,"
May Hashem preserve them and may they live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the upcoming annual event of the educational institution "Oholei Torah" during this month of Kabbalas HaTorah. May Hashem Yisbarach grant that the event be a great success in all respects.

Since everything occurs through Hashgacha Pratis, it is of special significance that this letter is written on the second day of the month of Sivan. The Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, reminds us in his Shulchan Aruch (Orach Chaim, end of siman 494) that on this day, Hashem said to the Jewish people through Moshe Rabbeinu: **"And you shall be to Me a kingdom of priests, etc."** — "You shall be to Me a kingdom of priests (and a holy nation)." This means that although Jews are divided into Kohanim, Leviim, and Yisraelim—which is relevant to certain laws and mitzvos, etc.—in a general sense, the entire Jewish people are on a level of Kohanim, where every Jew has the obligation and the merit to spread kedushah, Torah, and mitzvos in their surroundings.

It is understood that the preparation to reach this level of "a kingdom of priests and a holy nation" must begin from the earliest youth. This brings us to the importance of chinuch al taharas hakodesh, as it is carried out in practice at the educational institution "Oholei Torah."

In these days of preparation for the Yom Tov of Kabbalas HaTorah, and in the spirit of Zman Matan Toraseinu, it is to be hoped that everyone will come to the aid of the "Oholei Torah" institution with a special hisorerus and significant support, to help maintain and expand this institution of chinuch al taharas hakodesh. Thereby, one will also expand the channels to receive Hashem’s blessings in abundance, for each person and their household, may they live, with all that they need, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing for success and for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9797

[9797](#_ftn_663)

B”H, 12 Sivan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. [664](#_ftn_664) Shneur Zalman Maschari, may he live

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge with many thanks the receipt of your letter dated 25 Iyar, along with the enclosure.

It is understood that the idea regarding the creation of employment is very correct—an excellent idea. And naturally, you are correct that the matter depends on whether one can find Chabad people who are free, at least to a significant degree, from other communal activities, etc.

Therefore, first and foremost, the situation regarding this problem must be clarified. This is generally difficult, as there is a great shortage of manpower, especially in this most recent period, which requires special attention from Chabad people in connection with the needs of the immigrants (the newest ones; a hint is sufficient for the wise).

Despite all this, it is understood that in accordance with the great importance of the idea, one must take an interest and reflect upon it. My hope is strong that you will continue to show activity in this direction and the like, and with even greater intensity. Many thanks, many thanks for the past and for the future.

In response to your question regarding this, my suggestion—and this is what I am [writing](#_ftn_665) to anash, may they live, regarding this—is that they should all consult together. It is understood that this should be done confidentially, and therefore with a limited number of participants, for obvious reasons. Then they should discuss the aforementioned problem in detail, and the merit of the many will assist them in a good discussion and clarification.

With respect and with a blessing for success in good health and for good tidings—also in personal matters.

## 9898

[9898](#_ftn_666)

By the Grace of Hashem, 19 Sivan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

[Mrs.](#_ftn_667) Geula Cohen, may she live

Blessings and Peace!

Some time ago I received your letter, and due to circumstances beyond my control, the response has been delayed until now.

We begin with a positive note: I derived special satisfaction from the news regarding the Torah study shiur conducted by Rabbi Chefer, may he live, and so on. It is my hope that it continues even now, despite recent events—or perhaps one should say, on the contrary: precisely because of recent events, one must increase this shiur and others like it. A shiur in our Torah (which is a *hora’ah*—a lesson/instruction) is both a Torah of truth and a Torah of life—a guide for life, as has been discussed many times regarding this matter.

Indeed, the Jewish woman has a special role in this, as is emphasized in this month of the Giving of the Torah, based on what is [related](#_ftn_669) by our Sages, of blessed memory: that before the Giving of the Torah and the acceptance of the Torah, the Ribono shel Olam told Moshe to speak first to the women regarding the acceptance of the Torah, and only afterwards to the men. As with all the narratives of our Sages, this too contains a lesson for every Jewish man and woman, in every place and at every time—a lesson from our eternal Torah for the eternal Jewish people.

I am (somewhat) surprised by your wonderment as to why several circles, myself included, have not accepted, do not accept, and do not use the title "Medinat Yisrael" (State of Israel). The reason is understood and simple: The Land of Canaan was given as an inheritance to the Jewish people beginning with the Covenant Between the Parts with Avraham Avinu. In place of the name "Land of Canaan," the name **Eretz Yisrael** was **established**—an establishment spanning several thousand years, established in the Torah, and established on the lips of the people, from the smallest to the greatest. Matters such as these are not subject to a vote or a majority decision—a decision that is liable to change from time to time, a change whose form, by nature, cannot be known. After all the various and strange events that have occurred recently—strange for the good, but unfortunately, there are also strange ones to the contrary—one cannot be certain at all regarding the stability of this name change either. But in truth, there is no need for this concern about not accepting the new title, since, as mentioned, in my opinion, this is not a matter subject to a vote, just as it is not subject to a vote what the Jewish people should be called—whether as they are called in the Torah, "Am Yisrael," or "Canaan," etc. The same applies to Eretz Yisrael.

And if you wish to add another point: **if** one were to require further reasoning, this name change weakens the claim and ownership of the Jewish people over Eretz Yisrael, including even the limited territory that was liberated in 5748. This is because: a) A new name gives the entire matter the character of a novelty that began in 5748; consequently, the claim and ownership over Eretz Yisrael also begins then—or at the very least, it possesses some sort of novelty, which is the opposite of the Torah’s position. As Rashi states at the beginning of his commentary on the Torah—

And I emphasize this, for it is the custom of our people for generations that a [child](#_ftn_671) of five begins with Scripture—meaning that Rashi’s words are directed to the children of Israel starting from the age of five—

That if the nations of the world say to Israel, "You are robbers, for you conquered the lands of the seven nations," the children of Israel shall answer: "The entire land belongs to the Ribono shel Olam; He created it and gave it to whom He saw fit, and by His will, He took it from them and gave it to us."

And surely you are aware that this was indeed the argument of many of the nations of the world in our own time as well, and I have found no other answer than the most ancient, traditional response found in the words of our Sages mentioned above.

b) Some interpret the aforementioned title "Medinat Yisrael" as part of a general approach and plan to [be](#_ftn_672) like the nations, like the families of the lands—a plan which, [in the language of the verse](#_ftn_673), has caused many casualties, casualties in body and also in soul in the spiritual sense, and to our sorrow and our sins, it is still wreaking havoc among the sons and daughters of Israel.

I have an additional wonderment when such a question comes from you, for until now I have stated clearly that you are counted among those who say that Eretz Yisrael belongs to the Jewish people, and that its borders are specified in the Torah in detail [(in Parshas](#_ftn_674) Masei), as it is written: **This** shall be **your** land **according to its borders** round about, etc. It is only [that because](#_ftn_675) of our sins we were exiled from our land and distanced from our soil, but even during the time of exile, it is our land and our soil. The aforementioned title (Medinat Yisrael) provides room to speak regarding parts of Eretz Yisrael as being merely territories **conquered** by the IDF in the Six-Day War. And the entire concept of "conquest" implies taking by force from the hands of the owners through "[my](#_ftn_676) strength and the might of my hand."

I do not wish to dwell at length on this painful subject, and primarily on the general cause for all of the above—my intention being the approach of [being](#_ftn_677) like all the nations. Surely there is no need for lengthiness on my part, as you are undoubtedly reading about this in the newspapers and books appearing in the Land of Canaan (according to the perspective of the authors of the aforementioned articles and books, though some state this openly, while others hint that this is their intent).

And last but not least, I offer my thanks for the satisfaction caused to me by your raising the [issue](#_ftn_678) of increasing the birth rate in our Holy Land (and in all the Jewish Diaspora). It is my hope that you will not be content with discussing this once or twice on the pages of the press, but will continue to do so in appropriate ways and with even greater intensity.

May it be Hashem's will that you bring good tidings regarding all that has been written, and also regarding your personal matters which were discussed during your visit here.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Enclosed is a copy of my [general letter](#_ftn_679) to the annual meeting of the women's organization here, which also contains relevance to what was written above.

***

[It is not](#_ftn_680) clear to me what the reaction of Mr. [Name], may he live, will be to the following, but I said that in any case, it is better that he receive a copy of my letter directly from me than for it to reach him indirectly, and perhaps even in a distorted manner.

With appreciation, respect, and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9,399 

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with energy, etc., [Rabbi B.A.] may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following our conversation here prior to your departure on Thursday with Mr. Heller, may he live, who spoke in detail regarding his proposal: from the details provided, it appears that your concerns—that perhaps the business is not profitable, etc.—are unfounded, given that Barclays Bank in England has invested a large sum in it, etc.

He also added that the participation of the ministries in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, is relevant, and they should also cover the expenses of relocating the other branches to Kiryat Malachi; that is to say, this is not a matter of income for him. Furthermore, it is not necessarily required that they relocate all the branches at once; if for any reason they wish to do so, they can proceed step by step.

He further added that it is true that there are several factories of this type in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, but they are incomparably smaller than their factory, which supplies approximately sixty percent or more of all that is needed in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

He elaborated further on this, and his words ring true. However, there is no need to transcribe them here, as the transcript of his deliberations with the various ministries is in the possession of the esteemed Chossid, etc., R. A. Wolf, may he live, from which you will see the accuracy of all the above.

The intent of my letter is twofold: First, it seems there is some conflict between one ministry and another, and consequently, the entire matter is suffering, and a word to the wise is sufficient. Therefore, it is worthwhile to investigate all of this once more, especially since if they continue to engage Mr. Heller in Chabad matters, one can hope for benefit in other areas as well. Furthermore—and this is the main point—although he has already returned to London this past Shabbos Kodesh, he said that if there is any benefit in him visiting Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, you should telephone him from Eretz Yisrael, and he will come immediately. His telephone number, etc., is with R. A. Wolf.

It is understood from the above why I am sending this letter as a rapid, urgent dispatch, especially since, according to information here, Mr. Nathan Vogel, a friend of the aforementioned, is currently in Eretz Yisrael.

The [monthly] payment from the Joint has been received.

With blessings for success and for good news regarding the above, as well as in all other matters.

## 989

[989](#_ftn_684)

B”H, 24 Sivan, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. [Shifra](#_ftn_685) Yehudis, may she live, Morozov

[Blessings and Peace]!

I read your letter with great astonishment and sorrow. In it, you write about the lack of coordination among those participating in the holy activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad (Tzach) in general, and specifically regarding the *mivtza* for widows and orphans, may they live. Because of this, you suggest that you will reduce your participation in these activities, or, in your words, cease your involvement.

It is simple that there is no place for this at all. When a matter is in a state of disorder, one must strive to correct it as thoroughly as possible—or at the very least, to the extent that is possible—but certainly not, G-d forbid, to destroy it. If this is true for any matter, it is all the more so regarding a matter that concerns the many, especially when those "many" are widows and orphans, etc. To elaborate on such a simple point would be superfluous.

The conclusion to be drawn from the aforementioned situation is, on the contrary, that you must increase your activity. Do not be deterred by the difficulties; rather, strive to find ways to overcome them, and do so in ways of pleasantness and peace. [As it has already](#_ftn_686) been said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

Regarding your writing that there are people with whom it is pleasant to work and others with whom it is not: I do not suspect you at all of allowing unpleasant interpersonal relations to lead to a loss of activity on your part. What I do suspect is that someone else is inciting you and exploiting you for the sake of a dispute they have with so-and-so. If there is any basis for this fear, then that itself is proof that you must continue your activity and increase it. For anyone who strives to increase strife in Israel and cause a division of hearts, etc., is acting contrary to the approach of Chabad in particular, and the approach of our Torah—whose [ways](#_ftn_687) are ways of pleasantness and peace—in general.

Regarding your writing about the lack of order in [sending](#_ftn_688) invitations, etc.: this is a technical matter, and at most it involves minor expenses, which you will surely be able to resolve among yourselves. If there remains any detail that cannot be clarified, perhaps it would be worthwhile for you to write it down formally, with the addition that a copy is being sent to me.

I would add one more thing, though I do not know if it is entirely relevant to our matter: every single Jew has virtues and shortcomings, for there is none perfect but the Holy One, Blessed be He. Therefore, everyone has a role for which they are uniquely suited, and a role for which they are not suited at all; and for another person, the opposite is true—they are not suited for the first role but are uniquely suited for the second. Thus, when two people must work together, it is understood that the collaboration succeeds when the first person handles the first role and the second person handles the second, not when one enters the domain of the other. This is especially true regarding the management of a multifaceted operation like the administration of Tzach. It is possible that someone is capable of broad initiative, great vision, and possesses great energy; such a person should be utilized for matters requiring those specific traits. Someone who is organized, consistent, and possesses a sense of calculation—whose estimation regarding income, expenses, and the public’s reaction is more realistic and practical—belongs in the management of the general affairs. It is understood what the results will be when expenses are disproportionate to income and debts continue to grow; this is liable to damage the entire matter, the general affairs, and even the entirety of Chabad’s work.

I do not wish to dwell on this, as, mentioned above, it does not touch upon this matter at all. In any event, you must continue the holy task you have taken upon yourself: to encourage the hearts of widows and orphans with Chassidic vitality and light, and to continue in a manner of increasing from time to time—and you have indeed succeeded in this. As you increase your activity, Hashem will increase your success. As for the difficulties, unpleasantness, etc., a large part of them stem from incitement and from those who wish to increase strife. Regarding the remainder, one must certainly overcome it, or at the very least, most of it. If something remains unorganized, we are already accustomed to the fact that every good and holy matter is associated with difficulties, unpleasantness, and so on.

I am sending this letter as urgent, so that you may proceed with increasing your activities, and do so with joy and vitality. May the Almighty grant you success.

With blessings.

## 9 Tisa

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5729
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter containing a request for a blessing, along with the *pidyon nefesh* dated 6/5.

At an opportune time, it will be read at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize the necessity of strengthening one’s daily conduct so that it aligns with the instructions of our Torah—the Torah of life—and the fulfillment of its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and live by them." Beyond the fundamental fact that this is the command of the *Ribono shel Olam*, this is also the path to receiving the blessings that a person requires.

It is appropriate to have the *tefillin* of your husband and your son—may they live—checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, provided they have not been checked in the last twelve months, to ensure they are all *kasher* according to *halacha*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

Regarding your son—may he live—the doctors are obviously correct in opposing surgery. It should be treated through an appropriate diet.

If moving to another location would make it easier to maintain the diet and so on, it is worthwhile to move, and *Hashem* will grant success.

## 9702 

[B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, the Month of Redemption, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch for the Siyum celebration, Montreal

May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the Siyum celebration to be held on Wednesday, the eve of 3 Tammuz, in a good and auspicious time.

And it is surely known to you that this day is the beginning of the liberation and redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, from his imprisonment when he was seized during his activities of literal mesiras nefesh—for the dissemination of Torah study and the fulfillment of mitzvos in that land of decree. Through the mercies of Hashem, he emerged to freedom in complete victory, and its results continue to this very day.

And in anticipation of these auspicious days, the days of redemption that are approaching—which are "remembered and observed" year after year—

And the explanation of the Arizal regarding "And these days are remembered and observed" is well known: that at the turn of the year, all the matters of holiness and spiritual potency of those days are renewed, provided that they are remembered and observed as they ought to be—

I express my blessing to all the students who are completing [their studies], that from a place of **expansion** and from joy and goodness of heart, you may merit a great measure of the **inner** dimension of mesiras nefesh, which is the **surrender of the will**, as explained in many places in the words of the living G-d. And may the blessing of the Baal HaGeulah be fulfilled in you:

"May the Almighty bring a fresh strength into the eternal strengthening of Yiddishkeit, and it will be fulfilled that 'Hashem our G-d be with us, as He was with our forefathers; may He not forsake us and may He not abandon us', and 'for all the Children of Israel there shall be light' in both spirituality and physicality."

And may each and every one of those completing their studies, together with all the students of the Yeshiva, fulfill their role according to the hopes of the Baal HaGeulah, the founder of the Yeshiva—fulfilling their role in its entirety, going from strength to strength in the light of Torah and the lamp of mitzvah, with hiddur and Chassidic vitality, to the glory of the parents, the Roshei Yeshiva, the administrators, and the educators, may they live.

With blessings for outstanding success and for good tidings—in all that was mentioned, in both physicality and spirituality alike,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9758 

 B"H, 1 Tammuz, the Month of Redemption, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the venerable Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter in which you write regarding the question of the old and new synagogues, etc., in Kfar Chabad, and the differences of opinion concerning their expansion, etc.

In general, my opinion is **well-known**: that **all** matters concerning Kfar Chabad must be expanded, naturally and simply, without causing any detriment to matters of holiness and goodness. And it is certainly possible to fulfill this condition.

It is also understood that the aforementioned expansion is connected to financial expenditures, which necessitates taking into account the financial resources available in cash, or at the very least, promises that are close to cash.

Furthermore, I would add that if the financial means currently at your disposal do not permit the buildings to be expanded as much as is desired, the expansion and construction now must be carried out in such a way that when Hashem broadens your borders and you wish to expand further, it will involve minimal additional expense. That is to say, the current expansion should be designed to ensure that further expansion—and an increase far greater than the original—can be achieved with the greatest possible ease.

The details of all the above must be clarified on-site, as is obvious and simple.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon you will emerge from the straits, boundaries, and limitations—which, although they are partly external, it is apparent that at least part of them is simply due to a lack of true dedication, a true dedication that Kfar Chabad, even though it is called a "village" (kfar), is a center from which the dissemination of the wellsprings goes forth throughout the entire Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, to the point of "spreading out." This point must **permeate** all affairs of Kfar Chabad, and by way of this, the causes for the division of hearts, etc., will also be nullified. You will fulfill the complete verse, "Open wide your mouth"—and then it will be fulfilled—"and I will fill it." (One should also note the notation of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek on this verse).

 "Merit is brought about on a meritorious day," as this letter is written on Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, the Month of Redemption—the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Israel.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I have just received a letter from the Regional Rabbinical Court of Rehovot regarding the matter... I was extremely astonished by its content, as if the conflict between them is solely regarding Chabad customs, when in fact, over the course of time, that was not the version they wrote to me.

Since there has been a discussion with your honor previously, and several times, and surely you will now consult... with him, enclosed is a copy of my letter to the aforementioned Rabbinical Court... and you will surely inform me of the resolution and the continuation of these matters.

## 980

[980](#_ftn_715)

By the Grace of G-d, 3 Tammuz, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and Peace!

Although I do not know you personally, since I have heard much about you from your husband, Mr. [Name], I take the liberty of addressing you in these lines, and I hope you will not mind.

Following our connection through correspondence, it was a pleasure for me to get to know your husband personally during his relatively long visit here. Based on our conversations on several occasions, in which he shared the main chapters of his life story, I was happy to see that he has found inner tranquility through his connection—even more so—to a worldview stemming from our Torah, the Torah of life, the Torah of truth; a tranquility that borders on and leads to inner happiness, spiritual happiness.

And surely this aforementioned closeness, the results of which are tranquility, harmony, and happiness, is possible with the help of the "help-mate" [as the](#_ftn_716) verse puts it—namely, the wife. This is an opinion that was confirmed for me by your husband’s account regarding the help he found in you and your support in general, and specifically in the aforementioned matters.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the necessity of inner tranquility and harmony for a person’s life to be worthy of the name, especially in our current era, which is full of upheavals in the life of the community and the public, as well as in the life of the individual.

Therefore, my hope is strong that, just as in the past, so too in the future, you will stand at your husband’s right hand in this aforementioned closeness and progress, for like any living thing, this closeness will surely grow and advance. My intention is that both of you together will go and ascend in life according to our Torah, the Torah of life.

Regarding all this, I felt there was room to write about it explicitly—a writing intended to express hope, together with encouragement and strengthening. For sometimes, a person encounters difficulties and the like on his path of progress. This is especially true (according to what our Sages of blessed memory taught) when one encounters people who have not yet reached the aforementioned state and who try to bolster themselves in their own eyes and in the eyes of others by mocking and belittling those who have advanced further than them and reached a higher level in their worldview—our Torah and our faith. Yet, how much our Sages of blessed memory [warned](#_ftn_717) against feeling ashamed before mockers, knowing the nature of man, that this is no easy trial.

I also intend to address a specific detail, and that is regarding the [growing](#_ftn_718) of a beard, which was seen in your husband during his stay here—that he began to grow a beard. This is, [in the language](#_ftn_719) of our Sages of blessed memory, "the garment of the Holy One, blessed be He," and it bestows upon a Jewish man the [image](#_ftn_720) of G-d, as is recounted in several Midrashim. This was something that was not easy for your husband while he was here (primarily for the reason mentioned above, because of the mockers), and yet, without any outside influence, he began this. It seems that this, too, added to the establishment of his inner tranquility and the recognition that he stands on a strong foundation of Torah and mitzvos. This is one of the main purposes of my letter: to ask you and express my hope that you will also assist him in this and encourage him to continue in the future, and to do so with joy and tranquility.

It is understood that I am aware that there are many among the Jewish people who observe Torah and mitzvos but do not grow a beard, as the differences of [opinion](#_ftn_721) and the various approaches among the *poskim* are well-known. However, the matter at hand is not only from the point of view of the *halachic* ruling, but primarily from the results in the life of the individual in question—results that are not only satisfying, but **much** more than that. The matter of growing a beard has joined the other positive phenomena in his life over the past few years, including your attitude, etc.—to add light and life to his life, which will surely and certainly add to your life as well.

It is understood that there is no comparison between this achievement and this ascent in life and the mockery of a few in the environment, which, as mentioned, is essentially the mocker’s way of justifying himself regarding a matter that his conscience troubles him about from time to time; the easy way is to belittle those who, even in his own estimation, are superior to him. Surely there is no need to elaborate on this.

I will add just one more point, which in this context is also essential: a quote of the words of [our Rebbe](#_ftn_722), the *Tzemach Tzedek*, that growing a beard is a special *segulah* to draw down G-d’s blessing in abundance, both in quantity and in quality. From this, it is understood that anyone in need of an additional blessing from G-d—whether in matters of health, finances, and certainly in spiritual matters—must hold onto this progress more and more. Especially since in all such matters, we are [promised](#_ftn_723) that one who comes to purify himself is assisted from Above with great assistance.

May it be the will that your property matters—the house, etc.—also be settled in a satisfactory manner, and may you be blessed by Hashem, may He be blessed, with everything you need in both spiritual and material matters. May you bring good tidings regarding all the matters discussed.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9707

9707

By the Grace of G-d
3 Tammuz, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Dr. S. Stern-Mirz, may she live and be well
HaTishbi 91
Haifa-Carmel

Blessings and peace!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated June 3rd, in which you write regarding Mrs. . . . and your opinion that it would be for her benefit and for the benefit of her entire family if they were to move from their current location to Kiryat Gat or Jerusalem.

You are surely aware of the great difficulties involved in obtaining approval for the transfer of teachers to a central location, including those mentioned above, where there is a great surplus of teachers relative to the demand. Even if they were to succeed in obtaining approval for one of them—namely, the husband—the chances are extremely slim that at the same time they would approve employment in the field of education for the wife as well. For, in general, the Ministry of Education is not satisfied when a husband and wife work together in the same field and institution. Furthermore, based on my impression from the letters of . . . and also based on my conversation with her during her visit here, the fact that she brings benefit through her work in the field of education and guidance encourages her greatly and adds to her self-confidence and peace of mind—that is to say, to her health.

Furthermore, and perhaps this is also important, the public activity of . . . in her current location is easier, since there are only a few competitors in this regard in . . . and the like. On the other hand, the demand is much greater there than in Kiryat Gat, and certainly more so than in Jerusalem. And this activity is also an important component in the mental state of . . . and her tranquility.

Notwithstanding all this, since you see her now, if, even after receiving this letter, you come to the decision that it is worth pursuing the aforementioned transfer, I will turn to the activists in our school network and ask them to clarify the possibilities for the aforementioned transfer and to act accordingly.

I take this opportunity to add one more point, even though it is in your professional field: the course of events regarding the state of health of . . . proves (if proof is needed in this matter) the magnitude of the power of faith—especially when it is connected to and expressed in actual deed, public activity, the fulfillment of mitzvos, and so on—in establishing a person’s peace of mind, in diminishing and sometimes even nullifying internal conflicts, as well as the "grievances" one has toward their environment, and so on. This is despite the theory that faith and religion require a person to accept a yoke to restrain and suppress instincts and drives, and therefore it is not desirable in general, and especially in the case of a personality in need of nervous treatment and the like.

I have taken a special interest in the articles of Dr. Frankl (Vienna) on this subject, but to my surprise, it seems his method has not been disseminated and accepted as much as is required. And although several reasons can be found for this phenomenon—that his method is not so widely accepted—including the fact that it is connected with the living example of the treating physician, nevertheless, the question still stands.

With respect and with the blessing that you should succeed in your profession to heal the sick and bring them to healthy lives, lives worthy of the name.

## 9,615 

 B”H, the day after the days of redemption,
12-13 Tammuz, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

As we come from the days of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of our generation—which is also the redemption of each and every one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael—

Behold, the essence and content of every redemption is that it comes **after** imprisonment and exile. Moreover, it comes **from within** imprisonment and exile, in the language of Chazal regarding this and similar matters: "From within darkness, light." And Chazal have said, "Everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good." And there is a third point, which surpasses them all—that the **darkness itself** is transformed into light, and in the style of Chazal: "This, too, is for the good."

Our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, explained that this is the order of conduct: Chesed, Din, Rachamim. Therefore, after an event or occurrence of Din, the attribute of Rachamim is awakened, which is greater than the attribute of Chesed that preceded it, as is known—for it is the attribute of Yaakov, an inheritance without boundaries.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that, amidst expansion in both the physical and the spiritual, each person will contemplate how every created being is limited, and how his soul—which is a literal "part of Elokus from above"—is [found] in the imprisonment of a body of flesh and blood, and in a state of exile within it, etc. Therefore, he should set all his focus and desire to extract it and elevate it from this exile—through teshuvah and good deeds.

He should not listen to his yetzer at all; on the contrary, he should "provoke the good inclination against the evil inclination" and force his yetzer, until he reaches the service of Hashem and the love of Him "with all your heart"—with both your inclinations.

And when there is *iskafya* of the *sitra achra* and the transformation of darkness into light—one connects redemption to redemption: the redemption of his own soul to the redemption of the collective.

Thus, we hasten the true and complete general redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, when "the night will shine like the day," and "Hashem will be for you an everlasting light."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

 As I have seen—the discussion **here** with [the person] and the like regarding matters of [the organization], (including—Bnei Brak), is not only lacking in "feeling/understanding," but they do not even have the simple ability to hear. And since one is busy emitting, one does not absorb, and it does not even touch him.

## 9,856

12-13 Tammuz, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and elevated individual, who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, [Mr. Schneur Zalman] shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

This time, I will begin with the essence of the matter:

It was with the greatest astonishment (mingled with deep pain) that I read your letter. Beyond the content itself—which consists of claims **etc.** [in the style of] Satmar against me: "Why have you (meaning me) attached yourself to Eretz Yisrael, to Eretz HaKodesh, and to the Covenant Between the Parts, etc., and why do you involve the Ribono shel Olam, etc., etc.?"—the fact is that all those who have labored in this, all those who have stood and currently stand at its helm, and all those who speak in its name, say, emphasize, **and declare** that this is a **"state"** that was **founded** in the year **5708** in those territories that the British abandoned and from which the "Haganah" expelled the Arabs (or entered without resistance), and the representatives of the nations of the world (and the Communists—among those at their head) agreed among themselves to approve it, in a territory that is **partly in Eretz Yisrael and partly outside of Eretz Yisrael.**

Naturally, my response is: Heaven forbid. The aforementioned is not a new matter, etc., but rather that in 5708, they **liberated** an important part of Eretz Yisrael (and, incidentally, **conquered** a certain territory outside of it, which they added as an appendage and secondary to the main thing—Eretz Yisrael).

My words are dismissed with the claim that this is my own innovation. The proof, they say, is that every single year they declare—the year of [so-and-so] (not for liberation, etc., or for the founding of a government, etc., but) for the founding of the "State of Israel." It is clear that this is not a "matter of mere words," but the core and foundation of the entire approach: something founded in 5708 by the will or approval of the United Nations has no validity or substance to answer the claims of the Arabs, the Vatican, the UN, etc., and the Canaanites (both open and hidden) from among the Children of Israel: "You are [robbers](#_ftn_754) for you have conquered lands, etc."

I do not delude myself that they will win over the UN, the Vatican, etc., with arguments of justice and righteousness—but the most important factor is the morale of the youth (including the IDF), the students in the United States (and surely in other countries as well), etc.

And furthermore, and most importantly: The approach that the subject is the "State of Israel, which was founded with the approval of the UN in the year 5708"

(**And not** the Children of Israel **who returned** to Eretz Yisrael, the land of **their inheritance from the time of Yehoshua bin Nun**—an [inheritance](#_ftn_755) **that has no interruption**, even if it was stolen by force)—

An approach that has become a foundation and principle in the worldview of those who determine the position, the discourse, the activity, and the relations with the nations of the world in general and in particular—

Has destroyed and is destroying, has harmed and is harming the vital interests of even the State of Israel (as is known here regarding the United States and the UN, and surely it is the same in other countries), to the point that it has ultimately led to **actual** casualties—and this is what compelled me to step out of my framework and speak about these matters, which others should have been **sounding the alarm** about. And the wise will understand.

Out of my great pain, I have written the above, and I have still only touched the "tip of the staff," without citing facts—not even the "new ones every morning" that happened yesterday (**literally**), and before Shabbos, etc. And why should I cause you pain as well?

I did not anticipate that the above would be so lengthy, but since it is already written, I do not wish to cut it down. I ask for your forgiveness.

Regarding the order of your letter: "Let me be a Chabadnik"—you were a Chabadnik even before I was born. And may it be so, with the help of Hashem, for good and upright things.

The concept of a "state"—if the reference is to Eilat and its surroundings (which are **outside** the conquest of Yehoshua and Ezra) and they grant them independence in relation to Yerushalayim and Eretz Yisrael in general—then "State of Israel" may be called for them.

Regarding Yerushalayim, etc.—the name was already established by the Creator of the world and its Guide: until the conquest of Yehoshua, it was the Land of Canaan, and after that—Eretz Yisrael. And the matter is no longer subject to a vote or a referendum, etc.

It is **simple** that I have no objection to the name "state" even regarding the majority of this territory. On the contrary, **according to Torah**, Eretz Yisrael **includes** both the Temple and the state (as the Sages phrase it in their Mishnah), just as it includes Yehudah and the Galil, etc. But the subject of my letter is the **dispute** that existed between the two names (**and the worldviews**—as mentioned above), "Eretz Yisrael" and "State of Israel," and the victory of the latter (and I add) for the time being (for my hope and confidence is that ultimately the pride of Israel **that is within every** Jew will prevail—and they will declare before the eyes of all the nations that it was a mistake from the outset, and Eretz Yisrael is called by that name and content, etc.).

I did not say this to him yet, etc.—why should I cause him pain to no avail (since I do not see what he can do about it)?

[I wrote regarding this](#_ftn_758)—not to a journalist, but to one who organized Torah study in circles where, by the way of nature, there were no prospects for it (which also, and similar things, arouse the wrath of Satmar against me), who managed (and my hope is that she will continue to manage) a campaign against the plague of abortions **etc.**—and those who opposed these activities suspected that I was one of the causes of her activity, and they hit upon the invention of explaining it by saying that I am opposed to the State of Israel, and the proof is that my terminology is always Eretz Yisrael, and therefore she should not exert herself... regarding Torah study, etc. I feared a weakening in her activity, and therefore I wrote the above to her.

"I swore allegiance to the State of Israel"—it is simple that I know about this. And it is strange that you did not notice that a **long** time before the oath, I asked you not to refuse this appointment, and more than just a simple request—and certainly you know that even then I knew about the swearing-in ceremony, etc. But **I am certain** that when you swore and said "allegiance to the State of Israel," you clearly intended Eretz Yisrael, and more than that—Eretz HaKodesh, and even more than that—[the land](#_ftn_759) upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year.

Chabad discourse must be open-hearted, and one is obligated and permitted to say what is in his heart—and furthermore, I value this as one of the foundations of the friendship between us, [in the style of] the well-known "joy is fixed in my heart from this side," and my pain is that **in his heart** he suspects me of something that is not in me. **On the contrary**—I say and repeat and emphasize that the people dwelling in Zion are dwelling **in Eretz Yisrael**, a special land **the likes of which does not exist**—and it is **not at all** a matter of a state among the states of Syria, Lebanon, Jordan, and Egypt—and I **demand**, and not with "a little excitement" as you wrote, but with great excitement—that the representatives in Washington and the UN declare this and pound on the table—**and the foreigners** in Washington are also of this opinion, but the representatives of Israel answer that they were commanded not to speak in such a style, and certainly not to pound on the table—because they are representatives of a "state" that received permission and approval to be counted among the nations, and therefore they must behave with diplomatic etiquette. And when, twice, the patience of the representative at the UN ran out and he said **a little** of their "praise" in public—then **within 24 hours** a severe reprimand arrived from Yerushalayim: "How could you, etc.," and they forced him to retract it in public. By the way of nature, this and similar things are what encourage the provocations and the saboteurs, etc.—to the point of actual casualties, may Hashem avenge their blood.

And to conclude the letter regarding the letterhead and the page—certainly you will continue to write on the page as you have until now, and you will not withhold the good from me, and the pleasure I have in seeing once again "black on white" that it is you who holds this position. And when my spirit is "good within me," I add—and that at the same time, you are **deeply** pained, no less than I, by the choice of the aforementioned name (and worldview), and you are **awaiting** the day when the Children of Israel too (for it never crossed the minds of the foreigners otherwise) will write and establish the word **Eretz** instead of the word **State**.

This reasoning comes as an addition to the main point—that since I was among those who labored and requested and acted, etc., that you be chosen for this position, and once and twice, and invested trust in you, etc.—it is only right (and a privilege) that your letters to me and to them be written on the stationery of this position.

And as I opened my letter—since you are a man of the people and elevated above the people—continue in this service of yours in speech, in writing, and in action, and the merit of the many will assist you.

With appreciation, honor, and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9717

[9717](#_ftn_761)

[[Telegram](#_ftn_762)**, 23 Tammuz, 5729]**

In *Hilchos Ketanos* by the Rosh, *Hilchos Tefillin*, Siman 15, it is stated that because of the **fulfillment of the mitzvah of tefillin**, "which are placed upon the arm and the head," and their rectification, there will be fulfilled regarding the men of war, **"and he shall tear the arm as well as the crown"** (*Devarim* 33:20).

It is a mitzvah and a privilege to publicize this *halacha* [among the men of war](#_ftn_765) and all their relatives and friends, and [to] all the Children of Israel, may they live and be well, wherever they may be.
