## 9761

[9761](#_ftn_772)

[B"H](#_ftn_773), Erev Shabbos Kodesh Va'eschanan, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter and the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed, which will be read at the holy gravesite. Thank you for the good news.

Regarding what you wrote now, asking for my opinion in connection with "Mivtza Tefillin"—whether there should still be a special effort in this regard, with full force and in all circles—

The effort—using all appropriate methods—to strengthen the observance of the mitzvah of Tefillin and to disseminate it wherever a person, [and you are called "man" (Adam)], can reach,

Even though, naturally, every circle has its own way, all methods and approaches are founded [upon the mountains of] holiness. This is the common denominator among all circles, in the words of our Sages: "I am asleep (but) **my heart** is awake to perform them (the mitzvos), etc., for the Holy One, blessed be He, to redeem me (from exile)." This is especially true of the mitzvah of Tefillin, [to which] the entire Torah is compared.

When the one making the effort speaks words that come from the heart, it is promised that "words that come from the heart enter the heart." And since all the limbs are dependent on the heart, ultimately, it will surely have its effect.

My opinion is clear: the awakening, the request, and the demand regarding "Mivtza Tefillin," which have been discussed for two years and more, remain in full force even now. Indeed, with even greater intensity and strength, for the current situation is such that we require not only that "all the peoples of the earth... shall see [that you are called by the name of Hashem]"—a fear that comes through the mitzvah of Tefillin—but also, according to the content of the well-known *halachah*, as the *Rosh* writes (Hilchos Ketanos, Hilchos Tefillin, 15):

...**Because of the observance of the mitzvah of Tefillin and its proper fulfillment, the men of war will be sustained, and the arm and the crown of the head will be spared.**

Based on the above, the greatness of the mitzvah is understood, as is the privilege to publicize this *halachah* among all the men of war, their relatives, their friends, and all of *Bnei Yisrael*—may they live and be well—wherever they may be.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon we will merit—together with all our brethren, the Children of Israel—to say that this situation was only a thing of yesterday, for peace will reign in the world, and especially in the Holy Land, [of which] it is said: "And I will grant peace in the land."

And may each and every one of *Bnei Yisrael* increase in Torah and its *mitzvos* in peace, tranquility, and security.

With blessings for good news regarding the above,

**M. Schneerson**

***

P.S. Your letter of the 26th of Menachem Av was received, and the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed will be read at a time of favor at the holy gravesite. The expression of gratitude for this—through acts of *Ahavas Yisrael*.

## 9752 

 15 Menachem Av, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Chaim Eliezer Grinberg

Greetings and blessings!

Although I do not know you personally, I take the liberty of writing to you based on my acquaintance with your father and mother, may they live, during their visit to New York not long ago, and especially in connection with the fact that you are entering the IDF, as I have been informed.

First and foremost, I wish you that you should enter in peace and return in peace, and that your service in the IDF should also be successful and peaceful.

May it be the will of Hashem that these days serve as a preparation for an era of peace to such a degree that, in the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, even a "sword of peace" will not pass through the land, and everyone will be able to dedicate all their time, strength, and energy to matters of peace. May the prophecy be fulfilled: "They shall beat their swords into plowshares and their spears into pruning hooks; nation shall not lift up sword against nation, neither shall they learn war anymore" (Yeshayahu 2:4).

Since I have already taken the liberty of writing to you, I will permit myself to add one more point, which is connected to the above:

You have surely heard of my appeal and request, even before the Six-Day War, that every single Jew should strengthen himself and be meticulous in the observance of the mitzvah of tefillin. This applies all the more so to those who have merited to live in Eretz Yisrael, the Holy Land, and especially those who protect the land and its inhabitants—in the IDF in general, and the border guards, etc., in particular.

I emphasized that although one must observe the mitzvos because they are the commandments of the Creator—the Creator of man and the Creator of the world—nevertheless, certain mitzvos possess unique spiritual qualities (*segulos*). A unique quality of the mitzvah of tefillin is that it strikes terror and weakens the strength of the enemies of the Jewish people so that they will not dare to provoke us to war. In the words of the verse : "And all the peoples of the earth shall see that the name of Hashem is called upon you (and our Sages, of blessed memory, explained that this refers to tefillin), and they shall be afraid of you."

Furthermore, even when the situation deteriorates to the point of actual war, the mitzvah of tefillin—which one places upon the arm and the head—brings about a complete victory for the armies of Israel, as per the exposition of our Sages, of blessed memory, on the verse : "And he tears the arm, even the crown of the head."

There are some who ask and challenge: What possible connection can there be between putting on tefillin on weekday mornings for a short time, and the course of events at the front throughout the entire day and night? And since this cannot be explained through logic, they do not see why they should take it upon themselves to observe the mitzvah. And there are other such questions.

The answer to this comes from the army itself. The entire standing and state of the army is founded upon the acceptance of authority and the fulfillment of the orders and commands of the platoon commander, who in turn accepts the authority of the commander above him, and so on, higher and higher, up to the Commander-in-Chief. Only after the order is fulfilled, and during time free from any duty, does a soldier—if he wishes—inquire, study, and try to understand the matter. And even if he cannot understand it, he relies on the commander, up to the Commander-in-Chief.

Furthermore—and this is the main point—in matters of danger and *pikuach nefesh* (saving a life), people do many things that are in the category of doubt, or even multiple doubts as to whether they will be effective, and even things that involve great effort and the expenditure of much energy. This is all the more true when it is a danger to the many, not just a danger to an individual. In our case—according to those who believe in our Torah, the Torah of life—there is no doubt at all. It is a certainty that the merit of observing the mitzvah of tefillin protects and saves from danger, and as mentioned—a danger to the many. On the other hand, the "investment" required for this is only a few moments and negligible effort.

I would add that regarding you personally, for several reasons, your own conduct in this will surely influence others for the good. That is to say, even if you do the above out of a sense of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke) and do it every single day, your action is multiplied by all your friends who will do the same, and the merit of the many will depend on you.

It is certain that there may be someone who will ask you (or challenge you) with various strange questions. But it is precisely a characteristic of the youth of our time not to be impressed by questions, or even by the mockery of one's surroundings. On the contrary, they view it as a challenge, and this motivates them to do the thing specifically in public, visible to all.

Summary of the above: My belief and opinion are clear that you have now been given an exceptional opportunity to increase the security of the Jewish people in Eretz Yisrael and the strength of the Israel Defense Forces, both through your own personal action and conduct, and through the aforementioned action of spreading the matter of putting on tefillin among your friends, may they live. It does not matter so much if even some of them have not observed this mitzvah until now. In a certain sense, one who enlists in the army changes his entire way of life in fundamental areas.

I will repeat my blessing that Hashem, the Guardian of Israel, should protect you wherever you may be, and at the appropriate time and moment, return you healthy and whole, in body and soul, to your home.

I will add once again that the reason I have written the above is because of my firm belief that this is a matter of increasing the security of the Jewish people, of the IDF in particular, and of you in the most personal sense. According to our Torah, the Torah of life, I have no permission to refrain from writing this to you—at the very least in brief—for given the magnitude of the matter, these written lines are few in quantity.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9763

[9763](#_ftn_799)

B.H., 15 Menachem Av, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, etc.,
[Uri](#_ftn_800) Tzvi Greenberg, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Our friend, Dr. Hillel Seidman, conveyed to me the regards from your letter to him, as well as the news that your son [may he live](#_ftn_801) is being drafted into the IDF these days. At a time of favor, I mentioned him at the Tziyun that he should go in peace and return in peace, whole in body and soul.

Since [everything](#_ftn_802) is by Divine Providence, I saw in this (also) Divine Providence [to write to your son](#_ftn_803) directly. Although perhaps this is not the custom or the etiquette, etc., we are currently in a period where most matters are not routine, nor like last year, and perhaps not a matter of etiquette either. [In the style](#_ftn_804) of our Sages, why should the matter of "our complete Torah" be inferior to "their idle chatter"?

And even though you might hesitate, wondering what impression the content of my letter will make on your son—especially since I do not know him personally—it is nevertheless my request and my hope that you will deliver the letter to him in any case. Thank you in advance for the trouble. It is also my hope that, at the appropriate opportunity, you will add your own explanation and words when speaking with him or writing to him. The main thing is that it should be translated into action—I refer to the dissemination of the observance of mitzvos in general, and the observance of the mitzvah of tefillin in particular, until the point where they will no longer need the special protection of this mitzvah, once Hashem fulfills His promise: ["And I will grant](#_ftn_805) peace in the land, and you shall lie down and none shall make you afraid... and the sword shall not pass through your land... and I will be to you a G-d, and you shall be to Me a people."

With respect, [and in the style](#_ftn_806) of our Sages who inquire after the welfare of a wife through her husband, regards to your wife, may she live.

And with the blessing that you should see much true *nachas*—traditional Jewish *nachas*—and in his case, the tradition of his forefathers, the golden chain, as he told me about it, for long days and good years, from all their children, may they live and be well.

On this occasion, I will express my thanks once again for the books he gave me. I will take the liberty of [enclosing](#_ftn_807) with this a check for the labor and time, which is a permissible matter for anyone. Surely, you will also instruct those who carry out your wishes to send the rest of the books here, and thank you in advance.

As is the custom and practice of the Jewish people, it is impossible for a Jew to be without comments, so I, too, will offer a comment, at least briefly: Seemingly, there is room to say that the title of your book that has been most publicized, *Sefer HaKitrug VeHaEmunah* (The Book of Accusation and Faith), should have been *Sefer HaEmunah VeHaKitrug* (The Book of Faith and Accusation). If you were to say that this is merely a "pretext," it is not; it is a fundamental point. People in general, and the Jewish people in particular, [believe](#_ftn_808) by nature, and only after a time does a difficulty arise, etc., which sometimes leads to accusation. In other words: faith is a natural, fundamental, and essential matter, while accusation is a creation of the intellect combined with events external to the person. Furthermore—and this is also essential—the very existence of accusation is possible only in a person who believes, for then there is room for a difficulty and an accusation, even [to the claim](#_ftn_809) of the first believer, [the one](#_ftn_810) who was Avraham: ["Shall the Judge](#_ftn_811) of all the earth not do justice?" For in a capital that has no leader, there is no room for difficulty or complaint. And the rest is understood.

What is written above relates not only to faith in the G-d of Israel, but also to faith in the Jewish people, from whom [no one](#_ftn_812) shall be cast away. These are the words of the prophet: "You only have I known of all the families of the earth; therefore I will visit upon you all your iniquities" (Amos 3:2). Especially since every single Jew is a literal part [of G-d](#_ftn_813) from above, which is why they were commanded—and it is possible—[to cleave](#_ftn_814) to His ways. In the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in his *Tanya*, Chapter 32, that the souls of the Jewish people "who knows their greatness and their stature in their root and source in the living G-d, for they are all equal and one Father to them all."

## 9724

[9724](#_ftn_815)

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5729
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I read your letter regarding the school [9724](#_ftn_816) with great astonishment.

You list various matters there in which Anash—may they live—made promises but did not fulfill them, etc., and the resulting consequences, etc., and that as a result of all this, you are leaving the school, etc.

Now, it is understood and simple that the entire matter is between you and the talmidim—may they live—and, primarily, between you and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in whose name the school is called. This is surely significant, and you were privileged that the administration of the school was entrusted to you specifically through Divine Providence. With the help of Hashem and the inspiration of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, you succeeded beyond expectations. However, as with every matter of holiness, opponents arise, etc., etc.—as it is written, "Hashem your G-d is testing you to know, etc."

Without entering into an assessment of the culpability of those among Anash who—according to your letter—promised financial assistance and more, and then retracted (and if this is indeed the case, you may tell them in my name that regarding such things it is said that one’s word **to the High One** [is binding], and in this instance, this is a promise **to my father-in-law, the Rebbe**, Nasi of Yisrael. And where does anyone get the audacity and foolishness, etc., not to fulfill a promise to my father-in-law, the Rebbe?)—this does not affect your holy task at the **Oholei Torah** school, nor does it affect the fate of the talmidim in the coming school year [9724](#_ftn_820). You should certainly consult once more regarding this with friends who see the situation on the ground. May it be the will of Hashem that you decide for the best in the aforementioned, and may you succeed.

With blessings.

## 9725

[9725](#_ftn_821)

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs,
Rabbi S.Z. Kahana, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

It is surely known to you what my position has been for some time regarding several matters in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and in particular regarding Yerushalayim, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established speedily in our days, and the holy sites within it—both the Old City of Yerushalayim and that which is called "New," including Har Tzion.

In connection with this, I derived great satisfaction from the information shared in my conversation with Rabbi Zerach Warhaftig, who told me of the many trials concerning several parts of Har Tzion, accompanied by various strange legal claims from Arab families, etc., and that thanks to you and your efforts in this matter, and through your persistence, you succeeded in repelling these demands and the pressure, etc.

The purpose of this letter is not so much to express this satisfaction—for that is a simple matter—nor to offer thanks, for the fulfillment of a mitzvah does not require thanks from flesh and blood; on the contrary, that would diminish the magnitude of the mitzvah, especially a matter such as the one mentioned regarding Har Tzion, etc.

Rather, the primary purpose—since, according to reports, there are those who wish to increase pressure regarding the holy sites in Yerushalayim, the Holy City, both from the secular side and from those who sympathize with the Arabs, and even if not for the sake of the matter itself, the results of this sympathy are surely invalid and also detrimental to the security situation—is for me to also add encouragement from afar, which is close to the essence of the matter, that you will most certainly continue to stand your ground as stated, and indeed, even increase your efforts in this. May it be His will that you succeed beyond expectation.

It is understood that I would be pleased to receive good news regarding all of the above.

With respect and blessing,

## 9726

[9726](#_ftn_823)

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh Mevarchim Elul, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent communal worker,
R’ Moshe A. Yaffe, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 15th of Menachem Av, and I hasten to reply, as I am distressed that a misunderstanding has apparently arisen in our mutual relationship. It is my firm hope that, just as our relations have been friendly in the past, they will remain so in the future—and, indeed, with even greater intensity.

Regarding the subject of your letter concerning Mr. Volinsky, may he live: the matter occurred as follows. Mr. Volinsky visited me a few months ago and told me that he had long ago pledged certain sums to Chabad causes. Since he is particularly interested in *gemach* and *hachnasas kallah* initiatives, he wished to dedicate a portion of his aforementioned commitment to a *gemach* fund and a *hachnasas kallah* fund in our Holy Land. However—and as mentioned, every word of his was spoken in my private office and of his own volition—since the funds he earmarks for donations and communal matters in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) are held in the accounts of Heichal Shlomo, which is under your administration, he would not send the money from here (Canada). Instead, he would notify the administration of Heichal Shlomo to transfer the amount from there to the Chabad representatives in Eretz Yisrael. He also added that this first sum was to be counted toward his commitment. Incidentally, on that same occasion, he also spoke to me about his other activities conducted in Eretz Yisrael through you, and naturally, I took the opportunity to encourage him in this, and so on.

Therefore, when my brother-in-law, the Rabbi, may he live, told me that there was talk of establishing a special committee for this, and so on, I told him that this entire matter was news to me, as it had not been mentioned at all. The only discussion was, as stated above, regarding the technical matter of transferring the sum he had committed—not from Canada, but from within Eretz Yisrael itself.

I am most distressed that someone apparently interpreted these matters differently, even though, on the face of it, that should be impossible, as the conversation took place in my private office.

It is simple that there is no issue here of any lack of trust, *chas v’shalom*, in you or your associates. Rather, as stated, the discussion concerned Mr. Volinsky’s commitment to Chabad abroad and in Eretz Yisrael, and the methods by which he would bring this to fruition.

Regarding the aforementioned commitment, the entire sum can be handed over to Rabbi Ephraim, may he live, Wolf, who, when the time comes, will receive instructions from here regarding the distribution, and so on.

Since you do not mention anything regarding your family, may they live, and especially your sons, may they live, I hope this is a clear sign that all is well.

With respect and blessing.

## 9727

[9727](#_ftn_825)

Brooklyn, N.Y.

As we stand on Erev Shabbos Kodesh Mevarchim Elul, the month of mercy and forgiveness, the explanation of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, regarding the unique quality of this month is well known. He explains it through the parable of a king who, before entering the city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone, etc. (*Likutei Torah*, Parshas Re’eh, p. 32).

May it be the will of Hashem that each one of us utilizes this month to its fullest, and may He who suspends the earth upon nothingness grant you and all that is yours a good, sweet, and pleasant inscription and sealing for the year.

With respect and blessing.

## 9768

9768

B"H, 27 Menachem Av, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Alexander Cohen
Department of Fruit and Vegetable Storage
Volcani Institute of Agricultural Research
P.O. Box 15, Rehovot

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 27 Tammuz (July 13), which arrived with a delay, in which you ask for my opinion regarding the storage of esrogim that have ripened early or late for the time of the Yom Tov.

I see from your letter that you recognize this involves a complex question in halacha.

Allow me to say that although I am not an expert in the procedure you describe in your letter, based on your description it seems to me that it would be extremely difficult to find a halachic permit to use such esrogim for the purpose of the mitzvah. It is understood that in this very matter, there is a fundamental distinction between treatments performed while they are still on the tree and treatments performed after they have already been picked.

However, in general, it is not my practice to issue halachic rulings, nor is there a need, as you can turn directly to the leading poskim in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, who will also be able to see the procedure personally, on the spot, and provide a Torah opinion on the matter.

With respect and blessings.

## 9730

[9730](#_ftn_830)

[Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5729]

Based on what is written in the **accepted** commentaries on the Torah regarding the verse [in question] — and likewise based on: Tamid (32b), Zohar Chadash (285, end of side b) — it is understood that it should be "Avadon" (destruction).

However, according to what is written in Minchas Shai (which is cited in many places **regarding the final ruling**) — regarding that verse — there is also a *kesiv* (written form).

Some say that here there is only "Avdah" (even in the *kri*—the read form)—but, as mentioned above, this is the opposite of the aforementioned sources (Shas, Zohar, etc.).

(See also Eiruvin 19a: **seven** names, etc. — though it is forced to say that *Avdah* and *Avadon* are one and the same.)

There is further proof that, in any case, the *kri* must be "Avadon" from the fact that: 1) No companion for "Avdah" is found. 2) **From Mishlei itself** (15:11), **where by all accounts** it is written "Sheol and Avadon."

In the Koren edition — apparently following the Kittel (Christian) edition — they primarily brought the version that is the opposite of Chazal, and in a note [they mention] that there are those who say the *kri* is *Avadon* (in "Koren" — in the variations of the text **at the end**).

## 9731

[9731](#_ftn_833)

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Avreich, Rabbi Avigdor, may he live and be well,

Shalom and Bracha!

It was with special joy and *taanug* that I received your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Re’eh, along with a copy of the *semicha* and *hormana d’rabbanan* that you received in Eretz HaKodesh. This is especially noteworthy given that the text of the *semicha* contains several additions beyond the standard formula, which implies that those granting the *semicha* identified in the recipient qualities and matters beyond what is usual among those receiving *semicha*.

May it be the will of Hashem that just as He assisted you in ascending in the knowledge of Torah, to the point of *paskening halacha l’maaseh*, the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, [9734](#_ftn_834) will be fulfilled in you: "He who has one hundred wants two hundred; he who has two hundred wants four hundred." Naturally, I refer here to the knowledge of Torah and the like, as we discussed when you were here.

You are surely aware of my perspective on this—and even without that, it is also necessary to have knowledge of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the *Toras HaChassidus*. This is even more essential in our generation, a "generation of orphans" in a time of double and redoubled darkness. This knowledge is especially mandatory for all those who have been gifted with the talent to influence their surroundings, for true influence is achieved when one captures both the mind and the heart of the one in need of that influence. This requires an approach to the heart that comes from *chayus* and *hislahavus*, etc., all of which come primarily from studying *Toras HaChassidus* and living according to its path. May it be His will that you succeed in this as well, and bring good tidings.

A special *segulah* for these days, regarding the aforementioned, is [as explained by the Acharonim](#_ftn_835) that the month of Elul and the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah are days in which one must increase their involvement in the *avodah* of the heart, which is *tefillah*—even for those whose primary focus throughout the year is the study of Torah. Indeed, the matter of *tefillah*, as is explicitly ruled in *Shulchan Aruch* (Orach Chaim, sec. 98), has as its prerequisite and introduction the *hisbonenus* in the greatness of the Creator and the lowliness of man, all of which is the very content of *Toras HaChassidus*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and with the blessing of *Kesivah v’Chasimah Tovah*.

## 9733

[9733](#_ftn_840)

B"H, 5 Elul, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished [individual], engaged in communal needs, etc.
[Rabbi](#_ftn_841) Schneor Zalman, may he live.

Your letter dated 17 Av has just been received, in which you write regarding the hilula gathering and memorial day for your parents and your uncle, of blessed memory.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the gathering be successful. In a gathering such as this, success naturally means the drawing down of influence for the days that follow as well—to increase in the study of Torah and in the meticulous performance of mitzvos. This is achieved through the study of [Torah](#_ftn_842) preceded by yiras shamayim and conducted with yiras shamayim, as explained in the words of our Sages, of blessed memory.

This is also a matter relevant to these days, [as is known](#_ftn_843) that the final forty days—which begin and are mostly contained within the month of Elul—their essence is Torah and tefillah (teshuvah) combined, unlike the first forty days, whose essence is Torah, and the middle forty days, whose essence is tefillah (teshuvah).

May Hashem, the Giver of the Torah and the One who commands the mitzvos, bless you with long, good years, and may He increase your strength in the aforementioned matters—both for yourself and, more importantly, for the many, for the merit of the many will assist you—to accomplish all of this with proper health, in joy and with a good heart.

P.S. Enclosed with your letter was a copy of your letter from some time ago regarding your birthday. I believe I responded at the time. In any event, ["two are better"](#_ftn_844) etc., and may you be blessed with a good and successful year in both material and spiritual matters alike. And in the innermost point—to experience true nachas, which is Jewish, Torah-true, Chassidic nachas from all your descendants, may they live.

## 9736

[9736](#_ftn_856)

By the Grace of Hashem, 7 Elul, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Meir Azulai
Ma'abarat Bat-Yam
Barracks 50 A/B

Greetings and Blessings!

I have just received your letter, which was delayed for unknown reasons.

I will mention you for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good regarding the matters you wrote about, concerning yourself and your mother, may she live.

Judging by the tone of your letter, it is unnecessary to emphasize to you that daily conduct in accordance with the path of Torah and mitzvos—in addition to the primary point, which is the fulfillment of the command of Hashem—is the conduit for receiving Hashem’s blessings in all that is needed.

On this occasion, I will add that since you are in the IDF, you surely see tangibly, even in mundane, literal matters, how the Jewish people [are responsible](#_ftn_857) for one another. You see that the conduct of each and every individual and the fulfillment of the commandments, without questioning them, is not only for the benefit of the one who acts and fulfills them; rather, the success of the entire unit in which he is stationed depends upon it. From that unit, the situation in the entire sector depends, and so on, up to the situation of the entire front and the country.

From this, you can learn how it is also in spiritual matters, and the great responsibility of each individual in particular. In the words of the Rambam in his book, the Yad HaChazakah (Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 3, Halacha 4): "Every person should view himself throughout the entire year as if he is half-innocent and half-guilty; and likewise, the entire world is half-innocent and half-guilty. If he commits one sin, he tips the scales for himself and for the entire world to the side of guilt and causes its destruction; if he performs one mitzvah, he tips the scales for himself and for the entire world to the side of merit and causes salvation and rescue for himself and for them."

This is the point I wish to emphasize regarding the great merit you have now: that your strengthening yourself to fulfill the command of the Holy One, Blessed be He—who is called the L-rd of Hosts—has the power to bring about a complete victory over the enemy, without casualties, etc. Especially according to what is written [in this week’s parsha](#_ftn_858): "For Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp to save you and to deliver your enemies before you, and your camp shall be holy." And it was already promised [at the beginning of the parsha](#_ftn_859): "When you go out to war against your enemies"—a "going out" as it should be—"and Hashem your G-d will deliver them into your hand." And a "going out to war as it should be" is as it was prefaced in the previous parsha (Shoftim 20:1): "When you go out to war against your enemies and see horses and chariots, a people more numerous than you, do not fear them, for Hashem your G-d is with you, who brought you up from the land of Egypt." And Rashi explains: "In your eyes they are numerous, but in the eyes of Hashem, they are all like a single horse."

What is written above applies to all the mitzvos of Hashem. It is even more potent regarding the mitzvah of tefillin, which has a special virtue according to [the verse](#_ftn_860): "And all the peoples of the earth shall see that the name of Hashem is called upon you, and they shall fear you"—meaning that, initially, they will be afraid to come against us in war. And even if the situation leads to war, then by the merit of the mitzvah of tefillin, which we place upon the arm and the head, we merit the fulfillment of the promise [and he shall tear](#_ftn_861) the arm and even the crown of the head.

May it be Hashem's will that, in addition to acting according to the above yourself, you will also be a good shaliach to convey the above to your fellow soldiers, to encourage them to walk in the path of Torah, which is called *Toras Chaim*—a guide for daily life so that life will be worthy of the name—and it is also called *Toras Emes*, because it is eternal. With appropriate explanation and words that come from the heart, and especially by being a living example of the aforementioned conduct, you will surely be able to bring merit to the many, and the merit of the many will depend on you.

These days are days of special virtue, days of awakening and days of mercy; it is the month of Elul, the month of preparation for receiving Hashem’s blessing in all that is needed, and especially for a good inscription and sealing, for a good and sweet year.

With blessings for success and good tidings.

## 9737

[9737](#_ftn_862)

By the Grace of Hashem, 11 Elul, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 4 Elul:

The statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, is well known, and it carries the weight of a halachic ruling: "If not now, when?" This refers to one's younger years, when one is capable of ascending in the study of Torah. There are two reasons for this: First, the mind is capable of absorbing the holy and refined matters of Torah better and more deeply than it can later on, after the mind has spent a certain amount of time occupied with other things—even matters that are permissible, but are nonetheless matters of *reshus* (optional activity), which is an entirely different reality than the reality of Torah. Surely, for someone who learns in a yeshiva, there is no need to elaborate on this.

Second, there is another aspect to this, similar to what the [Gemara](#_ftn_864) states—and this is also the law—that one may not do anything before *davening*. One of the reasons for this is that an action performed after *davening* is on an entirely different level. For this reason, even learning [Torah](#_ftn_865) is better after *davening* than before it. Likewise, in your case, all the matters that need to be accomplished will come out with a completely different level of success when they are done after your learning. Especially in your case, as you need to prepare yourself for life and arrange your future in due time with a suitable *shidduch*, etc., the true foundation for everything being truly good—good [for Heaven](#_ftn_866) and good for people—is when it follows the preparation of Torah during the years that should be dedicated to learning.

Knowing your family in general, and having met with your father, *shichye*, several times, as well as with your mother, *tichye*, I am certain that not only will they not be opposed to you continuing your learning in the yeshiva now for the maximum amount of time, but they will also encourage you in this and be pleased by it. May the Ribono shel Olam grant success, so that your going to learn in yeshiva, with the encouragement of your parents, *shichye*, will add blessing and success to your parents, *shichye*, as well—and by this I mean simply in matters of *parnassah*, health, etc.

With blessings for good news in all the above, and a special greeting and blessing for a complete recovery for your father, and *Kesivah v'Chasimah Tovah* for all the members of the family, *shichye*, with goodness, in body and soul.

## 9758 

[B"H], 15 Elul, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and G-d-fearing individuals who have ascended this year to the Holy Land—may it be built and established by Mashiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days—who are settling in Nachalat Har Chabad,

May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

In addition to what I have written to several of you individually, I am writing this general letter to you all together. Great is the merit of the public in general, and especially when many unite together in matters of goodness and holiness, and particularly—in the Holy Land and its settlement.

I send to each one of you, and to all of you together, my wishes, prayers, and blessings that your settlement and establishment in Nachalat Har Chabad should be in a good and auspicious hour in every detail, both materially and spiritually. May your settling in Nachalat Har Chabad be consistent with its name, for a name is a significant matter, in such a way that you will arrive at the "rest" and the **"inheritance"** (*nachalah*), with the nullification of all matters that disturb the peace of the soul and the peace of the body. And may you go from strength to strength with joy and goodness of heart upon the **"mountain"** (*har*) of holiness, through our holy Torah—its understanding and comprehension—in the **Chabad** of the soul, and in a manner of study that leads to action, the fulfillment of its mitzvos with *hiddur*.

As mentioned, these words are directed to those settling in Nachalat Har Chabad, both those who have already settled and those who will settle in the future.

These days are days of *segulah*, as per the words of our Alter Rebbe, that in the month of Elul, the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, is like a king who, before entering his city, is greeted by the townspeople who go out to meet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone, etc. (*Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh, p. 32*).

With blessings for success in all of the above—great success—and for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, and for good tidings in all things,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Why must they drag the Rebbe Shlita into their own business and politics? A word to the wise is sufficient. Especially since this is not merely a hint, but things that have been stated several times. It is a great wonder that, after all this, there are apparently still those who continue this despicable politics, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Surely, after the publication of this letter, all such slander regarding the settlement in Nachalat Har Chabad will cease. May it be His will that you bring good news in this as well.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year,

Nissan Mindel – Secretary

## 9440

[9440](#_ftn_881)

[B"H](#_ftn_882), 17 Elul, 5729

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad,

May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

Transcribed herewith is the text of the telegram sent to them today:

B"H.

To each and every Bar Mitzvah boy,

Orphans of the wars and terror in our Holy Land, may they live and be well,

Peace and blessing for a good and sweet year!

On this luminous day, [the birthday](#_ftn_884) of the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe—the two great luminaries who illuminated, and continue to illuminate, the lives of the Jewish people with Ahavas Yisrael, love of Torah, and love of Hashem—I wish to express my heartfelt participation in your joy on the occasion of your reaching the age of Bar Mitzvah. May it be Hashem’s will that you accept upon yourself the yoke of our Torah, the Torah of life, and its mitzvos with joy, and may you fulfill them in health and tranquility, for [Hashem will grant](#_ftn_885) peace in the land. The [merit](#_ftn_886) of Torah and mitzvos is great in protecting the land and our people wherever they may be, and in casting [terror](#_ftn_887) and fear upon every enemy and adversary. There is a special quality in the mitzvah of Tefillin, for [as our Sages have stated](#_ftn_888), "all the peoples of the earth shall see that you are called by the name of Hashem, and they shall be afraid of you," and it brings victory to the men of war. Through all this, you will cause true nachas ruach to your father, may Hashem avenge his blood, who from the World of Truth where he resides watches over what is happening to his children, derives great pleasure from their good conduct, and rejoices greatly as he sees them going from strength [to strength](#_ftn_889) in our Torah, the Torah of truth, and its mitzvos.

With blessings of Mazal Tov for the Bar Mitzvah, and for a good year in which you will be inscribed and sealed, for you and the entire family, may they live and be well,

**Menachem Schneerson**

With blessings for a Gmar Chasima Tova,

Secretary

9841

25 Elul, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Uri Zvi Greenberg,

Shalom u’Bracha,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter with thanks.

Naturally, I regret that I apparently caused you embarrassment by the enclosure in my letter. This was certainly not my intention at all; on the contrary, my entire intent was for the good, as I wrote in my letter, for it is at the very least a *schar batala*—which even in ancient times, and even the greatest of Israel, would accept with a pleasant countenance.

Furthermore, and this is the main point in my eyes, there is an intention here to wish you success, as the sum also comes from the fund of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which is in my hands. I have strong faith that the promise of our Sages (Bava Basra 15b, end of page b) is fulfilled through this: "He who takes a coin from the fund of a man who is whole, upright, G-d-fearing, and turns away from evil, is blessed." I, too, regarding myself, follow this practice from time to time. My hope is strong that you will judge me favorably, and the proof of this will be if you use the aforementioned for your needs and the needs of your household, may they live in joy and goodness of heart.

Since everything is by *hashgacha pratis*, and you mentioned in your letter the matter of a *segulah*, I am jumping at the "find" to use this as a pretext to send you (separately) the **Tanya** of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch. For all those who have tasted of the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov, his students, and the students of his students—and all the more so those who are links in the golden chain of his students—there is no better *segulah* than the study of his Torah. And the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov has been explained in a way that is understood and grasped even by the human intellect in the teachings of Chabad, of which the Tanya is the foundational book.

It is understood that I cannot refrain from responding, at least in a few words, to what has occurred recently in our Holy Land—may it be built and established speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—where sometimes, and especially in the recent period, people close their eyes to the exclusive interpretation of the events taking place. I refer to the uproar that was raised now with the setting of the fire by a non-Jew in a place that non-Jews consider one of their holy sites. Seemingly, it is not understood at all—why did this happen specifically in the weeks that it happened, and in general, what is the "purpose," since the arsonist was found immediately and it was clarified that he is not a Jew, etc.?

But one who does not ignore the direction of the times will immediately agree that there is a sign and a wonder here. For when the uproar began regarding the place holy to Jews—to distinguish, the Kosel HaMa’aravi, the remnant of our glorious House and our Sanctuary—due to the debate over whether it is a holy place or... a historical site, to the point that they prevented Jews from praying in part of it, etc., and the opinion of those who err in deciding it is a "historical site" began to spread and grow—a non-Jew came and set fire to the aforementioned place holy to the non-Jews. And behold, a wonder: immediately it was decided that it is not a historical site, and even more so, those who made noise to diminish the holiness of the Kosel HaMa’aravi jumped to the forefront to defend the aforementioned, to condemn the act of arson, and to declare that certainly and simply—it is impossible for Jews to have any part in such a desecration of holy sites, etc., etc.

And in the aforementioned event, in the language of the verse, "The voice of my beloved knocks: 'Open for me, my sister, my darling, my dove, my perfect one,'" He is knocking on the heart of every single man and woman of Israel, and certainly and surely also the hearts of those who err, the *tinokos shenishbu* among the idolaters who do not know, etc.

And in these days, days of *segulah* and favor, may it be His will that they open first, and in the style of our Sages, an opening like the eye of a needle, and immediately Hashem will fulfill His promise: "Open for me an opening like the point of a needle, and I will open for you an opening like the entrance of a hall"—*teshuvah ila’ah*.

With respect and with the blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year for you and for all your household, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

Many thanks for the newspaper clippings and the enclosure.

## 957

[957](#_ftn_942)

[B"H](#_ftn_943), Days of Selichos, 5729
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

It has been emphasized many times that all matters in Torah — which derives from the word *hora'ah* (instruction/teaching) — serve as guidance for our daily lives. The Yomim Tovim, naturally, provide very important and comprehensive instructions, each according to its content: Pesach — *Zeman Cheiruseinu* — provides an instruction as to what true *cheirus* (freedom) is; Shavuos — *Zeman Matan Toraseinu* — teaches us, primarily, to understand what Torah is; Sukkos — *Zeman Simchaseinu* — gives us a deeper feeling and understanding of what *simcha* is.

Rosh Hashanah — which marks the time of the world’s creation: **"This is the day of the beginning of Your works, a remembrance of the first day"** — provides a general instruction regarding creation and the purpose of the entire world’s existence.

***

A question is raised: Why is Rosh Hashanah designated as "the beginning of Your works," when in fact Rosh Hashanah is the **sixth** day of *Maaseh Bereishis*?

The explanation given by our Sages, of blessed memory, is: Since man is the purpose and the inner intent of **all parts** of creation, and since with man the **entire** creation was completed and perfected, it is as if man represents the entire creation, and before he was created, there was, so to speak, no creation at all.

However, a question arises: How can one say this, when there is such a vast world outside of man — as it is written: "How many are Your works, Hashem," "How great are Your works, Hashem"? On the contrary, when considering the entire creation, including man, the *min hamedaber* (man) is far fewer in number than the *baalei chayim* (living creatures), and even fewer than the *tzomei'ach* (plants), and fewer still than the *domeim* (inanimate objects, such as earth, stones, etc.)?

The answer to this — and this constitutes one of the **main** instructions of Rosh Hashanah regarding the **entire creation** — is:

The order that there is more of everything else — *domeim*, then *tzomei'ach*, then *chai*, and only afterwards *medaber* — is when one calculates by **kamus** (quantity). But when one looks at **eichus** (quality), the order is reversed: *Domeim*, which has no signs of life or growth, occupies the lowest place; higher than it stands *tzomei'ach*, which grows, but lacks the characteristics of life and movement of the *baalei chayim*; higher still is the world of *baalei chayim*, which are, however, lower than **man**, because they lack the intellect of a human being, the highest of all creatures. For although a *baal-chai* has intellect, the intellect of a *baal-chai* is not an end in itself; rather, it is a servant, serving the natural needs of the *baal-chai*. But human intellect — if a person conducts himself as a human and not as a *baal-chai* — is not meant to be a servant to his natural needs, such as eating, drinking, etc. Rather, the intellect is an end in itself. And furthermore: the goal and perfection of human intellect is that not only is the intellect not used merely as an instrument to satisfy physical needs, but, contrary to the *baalei chayim*, for man, all matters of eating, drinking, etc., become servants to the intellect, so that the person can ascend higher and higher in intellectual and spiritual matters.

However, this is not yet the **true** perfection of man. True perfection is reached when the intellect brings the person to the recognition that there is One who is higher than intellect, until the intellect becomes *batel* to that which is higher than intellect.

To put it more clearly: The perfection of man is when the intellect recognizes that man, and together with him the entire world, must strive to become *batel*, and they do become *batel*, to the Almighty, the Creator of the entire world and the Guide of everything in the world.

On the first Rosh Hashanah, this perfection was achieved by the first man, Adam HaRishon. Adam HaRishon [called out] (and carried out) to the entire world around him: **"Come, let us bow down, bend, and kneel before Hashem our Maker."**

This observation is relevant and must permeate our daily lives, as we see from the designation of the "Shir Shel Yom" (Song of the Day) for **each week** throughout the year: On the sixth day of the week (the day of Adam HaRishon’s creation), the song is: **"Hashem has reigned, He has donned majesty"** — the Almighty reigns, He has clothed Himself with greatness — because this was the achievement of Adam HaRishon, that he immediately recognized the Divine sovereignty and elevated himself and the entire creation to be *batel* before Hashem our Maker, the King of all the earth.

***

The general lesson from the above, in short:

[When a person reflects,] he sees that most of his life and most of his affairs are spent on things that are, at first glance, material and worldly, such as eating, drinking, sleeping, etc., with all the preparations for them. One also sees that among the *min hamedaber*, the number of worldly people is far greater than the "spiritual" ones, and in general, one sees around him a large material and physical world immersed in material matters. This can sometimes lead to a doubt and a false thought that perhaps material and physical matters are the essence of the world.

Rosh Hashanah comes and teaches us that the truth is exactly the opposite: There were indeed five days and [a] part of the sixth day of *Maaseh Bereishis* for all kinds of creatures. Nevertheless, it is specifically man — who in quantity, in time, and in space, is a very small part of creation — who is the essence and purpose of the entire creation. And within man himself, it is [not the body] which is **"dust from the earth"** that is the essence, but the soul that the Almighty breathed into him in one moment (**"And He breathed into his nostrils a soul of life"**), a soul which is a literal **"part of Elokus from above."** And only after man was created with this Divine spark did the entire creation receive value and perfection, such that man is rightly designated as the "beginning" of creation, of all parts of creation — **"This is the day of the beginning of Your works."**

From this comes an even closer instruction: When one speaks with a Jew about the fact that one must study Torah and fulfill mitzvos in daily life, according to the command of the Almighty, the Creator of the world, who watches over everyone and everything everywhere and at every moment — there are some who ask: If this is truly the purpose of creation, how is it that those who observe Torah and mitzvos with all their details are, for now, not yet in the overwhelming majority? And how is it that Jews are generally a small minority among the nations? Rosh Hashanah comes and teaches and emphasizes: **"This is the day of the beginning of Your works"** — the essence is not quantity but quality; every person can accomplish in his portion of the world, until one [person] can elevate the entire world. That not only he, but everything around him, should fulfill the **"Hashem has reigned, He has donned majesty,"** to crown the Almighty as King of the entire world.

This is also the [first] matter of the blowing of the Shofar — as an expression of the "coronation" of the Creator and King of the entire world.

***

May it be the will that everyone, within the entirety of the Jewish people, should accomplish the aforementioned in his portion of the world, so that through the [unification] of all parts, the entire world will recognize the Divine sovereignty, and the prayer will be realized and fulfilled in the immediate future, together with all our prayers: **"Reign over the entire world... and let every creature know that You have created it... and let everyone who has a soul in him say: Hashem, the G-d of Israel, is King, and His sovereignty rules over everything"** — "Reign over the entire world... and let every creature know that You have created it... and let everyone who has a soul in him say: G-d, the G-d of the Jews, reigns, and His sovereignty rules everywhere."

With blessings for a *Kesiva V'Chasima Tova* for a good and sweet year,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9,859 

[8 Tishrei, 5730]

The greatest wonder is that it seems [R' Y.] [did not] "grasp the matter": this is a question where it is **impossible** to say "let us follow the stringent view," "let us satisfy all opinions," **and the like**.

His proposal that there should not be a "strange" halachic ruling—meaning that he should not count for himself [(the opposite] of the Gemara)—requires clarification **in the poskim**: how can one **skip** one night and not count at all (or count twice), which is not only "strange," but the **opposite** of the concept of "temimos" (complete, without omission or addition).

And to add: my explanation can also be stated in a different style (not [merely] counting for himself—even though **that is** the foundation—but rather) that he acts as if he is in the place from which he departed, regarding Sefiras HaOmer, and consequently, also regarding the counting of the days of the month.

## 9751

[9751](#_ftn_973)

B”H, 25 Tishrei, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of the telegram signed by you regarding the shidduch of your son, sheyichyeh, and the mechutanim, sheyichyu, etc.

Yesterday, the mechutanim also spoke with me about this matter. I expressed my opinion that since it was discussed to hold the wedding in the month of Adar, b’sha’ah tovah u’mutzlachas, it is not [customary](#_ftn_974) at all to postpone the date of the wedding.

2) According to the custom in the vast majority of cases, the [wedding](#_ftn_975) takes place in the bride’s hometown. In this case as well, it is my opinion that this should be the case, especially since, as I recall, it was already agreed that the wedding would take place in the United States. If the mechutanim choose to concede and agree to change from [location] to New York, then this too is included in the aforementioned custom.

3) Although I believe this was also discussed, I reiterate that after the wedding, the chassan should learn in a kollel here in the U.S., in New York, for a period of time. Since the custom is that study in a kollel lasts approximately two years, my opinion is that this is certainly what should be done—namely, that he should learn in the kollel here after the kallah, tichyeh, completes her teaching position in [location] for the years 5730 and 5731. **After that**, the young couple will discuss between themselves where they will reside.

4) I was **greatly** astonished to learn that the back-and-forth regarding the aforementioned details and similar matters is being conducted by the chassan and kallah. This is not their business at all; it belongs solely to the mechutanim. The reasons for this are understood, [and I have already](#_ftn_976) publicized my opinion on this many times. What has been done is in the past, but I told the mechutanim—and I said I would write this to you as well—that, in any event, from here on out, neither the chassan nor the kallah should conduct these negotiations at all.

5) I also learned that many matters are being handled through intermediaries, messengers, etc., which has consequently caused misunderstandings and, as a result, distress, etc. I told them that, in any event, from here on out there is no place for the involvement of intermediaries, messengers, etc. The mail will deliver letters written directly from the mechutanim to one another; there is no need for intermediaries. On the contrary, and the wise will understand.

Because of the above content, and in order to prevent undesirable situations, this letter is being sent without waiting for its turn, and is marked urgent. Thank you in advance for confirming its receipt in the same manner.

With respect and blessings.

## 9756

[9756](#_ftn_985)

B"H, 11 Cheshvan, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Daniel, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 30th of Tishrei, which reached me with some delay.

I was very pleased to read your opinion regarding the religion of Israel, which you describe as "the exclusive factor that unites the people of Israel in all their dispersions." I interpret the expression "in all their dispersions" to include our brethren, the children of Israel, who are in Eretz Yisrael, as you continue in your letter, noting that within the religion of Israel "lies the moral strength of the people of Israel to stand their ground and defend the land."

Surely you are aware that the religion of Israel possesses two unique and interconnected characteristics:

The first is that it encompasses a person’s life from the very first moment of birth until their final moment on this earth, [in the words of the verse](#_ftn_987): "In all your ways know Him (Hashem)," which our [Sages](#_ftn_988) of blessed memory explain to mean that this includes even one’s eating, drinking, and business dealings, etc.

Furthermore, it is a practical religion, [in the phrasing of the Mishnah](#_ftn_989): "The deed is the essential thing." Therefore, when one examines the Five Books of the Torah, as well as the Six Orders of the Mishnah, etc., we see that the vast majority are practical instructions. Regarding ideas—especially abstract ideas—there is very little by comparison, both in quantity and in brevity and allusion, even though the quality is great, and "the little that contains the much."

In accordance with the aforementioned premise, my hope is strong that your feeling regarding religion is translated into actual practice in your day-to-day life. This brings a double and redoubled merit to you, for you surely serve as an example to many others—especially since your position as a brigade commander in the IDF adds strength to this. It is human nature to be particularly influenced by one’s superior, and one is influenced by him not only in the area where he is their commander, but also by his conduct in his other affairs and private life.

There is another point to consider: it is the nature of a military man, and especially a [military](#_ftn_990) commander, to be accustomed to accepting the yoke of fulfilling an order without questioning the reason or explanation, even if one has some difficulty with the order. In the traditional phrasing: [the priority of](#_ftn_991) "we will do" before "we will hear." This means that if your conduct, and that of your entire household, is founded upon the religion of Israel in actual practice, it is multiplied many times over by the many who will follow your lead in this. Therefore, even if the matter involves effort and exertion, it is certainly worthwhile, as you are thereby bringing merit to the many.

Surely for one such as yourself, there is no need to emphasize that one should not be deterred by difficulties or obstacles, even if one encounters them. I will only add one point based on the [teachings of the Baal Shem Tov](#_ftn_992), that from everything one must learn a lesson in one’s avodah to one’s Creator: The entire concept of parachuting is based on utilizing the resistance of the air to slow the descent; on the contrary, one utilizes it as a supporting force so that the parachuting will be successful. The analogy is understood.

As is customary when requesting a blessing, I will mention you and your family, may they live, at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned, and regarding the contents of your letter in general, and may you succeed in your role in defending the people of Israel and the land of Israel, [in the style of the verse](#_ftn_993): "And all the peoples of the earth shall see that the name of Hashem is called upon you, and they shall fear you."

With respect and blessing.

## 9758

[9758](#_ftn_998)

[B"H](#_ftn_999), Parshas Vayeira, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner
of Yeshivas Achei Tmimim in Newark,
May Hashem preserve them and keep them alive,

Shalom u’vracha!

It is the custom among Yidden to [connect](#_ftn_1000) the events of the week with the weekly Parsha, and to derive from it the true lessons of our [Torah](#_ftn_1001) (from the word *hora'ah*—instruction), the Torah of truth.

Today’s Parsha tells us how the birth and upbringing of the first Jewish child born to Jewish parents took place—Yitzchak, the son of Avraham and Sarah, the first parents of the Jewish people.

[Yitzchak’s](#_ftn_1002) birth was supernatural and miraculous. [His](#_ftn_1003) Bris took place when he was eight days old, and his upbringing was carried out amidst difficulties and *nisyonos*.

It was entirely different with Avraham’s son [Yishmael](#_ftn_1004), whose birth was natural, and who was circumcised when he was thirteen years old—that is to say, when he was already a *bar-da'as* (a person of understanding).

And the Ribono shel Olam assured Avraham that it is specifically Yitzchak who would be his true heir (**"For in Yitzchak shall your seed be called"**), and through him the Jewish people would be built.

Through this, the Torah teaches us that when one sets out to establish Jewish generations and a Jewish future, one cannot approach it with a "natural" approach or with human intellect and calculations.

Jewish existence is not dependent on natural laws, but on Divine guidance.

The same is true regarding the foundation of Jewish *chinuch*; it is not based on calculations of nature, as is the case among other nations. One does not wait until a Jewish child becomes a *bar-da'as* and can understand for himself how to conduct himself and approach *Yiddishkeit*. Rather, one provides him with a Jewish *chinuch* in the fullest and strongest measure from the earliest youth. In this way, one ensures that the connection with the Ribono shel Olam will be strong and eternal (**"an eternal covenant"**), and one will overcome all difficulties and *nisyonos*, and enjoy all Divine blessings in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

This is also the approach and the *shita* of Yeshivas Achei Tmimim in Newark, which this year has reached its "Bar Mitzvah." This means that the institution has matured and must now begin to ascend in the fullest measure, just as reaching the age of Bar Mitzvah does not mean a conclusion, *chas v'shalom*, but on the contrary, a beginning to ascend higher and higher.

I greet the administration of the Yeshiva, the esteemed guests and participants, and all the friends who have the great *zechus* to support and expand the Yeshiva. Surely all will further increase their participation, and the Ribono shel Olam will increase His blessings to each and every one, in *gashmius* and *ruchnius* alike.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9659

[9659](#_ftn_1007)

B”H, 14 Menachem Av, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

. . . Regarding the [initial thought](#_ftn_1008) to depart from your post — this is certainly nothing more than a mere initial thought. For we have seen and continue to see tangibly that in our times, and especially on the American continent (North America, and even more so in South America), any rabbi or spiritual guide who relocates from his community abandons (in a spiritual and psychological sense) many families in his community who were influenced by him directly, or at the very least indirectly (by hearing from a neighbor or the like about his activities and words).

This is analogous to the captain of a ship in the heart of a stormy, raging sea who abandons it and flees to save himself. When his conscience awakens, he tries to soothe himself with the pretext that there is little he can do, that he will leave someone in his place, that his soul yearns specifically for Torah in a different place, and the like! Yet it is accepted among **all** peoples of the earth—and all the more so is it an instruction of our holy Torah—that the captain is the **last** to leave the ship. We also see tangibly that the knowledge that this is how it must be awakens the captain’s inner, hidden strengths, and in many cases, he saves the ship and everyone on board, bringing them to a safe harbor. The analogy is simple. I ask for your forgiveness.

## 9793 

B”H, 17 Cheshvan, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Chaim Tzurya
Netanya, Emek Hefer 4

Greetings and blessings!

By the instruction of the Rebbe shlita, I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 4 Tishrei, with apologies for the delay due to the many pressures of the recent holiday season.

Regarding what you write concerning the study of the Aleph-Beis using the traditional method—in your words, "the method that was customary in the cheder"—first of all, one must distinguish between two matters:

1) The method itself: that is, teaching children the Aleph-Beis by naming the letters—Aleph, Beis, etc.—in their proper order, early and late, as well as teaching the vowels in their names and their combinations with the letters in an orderly sequence.

2) The manner of instruction in this method—the methodology—which is a specialized skill. For one must know **how** to utilize even the best method. After all, two people may use the same method, yet one succeeds while the other does not, or succeeds to a lesser degree. When one sees a lack of success with a certain method, one should not judge the method itself; rather, one must determine whether the instructor knows how to use that method and is actually doing so.

Now, regarding the first point: the foundation of teaching according to the order of the Aleph-Beis, etc., is established on holy mountains, as is well known and famous, and this is not the place to elaborate; you will certainly be able to find all the sources for this. Not only are we not permitted to abandon this method, but anyone who compromises on it causes great damage to the rooting of the feeling of holiness in the child’s soul.

Therefore, even if you were to argue (though in reality this is not the case) that learning in the aforementioned manner is not as "interesting" as modern methods, this does not justify retreating from the sacred method to adopt a modern one whose losses outweigh its gains.

But in truth, if one contemplates the words of our Sages, "He looked into the Torah and created the world," and "its ways are ways of pleasantness," it is clear that if the method of teaching the Aleph-Beis is utilized properly, in accordance with the instructions of our holy Torah, one will succeed not only in the matters of holiness connected to that method, but also, quite simply, in the actual learning and progress of the child. We have seen from experience that teachers who have specialized in the ways and modes of teaching beginning reading have realized that, in fact, teaching through this method is the most successful. For example, I am aware of several teacher-training institutions in Europe and the United States that, in teaching the methodology for beginning reading, have preferred the study of the Aleph-Beis as per the tradition over all other methods—provided, of course, that the method itself is studied so one knows how to use it.

In light of the above, not only should the method not be replaced, but one should encourage the teachers who use it. Those who, for whatever reason, find it difficult should be directed to experts who, in addition to their yiras shamayim, are proficient in guiding these teachers on how to instruct their students in the best possible way according to the aforementioned method.

We are confident that you, in your capacity as a pedagogical advisor for the Ministry of Education in religious schools, will contemplate and become more familiar with all of the above, and will yourself assist in this as much as possible. May you be among those who bring merit to the many, whose merit is very great and endures forever.

Many thanks for your interest in Chabad institutions.

With the hope of hearing good news and with blessings for all that is good,

Rabbi Ch. M. A. Hodakov
