Secretary

## 909

[909](#_ftn_1024)

B"H, 18 Cheshvan, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Yehudis Chaya Sternbuch

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters, which arrived with a delay:

It is a well-known principle that in matters pertaining to the intellect and the emotions of the heart—such as matters of fear of Heaven, the study of Torah, and the fulfillment of mitzvos—in order to succeed in a specific manner, one must act in the style of our Sages, of blessed memory: **in the place where one’s heart desires.** For the same reason, this also includes the **manner** in which one’s heart desires. This is also brought as a halachic ruling in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, at the end of section 240.

[And I have](#_ftn_1026) already emphasized previously that this is brought in the Shulchan Aruch not in the Laws of Torah Study, but in the Laws of Honoring Father and Mother—that the order of Torah study is also Torah. Through this, it is emphasized that it does not infringe upon the honoring of one’s father, and it must also be done with words and arguments of pleasantness, in a way that does not cause friction. We see tangibly that the best approach is to avoid all sorts of arguments, and there should only be the absolute minimum that is unavoidable in any other way.

On the contrary, the hope is strong that when they see that you are more precise in other mitzvos, including the mitzvah of honoring father and mother, this in itself will diminish the grievances.

May it be Hashem's will that, from a place of peace of mind in all details, you will go [from strength](#_ftn_1027) to strength in matters of fear of Heaven and Yiddishkeit in general, and that you will bear with pride and righteousness the name that the Torah gives to every daughter of Israel—a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 9796

[9796](#_ftn_1028)

B"H, 18 Cheshvan, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and elevated, involved in communal needs, etc.
[R' Eliyahu Moshe](#_ftn_1029) (may he live)

Peace and blessing!

Just recently, the photographic reproduction of the Amsterdam 1664 Mishnayos was received. I thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me, and also for the satisfaction it gave me to see that you are creating a memorial and bringing *nachas ruach* to the soul. Especially since it was done with *hiddur*. For if at all times the instruction of the Torah is—[“Beautify yourself before Him in mitzvos”](#_ftn_1030], a beautiful Sefer Torah, etc.—then how much more so in our time, when people are accustomed to demanding that the [vessel](#_ftn_1031) be magnificent, and through this, they are drawn to the magnificent wisdom contained within it.

May it be Hashem’s will that many will see from this and do likewise, on occasions of joy and goodness, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed, to create a memorial for themselves in matters of our holy Torah—the Torah of life—and its study with light and vitality, [and as our Sages of blessed memory instructed](#_ftn_1032), study that leads to action, [and great](#_ftn_1033) is the merit of one who brings merit to the many.

With respect and blessing.

## 9757

[9757](#_ftn_1034)

[B"H](#_ftn_1035), 22 Cheshvan, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, learned, and esteemed individual, a man of the people who is exalted above the people, who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, R' [Shneur](#_ftn_1036) Zalman, may he live and be well.

Greetings and blessings!

In addition to the words I conveyed orally through my shluchim, may they live, I wish to reiterate my heartfelt birthday wishes in writing: May you live long and good years together with your family, may you fulfill your role now and in the future with health, joy, and a good heart, in its entirety and perfection. [And in the style](#_ftn_1037) of our Sages, may you be whole and good toward Heaven and toward people, whole in body, soul, and Torah, and amidst peace in our Holy Land, [as](#_ftn_1038) it is written: "And I will grant peace in the land... and no sword shall pass through your land," "I am Hashem your G-d, who brought you out of the land of Egypt... and I led you upright."

[The words](#_ftn_1039) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, have already been printed: "It is a known custom that the Alter Rebbe received from his teacher, in the name of his teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, to recite the chapter of Tehillim corresponding to one's age after Shacharis, before reciting the daily Tehillim shiur, as is the custom." Based on this, the chapter of Tehillim to be recited beginning on Rosh Chodesh Kislev, may it come upon us for good, is Chapter 81.

May it be the will that what is stated in your chapter be fulfilled in you: ["I am](#_ftn_1040) Hashem your G-d, who brought you up from the land of Egypt; open your mouth wide and I will fill it" — along with the rest of the blessings in that chapter.

[We have already](#_ftn_1041) spoken on various occasions about the precision of the verse, "**Who brought you up** (*ha'ma'alcha*) from the land of Egypt," which is not the usual phrasing in most places, including the verse at the beginning of Parshas Bechukosai mentioned above, "**Who brought you out** (*hotzeisi*) from the land of Egypt." For the precision and emphasis here is on *ha'ma'alcha*—meaning an ascent (*aliyah*) from all matters of the land of Egypt, and obviously, first and foremost, from the essential aspect [of Mitzrayim](#_ftn_1042)—the straits (*meitzar*), boundaries, measurement, and limitation. This serves as a preface and explanation for the promise that follows: ["Open](#_ftn_1043) your mouth wide and I will fill it." For this expansion has no conditions or limitations; it depends only on the person, and it is promised that however much the expansion is, the promise "and I will fill it" will be fulfilled.

The explanation is as stated: Since it begins with "**I am**" (He who I am, [which is not](#_ftn_1045) hinted at by any letter or point at all), "**Hashem**" (who brings into being all of creation and all the worlds), "**your G-d**" (your strength and your vitality; for even though He created man as a soul in a limited body with 248 limbs and 365 sinews, etc.—a limitation in all details and matters—nevertheless, because "I am Hashem" is your strength and vitality, I am therefore) "**who brings you up from the land of Egypt**" (from straits and limitations; based on which it is understood, and it is even simple, that if you only) "**open your mouth wide**" (then immediately) "**I will fill it**."

And to dismiss the opinion of all skeptics and doubters, etc., the Tzemach Tzedek copies [in his notes](#_ftn_1048) on Tehillim regarding the verse "Open your mouth wide and I will fill it": Rashi explains, "Open your mouth to ask of Me all the desires of your heart, and I will fill it—as much as you ask, I will fulfill." And also the interpretation of the Ibn Ezra: "When you believe that I am Hashem who stands forever, delight in Me by asking with your mouth all your desires and the requests of your heart, and I will fill it."

With appreciation, honor, and blessing, and regards to all those participating in the birthday celebration wherever they may be, and especially [in the Land](#_ftn_1049) upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year, in the "Tzemach Tzedek" shul and beis medrash in Jerusalem, our holy city, may it be rebuilt and established speedily, and in Kfar Chabad—founded and directed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in which you have merited and succeeded in being among its primary builders, establishers, and expanders. May you continue to do so in the future, increasing and growing in light.

And with wishes that you may soon see the fulfillment of the verse where Hashem has fulfilled His word: ["In a moment"](#_ftn_1050) (in a short time) "I will subdue their enemies and turn My hand against their adversaries." And "He would feed them (Israel) with the finest of the wheat, and with honey from the rock I would satisfy you."

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

I have requested and urged that the *drushim* and notes of the Tzemach Tzedek from manuscripts on the Book of Bereishis be completed and published, in addition to those already printed. This will be released first on Parshas [Bereishis](#_ftn_1051) and Noach. I am urging this so that it reaches you by your birthday, and it shall be a gift and a token from the residents of Kfar Chabad, their sons and daughters, may they live and be well, and also a gift from me. Especially since [one](#_ftn_1052) of the *drushim* is the *maamar* "To Understand the Concept of Blessings," [a long *drush* from the Alter Rebbe, with the addition of notes, glosses, references, and abridgments by the Tzemach Tzedek]. My hope is that the book will also reach you in its proper time.

I have just received your letter from the 17th of Cheshvan. Many thanks for the great *nachas* and satisfaction from its contents, starting with the good news that the principle of "a shaliach performs his mission" was fulfilled—the shluchim who went from here to there and delivered the birthday blessing, along with matters regarding our Holy Land, etc.—and concluding with the good news confirming the information I received from Anash, may they live, that on the eve of Rosh Chodesh Kislev you will pray in the Tzemach Tzedek shul, and on the evening of that day you will be in Kfar Chabad.

May it be the will that, as with every good thing—and especially that which is good for Heaven and good for people—good fruits will follow, also for Heaven and for people, etc.

Regarding your writing about the printing of the volume of the Alter Rebbe's *maamarim* that was ready for print, etc., I am sorry [that apparently](#_ftn_1054) you did not receive the aforementioned volume at the time—the third volume of the Alter Rebbe's *maamarim*, which is the book *Maamarei Admur HaZaken – 5762*, which [was printed](#_ftn_1055) a few years ago. It was even mentioned [in the Kuntres HaKaf-Nun](#_ftn_1056) in the *maamar* of Rabbi Adin Steinsaltz, may he live, in the note at the end, as it was printed after he wrote his *maamar* in that *kuntres*. I requested then that they send you the aforementioned book immediately.

In the treasury of manuscripts here, there are two more small notebooks, most of which are [maamarim](#_ftn_1057) of the Alter Rebbe (a significant portion of them are short *maamarim*), and some of them, apparently, were printed in the books *Boneh Yerushalayim* and *Meah Shearim*. But as far as I recall, there are among them several *maamarim* that have not yet been printed. And there is room to say that even in the *maamarim* that have already been printed, there are several variations in these notebooks. How great the quantity of these *maamarim* will be—whether enough for a book like the ones published until now or more, etc.—can only be known after they are collected, edited, and compared with the other printed *maamarim* and those that are still in manuscript form here. How long the collection and editing will take is also difficult to estimate. Nevertheless, I found it appropriate to inform you of this, for surely everything is by Divine Providence, especially regarding Torah and the inner dimension of Torah, which in our days has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. And it is for [you](#_ftn_1058) to decide whether this is suitable for what has come to your mind and thought. The main difference here is that while the ["5762 Book"](#_ftn_1059) was copied from the original handwriting of the Mitteler Rebbe, the *maamarim* about which I am writing now are manuscripts of copyists [although apparently they copied them from the original handwriting or from an edited manuscript].

## 9768

[9768](#_ftn_1060)

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Although I have not heard from you directly since we met in person, it is my hope that everything is well with you, and that the order of a Jewish person is in accordance [1062] with the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life: to be constantly increasing in goodness, uprightness, and holiness from time to time.

With respect and blessings.

## 979

[979](#_ftn_1063)

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregants of the Ohev Shalom community,
And at their head, the Rav, the Chossid, the man of action, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi [Pinchas](#_ftn_1064) Aharon, may he live,
Miami Beach

Hashem, may they live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the upcoming Chanukas HaBayis of the new building for your shul, on the 3rd of Chanukah, G-d willing.

When it comes to a **beis knesses** and **beis medrash**, it means that a **beis mikdash me'at** has been added, and holiness is added among Yidden. This is true even if there are already other shuls of the same nusach in the area; and all the more so in a place where this was truly lacking.

Another point of joy is that the very fact that Yidden come together to create the shul, and subsequently to celebrate the Chanukas HaBayis, demonstrates an inner connection to the matter with **love** and dedication.

This also provides the certain hope that the shul will justify the name **beis knesses**—where Yidden gather and unite in a place of tefillah to the Ribono shel Olam, as such a holy place ought to be.

Furthermore, when along with a beis knesses it is also a **beis medrash** for shiurim kevuim in the Torah of Hashem, the influence has a hold on daily life even outside the four walls of the shul, so that life should be according to the Torah of Hashem, **Toras Emes** and **Toras Chaim**—[Torah](#_ftn_1066) from the word "horaa" (instruction)—which then brings true harmony and **shalom** in all areas of life: shalom between Yid and Yid, shalom between Yid and Avinu Shebashamayim, and shalom within every Yid personally, by freeing oneself from the yetzer hara and inner fragmentation. Such [shalom](#_ftn_1067) is surely the vessel for all Divine blessings.

Since the Chanukas HaBayis is taking place on Chanukah, may the Ribono shel Olam help that all matters of the shul should be permeated with the spirit of [Chanukah](#_ftn_1068), in a manner of "adding and increasing, adding and shining"—in an ascending measure of light, the light of **ner mitzvah v'Torah ohr**.

With honor and blessing for success and good tidings.

## 9880 

 Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the Chanukas HaBayis of "Beis Chaim Shaul" – of the Yeshivas Achei Temimim in Rishon LeTzion, in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the Chanukas HaBayis on the 15th of this month, a month whose conclusion and seal is the days of Chanukah, which also contains the concept of the dedication of the Beis HaMikdash. Indeed, every shul and beis medrash (yeshiva) is called a "mikdash me'at" (a miniature sanctuary). This is especially pertinent as the work of the Mishkan was completed in Kislev, on the 25th of the month.

May it be the will that this house fulfills its purpose to be a "great house", in accordance with the interpretation of our Sages of blessed memory, that one "grows" Torah and "grows" tefillah within it. This is the very essence of the Yeshivas Achei Temimim and Tomchei Temimim: that the Torah studied within them is permeated with yiras shamayim and tefillah.

This is especially so as the house is named after the founder of the aforementioned yeshiva, who dedicated his life (mesiras nefesh) to the study of Torah with yiras shamayim.

The hope is strong that the spirit of mesiras nefesh of the founder will influence the students, may they live, in this house. May it also be the will that this spirit of mesiras nefesh will influence the supporters, may they live, of the yeshiva who are participating in its construction and in all the affairs of the yeshiva in Rishon LeTzion, so that their support, too, will be permeated with mesiras nefesh and a desire born of joy and a good heart.

With respect and with blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9784

[9784](#_ftn_1088)

Brooklyn, N.Y.

In fact, the matter has already taken its course; protests against various issues there are increasing, especially in these very recent weeks and days, and in this country in particular. These are coming not only from rabbinical organizations but also from lay organizations, in connection with the issue of autopsies, television on Shabbos, and so on.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that in our immediate future we merit that every single Yid will recognize and know, as it is written in [the parsha](#_ftn_1089) of this week, that "Hashem is standing over him," and that "the land... to you I will give it" (that it was given by the Ribono shel Olam, and likewise "to your seed"). May they contemplate this as is fitting, for then the conclusion is immediate and certain: that all matters pertaining to it, both within the land and outside of it, must be in such a manner that all who see will recognize that it is a ["land](#_ftn_1090) upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are at all times, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year."

With respect and blessing.

## 9785

[9785](#_ftn_1091)

B"H, 7 Kislev, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. David Greenberg

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of 28 Cheshvan, in which you write regarding a family of Chabad descent that recently immigrated to Eretz Yisrael from that country, and who are facing a housing problem, etc.

It is well known that I am not at all pleased with the way enormous sums—relatively speaking—are being wasted in order to live specifically in certain locations in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established), even though it is much easier to obtain an apartment at appropriate prices and conditions in a neighborhood of G-d-fearing people outside of those specific locations.

Regarding this matter, we [established](#_ftn_1092) not long ago a settlement for immigrants from that country, named "Nachalat Har Chabad," in proximity to Kiryat Malachi, for immigrants, and with conditions that are incomparably more favorable than other places in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established).

It would be appropriate for the person you are writing about to contact Rabbi Efraim Wolf (P.O. Box 46, Lod) if he is interested in settling there and wishes to receive details regarding this.

With respect and blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. Since every matter is by Divine Providence, and you write at the end of your letter that you are a teacher in a high school in Jerusalem (the Holy City, may it be built and established), it is my hope that you utilize your influence to instill in the students fear of Heaven, love of Hashem, and walking in His ways without compromise. And if this is necessary everywhere, all the more so [in the Land](#_ftn_1093) upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year. And surely for someone like you, further elaboration on this is superfluous.

## 9,880 

[9 Kislev, 5730]

Your note is not entirely clear. It seems you have combined two **distinctly** different matters regarding the change in the count of days that can occur between: 1) one who is on one side of the International Date Line, 2) one who crosses it from east to west, and 3) one who crosses it from west to east.

The discussion in the sicha is **only** regarding the change—caused by crossing the line—in the **order** of the days for Sefiras HaOmer, the days of the week, etc.

There is a possibility of an additional change—caused by traveling from east to west or vice versa, which shortens or lengthens the **measure** of the twenty-four-hour day. This requires a specific and difficult analysis—to find foundations in the Gemara, etc.—**similar** to the Gemara in Shabbos (118b) regarding those who bring in Shabbos in Teveria and those who conclude Shabbos in Tzipori, though it is not exactly the same. And this is simple to understand.

Furthermore, in our times, it is possible for one to circle the globe several times within **one** twenty-four-hour period, and the sun would rise for him multiple times during this same period. **It is obvious** that he would not count Sefiras HaOmer according to these sunrises (or the days of the week). See the sources cited in Kitzur Shulchan Aruch, Shaarei HaMetzuyanim B'Halacha, at the beginning of the Laws of Shabbos, and elsewhere.

I will mention this at the holy gravesite.

## 9787

[9787](#_ftn_1098)

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Vayeitzei, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the 14th annual banquet of the Beis Rivkah School for girls in Montreal,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby send my greetings and blessing to all the participants, honored guests, and friends of the Beis Rivkah school on the occasion of this annual banquet. May Hashem Yisbarach grant that this endeavor be met with great success.

This celebration, taking place the day after 19 Kislev—the Chag HaGeulah of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya v’Shulchan Aruch and founder of Chabad—will surely lend a special significance to the event. For, [as](#_ftn_1099) is well known, the Alter Rebbe placed the greatest emphasis on the matter of chinuch in general, including the education of Jewish daughters. Within the family of the Alter Rebbe, there was also a tradition of learned women, even though in those years this was generally an exception, as the circumstances of the time did not strongly demand it, as is [recounted](#_ftn_1100) in the **Zichronos** of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

And since this has been told and described to us in great detail, it is a sign that this is an instruction that this is how it should be—especially in our times, when the entire conduct of the Jewish home is to a very great extent dependent upon the woman and mother, who is titled as the "Akeres [HaBayis]"—the foundation of the Jewish home. Therefore, it is a matter of vital necessity that Jewish daughters be well prepared for their most important life mission.

This is indeed the purpose of the Beis Rivkah school for girls, and therefore it is a primary duty, as well as a great zechus, to help support and expand the Beis Rivkah school. Those who have a share in this will surely be blessed with all good, and especially with Yiddishe nachas from their own children and grandchildren, may they live and be well, in good health and with success in both gashmius and ruchnius.

With respect and blessing for success.

## 9788 

B"H, 14 Kislev, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Zvi Itzkovitz
Mayor of Lod

Greetings and blessings!

From time to time, I inquire about your welfare from Anash who reside in Lod, and I also personally receive regards from you through visitors from there. Now, I was especially pleased to receive regards from you through Rabbi Ephraim Wolf, who also delivered your letter dated the 9th of Kislev.

May it be Hashem’s will that for many years to come you will bring good news regarding your personal affairs, and also—and this is the main point—good news regarding the affairs of the city, especially concerning the Chabad housing and institutions, since you have merited that Divine Providence has granted you the privilege and responsibility to fulfill the role of Mayor of Lod.

And although it is a great responsibility, our Sages of blessed memory have said that the Holy One, blessed be He, does not make demands according to His own power, but according to the power of His creations. Along with the position, He has given you the strength to fulfill your role completely and in the best possible way, and in the inner sense, that the city should befit its mission to be a **city and a mother** in Israel, in the Holy Land, upon which the eyes of Hashem are—always—from the beginning of the year until the end of the year, and to serve as an example to the other cities in Israel.

 And last but not least, a Mazal Tov blessing on your son Moshe entering the yoke of mitzvos. May it be His will that he accepts upon himself the yoke of Torah and the yoke of mitzvos with a whole heart and a good spirit, and may you and your wife—may she live and be well—succeed in raising him, along with all your children—may they live—in the traditional manner, for Torah, for the chuppah, and for good deeds, in prosperity, tranquility, and ease.

With respect and blessing.

## 9829

[9829](#_ftn_1108)

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Women and Girls of Chabad in our Holy Land, may they live,

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I read your letter dated 9 Kislev, along with the report of your activities and the good resolutions to increase your efforts in several areas of your program. May it be the will [of Hashem](#_ftn_1109) that what you desire succeeds, [and may](#_ftn_1110) the pleasantness of Hashem be upon you and the work of your hands, [to go](#_ftn_1111) from strength to strength in spreading Yiddishkeit and its matters, permeated with the spirit, vitality, and light of Chassidus.

Surely you will especially utilize these auspicious days, the redemption of our Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, who emphasized the great role of the Jewish woman as the "akeres habayis" (foundation of the home), for she is the one who determines, to the greatest extent, all matters of the home and the conduct of the home. [It is known](#_ftn_1113) that in the family of the Alter Rebbe, it was customary for the women to be literate, and some were even scholars—even though this was rare in those days, as it was not as necessary under the living conditions of that time—as is recounted and well-known in the Sefer HaZichronos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

And since we have been informed of all this, and in such detail, it is proof that it is an instruction for each and every one of us. On the contrary, it applies with even greater intensity and strength in our generation, where the education of girls is an absolute, vital necessity, as is obvious and simple.

Likewise, you will surely utilize the upcoming days of Chanukah following the preparation of the Chag HaGeulah—moving from one subject to another within the same theme—[as our Sages of blessed memory said](#_ftn_1114), "They (the women) too were part of that miracle"—to strengthen yourselves in the activities of spreading the "candle of [mitzvah](#_ftn_1115) and the light of Torah," illuminated with Chassidic light and vitality, in a manner of "increasing and continuing, increasing and lighting," [as instructed by](#_ftn_1116) the Chanukah candles, which increase in their light from day to day. Even though for each day the number of candles as prescribed by the order is sufficient, one must add another candle the next day, and so on for the day after, and what was sufficient yesterday is not sufficient today, and what is sufficient today is not the measure for tomorrow. It is easy to understand, for [we are commanded](#_ftn_1117) to ascend in holiness. And as has been said many times, [the commandment](#_ftn_1118) of the Torah is also the granting of strength from Above to fulfill the commandment in its entirety, and the matter depends only on one's will.

Blessings for a bright Chag HaGeulah and illuminating days of Chanukah, and for outstanding success in all your activities, which are also the channels to draw down and receive the blessings of Hashem in all that you and your families, may they live, require—both materially and spiritually—in a manner of "increasing and continuing."

## 9890 

B”H, 21 Kislev, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yechiel HaKohen, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I am writing to acknowledge receipt of your letter from the conclusion of Shabbos Kodesh, the festival of the Chag HaGeulah. It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, your health has already improved.

May it be Hashem’s will that this improvement, in all your affairs—both material and spiritual—continues to grow and increase, in accordance with the lesson of the days of Chanukah that are approaching.

This is especially relevant given that you are of the seed of Aharon HaKohen, whose purpose and role is, as it is written in the Torah of Moshe, "They shall teach Your judgments to Yaakov and Your Torah to Yisrael."

It is surprising that for a long time I have not seen any of your publications, aside from what you wrote regarding the book by our friend Dr. Nissan, may he live and be well, Mindel. In any case, it is puzzling: If you have not published anything, then—since Hashem has graced you with the talents of a swift scribe, capable of writing in the language of the country, and on the other hand, the state of Yiddishkeit in general, and among the youth in particular, is so confused—how can you remain silent? And if you have published, but simply did not send it here, although one could find a forced explanation for this, it is still strange, for the entire purpose of printing is that it should reach the widest possible circles.

It goes without saying that my intention is not to raise difficulties or complain about the past, but rather to address the practical side of this regarding the present and the future.

With respect and with blessings for good health, good tidings, and days of Chanukah illuminated by the candle of the mitzvah and the light of Torah.

P.S. Since it appears you do not have someone to type in Lashon HaKodesh, you may also write in English, although I especially appreciate that a letter connected to the Chag HaGeulah of 19 Kislev was written specifically in our language, which is Lashon HaKodesh.

## 9793

Brooklyn, N.Y.

It is surprising that I have not heard from you, even though I inquired about you through our friends, may they live and be well.

This is in accordance with the desire of the Alter Rebbe to demonstrate and bring into actuality that the [three](#_ftn_1136) loves—love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of a fellow Jew—are one. For if one loves a fellow Jew, one must strive that he be a lover of Torah and a lover of Hashem; and if one loves him in actuality, one must strive that he be a lover of Hashem and a lover of Torah in actuality, until his daily conduct in practice is in accordance with this. The connection between love of Hashem and love of a fellow Jew is explained in Chapter 32 of Tanya, [and as has been discussed](#_ftn_1137) many times, the order in Tanya is also significant, and the hint that this matter is brought in chapter "Lev" (heart) is highly meaningful.

Enclosed are Likutei [Sichos](#_ftn_1138) that have been printed here from time to time, which also contain the matter we discussed. May your strength be fortified, Mr. [Yehuda], for not taking into account those who wished to influence you to the contrary, and for printing and publicizing this viewpoint. It is a great pity that those who receive this viewpoint, whose numbers are constantly growing, were not convinced by intellect alone, but rather, unfortunately, through the daily actions [of the wounded](#_ftn_1139), etc., etc. It is difficult to elaborate on this distressing matter, which is "up to one" (in the language of our Sages, Menachos 18a, Tosafos s.v. "Ad").

With blessings for illuminating days of Chanukah and for good tidings.

## 9802

## 9804

14 Teves, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Sarah Ginzburg
Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter in due time, though for various reasons the response was delayed until now. In it, you write regarding the passing of your mother, a”h—may she, and all the children and your father, shichyu, be blessed with long and good lives—and the feelings and thoughts associated with this.

In truth, none of us can fully comprehend the conduct of Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, who is the Creator of man, his Guide, and the One who oversees him with Divine Providence. Yet, it is certain and absolute that He is the essence of good, and in the well-known phrasing—it is the nature of the Good to do good. That the conduct of Hashem is sometimes not understood at all by the human intellect is not surprising, for what value does a limited, measured, and finite creature have in relation to the Infinite and Boundless in general, and to the true Infinite and Ein Sof in particular? Nevertheless, Hashem desired to reveal a portion of His wisdom to human beings of flesh and blood—through His holy Torah, which is called *Torah Or* (Torah of Light) and *Toras Chaim* (Torah of Life). This means that it illuminates a person’s path in life in a way that the light is graspable even according to the measure of man’s limited faculties. Based on what is explained in our Written and Oral Torah, one can find an explanation and understanding—at least to some degree—even regarding such an event and others like it.

The explanation lies in two actual halachic rulings which, on the face of it, stand in contradiction to one another, and furthermore, both appear in the same section of the Shulchan Aruch (Yoreh Deah 394). At the beginning, it states: One should not grieve (in matters of mourning, etc.) more than necessary (as instructed by our Sages, of blessed memory), and anyone who grieves excessively, etc.—see there. And at the end of that section, it is brought: Anyone who does not mourn as the Sages commanded is cruel. Now, consider the dilemma: if it is natural to mourn in such an event, why the outcry against one who mourns excessively, to the point that the punishment for it is severe, as explained in the Shulchan Aruch there? And if the punishment is so severe, then seemingly it is not cruelty if the mourning is less than what the Sages commanded.

The explanation for this—found at the end of the section that clarifies the matter of mourning, and in the language of the Shulchan Aruch copied from the Rambam—is: "He should fear and worry, examine his deeds, and return in teshuvah."

It is understood and simple that the neshamah is eternal, for there is no logic to say that because of the illness of the flesh and blood, etc., the vitality of the nefesh should be diminished or that the vitality of the nefesh and neshamah should be nullified. This deterioration touches only the flesh and blood themselves and the connection between them and the nefesh and neshamah. This means that a severance of the connection can occur—death, r”l—and upon the severance of the connection of the nefesh with the flesh, the nefesh ascends and is liberated from the shackles of the body and its measurements and limitations. Through the good deeds it performed while it was in the body upon the earth, it is elevated to a higher state, even higher than it was before its descent into the body. As the well-known expression goes, the descent of the nefesh (into the body) is a descent for the sake of an ascent—an ascent higher than it was before the descent.

From this, it is understood that everyone close to this nefesh, and everyone to whom she was dear, must recognize that the nefesh has ascended to a level even higher than the one she occupied previously. It is only that for those living in this world, it is a loss. And just as the closer one is, the more precious the ascent of the nefesh from level to level is in his eyes, so too, in the second aspect—the pain is greater, because the void is greater due to her separation from the body and from life in this world.

Furthermore, there is also the fact that, seemingly, the nefesh could have ascended even higher specifically in this world, as our Sages of blessed memory said in their Mishnah: "Better is one hour of teshuvah and good deeds in this world than all the life of the World to Come."

Since in such an event there are these two opposing sides—the liberation of the nefesh from the shackles of the body and its ascent to a higher world, the World of Truth, and on the other hand, the aforementioned deficit and loss—from this come the results in the two aforementioned halachic rulings: that for the duration of time set by our Sages of blessed memory according to the Torah of Truth, there must be mourning, and together with this, it is forbidden to grieve excessively (to add to the days, and within those days themselves—to the content of the mourning). Moreover, the content of the mourning is that the living person needs an explanation as to why he deserves this loss and deficit—which is the primary reason why such an event is of the type one mourns over—so that he will fear and worry, examine his deeds, and return in teshuvah.

Added to this is the fact that a connection is then maintained between the living in this world and the neshamah that has ascended above. For it is existent and eternal, and it sees and observes what is happening with those connected and close to it. Every good deed done by them adds to its *nachas ruach*, especially that which is done by those whom she educated and raised with an education that leads to the aforementioned good deeds. This means that she has a share in these deeds performed through the education she gave to her children and those she influenced.

Since all of the above are instructions of our Torah, which is the wisdom and will of the *Ribono shel Olam*, the fulfillment of these instructions is *avodah* of Hashem, of which it is said: "Serve Hashem with joy." And since the Torah has commanded each and every one regarding this, and a commandment of the Torah is also a bestowal of strength, it is certain and absolute that every person has the strength to fulfill this, and more—as the aforementioned verse states, "Serve Hashem with joy."

All that has been said applies to each and every member of the family. And to a greater degree, with a greater bestowal of strength and also with greater responsibility, it applies to those who can influence the other members of the family, so that from them and their conduct, others will see and do and conduct themselves accordingly. Therefore, first and foremost, the necessity to fulfill the above in its entirety rests upon the head of the family and the eldest of the children—I refer in this case to you and your father, shichyu. And in this, too, is the promise: "You have labored and you have found."

In the above, there is also an answer to your question regarding how you can find relief, etc. The answer is understood from what has been said—through conduct appropriate to the content written above, and with a strong trust in Hashem that you will succeed in this.

May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all of the above, in a way that is good, seen, and revealed.

With blessings for success in all your affairs and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9440

[9440](#_ftn_1212)

[B"H](#_ftn_1213), Sunday, the day of reading [V'eileh](#_ftn_1214) Shemos Bnei Yisrael, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and supporters of Torah and mitzvos,

May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

In light of the yahrtzeit-hilula of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, which falls during this week, it is timely to once again recall his [well-known](#_ftn_1215) teaching: "A Yid must live with the times" — with the "Torah-time," which is filled with the content and spirit of the weekly parsha.

The parsha of Shemos begins by emphasizing the names of the children of Israel who came to Mitzrayim — **"And these are the names of the children of Israel who came to Mitzrayim,"** etc.

Through this, the holy Torah teaches us that when Yidden enter Mitzrayim — a land where the lifestyle and the entire worldview are the opposite of the Jewish spirit and the Jewish path — the first priority must be to ensure that the children do not forget who they are, and who their parents were. They must always know and remember that they are **Bnei Yisrael**, Jewish children, the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah (as is [alluded](#_ftn_1216) to in the word Yisrael), who carry their Jewish names with pride and conduct themselves in their daily lives in such a way that one can immediately recognize that these are Jewish children — Reuven, Shimon, Levi, Yehudah, and so on.

This can be achieved only when one provides children with a deeply rooted Jewish chinuch, which gives them the strength to remain a reality unto themselves, a people unto themselves, even under the most difficult trials of the galus of Mitzrayim. This is the guarantee that we will emerge from Mitzrayim with all our children, sons and daughters, and in our entirety — whole and proud Yidden — just as [our Sages](#_ftn_1217), of blessed memory, state: that they emerged from Mitzrayim with the same names with which they entered.

This is the eternal lesson of the [eternal](#_ftn_1218) Torah, which is valid for all times and all lands, especially in the present time and in this country: that the survival of the Jewish people, the integrity of the Jewish home, and the assurance that Jewish children will remain proud and conscious Yidden, is entirely dependent on a penetrating, Torah-true Jewish chinuch, without compromise and without dilution.

Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, which has a long-standing tradition of chinuch hakasher al taharas hakodesh, permeated with ahavas Hashem, yiras Hashem, and ahavas Yisrael, and which has, B"H, succeeded in raising generations of proud, conscious Yidden with a sense of responsibility and mesiras nefesh for a fellow Yid, is now making preparations for its annual celebration.

I hope that all lovers of Torah, and especially the askanim and friends of the Yeshiva, will make every effort to ensure the success of this endeavor, both financially and spiritually.

In reward for this, may the Ribono shel Olam grant them and their families success in their own affairs, and in particular — true Jewish nachas from their children and grandchildren, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9810 

, Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5730 
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

As we stand on the first day of the eleventh month, the tenth of which is the yom hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe,

It is a day of remembrance (a time of atonement and salvation for their souls from the hand of the enemy) for each and every one to remind themselves and all those around them of the core of his labor —the labor to which his soul dedicated itself during his lifetime in this world: mesiras nefesh for the dissemination of Yiddishkeit, the Torah of truth and the Torah of life, and the mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them" —without being affected, or even impressed, by any obstacle or hindrance, enemy or foe.

This remembrance is for the purpose of bringing it into actual practice, which is the essential thing: to walk in this path that he taught us and paved for us, to disseminate Torah and mitzvos, permeated with ahavas Hashem and yiras Hashem, and in a manner that is constantly increasing.

There is a special intensity to the period of the yom hilula this year (twenty years since the histalkus), as the calendar configuration is the same as in the year of the histalkus—on the day of Shabbos Kodesh, when we read Parshas Bo.

May it be the will of Hashem that this remembrance, the hisorerus that comes through it, and the practical action that follows, be enduring and exert their influence throughout the entire year.

And may this be a year of light, a year of blessing, a year of Torah, and a year of Geulah—the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, and with the coming of Moshiach, the resurrection of the dead, and "those who dwell in the dust shall awaken and sing", and he among them.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9811

[9811](#_ftn_1239)

[B"H](#_ftn_1240), Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

N'shei U’Bnos Chabad

May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

In light of the Yahrtzeit-Hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, on the tenth day of the month—which this year falls on the same day of the week as his histalkus [20](#_ftn_1241) years ago, on Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Bo—

It is surely superfluous to emphasize that the purpose of commemorating and observing a memorial day among Jews is to become permeated with the content and spirit of that day, so that it may be reflected in all the days of the year, in our daily conduct in actual practice.

So too in the case of this Yahrtzeit-Hilula, the intention is to be inspired by the light and influence of the Baal HaHilula, so that it may awaken in each and every one of us a strengthening of the activities conducted in his spirit, and a firmer adherence to [his](#_ftn_1242) ways, as he taught us and indicated through his own exemplary life and his own activities.

Especially regarding Jewish women and girls in general, and N’shei U’Bnos Chabad in particular, it is well known how deeply he interested himself in their behalf, to illuminate their lives and to help them understand the preciousness of their role as **akeres habayis**—not only as the pillars of a *bayis b'Yisrael*, their own Jewish home, but also as those who build and secure the future of *kol beis Yisrael*, of the entire Jewish people, upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

In this, he emphasized the great responsibility and the great zechus that this grants them, especially in our time—as can be seen from his sichos kodesh and his activities in the field of *chinuch habanos*, etc.

Furthermore: while pointing out the direction as well as the obligations that one must carry out in life, he also emphasized the necessity that all these matters and activities be carried out with vitality and simcha, with Chassidishe light and warmth. This adds a greater measure of success in both the quantity and the quality of the activities, both on the part of those who are doing them and on the part of those for whom they are done; for then all matters are performed and received with heart, according to what our [Chachamim](#_ftn_1244) say: "Words that come from the heart enter the heart"—heartfelt words have a heartfelt resonance—and they are not lost.

And another point in this: that activities performed with warmth, vitality, and joy provide a greater measure of inner satisfaction to those who perform them, and this evokes in them a strengthened desire to go *m'chayil el chayil* [from strength to strength] and to make everything brighter and brighter.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that all the above be fulfilled in you and in each one of you, in a manner of *mosif v'holech*, in an ever-increasing measure, and through this, the channels and vessels to receive the Ribono shel Olam's blessings will also be increased and expanded in everything that each of you and all of you need, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With the blessing for a good and successful month in general, and in all the above in particular, and for besuros tovos,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9812

[9812](#_ftn_1246)

[4 Shevat, 5730]

The point discussed at the farbrengen—regarding the interpretation of **Rashi on the Torah (for a five-year-old beginning Chumash) as he himself defined it**—is that it must explain the **literal meaning of the verse (peshuto shel mikra)**. This excludes **all** of the following justifications: 1) That Rashi relies on what is written in the Mishnah, etc. 2) That Rashi relies on his commentary in the Gemara, or even on his commentary on the Torah that appears **after** the current verse. 3) That Rashi relies on a logical deduction—unless that logic is so simple to a **five-year-old’s** understanding that Rashi does not need to mention it explicitly.

In my humble opinion, the aforementioned premises are clear and logically necessary, provided we accept that Rashi’s commentary on the Torah is what **Rashi himself** testifies it to be and how he defines it (Bereishis 3:8, and in many other places).

Based on the above, there is no room for the justification that Rashi relies 1) on what is written in... in Perek HaChovel! 2) on the logic [of the one who is] commanded, etc.—for even to the mind of a fifteen-year-old studying Gemara, this is not simple at all; rather, it is a subject of **dispute**.

Incidentally: This was noted as above, and at length, the **first** time we spoke about this Rashi. And the conclusion is that Rashi relies on what is written in **Rashi on the Torah before** the verse in question (Noach 9:5). Consequently, there is no place for a difficulty regarding **Rashi**—based on the sugya in HaChovel, etc. Surely all this was also recorded in the Reshimos.

In any case, thank you for the note and the scholarly exchange.

## 9823

[9823](#_ftn_1300)

[B"H](#_ftn_1301), 13 Shevat, 5730

Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, engaged in communal needs, etc.,

[Rabbi](#_ftn_1302) Moshe, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

[Regarding](#_ftn_1303) what you noted in Chagigah (9a) concerning the Gemara’s question, "What is the difference between them?" regarding one who was lame and then healed, and why it did not cite the "What is the difference between them?" regarding Pesach (Pesachim 93a), especially since that very same sugya in Chagigah compares and distinguishes between this case and Pesach.

At first glance, I would suggest that the explanation is that regarding Pesach, the difference in time between Pesach Rishon and Pesach Sheni is a full month, and it is impossible that there would not be a minor who grew up in the interim (and perhaps a convert who converted is also common). This is not the case regarding the *tashlumin* (make-up offering) for the Chag, which is from day to day—and it is not common (to such an extent, among those present in Jerusalem) for a minor to grow up and develop two hairs, etc., and certainly not for a convert to convert, which requires a **Beis Din**, etc., in the interim.

And what of a non-Jew in Jerusalem, especially during the Regalim? (And it is an extremely uncommon occurrence for a non-Jew to delay his conversion from the eve of the Yom Tov until Chol HaMoed!).

Therefore, the Gemara chose the case of one who was lame and then healed.

Upon further reflection, I realized that it can be explained **simply**: that in Chagigah, it chose the case of one who was lame and then healed because the novelty (that being lame is a specific law regarding the obligation to ascend for the festival) is more significant to it. Furthermore, it may be said that it comes to teach an additional novelty—to negate the assumption that a lame person is obligated in *tashlumin* according to all opinions, for that is merely "a lion crouching over him" (Eruvin 78b), and not a negation of the obligation in a matter such as a minor or a convert. And this is clear.

With respect and blessings.

## 9826

[9826](#_ftn_1315)

[With the help of Hashem](#_ftn_1316), Wednesday, the day of the Torah reading [“And you](#_ftn_1317) shall be to Me a kingdom of priests and a holy nation,” 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of
Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

On the occasion of the annual celebration of Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch, I send my greetings and blessing to the honored guests and to all the participants and friends of the yeshiva.

Since this celebration takes place the day after Shabbos Parshas Yisro—the parsha of Matan Torah and the Aseres HaDibros—it is appropriate to note a special connection between this endeavor and the content of the parsha.

[The](#_ftn_1318) [Aseres](#_ftn_1319) HaDibros, in which all 613 mitzvos of the Torah are rooted, begin with mitzvos **between man and Hashem** and conclude with mitzvos **between man and his fellow**. This underscores that even the most elementary concepts of morality and ethics can have value and endurance only when they are founded upon **“I am Hashem your G-d”** and **“You shall have no other gods.”**

The course of general human history has consistently shown that individuals and nations cannot progress when the laws of morality and ethics are not founded upon the basis of faith in the Creator of the world, but rather upon human intellect alone, and can therefore be changed and adapted to the unbridled inclinations of the time. The state of the world today is the best proof of this.

In Jewish life, in particular, there cannot be a separation between the mitzvos between man and his fellow and the mitzvos between man and Hashem. The unity of Jewish faith in **Hashem Echad**, and the unity of the Jewish people, **“one nation on earth,”** must permeate every Jew in all the details of daily life, so that a harmonious unity is created between material and spiritual matters in one’s daily conduct, where spirituality and holiness are the governing and deciding factor.

And just as the education of a child in the realm of *bein adam l’chaveiro*—to have good relationships with his peers, respect for parents and elders, etc.—must begin from childhood, a point upon which everyone agrees, so too must a Jewish child be educated in the spirit of Torah and mitzvos from childhood. Only then is it a true and complete *chinuch*, a Torah *chinuch*, in accordance with the instruction of the wisest of all men: **“Educate the youth according to his way; even when he grows old, he will not depart from it”** (Mishlei 22:6).

Such an education—a **complete** *chinuch*—is the objective of the educational institutions of Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch, which have already raised generations of **complete** Jews, **Tmimim**, both in *bein adam l’makom* and in *bein adam l’chaveiro*; an education that is permeated with love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Israel—the [three](#_ftn_1323) loves that are united and integrated in one’s daily conduct.

This is also the driving force that gives them the strength of *mesiras nefesh* to strengthen, spread, and revitalize Torah-Judaism in this country and in all other parts of the world.

This year, taking into account the major undertaking of the [new](#_ftn_1324) building for the central Lubavitcher yeshiva, it is to be hoped that all friends of the yeshiva will make a special effort on the occasion of this annual celebration to provide the necessary help and support for the yeshiva, so that it may continue its vital work.

May the Almighty grant success to each and every one of you to the fullest extent, in this endeavor as well as in all your affairs, both communal and personal, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With honor and blessing for great success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

Moving from one subject to another, although it warrants a letter of its own: special thanks for the most precious gift—a photocopy of a notebook of Chassidus from the estate of the late R' Avraham Chaim Rosenbaum, one of the famous Chassidim of his time. He is mentioned in the memoirs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in several places, and I believe it is also printed in Sefer HaSichos – Summer 5700 (p. 120). As a special personal note, I have perused what you also sent me: the two books, **Tzofayich Tzefas** and **Nasi V’Sofer**. As is the custom of Jewish men—a custom of ancient days—to offer comments, I will offer at least one: the surprise that the book **Nasi V’Sofer** contains no pictures other than the one at the beginning of the book, nor any facsimiles, nor a list of the books, maamarim, etc., that were published by him. Surely they will include all of this in the next edition, which will appear soon. Perhaps due to the pressure of time, it was not included in this volume.

## 9828

[9828](#_ftn_1338)

[B"H](#_ftn_1339), 22 Shevat, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Menachem [Begin](#_ftn_1340), shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

Rabbi Hodakov, shlita, conveyed to me the content of your letter dated 14 Shevat, regarding the bochurim who wish to come here to study Torah for a period of time, which is contingent upon a special permit, etc.

First and foremost, I wish to express my heartfelt gratitude to you for your personal interest and attention to this matter.

Regarding the matter itself: although, as you wrote, an exit permit for bochurim of this age is not a simple matter, we are not speaking of bochurim who have already been drafted into the IDF, but rather of bochurim whose heart’s desire is to come and study Torah here for a period of time, and who are convinced that here they will make great strides in their studies, their worldview, and so on. [It is well known](#_ftn_1341) that success in study is greater when it takes place in a location that one’s heart desires.

Furthermore, the guidance that the students receive here emphasizes recognizing and cherishing the responsibility placed upon them to utilize their strengths for the benefit of the many, whether in the field of education or as leaders in communities in Yisrael, with the added emphasis that upon the conclusion of their period of study and education, they will return to their place. In practice, all the students of the aforementioned type who have come here from Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh, have returned to Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh, after completing their course of study, and their time here has brought blessing not only to them, but also to Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh.

An additional benefit provided by the students coming from Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh, is that their connection with the students here influences their peers for the good, and also makes them cherish the Land and awakens in them the desire to travel to Eretz Yisrael to study for a period of time. Indeed, for years we have had a program of student exchange, from there to here and from here to there, and consequently, some of the students from the U.S. who travel to Eretz Yisrael to study remain there permanently.

"By the way," it is worth noting—though not for publication—another point: it is in the nature of young people to possess intense ambition and energy. If they are hindered from utilizing their strengths in a positive direction, this often causes them to utilize their strengths in undesirable directions and matters. This is an additional reason not to stand in their way in fulfilling their good aspiration.

In light of the above, my opinion is clear: when we see that there are bochurim, "dwellers of the tents," imbued with a serious aspiration to toil in Torah, and they believe that here they will make great strides in their studies and education, they are worthy of assistance in this. And as mentioned, the benefit of this is not only for them, but for the good of the entire people and for Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh, in particular.

However, the request must come from the Yeshiva administration in Eretz Yisrael, which will testify on their behalf, etc.

Thank you very much in advance for your assistance in this.

With respect and blessing and regards,

**M. Schneerson**

[9829](#_ftn_1342)

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Your letter was received with a significant delay, in which you write regarding [Name], may he live and be well, who suffers from asthma, and you ask if he would be able to manage in Brooklyn, etc., particularly in his profession, electronics.

Although this is entirely outside my field, as I have heard from several similar cases, the climate in Brooklyn is not suitable for those who suffer from asthma, and they travel to Texas and the like. Incidentally, it is difficult there from the perspective of Yiddishkeit. Regarding finding employment in the field of electronics, to my regret, I cannot offer advice on this.

However, I have the obligation to note that according to the Torah—the Torah of life, which is the instruction for life and the source of life—the [departure](#_ftn_1343) from Eretz Yisrael is not a simple matter, unless there are extremely significant reasons. If not, it is not advisable, neither from a spiritual perspective nor from a material one. Please forgive me.

With respect and blessing.

Regarding the time after a *histalkus*—generally, "it is very easy for his students (including all who walk 'in the straight path that he taught us') to receive their portion from the essential *ruach* of their master, etc., and not merely its radiance," "since it is not within a vessel nor in a physical place."

And after twenty years and more—for we have the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that from the age of twenty one is recognized as possessing his father's estate (and we have the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory: "Students are called children, and the master is called father").

And according to the explanation of our Alter Rebbe regarding this statement of our Sages, of blessed memory—it is understood that from that time on, there is an increase in vitality, desire, *taanug*, and the activities that follow from this.

And through all this, we also hasten the end of our exile and draw closer the Geulah, the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and with a blessing for success in the above and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is my participation, *bli neder*.

## 9831

[9831]

[B"H], 30th of the month of Shevat, which is Rosh Chodesh Adar Rishon, 5730. Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

At the beginning of the period of twenty years and more since the histalkus-hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of our generation, it was noted that after the histalkus—in general—it is "very easy for his students (including all those who walk 'in the straight path that he taught us') to receive their portion from the aspect of the essence of their Rebbe’s ruach, etc., and not merely their radiance," "since it is not within a vessel and not in a physical place."

And now that twenty years and more have passed—we have the teaching of our Sages that from twenty years old, one is recognized in the property of his father (and our Sages teach: the students are called children and the Rebbe is called a father).

And according to the explanation of our Alter Rebbe on this teaching of our Sages, it is understood that from this point on, there is an increase in vitality, in ratzon, in taanug, and in the good deeds that come about through this.

This is the demand of the hour and the opportune time to make a true accounting of all activities during the twenty years since the histalkus—activities in accordance with the demands of the Baal HaHilula during his lifetime in this world, and in all three pillars upon which the world stands:

—The world as it is commonly understood, and this "small world," which is man—

Torah, avodah (this is tefillah), and gemilus chasadim (mitzvos).

The purpose is to complete what is lacking and to add and elevate them from here on in.

One begins with engagement in Torah (nigleh and Chassidus)—with the prerequisite of the avodah of tefillah—and concludes with the performance of mitzvos, good and illuminating deeds.

And in all of these—with mesiras nefesh (which is the ratzon) and with simcha and Chassidic vitality and light.

May it be the will that this comes about in practice and with great success, until it is seen tangibly—in the words of the Baal HaHilula:

"Fortunate are we, how good is our portion in the avodah of the heart, and how pleasant is our lot in the avodah of the mind, and how beautiful is our inheritance to see and feel Elokus in everything, and to complete the supreme intent to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower worlds."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9833

[9833](#_ftn_1366)

[B"H](#_ftn_1367), 1 Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the activists and friends of the Beis Rivkah schools – in general, and to the participants in the annual Melaveh Malkah – in particular,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

The annual Melaveh Malkah is taking place this year in the middle of the [month](#_ftn_1368) of Adar Rishon, which is an additional month in the **leap year** (*ibur-year*).

The [concept](#_ftn_1369) of a leap year is, as is well known, connected to the setting of our Yomim Tovim at their proper time.

Our Jewish calendar is set according to the cycle of the moon, but since the lunar year falls behind the solar year by approximately eleven days, we have a leap year every two or three years, with an additional month, in order to complete the time, so that our Yomim Tovim should fall out at their proper time of the year (Pesach in the spring, Sukkos in the autumn, etc.).

However, like all matters in Jewish life, which beyond their own specific content also contain general guidance for each and every one of us in our daily lives, so too is it with the leap year.

The lesson of the leap year is: A Jew can, in one year, perfect that which he missed in previous years.

Furthermore: Just as the leap year is also an "extra year" (*iber-yor*) in that it does not merely complete the lagging days, but also gives "in addition" for the future—so too, it is not enough to merely perfect what was missed; it is necessary to also give "in addition" for the future.

I hope that on the occasion of the annual Melaveh Malkah, when the achievements of the Beis Rivkah schools in the past years are noted, consideration will also be given to the fact that with a little more effort, one could certainly accomplish much more.

And surely all the activists and friends of Beis Rivkah, who appreciate the vital importance of these educational institutions *al taharas hakodesh*, will accept the necessary resolutions, *bemaaseh b’poel*, not only to complete what could have been accomplished in the past years, but truly with "in addition" and an increase for the future, so that this current leap year should be for Beis Rivkah an "extra year" as mentioned above.

Hashem Yisbarach will certainly not remain behind, *Chas V’shalom*, and will bless each and every one with additional blessings in everything they need, together with their families, in both material and spiritual matters.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9834

[9834](#_ftn_1373)

[B"H](#_ftn_1374), Rosh Chodesh Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. [Chaim](#_ftn_1375) Landau,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive your regards through our friend Mr. Shlomo Maidanchik, Chairman of the Kfar Chabad Committee, during his visit here in connection with the [twentieth anniversary](#_ftn_1376) of the passing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on the past 10th of Shevat.

He also told me about your work in developing what lies beneath the ground, etc. You have surely heard the [well-known saying](#_ftn_1377) of our master, the Baal Shem Tov, in explanation of the [verse](#_ftn_1378), "For you shall be a land of desire" (*eretz chefetz*). He explains that every son and daughter of Yisrael is likened to land, in which all treasures and desirable qualities are hidden; one need only reveal them through digging and development—sometimes by removing a relatively thin layer of soil, and sometimes by digging deep. So it is with every single Yid: within their soul and neshamah are hidden and preserved treasures, virtues, and character traits beyond measure; one must simply bring them from potential into action.

This is, in essence, one of the foundations of the teachings of Chassidus in general, and Chabad Chassidus in particular: to reveal the good within every Yid, through ahavas Yisrael, [and as water](#_ftn_1379) reflects the face, so does the heart of one person reflect another. This, too, is one of the virtues of the "treasured people" (*am segulah*), that the heart of [Yisrael](#_ftn_1380) is awake.

I wish you much success in your work, in both senses of the term, especially since, according to the regards I received, your heart is awake to the problems of our generation—not only the economic ones, but the spiritual and moral ones as well.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9842

[9842](#_ftn_1413)

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 9850 

B"H, 5 Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

In response to your letter from the first day of Rosh Chodesh Adar...

In general, it is understood that when there is a conflict between an individual and the many, the Halacha follows the many; meaning, one must not endanger the many for the sake of saving an individual.

However, on the other hand, one must certainly find several ways so that the individual does not come to danger—for example, through isolation in a manner that she will not have close contact with the students, or by housing her in a private home where she will be cared for until her condition improves, and naturally, in a private religious home, etc. Indeed, there have already been several similar cases in educational institutions, and they did something similar to...

May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

It is my hope that you have already received regards and a report from here, from those who visited here for the farbrengens of Yud-Tes Shevat, before and after, and especially from the one who won the raffle among those who participated, and who served as their representative. And thank you in advance for writing in appropriate detail regarding this as well.

With respect and blessing,

P.S. Enclosed is a letter to the aforementioned so that you may deliver it to her with additional explanation if necessary, and thank you.

## 9851

[9851](#_ftn_1446)

B"H, 5 Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letters were received, and may Hashem, who oversees each and every one with *hashgacha pratis*, bless you with everything you need.

Regarding what you wrote about *nedarim* (vows), you should certainly refrain from making vows in the future. As for those made in the past, you should request *hataras nedarim* (the annulment of vows) and they will be annulled; there is no room for any concern or worry, *chas v'shalom*. Rabbi Chaim Yaakov [Schlamme](#_ftn_1447] *shlita* will certainly be able to arrange the matter of the *nedarim* for you, and you should put them out of your mind.

With blessings for good news regarding all of the above.

## 9852

[9852](#_ftn_1449)

By the Grace of Hashem, 7 Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the World Headquarters of N’shei U’bnos Chabad,
May Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

[On](#_ftn_1450) various occasions, I have already drawn attention to the necessity of strengthening the matter of **tzniyus**. However, taking into account the general situation in this area, I find it necessary to issue a most urgent appeal regarding this matter today.

From the standpoint of Torah, there is no need to elaborate on the importance of tzniyus. It is sufficient to note that our holy Torah, which is called **Toras Chaim** (the Torah of life)—because it is the true guide in all areas of daily life and ensures a dignified and truly happy life—emphasizes the matter of tzniyus very strongly, and in certain respects even more than in other areas of daily conduct. Thus, tzniyus is one of the **fundamental foundations** of Jewish life, as it is written in the verse: **"And walk humbly (hatznei leches) with your G-d."**

From the [reward](#_ftn_1453) that is promised in the Torah, the Gemara, and the Zohar for observing tzniyus, and from the accounts of our Sages, of blessed memory, regarding how Jewish women in various generations merited extraordinary Divine blessings in the merit of tzniyus—blessings not only for themselves but also for their husbands, children, and grandchildren—it is easy to understand how great is the importance and significance of conduct characterized by tzniyus.

On the other hand, the severity and warnings regarding the tragic consequences, Heaven forbid, of not observing tzniyus (as this is explicitly described in chapter 3 of Yeshayahu, etc.) leave not the slightest doubt regarding the seriousness of the matter.

There are those who, due to their ignorance of Torah in general and the matter of tzniyus in particular, think that the laws, ordinances, and customs associated with tzniyus "limit" the Jewish woman, rob her of her social rights, or infringe upon her honor, and the like.

This is an entirely false perception. The truth is the exact opposite: the holy Torah and our Sages, of blessed memory, emphasize countless times the honor and splendor of the Jewish daughter and woman, and many ordinances were instituted specifically to protect and preserve their honor and dignity. In this context, the well-known verse is often cited: **"All the honor of the king's daughter is inward"** (Tehillim 45:14). The Torah designates the Jewish woman as "splendid" (**kavodah**) and a "king's daughter" (**bas melech**), but demands that this be expressed in a manner of **pnimiyus** (inwardness), of **tzniyus**.

But even from a purely human standpoint, one can see, especially in recent years, to what the collapse of tzniyus can lead. The shameless "fashions" in women's clothing, aimed at arousing the lowest [inclinations](#_ftn_1454) of the *nefesh habehamis*, express the degradation of the "modern" world regarding the most elementary foundations of morality. The lawlessness and *pritzus*, Heaven forbid, of a large part of today's youth have led to shattering tragedies in many homes. It is certain that if that same youth had been raised on the foundations of tzniyus in accordance with our holy Torah, many tragedies would have been avoided and many young lives would not have been destroyed.

In light of the above, I hold that the matter of tzniyus must be placed as one of the main points on the agenda of responsible Jewish circles.

Especially as the central body of all branches of N’shei U’bnos Chabad in various parts of the world, it is your urgent duty at this moment to undertake an intensive campaign to stir the Jewish public, especially Jewish women's organizations—whatever their specific purpose may be—so that the question of tzniyus becomes integrated into their practical activities.

Jewish mothers must be alerted to the danger of neglecting tzniyus in the upbringing of their daughters.

The administrations of educational institutions for girls, of **all** ages, must be alerted to be more meticulous regarding the matter of tzniyus in their institutions, and to educate the students that tzniyus is the most beautiful *middah*, the crown of the Jewish daughter and woman.

One must strive to convince all those who understand and observe tzniyus that they have a responsibility for their sisters and must influence them, whether through word and especially through exemplary conduct, so that they should strengthen the matter of tzniyus in their homes and circles.

It is high time that Jewish women and daughters recognize their Jewish pride and their independence from the false, deceptive, and entirely empty "fashions" of the surrounding environment—fashions that have no content other than the greed of those who have a financial interest in them.

And in the merit of strengthening and spreading the matter of tzniyus in all areas of daily life, may the Almighty grant that the blessings which the Torah promises for observing tzniyus with *hiddur* (beautification) be fulfilled, and fulfilled to the fullest extent, especially in true Jewish *nachas* from children and grandchildren, with health and *parnassah* in abundance, with much joy together with one's husband, for long days and good years.

With blessings for outstanding success and for good tidings regarding all the above.

This is for the good of the individual, the good of the many, and the good of the collective.
