## 9854

[9854](#_ftn_1460)

By the Grace of G-d
10 Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Nechama Lifshitz
Greetings and Blessings!

I have just received your letter of January 22, and I thank you very much for your good wishes.

It gave me pleasure to receive news of your genuine success in London, especially since I hope that, in connection with and as a continuation of our conversation when you were here, your success will be utilized—by you and by others—to bring Jews closer to Yiddishkeit, true Yiddishkeit. Upon this depends the survival and the strength of Jews, wherever they may be and under whatever conditions they find themselves: whether these are conditions of oppression and external restrictions, or internal strife and conflict. In all of this, Jews must possess extraordinary strength to be able to resist and to succeed.

It is a certain fact, as one sees from the multi-thousand-year history of our people, that in the end, Jews prevail. However, it is a pity for the time, and a pity for the souls—Heaven forbid—and also for the bodies, that suffer due to the alienation, or the insufficient closeness and connection, of some Jews to certain parts of Yiddishkeit.

In essence, while the highest importance lies in a Jewish heart and Jewish feeling, both of which stem from the Jewish neshamah, this must be expressed through practical maasim. And just as one must be alive every day and all day long, so too must it be evident in a person’s daily life through their actions that they are a Jew, and that these actions are performed by a Jew in order to connect them with their source: they eat differently than others, conduct their business differently than others, and so on. Needless to say, when a Shabbos or a Yom Tov arrives, the entire day is different from other days of the year. This is not like other nations, where the difference is expressed in the fact that one is a workday and the other a day of rest; rather, as Jews call it: *vochendige teg* (weekdays) and *Shabbos’dige* and *Yom Tov’dige teg*—that is, holy days, in contrast to *vochendikeit* (mundane weekdays). Rest is merely a detail and a [consequence](#_ftn_1461) of holiness.

Having gone through what you have, you yourself have seen how all other approaches to ensuring the survival of the Jewish people have gone bankrupt. The only thing that sustains us is when a Jew is connected to Simchas Torah and to a shul; this sustains the Jew until the possibility arises for them to conduct themselves as a Jew in all details: to learn Torah—simply put, the Shulchan Aruch and mitzvos—and to perform them openly. Then, Simchas Torah fulfills its true function: the Jew rejoices with the Torah, which becomes **their** [Torah](#_ftn_1462) (from the word *hora’ah*—instruction) throughout the entire year, and the Torah rejoices with them, seeing that it is not something they keep in a museum, but a **Toras Chaim** that permeates their life.

I hope that, as we spoke when we parted, you will for many years utilize your opportunities to awaken in those you meet a deep connection to Yiddishkeit, and—now that we can speak freely—to add to this the content and spirit of what is written above, so that they may demonstrate their Jewish pride in the street as well. The logical and only possible conclusion of this is simple: to eat Jewish (kosher), to speak Jewish (without lashon hara, etc.), and in general to conduct oneself on weekdays, Shabbos, and Yom Tov as described above.

With wishes for continued success and good tidings.

P.S. Naturally, I felt pained seeing the publicity that was made regarding the situation and matter of [your](#_ftn_1464) good friends there. I hope, however, that our discussion about this will bring benefit in future cases, so that at least regarding them, one will follow the correct path, so that a good outcome may result for them, not, Heaven forbid, the opposite.

P.P.S. I take the liberty of adding the following remark, which was naturally uncomfortable to make when we met in the presence of other people. It is that I hope you are taking action and being careful regarding the situation and arrangements of Mrs. Nechama Lifshitz (I mean you yourself). As long as the initial impression, the warm reception, etc., is still strong, you should secure for yourself a suitable arrangement—including, simply put, settling yourself physically as well, according to the well-known folk saying: strike the iron while it is hot.

## 9857

[9857](#_ftn_1473)

B”H, Purim Katan, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished,
Engaged in the needs of the community,
Rabbi Shmuel Tuvia [Stern](#_ftn_1474),

Shalom u’Bracha!

Surely your honor has heard that on the tenth of Shevat just passed, a period of [twenty](#_ftn_1475) years was completed since the passing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation.

It is our firm hope that, just as with all days of remembrance in Yisrael—where the purpose is to draw the essence of the day into all the days of the year, in actual deed, for [deed](#_ftn_1476) is the essential thing—so too will this day of remembrance awaken in the heart of each and every one of us, and within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, the desire and energy to continue the activities of the Baal HaHillula in strengthening Torah and Yiddishkeit in daily life; activities imbued with Ahavas Hashem, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Yisrael, [which are all one](#_ftn_1477).

I was pleased to learn that your honor is receiving an honor related to Yerushalayim, the Holy City, may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days. Surely, for one such as yourself, there is no need to emphasize the [statement](#_ftn_1478) of our Sages of blessed memory that a name is significant, especially regarding Yerushalayim, where the precision of the name is in its absolute completeness. Our Sages of blessed memory explained (Tosafos, s.v. *Har*, Taanis 16a, based on Midrash Bereishis Rabbah, ch. 56) that it is called so after "Yirah" (fear/awe), as called by Avraham, and "Shalem" (complete), as called by Shem, son of Noach. [The Alter Rebbe](#_ftn_1479), author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, explains that the name indicates the completeness of Yirah. Since Yerushalayim, the Holy City, is called the [City](#_ftn_1480) of the Great King, it is understood that its influence—[in the words of the verse](#_ftn_1481), "and the word of Hashem from Yerushalayim"—must be in the completeness of Yiras Hashem, as must all activities connected with Yerushalayim.

May it be the will of Hashem that your honor acts upon all of the above by fully utilizing your strengths and your capacity for influence, in a manner of *mosif v’holech* (increasing and continuing), with joy and a glad heart.

With respect and with blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 9860

[9860](#_ftn_1493)

B”H, 17 Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, which was received with a significant delay:

In general, it is well known [from the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory](#_ftn_1494) that the Holy One, Blessed be He, only demands according to the capacity of each individual, and He does not deal harshly with His creations. This is also understood through logic: since He, may He be blessed, is the Creator and knows everything, there is no room for Him to demand of the work of His hands something without giving them the strength to fulfill that demand.

From this, it is also understood that when a person faces trials which—in his opinion, or in truth—are greater than those of another, this itself is proof that Hashem has given him greater, more elevated strengths to overcome them completely. And when he reveals and utilizes these elevated strengths to their fullest, he thereby receives a greater reward than those who did not have trials to that degree.

And if this applies to everyone, how much more so regarding a young man who still needs to establish a home in Israel and settle into family life, etc., which are founded upon the trials of the years preceding it.

Regarding your question on how one can influence his peers in his educational institution, it is known that there are two ways to achieve this: First, through words that come from the heart, [which we are promised](#_ftn_1495) enter the heart and accomplish their effect. Furthermore, and most importantly, through a living example; the influence of one who "preaches beautifully" is not comparable to one who "preaches beautifully and practices beautifully." [1496] On the contrary, one must be even more meticulous in personally fulfilling what he demands of others. Since less is always expected of the one being influenced than of the one influencing, in order for it to be accepted to a certain degree by the one being influenced, the meticulousness must be greater in the one influencing—and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Regarding your writing about a study schedule: in general, when studying in an educational institution, one is bound by the institution's schedules. As for the time remaining at your disposal, you should sit down with educators who know you, your capacity for diligence, your grasp of material, etc., as it depends on this how to best utilize the time available to you in order to ascend in yiras shamayim, the fulfillment of mitzvos, etc.

I trust you know of and observe the three daily study portions that are equal for every soul, namely the Chitas (Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya) study portions.

With blessings for success in going from strength to strength and for good news regarding all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 9861

[9861](#_ftn_1498)

B"H, 18 Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable Rabbi, G-d-fearing, esteemed, and distinguished
Rabbi Dovid Shauman, Chief Rabbi,
And with him, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker
Mr. Chaim Vitali, President of the Central Synagogue,
Milan

Peace and Blessing!

With pleasure and feelings of gratitude, I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Bo, containing blessings and heartfelt wishes in connection with the completion of [twenty](#_ftn_1499) years since the passing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael of our generation, on Yud Shevat.

May it be the will of Hashem that, just as with all days of remembrance in the life of the Jewish people—where the purpose is to carry the essence of the day into all the days of the year through actual deed, for [deed](#_ftn_1500) is the essential thing—so too may this day of remembrance awaken and strengthen in each and every one of us, and within the entire Jewish people, the desire and energy to continue the activities of the Baal HaHillula: strengthening Torah and traditional Judaism in daily life, activities imbued with love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of a fellow Jew, [which are all one](#_ftn_1501).

May those who offer blessings be blessed by Hashem, the source of all blessings, with everything they need and for all that is theirs, [as it is said](#_ftn_1502), "And I will bless those who bless you."

With respect and with blessings for outstanding success and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 9862

[9862](#_ftn_1505)

B"H, 24 Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent scholar,
Rabbi [Adin](#_ftn_1506) Steinsaltz, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

Thank you for the report—even if extremely brief—[regarding the delivery of the personal regards](#_ftn_1507) [at the beginning of the parsha](#_ftn_1508) from me, and regarding his visit here in general. I am sure that in time you will inform me about the delivery of the maamar of the Tzemach Tzedek and regarding the final decision concerning the future of the study circle, as you had some concerns and doubts about this.

[Regarding your question](#_ftn_1509) about participating in a debate or an exchange of views concerning Christianity and the like: considering the confusion of minds and the alarming blurring of all values in our current era, my opinion is in the absolute negative.

My reasoning is that even if we were to assume that your participation in such a meeting carries no concern at all from any side or aspect, in any such matter, the intent of the participants in the meeting is not what is most significant—and certainly not the intent of the speaker—but rather the reaction of the public. This includes not only those present at the meeting, but the public that will hear about the meeting. This is an immediate reaction, as has been seen in practice in the United States as well. [And the world is one,](#_ftn_1510) and it is considered worthwhile and correct to organize such meetings, [in the language of](#_ftn_1511) Daniel, "Many shall purify themselves, and make themselves white, and be refined" [etc.](#_ftn_1512) (without paying any attention at all to the continuation of the verse: "but the wicked shall do wickedly; and none of the wicked shall understand; but they that are wise shall understand," and the wise will understand).

An immediate result of this will be that everyone will think that he is worthy of that mantle—to contemplate such matters, to debate them, and also to decide upon them. This is an open door, and not just a door, but a great breach—a breach in both senses of the word. Furthermore, regarding the one who engages in these matters, he is transgressing an explicit prohibition from the Torah (Rambam, Hilchos Avodas Kochavim, Chapter 2, Halacha 2). Moreover, as I have seen and witnessed, this engagement with the books and the subjects, etc., leads to a confusion of opinions, to the point that through a lack of knowledge, one arrives at false and corrupt views, and even views that are the opposite of faith. And he does not feel or realize that he has not only strayed from the path, but "you shall stray," etc. [1513]

What is written above holds true even if there were some benefit to these meetings and debates; all the more so, as until now I have not seen or found even one man or woman who has been brought closer to the matters of Judaism, our Torah, and its mitzvos through this (see there in Rambam, Halacha 3).

Certainly, for someone like you, it is superfluous to emphasize that since we are dealing with a matter of Torah law, [and one of the](#_ftn_1514) things for which one must be killed rather than transgress, etc., even if it were only an accessory or a doubt, etc., it would be treated with stringency. All the more so when we have seen tangibly from the results of past meetings that they have gone beyond the realm of doubt.

To make it easier for you to refrain from participating as stated, let it be known—and surely it is known even without this—that despite all the declarations that the purpose of the meetings is not for incitement, etc., the reality is precisely the opposite. The majority of those who organize these meetings do not have the goal of finding the truth, but rather have secondary motives, and sometimes even motives that are the opposite of the truth. However, there is no need to speak and elaborate on a point that is not in the stature of Israel.

The conclusion of all the above is that if you are able to prevent others from participating in these meetings—and it goes without saying regarding yourself—it is best to cancel such meetings altogether. May a blessing come upon you, and the merit of the many will depend on you. As mentioned, this is a matter that touches upon the fundamentals of faith.

From the above, my position is also understood regarding participation in periodicals and journals whose purpose is such meetings.

As for the well-known question, "What will the perplexed of our generation do if they hear only the arguments of the idolaters and the voice of the faithful of Israel is not heard?" the answer is simple: For this, there is no need for debates and meetings, and especially meetings with those [whom it is doubtful](#_ftn_1515) whether it is permitted according to the law of our Torah to look at their faces. Rather, one should hold lectures, or in the style of the faithful of Israel, speak about the fundamentals of our faith, its foundations and details, and explain them well and with the force appropriate to our Torah—which is the Torah of truth and the Torah of life—not to be ashamed before the mockers (see Tur and Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, beginning of Siman 1). [And words](#_ftn_1516) that come from the heart enter the heart and perform their function. However, one should not confuse the listener with incorrect premises, even for the sake of refuting them.

May it be His will that you utilize your talents and knowledge, etc., in the best and truest way—[good](#_ftn_1517) for Heaven and good for the creations as well, permeated with Chassidic light and vitality, which is called the Tree of Life, in which there is no mixture of evil, G-d forbid (see Iggeres HaKodesh, Siman 26), utilizing your powers to their fullest and with joy and a good heart.

With blessings for success and good tidings in all the above.

P.S. [Since](#_ftn_1518) Professor [Zeev](#_ftn_1519) Green, shlita, will be visiting the Holy Land, may it be built and established, next week, it would be good if you could meet and speak. Perhaps it would also be appropriate for him to participate in the class for scientists that you give. You can get in touch with Dr. Green through Rabbi Zevin, shlita, who will know his address.

[9863](#_ftn_1520)

B"H, 24 Adar I, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished,
Engaged in the needs of the community and the dissemination of Chassidus, etc.
[Rashi](#_ftn_1521) shlita,

## 9864

[9864](#_ftn_1526)

[B"H](#_ftn_1527), 1 Adar Sheni, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 28th Annual Dinner of the "Netzivei HaYeshiva" Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal

May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

We bring about a [merit](#_ftn_1528) on an auspicious day — good things happen on good days. This year, the annual dinner takes place on **9 Adar Sheni**, the historic day when my father-in-law, the Rebbe — the founder of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal — arrived in America 30 years ago (also in a leap year).

In this context, it is worth recalling the unforgettable words that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, said immediately upon setting foot on American soil:

My coming here, with the help of Hashem, is so that, through the kindness of Hashem, I may continue my work in disseminating Torah, yiras shamayim, and avodah, and my involvement for the benefit of all our brethren, the Children of Israel, here in this land as well... (to create) a broad campaign of awakening for the study of Torah, so that Torah should illuminate the Jewish street and home. (Sefer HaSichos 5700, p. 5).

At that time, there were many prominent baalei-batim who expressed great doubts as to whether this task, which the leader of Israel, the Nasi of the generation, had set for himself upon his arrival here, could be realized. However, this did not weaken his resolve; on the contrary, it only doubled his mesiras nefesh.

His answer to all these doubts was simple:

"America is no different!" The Torah and mitzvos that are valid for Jews everywhere are also valid in America. And since Jews in America, too, must live according to Torah and raise their children in the way of Torah and mitzvos, it is certain that the Almighty has given the ability to carry this out. It only required the proper resolve, with the correct, earnest, and heartfelt approach.

Now, 30 years later, one can clearly see the extraordinary success, with the help of Hashem, that can be achieved in the field of disseminating Torah with yiras shamayim and kosher chinuch — if one only desires it with truth and acts with mesiras nefesh.

And one of the best proofs of this is Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal, the pride of Canadian Jewry and one of the greatest fortresses of Torah and chinuch al taharas hakodesh on the American continent.

I greet the esteemed askanim and friends of the yeshiva who are partners in its development. I hope to Hashem that the success of the past years will strengthen their resolve and double their assistance, to help this holy institution ascend [from strength](#_ftn_1530) to strength.

May the Almighty bless everyone together and each one individually to do this with breadth, with joy and a good heart, with success and expansion in their personal needs as well, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With honor and blessing for success and good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9865

[9865](#_ftn_1531)

[Rosh Chodesh Adar Sheni, 5730]

[In response](#_ftn_1532) to your inquiry regarding your arrangements for the coming year—

Since you have merited holy work—the education of the daughters of Yisrael in the path of our holy Torah—it is understood that you should continue in this, in a place and in a manner where your success will be greatest. That is to say, in an institution where the language spoken by the students, their nature, and their upbringing **etc.**, are the same as yours were when you were a student like them.

Therefore, the priority over all other possibilities is that you continue as a teacher at the Beis Rivkah seminary where you studied.

Regarding how a homemaker should manage her home, and where to live—you should consult with the seminary administration, and it will certainly be possible to arrange all of this.

Regarding New York **and the like**—after all (**in addition** to what was stated above), it is not advisable to expose yourself to the challenges that arise here.

## 9886

[9886](#_ftn_1533)

B”H, 3 Adar II, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs and is a man of many accomplishments, etc.
Rabbi [Moshe](#_ftn_1534) Munk, shlita

Greetings and blessings!

I am writing to acknowledge, albeit with some delay, the receipt of your letter and the booklet "Torah im Derech Eretz." Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the scientific institute, etc.: given the current situation, and since it is linked to a program of continuing studies in an atmosphere that is entirely inappropriate—as we discussed at length during your visit, and I do not wish to dwell on this distressing matter which does not redound to the credit of Yisrael—I cannot, for the time being, participate in a program that must ultimately lead to the aforementioned result. I ask for your forgiveness.

Surely, it is possible to find another, better way to resolve the problem we discussed, which you also touch upon in your letter now.

Moving from one subject to a related one: I do not know if this is relevant to you, but since you have an acquaintance with the management of the science institute, it is my duty to point out another fundamental issue that I have discussed orally with their members and also with their representatives in other countries. It is this: It is essential, as a matter of principle, to explicitly and clearly state that the institute has no authority to issue halachic rulings or to provide practical halachic guidance. This is the exclusive domain of Rabbis acting in their capacity as Rabbis and *morei hora’ah* (decisors of law), and not the domain of an engineer or a doctor—even if they possess rabbinic ordination—if they are ruling on Halacha in their capacity as scientists in their field.

In addition to many other reasons for this, there is a completely simple reason that requires no proof from books, for there is proof from actual experience. We see that such institutes that have sought to involve themselves in issuing halachic rulings—even if the intentions of the founders were desirable—after a year or so, it matters not, [and there arose](#_ftn_1535) a new king, and the results were destructive. Therefore, it is certain and simple that if the institute takes this authority upon itself, it is a matter that affects future generations, and the ultimate results will be a tragedy for generations.

I am aware that the institute has a special department called "Rabbanit," but in my opinion, no department of theirs, even a "Rabbanit" one, has the authority to issue a halachic ruling. There is no solution to this by announcing that it is only for theoretical Halacha and that for practical matters one should ask a Rabbi. For once they reveal a leniency in some matter, it will no longer occur to anyone to ask a Rabbi. Since Professor So-and-so, who is also a Rabbi, leans toward leniency, that is sufficient—and a word to the wise is enough.

It is understood that my intention is not to diminish the importance of the institute, but to emphasize that its role should only be to clarify the pros and cons, but not to decide which side carries more weight, whether for stringency or for leniency. The same applies to proposals. In every single question, they must emphasize that they are not coming to answer the question, but only to clarify all sides of the matter, similar to a court of law where the parties can present all kinds of arguments, but the final verdict belongs to the judge who will be [in those days](#_ftn_1536), [and who will be](#_ftn_1537) in his generation like Shmuel in his generation—the Rabbi and *moreh hora’ah* whose profession is the Rabbinate, and not the one who thinks that the authority is the one who understands the technique. As the [well-known](#_ftn_1538) saying goes, all the sciences are merely "perfumers and cooks" for the Torah, and not, G-d forbid, the other way around.

This is seemingly the place to elaborate on the subject of your booklet on Torah im Derech Eretz, especially as I saw it in Berlin itself, at Artilleriestraße 31. That was once the fortress of *yiras shamayim* for this approach, and yet, everyone there recognized the situation themselves and began sending their children to yeshivos that were entirely holy and contained no secular studies at all, despite the initial opposition to this. But ultimately, they realized that it was impossible otherwise. However, I do not wish to mix one matter with another.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. I will take the liberty of adding to the above the language of the Sma in Shulchan Aruch, Choshen Mishpat, siman 3, sub-paragraph 13, cited in *Netivos HaMishpat* there: "Do not sit with the community in any judgment, for I know that the rulings of laymen and the rulings of scholars are two opposites."

It is clear that this is not referring to a layman who is an *am ha'aretz* or who lacks ordination and is not a scholar, for if so, what is he teaching us? Certainly, the [Maharsha](#_ftn_1539) z”l would not have needed advice on this and proofs for the advice. Rather, it is speaking of a case where, were it not for the advice, there would seemingly be no concern about including this layman, and it is regarding this that the aforementioned warning comes.

The language is also certainly precise, that this is not a matter of mere stringency or a concern of leniency versus stringency in a place of doubt, but rather, as he states, that the ruling would be the opposite of the ruling of the scholars, and the matter is understood.

## 9867 

B"H, 7 Adar II, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
[Mr.] Yosef, known as Dr. Burg,

Shalom u’Bracha!

As we stand before the days of Purim, I take this opportunity, while sending you Purim greetings, to also express my gratitude for the publications you send me, most recently the booklet *Israel, Jerus. – Conference on Human Needs 19/69-6/16*.

Since it is an ancient Jewish custom to offer a comment or suggestion—in the spirit of "it comes to teach us good advice"—I wish to fulfill this custom, at the very least by expressing the hope that you will publish matters of Torah from time to time, as a remembrance of days of old, the days you studied in the yeshiva. Even though your engagement in communal needs does not facilitate the study of Torah or growth therein, it is the duty and privilege of every single Jew to overcome difficulties; on the contrary, "according to the effort is the reward."

May it be the will of Hashem that the concept of these days of Purim be fulfilled in each and every one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael: "The Jews had light, and gladness, and joy, and honor"—"light" refers to Torah, etc., and "honor" refers to tefillin—and may this be experienced through light, gladness, joy, and honor in the literal sense of the verse.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. For some time, I have had it in mind to write to you regarding the matter that follows, and I have been prompted about it several times. For various reasons, the writing was delayed, but better late than never.

The matter concerns an educational institution for children with special needs, etc., from religious homes. Although it seems to me that there are institutions of this type in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), they are not religious—at least not to the appropriate degree. And while I am not an expert in the planning of the Ministry of Welfare, it would seem that this falls within the scope of that ministry’s activities.

The importance and value of this matter, etc., certainly does not require length or explanation for someone like yourself. I will only recall the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "one only urges those who are already diligent," and "the deed is the essential thing."

As I have heard, there are several religious doctors and educators in Eretz Yisrael for whom this care and education is their specific profession. This means there would be no shortage of educators and doctors, and the matter depends only on a hand to organize it and the necessary resources.

May it be the will of Hashem that in this, too, you will bring me good news and I will hear good news, and thank you in advance.

## 9871

[9871]

[B"H], 11 Adar II, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

[To] Mr. Avraham, may he live and be well,

Shalom and blessing!

A few days ago, and again today, I happened to read about your seventieth jubilee. I join the chorus of those wishing you long life and good years. As is the Jewish custom, I immediately add the [statement] of our Sages: "Good to Heaven and good to people," which is the true good.

The essence of the month of Adar is not merely joy, but rather [increasing] in joy, [to the point] of "until one does not know."

I will take the liberty of expressing another of my wishes—though you will surely suspect me of this anyway—that the movement and shift of "returning to the source" may be fortified in your life through actual deed, in your practical, day-to-day life. This is especially true since you possess influence in a certain circle that is unlikely to receive such influence from anyone else; a bold (in both senses of the word) and surprising action on your part will surely lead many to see and do likewise.

In our times, there are many interpretations for every matter and thing, even contradictory and strange ones. But my intention in what I have said is in the [style] of the well-known "to know this child," or in the mother-tongue—quite simply. And since for several years in Yekaterinoslav you were specifically looking for that which is bold and against the current, there is nothing more against the current within your circle of admirers than a turn and change in the aforementioned direction.

It is simple that one does not begin to be meticulous in the performance of practical mitzvos just to show that one can go against the current, etc., but as a contributing factor, this trait of the soul is also active.

And as for the wonder of "what is different about today," the answer (if there is a need for one) is: the seventieth jubilee.

With respect, and with blessings for good and successful years and for good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Out of courtesy, I should have waited until I could gauge your reaction to this letter of mine, and only then express my hope that you will send your publications here (in addition to the first shipment: the book "Poems," two volumes). But since my letters are delayed more and more—which is to say that in any case I am not defined as a man who acts according to custom and the laws of protocol—I am appending this request to the margins of this letter.

## 9872

[9872](#_ftn_1587)

B"H, 17 Adar Rishon, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. [Shifra](#_ftn_1588) Yehudis, may she live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Adar Rishon and those preceding it,

Regarding your driving a car — as a general rule, one should strive not to be an "exception to the rule."

Since it is not at all customary in our community of Anash for a G-d-fearing woman to drive a car, why should you do so? [Especially since the incidents](#_ftn_1589) on the roads there have increased, etc.

It is understood that the car can belong to you for all intents and purposes, but the driving should be done by someone else.

With blessings for great success in your most important work of encouraging the spirits of widows and orphans, may they live, and bringing them closer to our Father in Heaven, and with tidings of good news in all your affairs.

Surely there were — within the framework of the aforementioned work — appropriate activities for these days of Purim.

## 9878

11 Nissan, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

Our Yomim Tovim—like all matters of Torah and mitzvos—possess both general, shared themes and unique, specific characteristics. The rich, inexhaustible content of the Yomim Tovim makes it possible to select specific points that can serve as specially tailored hints and directives for particular circumstances at a given time and place.

This is, of course, also true in connection with Pesach, and indeed with even greater force and significance, taking into account that Pesach is "the head of the festivals," and that the Yom Tov of Yetzias Mitzrayim is the birthday of the Jewish people.

***

The special importance of Pesach can also be seen from the fact that it is one of (no more than) two positive mitzvos for which the penalty for non-fulfillment is *kares*, Heaven forbid. These two mitzvos are: *milah* and *korban Pesach*. Both are also closely linked, for one who is uncircumcised cannot offer the *korban Pesach*. And of the two, Pesach is more stringent in this regard: for *milah*, there is an obligation to perform the *milah* even after the designated time has passed, but the *korban Pesach* can only be offered at its specific time and not later.

In one detail, however, the *korban Pesach* is entirely distinct from all other mitzvos and even other *korbanos*: it is not only the father who must be circumcised, but his children must also be circumcised. If he has a son whom he has not circumcised—whom he has not brought into the "bris olam" (eternal covenant) with the Ribono shel Olam—the father cannot (even) bring the *korban Pesach*!

***

Although the concept of *korbanos*, including the *korban Pesach*, is relevant only during the time of the Beis Hamikdash, and will only be renewed when the Beis Hamikdash is rebuilt by Moshiach Tzidkeinu, it is nonetheless well-known that **all** matters in Torah, which is eternal, contain within them clear and practical directives for daily life—at all times and in all places.

***

The Yom Tov of Pesach, which is named after the **korban Pesach**, underscores the supreme importance of *chinuch*—the education of Jewish children. In truth, one of the foundational aspects of the entire Seder is the *chinuch* of children—of every child, of all children—as is brought out in the Haggadah (*"Here the child asks,"* "The Torah speaks of **four** sons," *"And you shall tell your son,"* etc.). But the concept of the **korban Pesach** emphasizes in a most striking way how deeply the Jewish education of children touches not only the children, but the parents as well: if parents have not fulfilled their duty to their child and have not brought him into the eternal covenant with the Ribono shel Olam—in a manner that remains etched not only in the *neshamah* but also in the body (*"And My covenant shall be in your flesh as an eternal covenant"*), then it is not only that they rob their child, Heaven forbid, of the *bris olam* with the Ribono shel Olam and the blessings connected to that *bris* (and to the *korban Pesach*), but the parents themselves lose the ability to bring the *korban Pesach* with all the matters and blessings connected to it. And especially the reminder and awakening of *"Pesach is for Hashem... and I will pass over you"*—that the Ribono shel Olam has compassion on you, and even when undesirable things happen in the world—whether in *gashmius* or in *ruchnius*—He "passes over" you.

***

When the Jews were in Mitzrayim, the *korban Pesach* ensured that the "destroyer" (the plague) would not enter a Jewish home to seek victims. It was a matter of protecting the firstborn.

In our time, when Jews **everywhere** find themselves in *galus*—a *galus* in *gashmius* and a *galus* in *ruchnius*—some parents have unfortunately neglected the concept of the *korban Pesach*, as the content of this *korban* is explained in Torah: *"Draw out and take for yourselves sheep"*—withdraw your hands from *avodah zarah* and attach yourselves to *mitzvah* (turn away from foreign gods (ideals) and attach yourselves to *mitzvos*). The destroyer finds an open door to these homes and seeks to lead them away from the proper path, Heaven forbid, without distinction as to whether they are firstborn or not, boys or girls. The plague has spread into many Jewish homes, Heaven forbid.

And this is a direct result of the fact that some parents have not yet themselves turned away from foreign (and hostile to true Yiddishkeit) ideals, and even among those who themselves fulfill the *"draw out and take,"* they have cast off the yoke and responsibility to ensure that their children are raised from childhood in the path of true Yiddishkeit, the path of Torah and *mitzvos*. One does not have to look far today for the sad and tragic consequences of such an approach—sad and tragic consequences not only for the neglected children, but also for the parents who neglected them.

The Yom Tov of Pesach, and especially the concept of the *korban Pesach*, reminds us with the greatest emphasis that if Jews want them and their children to enjoy the *"and I will pass over you"* and, in general, the *"time of our freedom"*—to free themselves from all undesirable and harmful things, both internal (natural inclinations, etc.) and even more so from the harmful influences from without, at a time when the destroyer is roaming the streets and even in educational institutions—this can only be secured if they themselves reject all "avodah zarahs" and attach themselves to true Yiddishkeit, and give their children a thorough, Torah-true education from childhood on, in a way that should be **etched** into their body and their *neshamah*, by fulfilling Torah and *mitzvos* in **daily life**, **in actual deed**. Then one can hope and be certain that the parents together with the children, **all the children**, will be together at the Seder table and celebrate Pesach, the Yom Tov of the time of our freedom—liberation in all respects.

And this will also bring closer and hasten the true freedom—the *Geulah Amitis Ve'sheleimah* through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach and true freedom,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9879 

 11 Nissan, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and elevated individual, who seeks the good of his people and possesses noble character traits, a scion of a noble lineage, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Approaching the festival of Matzos, the season of our freedom, which is arriving for us and for all of Israel for good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and spiritual worries—from everything that hinders the avodah of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

And may this freedom and joy be drawn down into all the days of the entire year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as it is commanded to us in our Torah, the Torah of life, encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and night, as it is said: "In all your ways, know Him."

With appreciation, honor, and blessings for the holiday and for all good things,

**M. Schneerson**

With special pleasure, I received the news that you acted with alacrity and submitted your lofty contribution toward the publication and printing of the maamarim, etc., of the Alter Rebbe, most of which have not yet been published. Certainly, for one such as yourself, there is no need at all to describe the magnitude of the matter and its importance for the benefit of the individual and the benefit of the many. Indeed, there is also [the merit of] the alacrity in the delivery of the funds (see Likutei Torah of the Alter Rebbe, beginning of Parshas Noach; *Kesef HaKodashim* from the words "You have greatly longed for your father’s house"). And I believe I have already noted in the past the words of the Alter Rebbe in his Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 21, regarding the great virtue of alacrity, etc.

Despite the pressures of the holiday, it is my hope that even during these days, you will begin searching through the manuscripts to compare the aforementioned maamarim, etc., from notebook to notebook. This is especially true since some of the maamarim are taken from notebooks that were not in the manuscript treasury of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, but rather came into my possession later; therefore, comparison with what is found in the notebooks in the manuscript treasury of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, is even more essential.

My prayer and hope is that the merit of the many will stand by the publication—that it will be a refined work, words of the living G-d that give life to all those into whose hands they reach, reviving them in a way that they become a source of true life according to our Torah, within their own four cubits and in their entire environment, and in the manner—as the well-known expression goes—of spreading the wellsprings outward.

May this merit stand for you and for all that is yours for long and good lives in every respect, and may the merit of the many assist you.

## 9889

[9889](#_ftn_1656)

[B"H](#_ftn_1657), 25 Nissan, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. [Uri](#_ftn_1658) Zvi Greenberg

Greetings and blessings!

It has been a long time since I have heard from you, though of course I inquire about you, especially through our friend Mr. Hillel Seidman, who has also kept me informed—particularly in these days, [that your son](#_ftn_1659) is still serving in the IDF in the Paratroopers Brigade. May it be the will of Hashem that the verse be fulfilled in him, as well as in all those serving in the army of Israel: "And your camp shall be holy, and He shall see no shameful thing among you... for Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp to save you and to deliver your enemies before you" (Devarim 23:15, with a slight change in order).

After asking for your forgiveness for what follows, I feel I have no choice but to write this. The matter is as follows:

You are surely aware of the details of the problem regarding the "Who is a [Jew](#_ftn_1660)" law and the sequence of events. For someone like you, there is certainly no need to elaborate on the gravity of the matter, especially in the current situation. Therefore, the seriousness of the situation obligates every single person—even [the weak](#_ftn_1661) should say "I am a hero," and all the more so the hero, especially one who has influence over others—to publicize his opinion in bold letters that describe the matter in all its severity, seriousness, and vitality. In our generation, an orphaned generation in the footsteps of Moshiach, where the darkness is double and redoubled, it is imperative that immediately following the description must come the conclusion: that the matter cannot be rectified unless it is explicitly and emphatically defined in the phrasing of the law that it must be according to **Halacha**. For it is well known to all that there was a debate regarding the inclusion of this word, and they rejected it so that there would not be, as it were, a "dictatorship" of Halacha, and so on.

[I have spoken](#_ftn_1662) about this on several occasions, and I hope that echoes of these words have reached you as well. And although, as mentioned, for someone like you there is no need for explanation, in short, the summary of the matter is that the current phrasing of the law opens a wide breach without any restrictions, which means—Heaven forbid—a public declaration in the name of our people Israel who dwell in Eretz Yisrael, that from now on, we are abandoning and giving away, G-d forbid, Eretz Yisrael to all the nations of the world who wish to come and take it, the opposite of the Torah of Israel!

It is my strong hope that if you have already spoken your piece on the matter, you will not be satisfied with that, but will fulfill [the words of our Sages](#_ftn_1663) of blessed memory: ["You shall surely](#_ftn_1664) rebuke—even a hundred times." A hundred is not meant as an exaggeration; as emphasized in several places, our Torah, the Torah of truth, teaches us an approach here: that even when one has rebuked ninety-nine times and, Heaven forbid, it did not help, the mitzvah still stands in its full force—that he must rebuke, with the same intensity, the hundredth time. Especially since, after all, the heart of Israel is awake, and surely they will not need, Heaven forbid, to be rebuked many, many times, provided that they hear the words of rebuke from someone worthy of saying such things and with the appropriate intensity, and not listen to the opinion of those who entice, incite, and lead astray, who also claim that "if you grasp [too much](#_ftn_1665), you have not grasped."

Best regards to you. [We inquire](#_ftn_1666) about the welfare of your wife through you. Best regards to your wife, may she live and be well, and with wishes for a healthy and happy summer, both physically and spiritually, and with honor. Expecting good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I am sending this letter as urgent, because they have already invented another "argument" regarding the aforementioned problem and the like—that the matter is already at the stage of... status quo! After all, several weeks have already passed and no one is opening their mouth or chirping. To my argument, our Torah has a status quo of three and a half thousand years, and we are living, thank G-d... in a modern generation, [and "you shall bring out the old](#_ftn_1667) for the sake of the new." There is no need to elaborate on matters that do not speak to the benefit and pride of Israel.

May Hashem keep them alive

Peace and Blessing!

The [month](#_ftn_1674) of Iyar—during which, on the eleventh day, the annual gathering for the educational institution *al taharas hakodesh* "Oholei Torah" takes place—is distinguished from all other months by the fact that every day of this month carries the mitzvah of **Sefiras HaOmer**.

The concept of Sefiras HaOmer, as our [Sages of blessed memory relate](#_ftn_1675), began at the time of the Exodus from Egypt. The intent and the ultimate purpose of the Exodus was, after all, to receive the Torah at Mount Sinai [(“When you bring forth](#_ftn_1676) the people out of Egypt, you shall serve Hashem upon this mountain”). Thus, when Moshe Rabbeinu told the Jews in Egypt what the purpose of their liberation was, immediately upon leaving Egypt they began to count the days and weeks toward Kabbalas HaTorah. Seeing with what yearning Jews count the days toward Kabbalas HaTorah, Hashem gave us the mitzvah of Sefiras HaOmer.

Like all the narratives of our Sages of blessed memory, this story regarding Sefiras HaOmer also holds an important and permanent significance for all Jews, in all times, and in all places. And it is this: how precious a Jew must hold the Torah, and with what yearning, *hasmadah*, and *shekidah* Jews must study Torah and fulfill its mitzvos.

And this is, indeed, the mission of "Oholei Torah": to implant in the children the aforementioned yearning, *hasmadah*, and *shekidah* for Torah and mitzvos, which should express itself in their conduct in daily life.

We find ourselves now in the days of preparation for Kabbalas HaTorah, when every Jew, man and woman, must draw each day an increased measure from the wellspring of *ahavas haTorah v'hamitzvos* that is passed down to us as an inheritance from our forefathers, and utilize this regarding oneself and especially regarding the children—one’s own children and also all children, according to the interpretation of our Sages: **"And you shall teach them to your children"**—**these are the students** ([not necessarily your own students](#_ftn_1678)), the students of *chadaryim* and *yeshivos*. And when it comes to children, it is the nature of a person to ensure that the children receive the best and in the maximal measure.

Therefore, it is to be hoped that in these auspicious days, each and every one will respond and come to the aid of the institution "Oholei Torah" to the fullest extent, in accordance with the mitzvah of **"And you shall count for yourselves,"** through which one brings light and purity into one's own life, into all of one's household *shichyu*, and into *Klal Yisrael*, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**

## 9892

[9892](#_ftn_1680)

B"H, 7 Iyar, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 4 Iyar, in which you write about your state of mind, etc.

— In all such matters, our Sages of blessed memory have [assured us](#_ftn_1681): **"You have labored** — **and you have found."** This is especially true in your case, for it is certain that these confusions come solely from the Yetzer Hara, who (wants to be) [a king](#_ftn_1682) (while he is actually) an old and foolish one. And who is the simpleton that would listen to a fool?!

## 9893 

 13 Iyar, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all the students participating in the activities of the auspicious day of Lag B’Omer, may they live:

Shalom u’vracha!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the activities being organized in connection with the auspicious day of Lag B’Omer, which is approaching for the good. May it be His will that they be met with great success. Success in this context means that these activities will infuse additional vitality and strength [edn_247] into the progression from strength to strength in the study of our Torah—the Torah of life—which serves as a guide for life, for our day-to-day existence, in a way that is truly worthy of the name. It is a study that leads to action, to the fulfillment of mitzvos with hiddur, concerning which it is said, "And he shall live by them."

The story in the Gemara [edn_249] regarding Lag B’Omer is well known: that the students of Rabbi Akiva died because they did not treat one another with respect, and on the day of Lag B’Omer, they ceased to die.

Like all stories of the Torah, which are themselves Torah and whose purpose is to provide instruction, the aforementioned story regarding the students of Rabbi Akiva contains a lesson for every single one of the children of Israel, and in particular for the students—shlita. By way of introduction:

Since the Gemara testifies that they were "the students of Rabbi Akiva," it is understood that they were worthy of this title—meaning they studied in the manner taught to them by the great Tanna [edn_251] and brilliant sage, with diligence and perseverance, and fulfilled his mitzvos with mesiras nefesh.

From this, it is understood that their failure to treat one another with respect was not due to trivial matters, chas v’shalom. Rather, they had a basis and a reason for this, consistent with the stature of "students of Rabbi Akiva."

The explanation for this is based on what our Sages, of blessed memory, have said [edn_253]—that the temperaments of people are not the same. From this, it is understood that even in the avodah of Hashem, in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos, they are not the same: for one person, all of this comes primarily through ahavas Hashem; for another, it is primarily through yiras Hashem; for a third, it is primarily through kabbalas ol, and so on—even though, naturally and obviously, regarding the actual deed, there is no difference between them, and they fulfilled the Torah and mitzvos in their entirety and perfection. Being students of Rabbi Akiva, they were certainly people of truth, whose avodah was genuine and internal, permeating their very core. Consequently, their own path appeared to them as the only truly correct one, and anyone who had not reached that level was, in their view, lacking in perfection. And since they were students of Rabbi Akiva, who said, "‘Love your fellow as yourself’—this is a great principle of the Torah," they were not content with each individual progressing from strength to strength on his own path ascending to Hashem. Rather, they also endeavored to influence their peers to serve Hashem in that specific way as well. Those who did not accept this—they could not treat them with the respect required of the students of Rabbi Akiva.

From the above, it is understood that the story of the Gemara regarding Lag B’Omer teaches us how the conduct of each and every one of us should be. The lesson consists of three points:

a) The avodah of Hashem—the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos, both the mitzvos between man and Hashem and those between man and his fellow—must be a complete and genuine avodah, with a vitality that enlivens the entire person and his daily conduct.

b) This includes, naturally and obviously, the mitzvah of "Love your fellow as yourself," which must also be fulfilled with the greatest vitality and perfection.

c) Together with the above, a person must and is obligated to look favorably upon every observer of Torah and mitzvos and treat him with great respect, even if his path is not one’s own path. For he is a servant of Hashem, and the only difference is that one serves out of ahavas Hashem, another out of yiras Hashem, etc.

There is a further lesson included in this story: that even when one encounters someone who has not yet reached the level of avodas Hashem as they should, one must treat even them with respect, in accordance with the instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory, in their Mishnah: "Judge every person to the scale of merit." This is especially true given that the cause of the deficiency may not depend on him, but rather that he did not have the opportunity to be raised on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos due to circumstances entirely beyond his control. On the contrary, one’s compassion for him should be even greater, and one must strive all the more to help him ascend in Yiddishkeit, in Torah and mitzvos. This help must be provided in the best possible way—with love, respect, and in ways of pleasantness.

Let us take as our example the great Tanna Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, whose day of rejoicing is Lag B’Omer, who said, "I am able to exempt the entire world from judgment" (Sukkah 45b). He wished to give all his merits for the benefit of all those who have no merit of their own, for the entire world—including those he had never seen and who are at the ends of the earth; how much more so regarding one’s relatives, friends, and acquaintances.

May it be His will that each and every one of you, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, will act in all of this to the greatest extent and with joy and goodness of heart. May you go from strength to strength in all your affairs,

Until the verse in the parsha of the week of Lag B’Omer is fulfilled: "And I will break the bars of your yoke and lead you upright"—in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for success in all the above and for good tidings in all the above.

**M. Schneerson**

## 9894

[9894](#_ftn_1693)

[B"H](#_ftn_1694), 13 Iyar, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and elevated, who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, R' [Shneur](#_ftn_1695) Zalman, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I have just received your book, "The Hope for the Year 500," which was published in its proper time.

First and foremost, after my heartfelt thanks for the gift, I must note to your credit—and to the credit of your pen—that you have published material written decades ago, yet it is still read with great appreciation and interest. I am certain that this is the case regarding other similar matters as well.

This is the place to mention what [is brought](#_ftn_1696) in the name of the Gaon R' ShZ of Lublin, author of *Toras Chesed*. When he was asked regarding the reading of *Zecher Amalek*—whether it should be read *Zecher* (with a tzeirei) or *Zecher* (with a segol)—after an extensive back-and-forth, he concluded: "Whether *Zecher* (segol) or *Zecher* (tzeirei), the main thing is to wipe [them] out."

We, too, shall say regarding the calculation of the *Ketz* (the End): whether it is in this manner or that manner, may it be His will that the *Ketz* arrives in actuality, in the true and complete Redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

On this occasion, it is a pleasant duty to express my special thanks to you for your efforts regarding...

With appreciation, honor, and a blessing for a most successful Lag B'Omer, and in accordance with the instruction and ruling of the Torah in the *parsha* of this day—leading up to the promise at its conclusion and seal: "[And I will break](#_ftn_1697) the bars of your yoke and lead you upright."

**M. Schneerson**

## 9898

[9898](#_ftn_1712)

[B"H](#_ftn_1713), Lag B'Omer, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the Chanukas Habayis celebration of the Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

[Megalgelin](#_ftn_1714) zechus l’yom zakai — it is certainly a fitting day to celebrate the Chanukas Habayis of the new building of the central Lubavitcher Yeshiva on the first day of the [Sheloshes](#_ftn_1716) Yemei Hagbalah, on the eve of the Yom Tov of Matan Torah.

Shavuos is, after all, the Yom Tov when the Divine promise was fulfilled: **"When you bring the people out of Egypt, you shall serve Hashem on this mountain."** Although in a general sense this is the announcement regarding Matan Torah, there lies within the words "you shall serve Hashem" a clear indication that **Kabbalas HaTorah** is bound up with **avodas Hashem**, and that the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos must be with yiras shamayim and kabbalas ol.

And this is also the significance of the Chanukas Habayis of the new building of the central Lubavitcher Yeshiva: that here, a building is being established and sanctified whose purpose is to serve as a center for the study of Torah with yiras shamayim, filled with talmidim, may they increase, who study Torah with ahavas Hashem and yiras Hashem, [limud hamavi lidei maaseh](#_ftn_1718), the fulfillment of mitzvos with hiddur, whose chinuch and conduct are founded upon the three pillars of Toras HaChassidus: ahavas Hashem, ahavas HaTorah, and ahavas Yisrael, [shekuli chad](#_ftn_1719), in the full sense of "Tomchei Tmimim," according to the intent of the first founder of the Yeshiva, the Rebbe Rashab, and his son and successor, the Rebbe Rayatz, the menahel poel of the first Lubavitcher Yeshiva who transplanted the Yeshiva onto American soil.

Great is the zechus of all those who helped realize the great undertaking of this new building. Surely they will not only continue their support, but on the contrary — in an increased measure, in order to enable the Yeshiva to conduct its work and carry out its mission to the fullest extent. And may others see and do likewise, so that those who have not yet acquired a share in the new building will do so now and become active partners in the Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch.

In this zechus, may Hashem Yisbarach bless everyone and their families, sheyichyu, with the fulfillment of their hearts' desires for good and for blessing, and — this will hasten the fulfillment of the promise of our Sages, of blessed memory: "The synagogues and houses of study in Bavel (including all exiles) are destined to be established in Eretz Yisrael" (Megillah 29a), that the shuls and yeshivos will be transplanted from the lands of exile to Eretz Yisrael, in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for outstanding success in all the above and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9899

[9899](#_ftn_1720)

[B"H](#_ftn_1721), Lag B'Omer, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Fifteenth Annual Convention
of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad
May Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

Based on the profound [teaching](#_ftn_1722) of the Alter Rebbe, the founder of Chabad, that "a Jew must live with the times"—which means living with the time of the weekly Torah portion, **Toras Chaim**, the "guide" (from the word [*hora'ah*](#_ftn_1723)) for daily life, such that every day of the week is enlivened by the parsha of the week—

It is fitting to focus on the verses in the sedra of the Shabbos of the convention, where the Divine blessings are enumerated as the reward for "[*Bechukosai*](#_ftn_1724) you shall walk and keep My mitzvos."

The climax of these blessings is: **"I will place My *mishkan* (dwelling) among you... I will walk among you and I will be your G-d, and you will be My people."** Although this blessing is also contingent upon the general observance of Torah and mitzvos, as mentioned at the beginning of the sedra, the conclusion of these blessings specifically underscores the importance of **kedushah**, **taharah**, and **tzniyus**, for these are the foundations for the Divine *mishkan* and *Shechinah* to reside among the Jewish people in general, and within every Jew—man and woman—in particular.

This is clearly emphasized elsewhere in the Torah: **"Your camp shall be holy, that He (Hashem) shall not see anything unseemly among you and turn away from you"** (Devarim 23:15).

[Our](#_ftn_1727) Sages explain clearly that *tzniyus* and *kedushah* must be maintained in all matters, certainly in speech, and all the more so in dress and conduct.

On various occasions, it has already been mentioned that Jewish women and girls "set the tone" in certain areas of Jewish life, as we see tangibly. This is especially and uniquely true in the realm of [*tzniyus*](#_ftn_1728), [as](#_ftn_1729) is brought many times in the words of our Sages, to the point that it is said that the greatest *nachas* from children, both materially and spiritually, is connected to the *tzniyus*-dik conduct of the mother.

May Hashem help that the convention—whose main theme is **tzniyus**—should bring out in practice the true ideals of the Jewish woman and realize them in life, in **ma'aseh** and **dibbur**, which are connected to the *tzniyus* of **machshavah**.

And just as regarding all good activities, Chassidus demands that this should reach even **chutzah** (the outside), it is to be hoped that the voice, and primarily the actions, of the convention will reach even very distant circles that are currently still "outside," and the strongest influence is through showing a living example. The *zechus harabim* will surely assist you and bring Hashem's help and success.

With blessings for success in spiritual and material matters, and for good tidings in all that was mentioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9901

[9901](#_ftn_1733)

B"H, Lag B'Omer, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, noble, and distinguished individual, who seeks the good of his people and possesses refined character, a scion of noble ancestors, R' [Shneur](#_ftn_1734) Zalman Shlita,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I am uncomfortable troubling you with what follows, but since the matter came to my attention inadvertently, through Hashgacha Pratis, I feel I have no right to ignore it. Even if it concerned only one individual, a single [neshamah](#_ftn_1735) in Yisrael is an entire world; how much more so in the present case, where he is a family man whose fate affects his wife, his children, and so on.

The matter concerns Mr. [Name], who, as he writes, appealed to you on May 3, 1970, with a request for clemency, and on whose behalf several important people in Eretz Yisrael have advocated. Now, they have also turned to me to support his request.

It should be noted that those who have also approached me regarding this matter are not relatives of the man, but rather people of integrity who have no connection to any personal biases and are, in general, not given to compromise.

As for the matter itself, according to the copy I received, you have already been approached at length and in detail, and I will not take up your time by repeating the points once more. Especially since what is being discussed here is a matter of *chaninah* (clemency), which stems from the root *chen* (grace). And *chen* [is a quality that](#_ftn_1736) transcends logic, and all the more so when, according to the copies sent to me, there is also logical reasoning and a basis for clemency.

We bring about [merit](#_ftn_1737) on a meritorious day, writing this letter on a day of *segulah*, Lag B'Omer. As I concluded in my [general letter](#_ftn_1738) for this day—which is the day of the rejoicing of the Rashbi—its crowning achievement regarding the entire world is his [declaration](#_ftn_1739) in the Torah of Truth before the G-d of Truth, that he is able to exempt the entire world from judgment.

With appreciation, honor, and blessing.

P.S. I trust my [letter](#_ftn_1740) of 13 Iyar was received.

## 9905 

 B"H, the day after Lag B’Omer, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, engaged in communal needs,
R’ Chaim Yehuda, may he live and be well, Paldi

Greetings and blessings!

It is surprising, and even somewhat worrying, that I have not heard from you for such a long time. I certainly do not suspect you of treating me with "measure for measure"—that because you have not received letters from me (due to the multitude of preoccupations, etc.), you are therefore acting toward me in the same way. The reason I do not suspect this is that you surely judge me favorably, understanding that the lack of letters from me is due to the aforementioned reason, especially since that is the truth.

When I conveyed several matters by telephone, I requested that they also inquire about you and your well-being. They immediately informed me that you participated in the joy of the Rashbi on the day of his celebration in Meron, and that they had spoken with you afterward. Many thanks for the good news. May it be His will that you yourself bring good tidings, and as we have spoken many times, in a manner of "increasing and continuing."

 I believe I have already expressed my gratitude and great satisfaction regarding the article you published concerning the regrettable and alarming error of calling our current exile—a double and redoubled darkness—by the name "the beginning of the Redemption," etc. And as we have discussed many times, especially when one sees the results of this, etc. The merit of the many assists anyone who protests against this. Of course, there is no room for despondency if the protest is not received in the way it ought to be, although I hope that it makes an impression nonetheless; who has stood in the counsel of Hashem to know the results? Naturally, this does not exempt one from protesting again and again, especially in light of what has been discussed and explained many times regarding the seriousness of the matter and the damage, etc., etc. There is no need to elaborate on such a distressing subject.

Knowing your interest, you have surely read with the appropriate attention what was printed from the farbrengen of the days of Purim. My hope is that you will also receive at least a summary of what was discussed on the day of Lag B’Omer—the aforementioned day of the Rashbi’s celebration—which is famous for his attitude toward the "kindness of the nations." As our Sages of blessed memory relate (Shabbos 33b), "They established it for their own benefit," and especially the nations of our generation, etc. Along with this, he declared, "I can exempt the entire world from judgment." Certainly, his intention was not to publicize his own importance or value, Heaven forbid, but rather to lighten the judgment, even to the point of nullifying it. And he emphasizes "the entire world," including those who err regarding the "kindness of the nations," etc., and those who are on a lower level than them, etc.

With blessings for success in all your affairs, in good health and with joy and goodness of heart,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Following the above, enclosed is a copy of my general letter for Lag B’Omer.

## 9906

[9906](#_ftn_1762)

B”H, the day after Lag B’Omer, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs and the needs of the community, etc.,

[Rabbi Avraham](#_ftn_1763)

Shalom u’Bracha!

To address the first matter first: Many thanks for fulfilling the mission and for the effort you expended in visiting the places and people I requested you to visit. Surely, this will yield positive results.

2) I have just received the book *Tosafos Chachmei Anglia*, and I thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me. Seeing a proof is not the same as seeing a finished, complete, and printed book. May it be the will of Hashem that the [statement of our Sages](#_ftn_1764) of blessed memory be fulfilled in you: "He who has one hundred wants two hundred; he who has two hundred wants four hundred." May your desire to publish the words of the [Rishonim, who were like angels](#_ftn_1765), grow, and may the Ribono shel Olam fulfill this desire of yours in actuality, in a manner of "increasing and continuing," as mentioned above.

3) Another point—and this is why this letter is being sent as a rush delivery—is in continuation of what I spoke with you regarding a visit to the university in Bologna, Italy. There has been a change in this regard: (a) It has become clear that the vast majority of the students whom we wish to influence are speakers of Hebrew or English; (b) one of the young Chabad activists will be visiting there according to his own schedule in the coming weeks, and perhaps even with the intention of staying there for an extended period, etc. In light of the above, there is no need to trouble you to visit there. If, following the aforementioned activist's visit, there are any changes, we will inform you.

In closing, as in the opening, thank you for writing regarding your impressions of the Chabad evening in Yerushalayim, the Holy City. Especially since, as you wrote, it is exactly as we spoke—without [any](#_ftn_1766) paint or powder, and with true grace.

With respect and a blessing for success in the aforementioned, and for good tidings in health and joy.

P.S. Since my letter comes close to the day of Lag B’Omer, I am enclosing a copy of a [general letter](#_ftn_1767) that I hope will be of interest to you.

## 9907

[9907](#_ftn_1768)

B"H, 37th of the Omer, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Ms. Devorah Steinmetz, may she live

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 21st of Iyar, in which you ask regarding the study of Gemara for young women:

Transcribed here is the language of the Alter Rebbe in Hilchos Talmud Torah (end of Chapter 1):

"Women are also obligated to learn the laws that they need to know, such as the laws of Niddah, Tevilah, salting [of meat], the prohibition of Yichud, and the like, and all positive commandments that are not time-bound, and all negative commandments of the Torah and of the Sages regarding which they are warned just as men are."

In accordance with the above halachic ruling, there is a great deal of study available for young women in Gemara, and primarily in Shulchan Aruch and Kitzur Shulchan Aruch—study that leads to action, as our Sages said: "Action is the essential thing."

Based on the tone of your letter, it is my hope that you are studying in the manner mentioned—[according to the style of the Gemara](#_ftn_1771)—that great study which leads to action, the fulfillment of the mitzvos, which is appropriate for a daughter of Israel. For every one of them is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah, who built the house of Israel. Included in this is the responsibility to be a living example to influence all of your friends, for the mitzvah of "Love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle of the Torah.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

Enclosed is a copy of the letter for Lag B'Omer, as well as a copy of the letter to the N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, the content of which is relevant to every single person among the children of Israel, and you will find in them several matters that are relevant to you.

## 9811

[9811](#_ftn_1781)

**[Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5730]**

To the Honorable Chief Rabbi,
[Rabbi Unterman](#_ftn_1783) shlita,
25 Keren HaYesod Street, Jerusalem.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, my [opinion](#_ftn_1784) on these matters is explained [in my remarks](#_ftn_1785) on Purim [and Lag B'Omer](#_ftn_1786), and since then, the concerns, etc., have only become more firmly grounded.

The current phrasing of these pressures is interpreted by many—especially the youth—according to its literal truth: as a nullification, G-d forbid, not only in reality but also in an official and legal sense, of the distinction that Hashem, blessed be He, has made in our holy Torah between Israel and the nations. **This is a danger, G-d forbid**, to the very existence of our nation, both in the Diaspora and in the Holy Land.

Every religious representative currently sitting in the government only adds a religious stamp of approval to all of this—the opposite of the law of the Torah of truth! It is impossible to strengthen the security and morale of the Jewish people through that which is the opposite of the truth; on the contrary.

May it be the will of the G-d of Hosts that the army, which defends our holy land and our people who dwell within it with true mesiras nefesh, **be victorious, and soon, with a complete victory and without casualties, G-d forbid, and may peace come to the land** ["and you shall lie down](#_ftn_1787) and none shall make you afraid."

And the army of religious activists whose duty it is to guard the sanctities of our people, with the Rabbis at their head, must state their opinion clearly and openly regarding these laws, along with all the conclusions that follow.

Ultimately, even those who do not yet recognize the terrible danger in these laws will join them and repair the breach, for the [heart](#_ftn_1788) of every man and woman in Israel is awake to Hashem and His Torah of truth.

With respect and with wishes for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, looking forward to good tidings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9915

[9915](#_ftn_1808)

B"H, Days of Limitation, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Aharon [Yariv](#_ftn_1809)

Shalom u’Bracha,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 22 Iyar, along with the enclosure, and I thank you.

I offer a double thank you for your thoughtfulness in including the excerpt related to our conversation. Especially for your note regarding the matter of the "Kaf," which puts my mind at ease, as I interpret general statements in the most favorable light.

As we approach the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, I hereby express my blessing in the traditional phrasing—

That you may receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

With holiday blessings,

P.S. Following up on what I wrote in the body of my letter, and in a related vein, it is a pity that the news regarding the intervention in Sudan was leaked to the press.

Regarding your writing about insisting [concerning](#_ftn_1810) the line of the Canal, etc.—although I am not a great strategist or the like, even with simple logic there is no alternative here. It is impossible to establish a border in the middle of a territory without having some hold on the topographical conditions of the place. That is to say, if—G-d forbid—it is not the Suez Canal, then it is a retreat to an artificial border that can be changed from hour to hour. And what is even more important, it is impossible to defend it except with the greatest of efforts, and in the natural order of things, one cannot be certain that even such an effort will suffice. In other words, establishing such a border is an "invitation" to discussions, conflicts, and skirmishes, etc., at any given moment.

To add to this: it seems that the efforts on the part of those who only recently began to intervene in the matter are not so much for the sake of further conquest, but rather for the possibility of using the Canal for their own interests. From this, it is understood that if the opposing side were to reach the conclusion that using the Canal is impossible because it has been destroyed and ruined—and even after great effort, it would only be capable of accommodating the smallest of vessels, etc.—there are significant chances that this calculation would influence them, at the very least, to reduce their intervention. Further to my conversation with you on a similar matter, an effort in the aforementioned direction does not require as much exertion as bombings, etc., and it is possible to carry this out in a way that does not provoke those whom it is not worthwhile to provoke. Furthermore, [it is] possible that it could be done by "others."

I will conclude with the news of further satisfaction caused by a report last week: that, contrary to the practice until now, there were those who wanted [to organize a massive demonstration](#_ftn_1811)—and specifically with the greatest publicity and the greatest noise—to exert pressure on the government here, the government we spoke about. However, they asked the Ambassador, and he forbade it. May it be the will [of Hashem] that this marks a **turning point** in the approach to the matter of demonstrations, etc., as we discussed during your visit here.

And thank you in advance for acknowledging this letter of mine, and primarily for your open response to everything written in it.

## 9919

With blessings.
