## 9925

[9925](#_ftn_1834)

[With the help of Hashem](#_ftn_1835), Tuesday [the day](#_ftn_1836) [on which it was doubled](#_ftn_1837) "it is good," Parshas Korach, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch for the Siyum, Montreal

May Hashem grant them life

Peace and blessing!

In response to the news regarding the [celebration](#_ftn_1838) of the Siyum, may it be the will that it takes place in a good and auspicious hour.

According to the well-known [maamar](#_edn_274) of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe—who is the final authority in the inner dimension of Torah and the Shulchan Aruch (the final authority in the revealed dimension of Torah)—that "one must live with the times," this means that, in accordance with the content of the weekly parsha, the celebration will surely be illuminated and permeated by the light and vitality of this week’s parsha. Its focal point is the account of the dispute of Korach and his congregation against [Moshe](#_ftn_1839), for Moshe is truth and his Torah is truth.

The matter is—based on what our Sages, of blessed memory, testified, that Korach was [clever](#_edn_275)—that his arguments were intellectual arguments, and furthermore, there was a *ka salka da'atach* (a plausible line of reasoning) that they had a place within the logic of Torah. From this it is understood that a miracle and a new creation were required, [which](#_ftn_1840) Hashem would create to prove the truth of the Torah of truth.

[One](#_ftn_1841) of the explanations for this is based on the [account](#_edn_276) of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the beginning of Korach’s argument was: "A garment that is entirely blue—is it exempt from tzitzis?" If so, since the entire congregation is holy, there is no need for the Kehunah (priesthood) of Aharon. In the [words](#_ftn_1842) of the verse: "Why do you exalt yourselves?"

The [point](#_edn_277) of the argument regarding a person’s avodah to his Creator, Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, is that when the matter of holiness is in a comprehensive manner—like a tallis [that covers](#_ftn_1843) a person, his head and his entire body—that is sufficient, and there is no need for tzitzis, strings tied to the corners of the garment, which is a symbol of drawing from the encompassing (makif) into the inner dimension (pnimiyus) of the person. From here, it extends to the Kehunah of Aharon: since the entire congregation is holy, even though they are occupied for several hours a day with matters of livelihood—work according to Torah, as it is [said](#_ftn_1844), "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you **do**"—and thereafter with various optional matters, such as eating and drinking, etc., which are also according to Torah, provided that one’s conduct is such that "all your deeds are for the sake of [Heaven](#_edn_279)"—then this is sufficient.

The response of Moshe Rabbeinu was that influence is also required in the inner dimension, and that there must be a Kohen, and regarding the Kohen Gadol it is [said](#_ftn_1845), "And he shall not leave the Sanctuary." This means that all his affairs are in holiness and in the Sanctuary, openly. On the contrary, specifically in such a manner is holiness drawn into the inner dimension even during the hours of the day when one is occupied with optional matters—not only that all deeds are [for the sake of](#_ftn_1846) Heaven, but even more than that, "[in](#_ftn_1847) all your ways **know Him**," and even to the point of studying Torah and performing mitzvos in practice for the majority of the day, as if it were the whole day. Then the tallis also possesses holiness, and the holiness of the entire congregation is manifest, as is explained at length in the discourses of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im.

Based on the above, it is understood that a holy task rests upon a yeshiva student in general, and students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in particular, for they must demonstrate *temimus* (wholeness/sincerity) and perfection in all matters. A [student](#_edn_280) of a yeshiva must have Torah as his profession, and through this, holiness is increased for all those who are connected to the yeshiva and who support the yeshiva—[of whom it is said](#_ftn_1848), "and those who support it are happy"—in addition to the fact that through this, the holiness within each and every one of them stands revealed and in practice.

May it be the will that each and every one of those completing their studies, together with all the students of Tomchei Temimim wherever they may be, will fulfill the aforementioned task, in accordance with the hopes of the founders of the yeshiva, our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, and be a source of pride to their parents, their teachers, their mashpi'im, and the administrators—may they live and be well.

And the addition in the beauty of studying the revealed and inner Torah with fear of Heaven—[study](#_ftn_1849) that leads to the action of performing mitzvos in practice—will hasten the end of our exile and bring the true and complete Geulah, when [G-d](#_ftn_1850) will save Tzion and build the cities of Yehudah, and they shall dwell there [and inherit it](#_ftn_1851), and the seed of His servants shall inherit it, and those who love His name shall dwell therein.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all the above.

## 9926

[9926](#_ftn_1852)

[B"H](#_ftn_1853), Tuesday, [the third](#_ftn_1854) of Tammuz, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter . . .

In these days preceding the days of the Festival of Redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, and especially beginning from the third day of this month—the day when (in the year of the imprisonment and redemption—the year 5687) [my father-in-law, the Rebbe,](#_ftn_1856) the master of the redemption, turned to the crowd standing there to accompany him and said (among other things):

"Only our bodies have been delivered into exile and the subjugation of kingdoms, but our neshamas have not been driven into exile, nor have they been delivered into the subjugation of kingdoms. We must declare openly for all to see that as far as our religion, Torah, mitzvos, and the customs of Yisrael are concerned, we Jews have no one to dictate to us."

May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, be aroused to strengthen ourselves and increase our efforts in all matters of our religion, Torah, mitzvos, and the customs of Yisrael—

Which are divided into the three categories, the [three](#_edn_287) pillars upon which the world (in general, and [the person](#_edn_288) in particular) stands: Torah, avodah ([tefillah](#_ftn_289)), and gemilus chasadim (which includes all the [mitzvos](#_ftn_1857)),

And may this arousal be drawn down into action [and deed](#_ftn_1858)—which is the essential thing—in daily life, so that one is occupied ["with Torah](#_ftn_1859) and the avodah of the heart, which is [tefillah](#_ftn_1860), and fulfills the mitzvos with pure faith and the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven, without being affected at all by any obstacle or hindrance."

[And this](#_ftn_1861) will also hasten and accelerate the fulfillment of the [promise](#_ftn_1862): "For Hashem will save Tzion and build the cities of Yehudah, and they shall dwell there and inherit it; the seed of His servants shall inherit it, and those who love His name shall dwell therein."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

The [proposal](#_ftn_1863) regarding Nachalat Har Chabad is correct and good, and may it be successful.

With blessings for good tidings in the above,

## 9927

[9927](#_ftn_1864)

B.H., 3 Tammuz, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. [Eliezer](#_ftn_1865) Levna, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter.

Regarding the main point therein, [concerning Hebron](#_ftn_1866) and the settlement there: it is somewhat surprising that, even though you are on the scene, you are apparently unaware that from the very outset, a significant portion of those who determine these matters in our land did **not** agree to this, and did not accept the aforementioned matter. Those who support them have grown in number, and recently, it seems, they have gained the upper hand, and their influence is steadily increasing.

In other words, it appears that the entire matter is not practical **at all**. However, following the current situation and the relations between the parties—and within the parties themselves—it is unclear in what style or manner they will cancel the matter. But as stated, this concerns only the external form of the cancellation, not the essence of the matter itself.

It is not my intention to publicize these things, for: a) It is not my way to fight against the government of Israel on such matters, even if there were good prospects for results; b) In the natural course of events and given the current political situation in Eretz Yisrael, I do not see any prospect that the plan for settlement in Hebron will be implemented, at least in the near future—and I would be happy to be proven wrong.

The heartache and deep sorrow over the above are understandable, and I am certain that this is the sorrow of the vast majority of our people, the children of Israel, wherever they may be. But unfortunately, this is not what determines many important matters. It has reached the point where things have been done that were not necessary in the slightest, and which touch upon the honor of the people of Israel, and even more, etc.

For example, regarding the matter of Hebron itself:

Until now, I have not received an explanation—at least not a partial one—as to what [was](#_ftn_1867) the necessity **to decide publicly at the cabinet meeting and to publish it**, etc., when the subject of Hebron was discussed, that they would permit, in due time, the construction of apartments in the area **adjacent** to Hebron. In other words, a declaration in the name of the entire people dwelling in Zion that in Hebron itself, the residence of a child of Israel is forbidden! The reason is understood—because it belongs to those who dwell there now, and in the biblical phrasing, ["Have you murdered](#_ftn_1868) and also taken possession?" For it was through murder, in the literal sense, that the children of Israel were driven out of the City of the Patriarchs. And the "consolation" in the aforementioned decision, as the news of the "great victory" in this decision was brought to me—that they finally decided to settle Jews outside of Hebron—is that they knew from the start that even for this, they would need to receive approval from several powers, primarily Washington and the State Department, whose custom is that all concessions on the part of Israel are accepted immediately and there is no room for retraction or regret, whereas Israel’s demands are discussed with long-winded negotiations, etc., etc. They could have done this quietly—as they did in Jerusalem—and not **stipulate and publicize** the prohibition in Hebron, and in the name of **all** the ministers!

I asked the aforementioned question several weeks ago, and as noted, I have not received **any** explanation to this day. There is no need to dwell on this distressing matter.

As mentioned above, this letter of mine is for you and for those whom you deem it beneficial to know its content, but not for publication in the press, for it is not my intention to wage war against the government.

I will take this opportunity, and the pleasant surprise of receiving a letter from you after the longest interval since your visit here, to fulfill a pleasant duty: **to express my gratitude** for your defending me against the lead article printed in *Haaretz*. Especially since my personal honor is not so affected by this, for I have been [accustomed](#_ftn_1869) to such "reactions" against me, and even more sharply, since my youth when I lived in the Soviet Union and was the eldest son of the Chief Rabbi in a district city. Since I had acquaintances among the students, etc., it is understood that during debates, etc., they attacked "me as well." On the contrary, since I had knowledge in the fields the aforementioned students were studying—some of whom were Yevseks, Communists, etc.

However, what does concern me is the matter of spreading Yiddishkeit, and first and foremost the [Mivtza](#_ftn_1870) of Tefillin. I have merited that my words of inspiration on this are accepted among many circles. Since they attacked me in the newspaper, etc., there are those who conclude from this that one should not put on Tefillin, Heaven forbid, because the initiator of the activity is written about in such-and-such a way in a certain newspaper, and yet he stands and speaks and encourages people to put on Tefillin.

The hope is that the attack will not cause harm, since there is no logical connection or relevance between the two matters—[for even if the attack were one hundred percent justified, what is the connection to the fulfillment of the mitzvah of Tefillin, which is written in our Torah, the Torah of life and the Torah of truth, in four places in the Written Torah and in numerous places in the Oral Torah, etc., etc.—] however, to our sorrow, we live in a generation of upheavals, where not all matters are decided precisely according to logic and exact reasoning. And certainly, for someone like yourself, there is no need to elaborate on this.

With respect and blessing.

## 9928

In the phrasing of our Sages, of blessed memory: "The soul of a poor person (which includes one who is [poor in knowledge](#_ftn_1874)) [was struggling to depart from hunger and] you gave him sustenance and revived him (which includes spiritual sustenance), by your life, I will repay you..." [(Tanchuma](#_ftn_1875) Parshas Mishpatim [on the verse](#_ftn_1876) "If you lend money").

– and to note the words of the great teacher, the Rambam: That the body be healthy and whole is among the ways of Hashem (Hilchos De’os, beginning of Chapter 4) –

and with joy and a good heart.

With respect and blessing,

## 9933

[9933](#_ftn_1892)

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Moshav Avivim, Merom HaGalil

Greetings and blessings!

May there be fulfilled for each and every one, and especially for the parents, among all the residents, the [statement](#_ftn_1896) of the holy ones of the Most High, the tzaddikim of the Jewish people in the generations before us, who prayed for the peace of every single Jew wherever they may be. Their merit protects us even now, and especially the merit of their actions in the love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Israel.

For one whom the attribute of judgment has struck, *rachmana litzlan*, after this, the attribute of mercy is awakened—the mercies of the Holy One, Blessed be He, which are without limit, [and in the language of the verse](#_ftn_1897), "an inheritance without boundaries," extending from one end to the other, to bestow upon them blessing, salvation, and success in all that they and their families, may they live, require.

And especially regarding the residents of our Holy Land, for the merit of the Holy Land protects and saves.

With respect and blessing for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

[And it is a special segulah](#_ftn_1898) to be precise in these mitzvos, as is explained in our holy Torah.

## 9934

[9934](#_ftn_1899)

B"H, 16 Tammuz, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Moshe Levi

Greetings and blessings!

Through our friend Mr. Shlomo Midnatchik, I received a request for a blessing for your improved health and for a *refuah*. I will mention you at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

May it be His will that just as I have received the request, so too shall I receive good news regarding the aforementioned.

Your activities in defense of the holy people who dwell in the Holy Land will stand you in good stead to hasten your recovery, that it may be swift and complete, and may you be blessed with all good for yourself and your household.

For if one who defends [1900](#_ftn_1900) even a single soul of Israel is as one who defends an entire world, how much more so is this true for those to whom Divine Providence has entrusted the responsible task of defending tens of thousands of thousands of Israel.

I will take the liberty of adding a few lines, and it is my hope that you will receive these words with a favorable countenance and with the same warmth with which they are spoken.

I have [1901](#_ftn_1901) already spoken on several occasions regarding the magnitude of the *mitzvah* of *tefillin*. And although every single *mitzvah* is great, important, and of the highest value—being the command of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, who in His great kindness and infinite goodness gave to Israel, His close people, the Torah and its *mitzvos*, [1902](#_ftn_1902) and made known that He derives *taanug* when a son or daughter of Israel fulfills His will—

The Holy One, blessed be He, the Commander of the *mitzvos*, divided them into various categories and made known in our Torah, which is called *Torah Or* [1903](#_ftn_1903)—the light that illuminates a person’s path in life—the unique *segulos* inherent in each and every *mitzvah*.

Among the *segulos* of the *mitzvah* of *tefillin* is that which—[in the language of the verse](#_ftn_1904)—"All the peoples of the earth shall see that the name of Hashem is called upon you, and they shall fear you." And another *segulah* is that [by virtue of](#_ftn_1905) the *tefillin* placed upon the hand and the head, the blessing comes, "and he tears the arm and even the crown of the head."

Since [all](#_ftn_1906) Israel are friends, members of one family, and even more so, since [all](#_ftn_1907) Israel is one complete stature, it is [like the limbs](#_ftn_1908) of a single body, where a benefit to one limb adds benefit to all the other limbs; that is to say, the good of one Jew is the good of the entire Jewish people.

How much more so when the matter concerns the soldiers themselves, and even more so those who stand at their head and lead them; the fulfillment of this *mitzvah* by them greatly increases the [awe](#_ftn_1909) and fear upon every enemy and adversary, to the point that many times no spirit remains in them to wage war, and even when they do come to battle, the blessing is fulfilled, "and he tears the arm and even the crown of the head," and they are victorious.

And if, in the tactics of war, every possible weapon is utilized—even if its effectiveness is in doubt, and even if it will bring benefit only to a small group or even to individuals, and furthermore, they strive to obtain it and do not spare effort or money, etc., just to employ such a weapon—how much more so regarding the "weapon" mentioned here: the fulfillment of the *mitzvah* of *tefillin*. The effectiveness of this is testified to by our Sages, of blessed memory, from generation to generation, and they also testify to its scope—my meaning being that it is for the benefit of the one who puts on *tefillin*, his immediate surroundings, and also those far away, extending to the entire Jewish people wherever they may be.

Great is the merit of all who fulfill this *mitzvah*, especially when done with joy and vitality, and infinitely greater is the merit of those who enable others to fulfill this *mitzvah*. There is a special capacity for commanders, officers, leaders, and so on, for it is in human nature to be impressed by those in positions of authority, even in areas that seemingly have no connection to their routine relations.

With respect and esteem,

With blessings for a swift recovery and good news regarding all the aforementioned, and with Hashem’s blessing for all that is needed for you and your household.

## 9938

## 9939

[9939](#_ftn_1917)

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc.,
[Rabbi Shneur Zalman](#_ftn_1918) Shragai, may he live:

I have just received your two books, *Sugyos HaDor* and *Zemanim*. Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending them; I assume you will do so in the future as well, especially since our library is for the benefit of the many.

May it be the will of Hashem that for many years, in longevity and good years, you increase your strength in Torah—in the dissemination of Torah, the Torah of truth, which by definition rejects all compromise. If it was always necessary to emphasize this, how much more so in our generation—a generation of confusion and upheaval, where values are blurred to an alarming degree—and especially in this time, the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, as it is said, in a humorous vein, that some are even more diligent and vigorous in fulfilling the "signs" of the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*.

[My letter](#_ftn_1919) in response to your letter was certainly received some time ago. To my great regret, the [developments](#_ftn_1920) in the weeks since then reinforce the rumors and the concerns I wrote of at that time.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in any event, there will be no need for debate and defense by our Jewish brethren themselves regarding Jerusalem, the Holy City. May it be—in the phrasing used on the title page of your book—"Jerusalem Liberated," a true liberation and freedom, in a manner that fulfills [its prophetic destiny](#_ftn_1921): "And the word of Hashem from Jerusalem."

## 9940

[9940](#_ftn_1923)

[B"H](#_ftn_1924), 27 Tammuz, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, the G-d-fearing man, who is distinguished in his Torah and his mitzvos, etc.,

Rabbi [Avraham](#_ftn_1925) Mordechai Hershberg, may he live,

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letter, which reached me after a long delay, and which contains a matter that, in its phrasing, is a "private matter"—but after your request for forgiveness, it is actually a most general matter—regarding the position of Chief Rabbi of the Federation in London, etc.

It is a well-known [principle](#_ftn_1926) that in a dispute between an individual and the many, the halacha follows the many. From this, it is seemingly understood that this rule applies as well regarding the benefit of the individual versus the benefit of the many. Based on this, [in my opinion](#_ftn_1927), there is no doubt that the necessity of the work in spreading traditional Yiddishkeit, and especially in the area of kosher chinuch, in the countries of South America—including Mexico and its neighbors—is incomparably greater than in London. This holds true even if one were to say that there is a greater possibility, in both quantity and quality, to act in this regard in London, especially since the possibilities there are limited due to several reasons that are surely known to you as well.

Furthermore, and this is also essential: in the present case, even the benefit of the individual—that is, yourself—is incomparably greater in your current location, provided that you utilize the possibilities as much as is required, and the possibilities are unlimited. As for the opposition to kosher chinuch and the spreading of traditional Yiddishkeit, for the time being, it is not organized; and in many areas—and in certain respects, in all areas—"whoever arrives first wins." The primary role of a Rav is to lead the Bnei Yisrael in the path of Torah and mitzvos, and in our generation, there is the added task of awakening in them the desire and enthusiasm to be led by the Rav.

I do not know how many ready-made helpers you will find on the spot—I refer to South America, etc.—but there are many potential helpers. It is just that they, too, are unorganized, and perhaps one does not even know of the other, or perhaps he does not even know about his own strengths and capabilities.

It is possible that regarding rest, London is a more suitable place, but in my opinion, that is not the purpose and goal of a Rav, nor even of any individual—whoever they may be—among the Jewish people, wherever they are. It is my hope that for someone like you, the above does not require elaboration or even explanation.

On this occasion, and in continuation of what I heard from you on Motzaei Chag HaShavuos, that over time there have been about twenty issues published of the collection "Kol Yerushalayim"—since my library contains only the first two or three issues, I thank you in advance if you would be willing to instruct those who carry out your wishes to send any duplicates to the library. As mentioned, thank you in advance.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I have personally requested that the publisher here send you [a copy] via Kehot.

## 9941

[9941](#_ftn_1928)

[B"H](#_ftn_1929), Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the graduates of Chabad schools in our Holy Land,
May it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days,
Hashem, may they live.

Peace and Blessing!

As we stand in this month—a month of "weeping on one side and joy on the other," a remembrance of the events of the Churban, and at the same time a month designated for "double consolation," as its name **Menachem** Av implies—

It is understood that the purpose of this remembrance is that it should influence and lead to actual deeds regarding the content of this memory: the Churban and its cause. As is explicitly stated in many places in Tanach and in the language of our Sages: "Because of our sins, we were exiled from our land," etc.

From this, the conclusion is that one must act to weaken and diminish the cause (our sins), for by doing so, we weaken and diminish the effect (our exile, etc.) and bring closer the Geulah—the complete and true Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

In this, there is a special role for the youth, and especially for those who have graduated from school—even if they are moving on to another school. For the very fact that one is a graduate shows that one is mature and has reached a certain level of independent thought, combined with the quality of youth, which by nature rejects compromise and resignation to the status quo or the prevailing trend. This is especially true for those who are graduates of Chabad schools, for the essence of Chabad is to grasp every matter with inwardness and vitality, illuminated by the light of our Torah—Toras Chaim—both its revealed and its inner dimensions.

The special role of the youth is clear and simple: first and foremost, that they themselves be a living example in their conduct in daily life, in the meticulous observance of Torah and mitzvos, and also in influencing and advocating within their surroundings in the direction and spirit mentioned above. [And we have been promised](#_ftn_1934) that "one who comes to purify himself" [(and as our Alter Rebbe precisely notes: to purify himself and to purify others, both himself and others)](#_ftn_1935) is assisted.

Through this, each and every one will also do what is within their power to hasten the end of our exile and bring closer the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu and our Geulah, and we will merit the fulfillment of the [prophecy](#_ftn_1936) that these days will be turned into gladness and joy.

With blessings for outstanding success in all your affairs and for good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned,

**M. Schneerson**

9942 

 B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the National Convention of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in Kfar Chabad, in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days—

May Hashem grant you life!

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the convention, and may it be the will [of Hashem] that it be met with great success.

The content of this month is a remembrance of the events of the Churban and the Galus, yet at the same time, it is the month of consolation, as its name implies: **Menachem** Av.

The purpose of remembrance is that it should lead to actual deeds—deeds appropriate to the content of the matters mentioned.

Regarding this month, which begins with sorrow, the content of the matter is clear and simple, [derived] from the accepted and traditional formulation of the prayer: "And because of our sins we were exiled from our land." From this, it is understood that the rectification and the consolation lie in the weakening, reduction, and ultimate nullification of the cause (our sins), by turning away from evil and doing good, and by strengthening the observance of Torah and mitzvos in daily life.

As the N'shei U’Bnos Chabad gather for their annual convention, they will surely utilize this opportunity to its fullest to emphasize the most important role of the Jewish woman in all the serious and vital matters in the history of our people. This begins with the righteous women in whose merit our ancestors were redeemed from Mitzrayim—the first and general Galus—and to whom the word was addressed first at the giving of the Torah ("Beis Yaakov" first, and only afterwards "Bnei Yisrael"). Likewise, from time to time, the righteousness and stature of the women and daughters of Yisrael were reaffirmed and renewed in several important and fateful events in the history of our people.

Regarding this month in particular—our Sages, of blessed memory, taught us in their Mishnah that "there were no better days for Yisrael than the fifteenth of Av... when the daughters of Yisrael (Yerushalayim) would go out... and what would they say... (that the foundation of a family and a home in Yisrael, which is to be an everlasting edifice, is when they are founded upon Torah and mitzvos in general, and primarily—) 'Grace is false and beauty is vanity, but a woman who fears Hashem, she shall be praised.'"

And even according to the version [that they were] the daughters of **Yerushalayim**, Yerushalayim is the capital city of the entire land of Yisrael and of all the Jewish people wherever they may be. Especially so in providing a way of life and a living example, for the verse explicitly states: "For from Tzion shall Torah go forth, and the word of Hashem from Yerushalayim."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the convention succeed in fulfilling its role completely, through actual deeds, to establish the home of Yisrael upon a life founded on the fear of Hashem and the love of Hashem, and—fitting for the demands of the hour—with an emphasis on the area of *tzniyus* in particular.

With blessings for success in all the above and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9943

[9943](#_ftn_1951)

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Uri [Tzvi](#_ftn_1952) Greenberg,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I am certain that you received my previous [letter](#_ftn_1953) in due time. I am writing to you now regarding the point raised in my previous letter, [the question](#_ftn_1954) of "Who is a Jew." I ask your forgiveness for writing again before having received confirmation or a response. However, the extreme gravity of the matter compels me, especially since, based on our acquaintance, I am confident that the reason you have not yet responded is merely due to peripheral circumstances, and there is no doubt that you, too, recognize the gravity of the situation and that action must be taken, etc. And since our Sages, of blessed memory, [have taught us](#_ftn_1955) that "one only urges those who are already diligent," I wish to stir you once more. We see the great confusion that this situation has brought about in Eretz Yisrael, and especially abroad. Surely there is no need to repeat the reasons and arguments—which were unnecessary even in the previous letter, as they are well known to you. Therefore, in my opinion, it is incumbent upon everyone to act on this with vigor, and the sooner, the better.

May it be the will of Hashem that these days, which are destined to be transformed into joy and gladness, be transformed in this matter as well into joy and gladness—a revealed joy that will unite all circles of our people, the Children of Israel. And since the [heart](#_ftn_1956) of a Jew is sensitive, and even [one](#_ftn_1957) who has sinned remains a Jew, I am confident that even the initiators of this terrible decree will be satisfied with the change for the better. Through this transformation into joy and gladness in many areas, the true and complete Geulah will come for all the Children of Israel, from both the internal and external exile, until these days are [transformed](#_ftn_1958) into joy and gladness in the literal sense of the verse.

With respect and appreciation, awaiting good news regarding the above and regarding your family, may they live.

P.S. Another reason that prompted me to write to you again without waiting for confirmation of my previous letter is that a rumor reached me that the initiators of the aforementioned decree have seized upon the opportunity to silence public opinion through a general silence on this issue—that is, to influence the newspapers to cease discussion of the matter and to refrain from answering inquiries and questions about it, etc. This is especially true now, during the summer days, which are days of vacation and rest from anything serious. After the summer, the matter will already be considered "old news." Past experience has shown that removing a topic from the agenda has succeeded in silencing the response, and may it not come to pass, G-d forbid, in this terrible matter.

May it be the will of Hashem that from now on, a person will only bring good tidings to his fellow.

## 9944

[9944](#_ftn_1959)

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Shimshon Yaakov Ginzburg
5 Amindav St., Jerusalem

Greetings and blessings!

Following your visit and our conversation, I have just received your letter dated 27 Tammuz.

I thank you very much for your willingness to come to the aid of the teachers who will reach out to you, to guide them and assist them in every way possible, etc. However, I must comment on what you wrote regarding the *bagrut* (matriculation) exams. While it is indeed necessary, in my opinion **everyone** agrees that this is not due to the subject matter itself, but rather because of the law. And surely everyone also agrees that laws must adapt and change in accordance with the demands of the **present** situation, rather than the situation being forced to adapt to the laws—for that is the foundation and purpose of human laws.

As we stand in the days of "Bein HaMetzarim," may it be His will [that they be transformed](#_ftn_1960) into joy and gladness with the redemption of the entire Jewish people—the redemption of the collective and the individual alike—including the matters we spoke about, and culminating in the fulfillment of the [prophecy](#_1961), "And I will break the bars of your yoke and lead you upright," with the true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and blessings.

9945

By the Grace of G-d
Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Aharon Yariv
Shalom u’Bracha,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, and I thank you for your attention in responding to my letter.

In truth, I was unsure whether to continue with this matter, as it is not clear from your letter whether the decision regarding the manner of response and combat in this area has already been finalized, etc. It is certainly not my place to intervene without being asked, and all the more so to seek out difficulties and the like. Especially since what I wrote is straightforward, and surely it has not escaped the notice of those on the ground. Since they have not acted upon it, they surely have their reasons and justifications.

Nevertheless, since everything is by Divine Providence, and the matter is extremely serious, of the utmost importance, and so on, I feel I cannot refrain from responding—even if only to address the doubt and the doubt of a doubt—at least briefly:

Regarding the method of execution to ensure that the Canal cannot be used for a long time: as long as flights are conducted over this area day after day, there are surely several opportunities to accomplish this—whether with overt intent or as if by accident—to the point of fundamentally disabling the Canal. This is especially true given that its length extends for 100 kilometers or more; if it is disabled in one, two, or three places, it would, by default, negate the possibility of using the entire Canal.

It seems the policy until now has been to avoid taking drastic measures so as not to provoke the Bear too much—

This is the only explanation I have found for why, some years ago, the area around Aswan was not disabled in a way that would have prevented the construction of the dam there.

But in the current situation, it seems there is nothing left to lose, especially since the hope that it will be possible to bomb it day after day for many months is extremely slim.

And if you were to say that one should also learn from the Aswan matter—that it would have been worth provoking them then, rather than arriving at the current situation, where there is a strong, fortified area, closed off to the entire world—then consider this: If the Bear wishes to establish a center for atomic industry there, not only for defense but also for offense, in all its details, without endangering the residents of his own country, and in a place that serves as a testing ground, etc.—there is no place more suitable than the area of the Aswan Dam.

This is especially true if the proposal for a three-month ceasefire, or thereabouts, is accepted. It is understood that the promises that they will not exploit this time to establish and fortify the western area, etc., have no substance, for it is not in human power to guarantee this—even if there were not already three precedents in the past, including recently. This is particularly true when they use the distinction between "defense" and "offense," where everything is allegedly permitted for "defense." In this regard, one might add that they are returning and resettling the ruined cities on the western bank.

On the other hand, since the benefit to the Bear from opening the Canal is immense, he will certainly not forgo this opportunity, as long as the possibility of opening the Canal is not ruled out due to technical reasons that cannot be repaired for a long time, etc.

Given the pace of events now, it is possible that only for a very short time will there still be an opportunity for you to fly in this area without commitment or without scrutiny, etc. Thus, the decision regarding the aforementioned is also urgent. I ask for your forgiveness that a civilian who has never been in the military is nevertheless expressing an opinion on such a matter.

By the way, and perhaps this is also a continuation of the above: the entire condition that there must be a definitive ceasefire together with the commencement of negotiations for peace—these two matters have no logical, security, or economic connection, etc. A proven proof is that for three years they have been trying to talk about peace alongside bombings, etc. The only explanation is that the opposing side wants to exploit this ceasefire time to rebuild what was destroyed, to fortify, etc.

I have sought to find an explanation anywhere regarding the connection between these two matters, and to my astonishment, not only did I not find any explanation, but I did not find anyone asking openly: If they truly will not exploit the time for fortification, etc., what is the emphasis and the condition—without which it is impossible—that there must be a ceasefire?

I understand that I have seen the explanation that this is the demand of the opposing side. But consider the alternative: if there is no other explanation, then this is a clear declaration from the opposing side that they will fortify the area, etc., even more than it was before. For everything needed for this is ready—some of it in Libya, some of it on ships located in close proximity—and the experts are either already on the ground or can arrive within a few hours.

Surely no one hopes that after they begin negotiations for peace, the opposing side will forgo the possibility of fortification, etc. And if such a naive person exists, in diplomatic terms, he is not at all in touch with reality.

Seemingly, I have written at too great a length, but surely you too will feel that I have restrained myself—not only in my expressions but also in the explanation and even in the content, to which much more could be added.

The analogy from the medical field is well-known: when, G-d forbid, a serious and major surgery is required, there are seemingly two approaches: to perform the surgery all at once, or to perform it in stages over several days or months, etc., with the explanation that since it is a large and serious surgery, it should be divided into parts. The result of this is that instead of the first approach—performing it all at once while the patient is still in a relatively good condition and under known conditions in every detail, so that one can prepare a remedy for every change—the surgery itself, with several interruptions, exhausts the patient's strength, his condition becomes worse and worse, and sometimes there are complications that were not foreseen, which confuse the calculation of how to continue the surgery. This is especially true when one encounters an emergency situation where there is no time for proper preparation. And what they wanted to gain—not to weaken the patient or provoke his relatives—is unavoidable; on the contrary, they provoke them several times instead of once. The lesson for our situation is simple.

As we find ourselves in these days of "Bein HaMetzarim," and in accordance with the virtue of these days, as we are promised in the words of the prophet that they "shall be turned into joy and gladness," may it be His will that this also be the case regarding the content of this letter—that the situation be turned into joy and gladness, "and Israel performs valiantly."

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings.

## 9949

[9949](#_ftn_1985)

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the members of the Kfar Chabad Committee, founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of our generation, in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days—

May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

I have just received your letter dated 10 Menachem Av, in which you write that you have been elected as members of the village committee, and you conclude with a request for a blessing, etc.

At an auspicious time, you will be remembered at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, together with all the residents of Kfar Chabad, from young to old, children and women—may they live—for the fulfillment of their heart’s desires for the good in all the matters you write about, and in all matters of Kfar Chabad, in general and in particular.

May it be Hashem’s will that, as you write, you merit to share good news from time to time regarding all of the above, in a manner that is ever-increasing.

It is known [1986] from a maamar of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding a blessing, that the common expression used in this connection is "gishmei bracha" (rains of blessing). This means that a blessing in general is like the rain [1987] that descends upon the earth to make it give birth and sprout; however, there must first be plowing and sowing, and after the rain, there must also be cultivation, etc. All of this serves as a vessel for the effect of the rain and the blessing that depends upon it—and even to the extent of "many times over." The analogy is understood.

May Hashem, blessed be He, grant that in this, too, the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, will take effect, such that each one of you—and indeed, every single resident of the village—will do everything that depends on them for the benefit of the village, its stabilization, and its development, both materially and spiritually. This should be with effort and energy in the manner of our Sages’ expression [1988], "If you have labored," so that the promise, "you will find," will also be fulfilled—success beyond all proportion, reaching the level of a "finding" (a windfall).

And in this month—Menachem Av—in which we have been promised [1989] that it will be transformed entirely into joy and gladness, may the success in all of the above begin, and in a manner of "ascending in matters of holiness" [1990], especially in the Holy Land, and particularly in the point that from Kfar Chabad the wellsprings shall spread outward, both in material matters and in spiritual matters. May you succeed in all of the above with joy and goodness of heart, with the drawing together of the hearts of all the village residents, the unification of forces, and cooperation, for we have been promised [1991]: "Bless us, our Father, (for) we are all as one."

With blessings for success in all of the above and for good news [1992] in everything, from everything, and all.

9953

[9953](#_ftn_2003)

B”H, 18 Menachem Av, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. [Ari](#_ftn_2004) Sharon
Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge with thanks receipt of your letter dated August 16th. Because of the importance and urgency of the matter, I am hastening to reply, especially regarding the conclusion of your letter.

[As we discussed here](#_ftn_2005), in my opinion, your place is in the IDF, where, with Hashem’s help, you have succeeded and will continue to succeed. Naturally, this is in addition to the benefit to the many—I refer to the people of Bnei Yisrael, the holy nation dwelling in Eretz Yisrael, the Holy Land—whom Hashem has blessed, and whom you have succeeded in protecting through your talents, your exertion, your energy, and so on.

Therefore, and as I spoke with you when you were here, you must certainly continue in your position and in your most responsible role. I have a strong hope that even if there is someone whose relationship with you requires improvement or correction for whatever reason, ultimately, even that person will acknowledge your seriousness, your sense of responsibility, and your dedication to your role, to the point that you live it.

Based on the above, my opinion is also understood that there is no logic, G-d forbid, for you to resign for any other pursuit, and certainly not in the political arena, including a ministerial position or the like. That is not your role, nor is that where your talent and knowledge would be utilized; on the contrary.

In this vein, I wish that Mr. Ezer Weizman had not resigned from the army either. Even though, according to reports, he was insulted and promises made to him were not kept, and so on, there is no reason for the logic that because someone committed an injustice against him, he should therefore harm himself. His resignation from the army caused him harm, in addition to the loss that was apparently caused to the army by not utilizing his knowledge and talents. This applies even if he had remained in the government, and all the more so as events developed thereafter.

It is not my business to intervene in army procedures and the like, but in general, it is strange that if a simple soldier, in whom the army has invested several months of military training, wishes to leave the army, it is considered—rightfully—a grave offense; yet, specifically for a general or the like, in whom the highest level of training, energy, and money has been invested, if he wishes to leave the army, it is left to his private discretion, even if he explicitly states that his reasons are personal, and even when it is clear that the army—and consequently the overall security situation—will suffer as a result!

The above is by way of a side note. But regarding you, as written above, I have no doubt—not even a shadow of a doubt—that your role and your success lie specifically in the army, especially now that you are at a high and vital level regarding the situation in the entire country. Of what consequence is it if this involves some unpleasantness or friction, etc., compared to the benefit of the many and the protection of the many?

All of the above applies even to the current situation. But although I am not a pessimist at all, one cannot ignore the reality that if, G-d forbid, matters continue in a natural way, the position of the other side across the Suez Canal will strengthen and fortify itself. Despite all official protests, the enemy is certainly utilizing every day to increase its strength, bringing in the most effective weaponry, and so on, for there is no doubt that the United States will not enter into a war with the Soviet Union over this. And as for the claims and the outcry regarding how it is possible that they did not keep their promise (which, from the outset, no one believed—that they would not utilize the ceasefire to fortify their position and status, as General Chaim Herzog also said publicly in a newspaper interview; meaning, it has been proven that it is impossible to deceive even the fools, if there were any who believed they would not utilize the ceasefire, and all the more so that the members of the government in Eretz Yisrael, or in the U.S., or in the USSR, etc., did not believe it, just as it was three years ago, and fourteen [years](#_ftn_2006) ago, and many times before that)—they will continue to drag out the arguments as much as possible, and afterward, they will decide on a *status quo* as it stands at the end of the discussions. From this, it is understood that in any negotiations regarding peace terms—after the other side has fortified itself, etc.—the Israeli side will then be at a disadvantage, since the security situation will have changed from one extreme to the other from the day of the ceasefire to the day the negotiations regarding the demands and terms conclude.

I fear to say—and perhaps it is not a fear but, on the contrary, a form of hope—that just as it was at the beginning of the Six-Day War, the other side will take a foolish step that will force the cancellation of the ceasefire. And Hashem will again perform miracles and wonders, such that within the shortest time after the cancellation of the ceasefire and the renewal of defense—the only way for which is an offensive—they will deploy all forces, not in a half-hearted manner as has been the case until now, but rather a true defense. Then there is hope that the fire will be ceased in a lasting manner, and they will finally arrive at peace; not like the current situation, which, as mentioned above, is the path leading directly to the renewal of war, G-d forbid, only under conditions much, much worse than the conditions on the day of the ceasefire.

I have written at length in connection with what you wrote, that what I wrote [regarding the Canal](#_ftn_2007) and so on has already passed its time. For I fear to say that in not much time, the aforementioned matter will be *actual* once again. I wish that I would not be correct in this assessment and that I would be proven wrong, although in my opinion, according to the current trend of events in the natural way, it does not appear so.

It was pleasant to learn from our friend Mr. S.M. that there is peace for your family and peace for you. May it be the will that we finally hear news of true peace in the land. Certainly, the way to this is not through showing signs of weakness and a readiness for far-reaching compromises and concessions, according to the rhetoric being spoken now, to the point that it is published in all the newspapers. Rather, on the contrary, as the well-known adage goes: if one truly desires peace, one must show that one is also prepared for the opposite, with full force and under good conditions.

With respect and a blessing for success and good tidings.

P.S. I did not want to mention this in our conversation with you during your visit here, but on the other hand, I do not see the permission to refrain from mentioning it, at least now: I have a strong hope that you are precise [in the laying of](#_ftn_2009) Tefillin every weekday. In your case, this is not merely the fulfillment of a private mitzvah by a private individual, but also a matter that concerns the benefit of the many. And although your many preoccupations related to the security situation and so on are known, on the contrary, the preoccupations and the situation are an additional reason to be as precise as necessary in the fulfillment of this mitzvah, both the Tefillin of the hand and the Tefillin of the head. Please forgive me for writing the above.

## 9954

[9954](#_ftn_2010)

By the Grace of G-d, 18 Menachem Av, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. [Avraham](#_ftn_2011) Macherowski

Aruba

Greeting and Blessing!

I thank you for your letter from Erev Shabbos Nachamu, along with the enclosed copy [of the telegram](#_ftn_2012) from your Jewish community. May the Ribono shel Olam help that, at long last, the repeated appeals regarding this matter should be effective, and that the greatest disgrace one Jew can inflict upon another—and in this case, not just another Jew, but the entire Jewish people, involving Chilul Hashem and the desecration of the honor of the Jewish people—should be nullified. For everyone sees the greatest falsehood in proclaiming to the entire world that a non-Jew who pays 25 dollars to a rabbi sitting in California—whose name and address are known—receives in return a confirmation and certificate declaring that non-Jew to be a Jew. And he is then recognized in Eretz Yisrael as a Jew with all the rights the government grants to Jews; and it goes without saying that this non-Jew is issued a passport stating that he is a Jew, without any qualifications. Such a horrific thing the Jewish people have not experienced in thousands of years, not even from their greatest enemies; and yet, it is precisely in our generation that this has occurred.

It is not worthwhile—especially as we approach the month of Elul—to write about things that do not bring honor to Jews, and on the contrary, etc.

May the Ribono shel Olam bless and grant success—in accordance with the date of your writing, Erev Shabbos Nachamu—that there should be the true consolation of the nullification of the aforementioned law, Rachmana Litzlan, and very soon indeed. May Jews be proud of their Yiddishkeit, truly proud, and not bow down to every non-Jew, flattering them and trying to appease them, convincing themselves that through this the non-Jew will eventually become a good friend. They forget what has happened in our generation regarding the chasing after non-Jews, and what has happened in previous generations. From now on, Jews themselves must stop disgracing the Jewish people and desecrating the honor of Yisrael; this is the only way that the non-Jew, too, will know that one must respect a Jew.

With blessings that you should be able to report good tidings regarding all the matters about which you write in your letter, and very soon.

## 9905

[9905](#_ftn_2013)

[B"H](#_ftn_2014), 21 Menachem Av, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mrs. [Sheina](#_ftn_2015) Zelda, may she live:

Blessings and peace!

I received your letter some time ago, and for understandable reasons it was difficult to reply, as it is hard to find the appropriate words and the appropriate subject matter. However, on the day following the Yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and in connection with the thoughts of the Yahrtzeit, the time and the sentiment are more conducive to responding to your letter and expressing a few thoughts in continuation of yesterday, among them:

[Certainly,](#_ftn_2016) Hashem is the essence of goodness, [and it is the nature](#_ftn_2017) of the Good to bestow good. Therefore, it is absolutely certain that in every matter, affair, and event, there is good—and not only regarding the life of the World to Come, but also in this world of ours, in [which](#_ftn_2018) the Torah and its mitzvos were given. Indeed, its primary purpose is in this world, [as it is stated,](#_ftn_2018) "It is not in heaven."

Another point, which is one of the fundamental instructions for the life of the Jewish people—both for the collective and for the individual—is that [action](#_ftn_2019) is the essential thing. And in every matter, the essential thing is to be found.

Based on the above, it is understood that even in an event of this nature that has occurred to you—namely, that the soul of a close relative, a very close one, etc., has ascended to heaven—one must certainly, despite the feeling of loss and so on, seek the good even in this, and translate it into the practical sphere, into practical life, and even into daily life.

One of the points in this regard is that since we are speaking of the ascent of a close soul to heaven, those close to the departed must continue the activities in which the departed was engaged during their lifetime in this world. And as mentioned—this must be done through actual deeds, in addition to the part that each person must play in being active and energetic in this world to the best of their ability, to fulfill their own obligations.

And since, according to Divine Providence, an additional role and additional activity have been placed upon the living on earth, [certainly](#_ftn_2020) the necessary strengths to fulfill that role as required have been granted beforehand. Like any task imposed by Divine Providence, this must be done with energy and vitality. Any thought or matter that confuses or detracts from this must be banished with both hands, for such thoughts disturb not only the living, but—if one may make the distinction—also the soul of the departed. For the aforementioned activity brings the soul satisfaction and elevation; being in the World of Truth, the soul knows the truth, that this activity is connected to and performed for its merit, as if it were a mission.

From the above, it is understood that there is no room for the conclusion of loneliness and so forth. On the contrary, precisely such an event should lead to activity among people, with increased energy and on a larger scale. [As has been discussed](#_ftn_2021) in several places—and it is something that any simple person understands without doubt—there is no basis to say that bodily illness, whatever it may be, affects the soul, its vitality, or its eternity. That is to say, the change is only in the connection of the soul to the body—a connection that also brings certain limitations to the soul—and when that connection is severed, the [limitations](#_ftn_2022) are also removed. Activity in any place whatsoever is known immediately to the soul, for it is no longer limited by place, time, or the instruments of sight and hearing, etc.

I will conclude with the wish that you arrange your life in a way that you can utilize the talents with which you have been gifted, for the benefit of the many, in addition to the benefit of the individual or individuals, and with energy and vitality. May Hashem bless you with long, good days and years, and with a good arrangement in a revealed and manifest good in all details.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above, and soon,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I would certainly be interested in every detail regarding your arrangements from here on, including—and this is also essential—regarding your financial situation. You should certainly write about all of this as it is, based on our family closeness, etc., especially since only a few remain of the survivors of our family in our generation.

## 9957

[9957](#_ftn_2025)

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Aluf [Rechavam](#_ftn_2026) Ze’evi, may he live, Commander of the Central Command,

Greetings and blessings!

It is with deep and profound sorrow that I received the news that there are certain difficulties [regarding the delivery](#_ftn_2027) of greetings and blessings to several units of our brethren, the Children of Israel, may they live, who are defending the People of Israel in the Land of Israel with mesiras nefesh, even though I do not know the reason for this clearly.

Since I do not know the reason clearly, I am not in a position to respond to it, other than to write these lines in a general sense, with an introduction that may perhaps seem strange to you. However, since it expresses my heartfelt feelings, my hope is strong that you will not mind that I am taking your time to read the introduction as well, which is:

I believe with complete faith, founded upon what I have seen throughout my life on several occasions, and—perhaps even more importantly—what I have heard from other authoritative figures in this regard, and primarily because it is founded upon that which is discussed decisively and explicitly [in our Torah](#_ftn_2028), the Torah of life (a guide for life), that a faithful and heartfelt blessing from one person to another has validity and is effective—sometimes in its entirety and sometimes in part, sometimes immediately and sometimes after a time; this is in addition to the psychological aspect of the matter, that it brings hearts closer, encourages the spirit, and so on and so forth.

I likewise believe with complete faith, as above, regarding the [segulah](#_ftn_2029) of the mitzvah of tefillin, especially for military personnel.

It is understood that this does not obligate anyone to be as firm in that faith as I am, but since, on the face of it, there is no room to suspect that I am motivated by personal bias, etc., then in any event, it should surely arouse in one a doubt that perhaps there is substance and benefit in the matter. Furthermore—and this is the main point—since the psychological impression and the encouragement of spirit are seen tangibly before everyone’s eyes, then certainly and surely, the matter is close to gain and far from loss, Heaven forbid.

As mentioned above, since I do not know the reason for the difficulty, etc.—even if you were to say that there is a reason for irritation, etc., and a well-founded and strong reason—the irritation could be directed at me or at certain people in my surroundings or in the Land of Israel, but this has no connection or cause to create difficulty in bringing a blessing and greetings, etc. This is especially true when we are speaking of soldiers and military personnel, whose encouragement is not merely the encouragement of a private individual, but relates to the environment and the general morale, etc. Would that everyone who has the ability to encourage them and strengthen their spirit, etc., would do everything in their power to do so.

In these last lines, I intend to address a reason that may also have been taken into account: that if permission is given to bring the aforementioned blessings and greetings, someone else will come tomorrow or the next day and request permission as well. As stated, if there is hope that through this the morale, self-confidence, and spirit, etc., of the soldiers of the IDF will be strengthened, then all the more so, let him come as well. Surely it is within the power of you and your colleagues to arrange matters in such a way that there will be no interference whatsoever with the order and the process of life, etc., that must be maintained in the aforementioned areas.

You surely understand that the intent of my letter is not, Heaven forbid, to raise difficulties or to ask questions, etc., but only to request of you, again and again, that you not only do everything within your power so that my emissaries can speak with those under your command regarding the blessings of many of our brethren, the Children of Israel, to them (as I speak in the capacity of their shaliach), and to tell them that [we] feel their efforts, and that even those who are far away are thinking of them, their situation, and their mesiras nefesh, etc.; but also to speak to them and tell them about the strong faith of many of the Children of Israel regarding the segulah of the mitzvah of tefillin, and that they are prepared to help them in this as well by providing a pair of tefillin, etc., etc.

Furthermore, that you should also do what is within your power for the success of this endeavor—despite the aforementioned reason and your preoccupations, etc.

Based on what I have heard about you and your activity and dedication to the fulfillment of your most responsible and most important role, I am certain that there is no need to elaborate further on the aforementioned matter. May it be the will [of Hashem] that you receive these lines—even though they are few in quantity, and especially in relation to the matter and its importance—with a favorable countenance, and that you will not suspect me of any personal bias whatsoever, and that you will do everything within your power for the success of the mission I have requested, and that you will also influence your colleagues, may they live and be well, in the aforementioned matter, and with success.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned. And may Hashem, who watches over every man and woman with Hashgacha Pratis, grant you success in the fulfillment of your role, the defense of the Holy People in the Holy Land—a defense with success in all respects—until we see with our own eyes, and very soon, the fulfillment of the [promise](#_ftn_2030): "And I will grant peace in the land... and no sword shall pass through your land, and I will break the yokes of your burden and lead you upright."

With respect and blessing,
