## 9864

[9864](#_ftn_2047)

B”H, 13 Elul, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. [Yosef](#_ftn_2048) Ciechanover

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 7th of Elul, and in accordance with the tone of your letter, I am answering you not in the order [of your questions], especially since in my opinion the question is not merely personal, as you wrote, but is also a matter that concerns the many.

The question is: should you continue in your current position and office, or should you accept a position offered to you at an investment firm, etc.?

Now, without entering into the details of the offer for a new position, your current position is in the security sector, and surely this is not the time to do anything that might affect or detract from this area.

And even if you were to say that they would find a replacement, etc., someone who has seniority and experience in this field for some time is not comparable to new faces, as there are always complications of integration and adjustment between a new employee and the mechanism, and especially with those who oversee it.

Surely this was my attitude toward the aforementioned question when you were here—even several weeks ago—but now, it is with even greater intensity. And all the more so, this is my absolute opinion in connection with the current situation, where it is most necessary that there be no upheaval, not even a slight upheaval, within the framework of the security apparatus. Especially as you told me during your visit here, and as you hint at in this letter, that you are in close contact with those at the helm. And if, in the past, if only they had held a firmer line and had not accepted the opinion of the compromisers and those who make concessions, then surely that is how it should be now, when even (at the very least, a portion of) the compromisers have already realized this. Despite this, there is still a noticeable tendency among several people who have influence to continue with concessions and pleas, etc. (even though they have realized that every proposal of compromise is interpreted in all corners of the globe as a clear sign of weakness, and immediately brings about an even greater attack). Therefore, the presence of all those who support the aforementioned line in positions that have influence in this area is even more necessary, especially those who have direct influence. And my hope is that you are among those who support with a whole heart the authority of Am Yisrael, which is worthy of being relied upon—and all the more so, the Rock of Israel, Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, whose [as it is written](#_ftn_2049) eyes are upon the Holy Land (and upon the holy people wherever they may be) "from the beginning of the year until the end of the year," and who [walks](#_ftn_2050) in the midst of the camp of Israel to save them and to deliver their enemies before them. And surely for someone of your caliber, there is no need for further explanation of my position on the aforementioned.

I wish you success in utilizing your talents and opportunities to their fullest for the strengthening of all matters of security, through trust in the G-d of Israel and in Am Yisrael, beginning in these days, the days of the month of Elul, in which it is the [custom](#_ftn_2051) of the Children of Israel to recite twice each day, "[Hashem](#_ftn_2052) is my light and my salvation; whom shall I fear? Hashem is the stronghold of my life; of whom shall I be afraid? Though a camp should encamp against me, my heart shall not fear... and now my head shall be lifted up above my enemies round about me... Hope in Hashem; be strong and let your heart take courage."

With the blessing of *Kesivah v’chasimah tovah* and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 9965

[9965](#_ftn_2053)

[B"H](#_ftn_2054), 15 Elul, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter . . .

As we stand in the month of Elul, a month unique among all the months of the year—for it is the month of [accounting](#_ftn_2055) for the year that is passing and the month of preparation for Rosh Hashanah and for the entire coming year—its uniqueness is also expressed in the fact that on [every](#_ftn_2056) day of this month, we [recite](#_ftn_2057) twice the [psalm](#_edn_296) beginning: "Hashem is my light and my salvation, whom shall I fear? Hashem is the stronghold of my life, of whom shall I be afraid?"

Regarding this—[in the simple](#_edn_297) sense—[we must explain](#_edn_298) the content of these three general [titles](#_edn_299):

Since [two paths](#_edn_300) lie before a person—the path of [life](#_ftn_2058) and good, and the opposite path—

"Hashem is my light"—to see [which is](#_edn_302) the path of life and good;

Since there are many obstacles and trials in a person's path, [and our Sages have said](#_edn_303) that every day a person's inclination overcomes him,

"Hashem... is my salvation"—the Ribono shel Olam helps him to be victorious in the war against the yetzer, to overcome all obstacles, and to withstand all trials;

Since the [perfection](#_edn_304) of a person's avodah in this world is to go [from strength](#_ftn_2059) to strength—from good to something better, and [from life](#_edn_305) to life, which is more vibrant (lebedig)—

"Hashem is the stronghold of my life"—He gives strength to the vitality in a person's life, and then he begins anew—but with added vitality and on a [more elevated](#_edn_306) level—the sequence of "my light," "my salvation," and "the stronghold of my life."

All of this is also hinted at in the blowing of the shofar, which also expresses the uniqueness of this month, in that on every [day](#_edn_307) of it (except for Shabbos and Erev Rosh Hashanah—for a specific reason regarding them), we blow the shofar, etc., [as it is said](#_ftn_2060), "Hashem has ascended with the teruah," [and it is said](#_ftn_2061), "If a shofar is blown in a city, will the people not tremble?"

The Rambam [explained](#_edn_308) the hint contained in the blowing of the shofar: "Awaken, you sleepers, from your sleep, and you slumberers, rouse yourselves from your slumber" (for the [vitality](#_edn_309) of one who is asleep and slumbering is not at all comparable to that of a person who is awake), "[search](#_edn_310) your deeds" (to distinguish between those that are of the side of life and good and those that are, etc.), "and return in teshuvah" (that he overcomes his yetzer, and [He who knows](#_edn_311) secrets [testifies](#_edn_312) regarding him that he will not return to folly again), "and remember your Creator" (who is "my light," "my salvation," and "the stronghold of my life"—for through this, he awakens from his sleep, etc.).

May it be the will that every man and woman do what is dependent upon them in all that has been stated, and see that "Hashem is my light and my salvation and the stronghold of my life," and that He fulfills everything one asks and requests for the good, up to the fulfillment of the [promise](#_ftn_2062), "And I will sacrifice in His tent sacrifices of teruah"—in our third Beis Hamikdash, which [will be built](#_edn_313) in its place by Moshiach Tzidkeinu, in the true and complete Geulah, very soon.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

9896

[9896](#_ftn_2063)

[B"H](#_ftn_2064), Erev Shabbos Kodesh Tavo, 18 Elul, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner
of Yeshivas Achei Tmimim in Newark
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

In response to the news regarding the upcoming gathering, the annual dinner of the Yeshiva, on the coming 22nd of Elul—

The month of Elul is a special month among all the months of the year, in that it is [the](#_ftn_2065) month of *cheshbon hanefesh* for the past year, and preparation for the new year.

The content of this month is also expressed by the fact that [from](#_ftn_2066) Rosh Chodesh Elul we begin to recite the 27th chapter of Tehillim: **"L'Dovid Hashem Ori V'Yishi... Maoz Chayai"** — "Hashem is my light and my salvation... the strength of my life."

The explanation of these three concepts—light, salvation, and strength—is as follows:

A person has two paths before him in life, the path of good and the path of its opposite, and he must choose between them. Therefore, he must turn to Hashem to **illuminate** the correct path.

However, there are stumbling blocks and difficulties along this path; therefore, one must also turn to Hashem for help and **yeshuah** to avoid stumbling blocks and overcome difficulties.

And since perfection demands that one should walk on the good path **"meichayil el chayil"** (from strength to strength) and ascend in all good things—from good to better, and from *simcha* and vitality to greater *simcha* and vitality—one must ultimately turn to Hashem as the **"maoz chayai"** (the strength of my life).

In light of these thoughts regarding the month of Elul and in the spirit of this month, as explained above, I hope that the annual event will be carried out with great success, in order to help the Yeshiva strengthen and expand its educational activities; an education *al taharas hakodesh*, founded upon this "Elul-like" approach, to raise the students to true perfection based on these three foundations: Hashem as **"Ori"** (my light), **"Yishi"** (my salvation), and **"Maoz Chayai"** (the strength of my life).

With greetings to the administration of the Yeshiva, the esteemed guests, and all the participants and friends who have the great *zechus* to support the Yeshiva so that it may flourish and grow and produce good fruit,

With honor and blessing for success, good tidings, and for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9867

[9867](#_ftn_2068)

[B"H](#_ftn_2069), Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, 18 Elul, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel everywhere,

May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

The month of Elul, the conclusion of the year, is—as is well known—a time for *cheshbon hanefesh* (soul-searching) regarding the past year, and a time of preparation for the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing. For this reason as well—in order for the preparation to be a proper one—there must first be a *cheshbon hanefesh* regarding the past.

It goes without saying that this must be a *cheshbon tzedek* (a true accounting), a correct assessment: what did one do incorrectly, what was left undone, and what was accomplished.

This must be accompanied by a firm resolution to rectify that which requires correction, to complete that which was left undone—utilizing all one’s strengths and capabilities—and to ascend, to elevate oneself to a higher level than the previous year, going *meichayil el chayil* (from strength to strength) in all matters of goodness and holiness.

***

The extent to which it is necessary to make a *cheshbon tzedek* when transitioning from one year to the next can be seen from the fact that multiple opportunities and times have been provided for this at the conclusion of the year:

— The month of Elul, as mentioned above;

— The twelve days from 18 Elul until Rosh Hashanah, which, as is known, correspond to the months of the year—one day for each month—in order to rectify each month;

— Rosh Hashanah itself, whose special *mitzvah* is *tekias shofar*. The hint and concept of *tekias shofar* is, as the great teacher the Rambam teaches us, to awaken Jews to *cheshbon hanefesh*;

— The *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* (Ten Days of Repentance) in general, and specifically the seven days between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, which correspond to the seven days of the week: the Sunday of these seven days serves as a rectification (according to this calculation) for all the Sundays of the year; Monday for all the Mondays, and so on; until the climax is reached on—

— The *Yom HaKadosh*, Yom Kippur.

***

As stated, *cheshbon hanefesh* must lead to a correct assessment of all deeds performed and those neglected. However, a person is a *nogeia badavar* (an interested party); he is personally involved, and therefore too subjective to judge himself without ever making a mistake. One’s own intellect and the feeling of self-love intervene, which creates a bias toward an incorrect assessment.

Furthermore, human intellect in general—which is limited—is not always reliable in judging what is good and what is the opposite. Therefore, the Almighty, the Creator of the world and of man, who knows human limitations and difficulties, gave us the Torah, which is called *Torah Ohr* (Torah is Light)—to illuminate our path in life. When a Jew accepts *Torah u’mitzvos* with *kabbalas ol* (without the interference of human intellect), he unites with the Divine intellect of *Torah Ohr*, and it becomes bright and clear to him what he must do and what he must not do.

This is the content of the words *Hashem Ori* ("Hashem is my light") at the beginning of Psalm 27 in *Tehillim*, which we begin reciting twice daily from Rosh Chodesh Elul.

Yet, even when one knows clearly what is good and what is not, it is not always easy to actually perform the good and correct thing to the fullest extent, especially since this sometimes requires acting against one’s own (limited) intellect, or against one’s own strong desires and *taavah*. There are, or it appears that there are, various difficulties and *nisyonos* (trials)—which is why every Jew, even a *tzaddik*, prays every morning at the start of the day: *Al tavi’enu lidei nisayon* (Do not bring us into the hands of a trial), etc. In this, too, the Almighty comes to our aid—if one makes a firm resolution to withstand the trial.

And this is the content of... *yishi* ("Hashem is my salvation"), the continuation after *Hashem Ori* in the aforementioned verse.

The transition from one year to the next is not merely a "calendar" event; one has gained another year. The intention and purpose are to have more in *tov u’kedusha* (goodness and holiness), to elevate oneself to a "greater" and higher level, so that there should be an increase in matters of *Torah u’mitzvos*, in an ever-increasing measure. For no matter how good it was previously—even for great people and *tzaddikim*—it is not good enough if one stands in one place; rather, one must strive to go *meichayil el chayil*, ever higher and higher. In this, one must again turn to the Almighty, that He should help and provide the necessary strength to ascend in daily life, so that today should be better than yesterday, and tomorrow should be better than today.

And this is the meaning of the words... *Hashem maoz chayai* ("Hashem is the strength of my life")—the continuation in the aforementioned verse.

***

May the Almighty help that, coming from the bright day of 18 Elul—the birthday of the two great luminaries, the giants of Israel in their generations and in the generations to come—the Baal Shem Tov, founder of the general teachings of Chassidus, and the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*—who dedicated their lives to strengthening the matters of *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*, which includes even a "stranger" whom one has never met, that toward him, too, the *ahavas Yisrael*, the "love your fellow as yourself," should be "as yourself," as to one’s own self—

May every man and woman act in the aforementioned matters, both for their own benefit and for the benefit of others, in an increasing measure. This will surely evoke and draw down from the attribute of the Holy One, Blessed be He, which is *midah k’neged midah* (measure for measure—though far greater and more abundant—from His full, open, holy, and wide hand).

May it be fulfilled in actual reality: *Hashem Ori V’yishi*... *Hashem maoz chayai*, and may we carry out all matters with expansiveness, joy, and a good heart.

And this will also hasten the fulfillment of the Divine promise (as the continuation in that Psalm states): "To behold the pleasantness of Hashem and to visit in His Temple... and I will sacrifice in His tent sacrifices of *teruah* (shofar blasts)"—

In the *Beis HaMikdash* that will be built in its place by the King from the house of David—Moshiach Tzidkeinu, in our true and complete Redemption, very soon.

With respect and blessings for a *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9969

[9969](#_ftn_2088)

B.H., 21 Elul, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, man of G-d, who is involved in communal affairs and accomplishes much,
Rabbi Simcha HaKohen Kook
Netanya

Shalom u’vracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 12 Elul, along with the enclosure, in which you write regarding the difficulties in instilling the recognition of the statement of our Sages [Chazal](#_ftn_2089): "Bereishis — for the sake of the Torah, which is called 'beginning' (reishis)... and for the sake of Yisrael, who are called 'beginning' (reishis)," and you ask for my opinion on this.

Now, surely the words of our Sages do not require proofs and evidence, etc., particularly regarding such fundamental matters as the one mentioned. And certainly, they—Chazal—also appreciated the opposition of the entire world to accepting such a statement, especially in light of the verse [that](#_ftn_2090) "you are the fewest of all the peoples," [and Yisrael](#_ftn_2091) are "downtrodden and cast aside," etc. Yet, despite all this, they publicized the aforementioned statement with absolute certainty, to the extent that Rashi, in his commentary on the Torah, transcribed this very statement. And the line of Rashi in this regard is to explain the simple meaning of the verse, [as he states in several places](#_ftn_2092): "I have come only to explain the simple meaning of the verse." [From which it is understood](#_ftn_2093) that even when Rashi brings a *drash* or *midrash*, it is also relevant and necessary to the simple meaning of the verse, only that it is not on the most superficial level. And since at the very beginning of his commentary on the Torah he transcribed the aforementioned statement of our Sages, this means that even a [five-year-old](#_ftn_2094) beginning the study of Scripture should be informed of this; it is therefore understood that it is possible to explain it even according to his level.

We have seen throughout the generations of our people, the Children of Yisrael, in their exile—both in the simple sense and in the spiritual sense—that all efforts to cover up the truth of our Torah, the Torah of truth, in order that the Torah might be more acceptable to a certain circle or to the mindset of a certain person—as the term for this is usually called, the "apologetic approach"—not only failed to bring any lasting benefit, but actually caused damage, whether in the near term or after a period of time. This is in addition to the point that any compromise with the truth is a deviation from the truth; in other words, it is the opposite of truth, for compromise and truth are mutually exclusive.

I do not know the extent of your influence, although the [statement of the wise man](#_ftn_2095) also applies to this matter: "Accept the truth from whoever says it," and all the more so when it comes from a Rabbi and teacher of instruction in Yisrael, and in education, etc. But if, for whatever reason, the aforementioned premise cannot be accepted, at the very least one must endeavor to highlight the point that the history of Yisrael is above the natural order, and is marked by *hashgacha pratis*, etc. This is especially true when, by explaining the events in the history of other nations, one emphasizes the implications regarding our people, the Children of Yisrael, and their lives and the adventures they have endured, etc., etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in utilizing your influence, directly and indirectly, to instill a pure *yiras Hashem*—which is one with the *ahavas Hashem*—into the daily lives of all those you can influence. The line in this is [as](#_ftn_2096) it is said, "In all your ways, know Him"—in all ways and manners, etc., and all the more so regarding textbooks and education in general.

With respect and with the blessing of *Kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, and for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and may the merit of the many assist you.

## 9974

[9974](#_ftn_2113)

B”H, Days of Selichos, 5730
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr.[2114] Eliyahu Amikam, may he live,
Peace and Blessing!

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and with a blessing for success in instilling true Yiddishkeit wherever your hand can reach.

P.S. The delivery was delayed, and your letter of 27 Elul has just been received. Thank you for the blessings. May it be the will of Hashem, Creator and Leader of the world, that He fulfill all the blessings that the children of Israel bless one another with, in their entirety and in their innermost essence. From here on, may the content of letters and news be only good, and in the well-known style of "good that is visible and revealed."

Although, on the face of it, according to the way of nature, this is not a matter for today or tomorrow morning, yet the [salvation](#_ftn_2115) of Hashem is in the blink of an eye. Especially since, in these very last years, we have already become accustomed to miracles, even to revealed miracles. Yet, it is painful that these revealed miracles do not negate the possibility of performing undesirable acts, or worse, at a time when the time has long since come to understand the negation of such undesirable acts—especially when it concerns the many. It is particularly painful that the nations of the world say with one voice that the method and the action are undesirable, yet with some of our own brethren, the children of Israel, one must argue and bring proofs that this is not the way, and that the results, naturally, will be the opposite of what they hope for. All this *shakla v’tarya* (debate) is of no avail until reality comes and slaps them in the face, and the next day the whole thing repeats itself.

One should not dwell at length on such a painful matter, yet I cannot restrain myself from writing at least a few lines regarding the alarming matter [of the decree](#_ftn_2116) of "Who is a Jew" according to the law as it currently exists. The blowing of the Shofar on Rosh Hashanah emphasizes, again and again, the concept of the uniqueness and unity of our people, the children of Israel. As [our teacher](#_ftn_2117) Rav Saadia Gaon said—who in his time fought against those who held onto the Tanach while rejecting the words of our Sages of blessed memory, with the well-known claim that "times have changed, intellects have changed, and nature has changed," including the nature of the Jewish people—the *Rasag* writes in his *Siddur* that one of the purposes of blowing the Shofar on Rosh Hashanah is to remind each and every person of the sound of the Shofar that was heard before the giving of the Torah, and of the Torah and the standing at Mount Sinai. The point of this is, in the language of the prayer: "And You have chosen us from among all peoples and tongues."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that, at the very least, from here on, the son of the mistress—the children of Sarah—will not run after the son of the handmaid—the children of Hagar—[as per the promise](#_ftn_2118) of Hashem to Avraham, "For in Yitzchak shall your seed be called." May the prayer of Rosh Hashanah be fulfilled: "Sound the great Shofar for our freedom (freedom from internal exile, and through that, also freedom from external exile) and raise a banner to gather our exiles," etc., with the true and complete Redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

## 9996

[9996](#_ftn_2122)

[B"H](#_ftn_2123), Days of Selichos, 5730

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, whose work is the work of Heaven, etc., etc., [Rabbi Yitzchak](#_ftn_2124) (may he live and be well),

Peace and blessing!

Regarding his [reply](#_ftn_2125) to the matter raised — a session [of halachic deliberation](#_ftn_2126) — and regarding his daughter (may she live and be well),

May it be the will of Hashem that this fulfills [“Give thanks](#_ftn_2127) to Hashem,” etc., and [for us](#_ftn_2128) — who also recite the blessing upon traveling by airplane over the sea — all four matters were present in this.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all who are yours: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. Your letter has reached me, and I thank you — the merit of the many is great, and “with the many [they](#_ftn_2129) stood.”

Regarding the nature of the event (and concerning the “therefore” and the practical application):

Our Sages of blessed memory state (*Bereishis Rabbah*, ch. 30:8) that there are events after which one “sees a new world.” And since it includes (ibid.) Noach with the others, up to Iyov, it stands to reason that this is not limited to *tzaddikim* alone; rather, Noach himself became new and for the better (similar to Iyov), and Iyov saw the world — a new world (similar to Noach).

And even though it requires a major event such as the one mentioned above — which is why they said there that there are only five such instances (and with this, it is understood why regarding Iyov it does not cite the verses from the beginning of the book that detail [his losses], but rather [“He pours](#_ftn_2130) out to the ground,” etc., as only that is a miraculous occurrence (*Chullin* 43a and *Tosafos* s.v. *Yiflach*)) — nevertheless, in many matters we find one-sixtieth of them (and their effect).

And since in the present case the participation of many was involved — this seemingly awakens the logic that the renewal will be in relation to speaking to the many, etc. — as we discussed during our last meeting.

And it is worth noting that the day itself is a factor, for on Rosh Hashanah the entire [world](#_ftn_2131) (great and small) is renewed (and there are wondrous things regarding this in *Iggeres HaKodesh* by the Alter Rebbe, Epistle 13).

## 9978

[9978](#_ftn_2135)

B”H, Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. [Aharon](#_ftn_2136) Yariv, may he live and be well,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter with thanks.

## 9979

[9979](#_ftn_2138)

B"H, Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. [Uri Zvi](#_ftn_2139) Greenberg, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby extend my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I received your letter in due course, in response to [my letter](#_ftn_2140). After asking your forgiveness, I must say that this is not the response I had hoped and waited for. For even if one were to say that you are correct in your reasoning and justifications for refraining from writing and sounding a great cry regarding the [law](#_ftn_2141) of "Who is a Jew"—as per the content of your letter, that "there is no one listening," etc.—the fact remains that by remaining silent and letting it pass in silence, even when that silence stems from great pain and sorrow, it remains within the domain of the individual who is suffering and has no influence outside of him. This is not the case when one responds; especially a response in your style, utilizing the talents granted to you and the influence you possess, where one can hope for the deepest impact both at the time and thereafter. For a printed word has an influence that is not limited to the time of printing or the first reading.

I must add another reason, which in my opinion is the primary one: the argument—in the style of [our Sages](#_ftn_2142), of blessed memory, "It is revealed and known that if one protests to them, they will not listen"—has no place in our current era, an era of a mixture of light and darkness, bitter and sweet, and even—from one extreme to the other. If there were someone who would endeavor to convince them, even with the simplest and most understandable words, there are certainly, most certainly, those who would accept such persuasion. Moreover, they would be happy for just and good persuasion, and beyond that—they are waiting for it; they are waiting for someone to persuade them.

And if the above holds true for every issue, it is all the more so regarding a matter that concerns the very existence of our people, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be—in Eretz Yisrael and in the Diaspora.

[It seems](#_ftn_2143) I have already pointed out to you the words of our Sages (Bava Metzia 31a), whose language is precise to the ultimate degree. Their instruction is clear: [“You shall surely rebuke”](#_ftn_2144)—even a hundred times. This means that even if a rebuker who is worthy of the name and knows his craft has rebuked [someone] **ninety-nine** times and it was of no avail, he is commanded by our Torah—the Torah of life—to rebuke for the hundredth time. Furthermore, the command for the hundredth time is included together with the command to rebuke the first time—that is, with the same intensity, the same vitality, and the same confidence that even in an era where [truth is absent](#_ftn_2145), etc., in the end, [“Truth will sprout from the earth”](#_ftn_2146).

I do not wish to dwell on this further, for surely the above is not new to you. I have only come to awaken and strengthen your thoughts on this, based on [the principle](#_ftn_2147) that one encourages those who are already encouraged.

I will conclude with something I heard regarding why your [ancestor’s](#_ftn_2148) name was "Saraf" (I believe you told me he was your great-grandfather)—because he would be "burned" (consumed) in his prayer. And yet, he would come to the subsequent prayer, and again to the next, with the same enthusiasm as the prayer before it, and perhaps even more.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that in your style—where you sometimes write with fire upon fire—you will succeed in burning away every undesirable matter, and subsequently ignite the readers with the fire of enthusiasm for everything good and holy. And regarding the core content of this letter: to declare openly to all nations, including—to make a distinction—our people, the Children of Israel, that a Jew is one who denies *avodah zarah* (Megillah 13a)—a service (and concept) that is [foreign](#_ftn_2149) to him, foreign to the Torah of the people of Israel and its 613 *mitzvos*. And all the more so in its literal sense—*avodah zarah*—and especially the *avodah zarah* of our current era: servitude and *bitul* before the **worshippers** of *avodah zarah*, the nations of the world.

It is my hope that you have seen what has been published regarding the matter discussed here on several occasions, at the very least what has been printed about it in Eretz Yisrael.

9980

[9980](#_ftn_2150)

[B"H](#_ftn_2151), Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and accomplished individual, engaged in communal affairs, Mr. Yaakov Rosenthal,

Shalom u’vracha!

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Although it is delayed, I acknowledge receipt of your two letters along with their enclosures. From them, I have seen that our friend, Mr. Avraham Parshan, did not exaggerate at all in his description of you and your affairs; on the contrary, he spoke only [a fraction of your praise](#_ftn_2152), even though it was not in your presence.

Based on the above, my hope is strong that you will not be offended at all that I did not acknowledge receipt of your letters until now; furthermore, may your forgiveness and pardon be complete.

The reason for the delay in my response is not only due to the multitude of pressures—for at the head of these pressures is the very problem discussed in your letters—but rather, and primarily, because I hoped and anticipated that perhaps, finally, the moment would arrive when the entire [terrible](#_ftn_2153) decree would be annulled. It is a decree the likes of which has never been seen in the history of our people, the Children of Israel—a history saturated with blood, fire, and pillars of smoke, and various strange and bizarre decrees. Yet, despite all this, no man or woman among all the nations of the earth dared to come and annul the very existence of the Jewish people by declaring that anyone who brings a scrap of paper stating that he is a Jew, is indeed a Jew.

[They say that in the past, there were associations of beggars, and even to be accepted as a member of the association, there were restrictions and requirements, and [not](#_ftn_2154) everyone who wished to take the name could simply come and take it. And here, we have merited in this enlightened generation—which produced Hitler and his cohorts and the like—a most enlightened and democratic innovation: our people, the Children of Israel, are distinguished from all the nations on the face of the earth in that there is no fence, partition, or restriction, etc., and permission has been granted, in the form of law, that anyone who wishes to enter or leave—the only requirement, as mentioned, is to bring a scrap of paper on which it is written that he is a Jew. For certainly, even those who were enthusiastic about fighting for the law in its current phrasing knew clearly what the meaning of "conversion" is without the definition "according to Halacha."]

I do not know if, after what is written above, there is any point in entering into the details of the arguments and reasons that you wrote in your letter. I will, G-d willing, write more about this. In any case, I wish to add one point: as far as I know, it is accepted in all courts, in all countries, and among all peoples, that before a judge approaches a case to render a verdict and judgment, he must examine for himself whether the matter is within his jurisdiction, and whether he is not biased in the matter at hand, etc., etc.

Based on the above, it is seemingly difficult that when the discussion regarding the aforementioned law came before the Knesset, it would have been appropriate for the Christian and Muslim members of the Knesset, and all those who do not believe in the existence and destiny of the Jewish people, to refrain from voting and participating in the debate on this subject. Furthermore, they should have announced the reason for this: that when the matter concerns a Jew, a Christian or a Muslim has no place to express an opinion, and those who are opposed to the very existence of the people—and certainly to its uniqueness—should not express an opinion. This applies to several others of this type among the Knesset members, with all due respect and apologies.

In the same vein, regarding judges who declare that the laws of the Torah of Israel are Nazi and cruel laws: they should announce that they are not fit to judge the matter, and certainly they are not fit to participate in an international assembly to defend the religion of Israel and the persecutions against it.

Unfortunately, not only did they not act in this way, but I have not found in any place, newspaper, pamphlet, or record, etc., that anyone raised the aforementioned question: was so-and-so permitted—from a moral, conscientious, or even legal standpoint—to participate and vote in such a debate?

It is understood that one can adopt an approach in the well-known style—"on the basis of democracy"—and democracy is supposedly in opposition to any discrimination. But then, one cannot do things halfway. If they must abolish discrimination regarding who has a share in the territory called Eretz Yisrael and who does not, they must also abolish the discrimination that the one performing the conversion must be a Jew. For what matters is that the intention of the "convert" is sincere to be a Jew, and that is enough. For this, it would be more appropriate that the one performing the conversion be a psychologist of any nation or religion, provided he is a trustworthy person and an authority in his profession, so that after a conversation of a few moments with the one who wants to receive the scrap of paper that he is a Jew, he will be convinced by the power of his wisdom that the intention is true—[and the Merciful One](#_ftn_2155) desires the heart—and this is sufficient to give him a certificate—a certified psychologist’s certificate—that he is a Jew!

It is difficult for me to elaborate on this matter, especially in these days when we teach merit for every single one of the Children of Israel. And what I have written above is also based on [what is brought regarding these days](#_ftn_2156), [that "when there is](#_ftn_2157) judgment below, there is no judgment above," and below there is enough judgment and debate. May it be the will that I fulfill my obligation with this writing, and may we merit the victory of truth and the nullification of falsehood—especially such a blatant falsehood, where they deceive the non-Jew and tell him that he has become a Jew and "you are our brother," [and](#_ftn_2158) they deceive the environment and the public that there is an "achievement" here, while at the same time it is destruction and ruin. And ultimately, they deceive themselves, in the style of [our Sages](#_ftn_2159) of blessed memory, that "my bowels are stirred"—that democracy has won, discrimination has been abolished, hearts have been drawn together, the partition between Israel and the nations has been abolished, and all the walls that protected our people, the Children of Israel, for several thousand years have been breached, and the enemies of Israel have made it fair game for the beasts of the field, etc.

And we conclude with good, in the style of the Rosh Hashanah prayer: "And so, give **honor** to Your **people**, Hashem... joy to **Your land**, and gladness to **Your city** (and immediately following this) the preparation of a light for the son of Yishai, Your Mashiach." May he come and redeem every single one of the Children of Israel, wherever they may be, from the internal exile (of the *yetzer*) and from the exile in the literal sense. May it be the will that this happens in our days.

## 9982

[9982](#_ftn_2163)

[5730]

1) Regarding the matter of the time of Sefirah – (do the chroniclers say so)?! – See Yevamos 62b. And in many places this is **explicit** in the **Poskim**.

In the example of the Three Weeks, there are also days of Shabbos and Rosh Chodesh.

And in the case at hand, it is not as difficult as the above, according to the words of our Sages that the reason [for the mourning] is that they did not treat one another with respect (Yevamos, ibid.), and it is obvious (according to the **nature** of human beings) that on days of joy, the lack of respect is less prevalent.

2) Regarding Gehinom, etc. See also Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah (Chapter 8, Halacha 5 and onwards), where it states, "There is no way in this world to grasp it" (the reward, and from this it is understood regarding its opposite – the punishment. See there).

Regarding the warning – even when the warning is for the death penalty in its literal sense – the essence and quality of the **actual** pain of death is not known, except that they tell him that the pain is incomparable, etc., and that is sufficient.

3) Regarding which seforim to study – see Hilchos Talmud Torah by the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 1, end of Halacha 4, from which the answer to his question is understood.

Regarding Crown Heights – and since, according to [what was discussed during Acharon Shel Pesach 5729](#_ftn_2168), this is a ruling of the holy Torah and for the benefit of the **many**, certainly through this, the blessings of Hashem will be increased in whatever is needed. And surely everyone is in need of Hashem’s blessing.

I will mention [you] at the Tziyun.

To remain in Crown Heights – that you should accept a position here in Crown Heights.

## 9983

[5730]

The reason—at least in brief: It is **exactly** the same reason that the government of Israel pays in foreign currency (**which is immediately necessary**) and in **staggering** amounts, and exerts itself **by all means** to ensure that they accept the money—to purchase weapons in the U.S.A. **and in Germany**, etc., and is not satisfied with the rifles **and the like that it** produces in Eretz Yisrael itself. And no one opens their mouth or chirps. **On the contrary.**

And the reason is that when one wishes **to defend** the Jewish people, one must have weapons and mitzvos **as they ought to be**. And it is **impossible** to swap a Phantom—and, lehavdil, an esrog that has a tradition from our forefathers—for an "Uzi," and, lehavdil, an esrog without a tradition, etc. And he who wishes to swap, etc., **and a word to the wise is sufficient**.

[Apparently the conclusion was not transmitted (in response to A):] Beyond the above: In every army there are several divisions and types: infantry, [those] in chariots, and those, etc., and for each one there is the weapon specific to it, and only with the weapon specific to it will it succeed. And he who wishes to force one type to be armed with the weapon belonging to another type (mitzvos that are connected to and dependent upon the tradition of the forefathers)—this places the entire matter of defense in danger, etc. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

## 9984

Regarding your writing that my lack of response (at times) to questions in Chassidus, etc., is interpreted as a slight, etc. — it is obvious that there is no basis for this whatsoever. ## 9885

[9885](#_ftn_2178)

[5730]

It is a well-known statement of the Rambam that there is a common denominator between the illnesses of the body and the illnesses of the soul (Introduction to Pirkei Avos, Chapter 3; Hilchos Deos, Chapter 2). Just as a body that has been weakened by hunger—especially prolonged hunger—finds it extremely difficult to grasp wisdom and knowledge, including the knowledge that explains the importance **and necessity** of certain foods—**especially** if one has not been accustomed to studying this knowledge—so too is it **as mentioned above** regarding a soul that has been weakened by a lack of fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos, which are its nourishment, **and so on**.

After that, either decide for yourself or (if you are in doubt) ask a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah* **in practice**—for his instruction according to *Shulchan Aruch*.

Many whose lives were similar (regarding suffering, etc.) to yours have found salvation by dedicating their energy, time, and **attention** to helping people who are in distress, confusion, or similar situations, and by engaging in this consistently as part of their daily routine.

Through this, they also viewed and "valued" their own lives in a **completely** different way [which added to their joy of life, their self-confidence, and led them to find new meaning in life, **etc.**].
